## Assistant (2026-04-25 16:28:13)

I’ll treat the pasted handover as the controlling prompt and the TeX as the current draft. I’ll focus specifically on Zeta B: actual-source realization/freedom, not paper-editing.

Initial read: the prompt’s key distinction is formal failure versus literal zeta-source failure. Zeta B has to test whether actual one-pair zero contributions impose a hidden jet relation strong enough to kill the formal countermodel.

_Thought for 2m 25s_

## Zeta B verdict

The actual one-pair zeta source class **does not appear to contain the hidden jet-locking law needed to rescue Bottleneck C**.

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The map from an exterior zero-pair contribution to post-affine jets has enough freedom to approximate }r(u)=u^2.
}
\]

So the local obstruction is not merely an artifact of allowing arbitrary formal sources. The current draft’s only remaining rescue route would need a **global aggregate identity over actual zeta zeros**, not a local one-pair jet identity. The handover correctly identifies that the formal Bottleneck-C package already fails unless actual zeta sources satisfy a strong hidden restriction excluding \(r=u^2\). 

---

## 1. Actual one-pair source

The draft’s omitted-zero contribution is

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

Set

\[
u=t-m,\qquad x=2m-\gamma,\qquad a\in\{\beta,1-\beta\}.
\]

Then

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(m+u)
=
\sum_{a\in\{\beta,1-\beta\}}
\frac{a}{a^2+(x+2u)^2}.
\]

After midpoint affine subtraction,

\[
r_\rho(u)
=
f_{\beta,\gamma}(m+u)
-
f_{\beta,\gamma}(m)
-
f_{\beta,\gamma}'(m)u.
\]

Thus affine subtraction kills only the \(u^0,u^1\) terms. It does **not** impose any relation among the \(u^2,u^3,u^4,\ldots\) jets, matching the handover’s warning. 

Write

\[
r_\rho(u)
=
\rho_2u^2+\rho_3u^3+\rho_4u^4+O(u^5).
\]

A direct differentiation gives:

\[
\boxed{
\rho_2
=
\sum_{a\in\{\beta,1-\beta\}}
\frac{4a(3x^2-a^2)}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\rho_4
=
\sum_{a\in\{\beta,1-\beta\}}
\frac{16a(a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4)}{(a^2+x^2)^5}.
}
\]

These are the coefficient-normalized jets, so for the formal model \(r(u)=u^2\), one has

\[
\rho_2=1,\qquad \rho_4=0.
\]

---

## 2. The needed locking law is not present

The local obstruction formula in the draft has the form

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

For identical source shapes, \(\nu_{21,7}=0\) would require

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
}
\]

This is the jet-locking identity the Zeta agents were asked to test. The handover correctly states that without such an identity, the local package should be considered failed, not merely incomplete. 

But the actual one-pair ratio

\[
R(\beta,x):=\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
\]

is a genuine function of the exterior zero-pair displacement \(x=2m-\gamma\) and horizontal zero parameter \(\beta\). It is not tied to the frozen baseline quantities \(q_0,q_0''\).

For large exterior separation \(|x|\to\infty\),

\[
\rho_2
=
\frac{12}{x^4}
-
\frac{40(\beta^3+(1-\beta)^3)}{x^6}
+
O(x^{-8}),
\]

\[
\rho_4
=
\frac{80}{x^6}
-
\frac{560(\beta^3+(1-\beta)^3)}{x^8}
+
O(x^{-10}),
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}
+
O(x^{-4}).
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}\to 0
\qquad (|x|\to\infty).
\]

So the actual exterior-pair family contains normalized sources with

\[
r_\rho(u)/\rho_2
=
u^2
+
O(x^{-1})u^3
+
O(x^{-2})u^4
+
O(x^{-3})u^5+\cdots .
\]

This approximates the formal countermodel \(r(u)=u^2\) arbitrarily well on finite jet level by taking a sufficiently far exterior zero pair.

---

## 3. Concrete critical-line subfamily check

Even on the critical-line subfamily \(\beta=1/2\), the ratio is not locked. In that case,

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{16(80x^4-40x^2+1)}
{(4x^2+1)^2(12x^2-1)}.
\]

As \(|x|\to\infty\),

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4}).
\]

Thus even under the RH-compatible horizontal parameter \(\beta=1/2\), the actual one-pair source family still approaches the \(r=u^2\) model.

This is important: the obstruction is not caused by allowing off-critical \(\beta\)-freedom. It already survives in the critical-line one-pair shape class.

---

## 4. Local rank/freedom statement

The map

\[
(\beta,x)\mapsto (\rho_2,\rho_4)
\]

is generically rank \(2\). One quick asymptotic check:

\[
S_3(\beta):=\beta^3+(1-\beta)^3,
\qquad
S_3'(\beta)=6\beta-3.
\]

Using the large-\(|x|\) expansions,

\[
\det
\frac{\partial(\rho_2,\rho_4)}{\partial(\beta,x)}
=
-\frac{7680\,S_3'(\beta)}{x^{13}}
+
O(x^{-15}).
\]

So for \(\beta\ne 1/2\), the two-jet map is locally open in the \((\rho_2,\rho_4)\)-plane. At \(\beta=1/2\), the symmetry kills first-order \(\beta\)-variation, but the displacement parameter \(x\) alone still varies the ratio \(R=\rho_4/\rho_2\), and far exterior pairs still approximate \(R=0\).

Thus there is no local one-pair analytic constraint forcing

\[
\rho_4/\rho_2
=
10q_0^2/9-5q_0''/(18q_0).
\]

---

## 5. Relation to \(q_0,q_0''\)

In the Bottleneck-C source calculation, \(q_0,q_0''\) are frozen baseline quantities; the exterior source contributes through \(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm,\eta\) after affine subtraction. The one-pair source jets \(\rho_2,\rho_4\) are therefore not intrinsically tied to \(q_0,q_0''\).

So the realization map has product-type freedom:

\[
(\text{baseline})\quad \leadsto\quad (q_0,q_0''),
\]

\[
(\text{chosen exterior pair})\quad \leadsto\quad (\rho_2,\rho_4).
\]

The draft does not prove any source theorem coupling these two blocks. The handover explicitly says that the only viable rescue would be an actual zeta-source restriction strong enough to exclude \(r=u^2\); the calculation above shows no such restriction exists at the local one-pair level. 

---

## 6. Consequence for the obstruction

Take a good patch with

\[
q_0\ne 0,\qquad q_0''=0.
\]

For a far exterior pair, normalize its source shape so that \(\rho_2=1\). Then

\[
\rho_4=O(x^{-2}).
\]

Substituting into the draft’s obstruction coefficient gives

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}O(x^{-2})
-
\frac{q_0^3}{216}
\right].
\]

For \(|x|\) sufficiently large,

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}\ne 0.
}
\]

Indeed,

\[
\nu_{21,7}
\to
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}},
\]

which is exactly the formal \(r=u^2,\ q_0''=0\) obstruction.

So the local obstruction is **source-realization compatible** in the sense Zeta B was asked to test.

---

## 7. What this does and does not prove

This proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{There is no local one-pair zeta jet-locking law strong enough to rescue Bottleneck C.}
}
\]

It also proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The formal }r=u^2\text{ countermodel is approximable by actual exterior-pair source shapes.}
}
\]

It does **not** prove that the literal full zeta tail at a fixed height \(m\), after summing all exterior zeros with their actual amplitudes, has nonzero aggregate obstruction. That would require ruling out a global cancellation identity over the actual zero set.

But that is now the only possible rescue:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any rescue must be a global aggregate zeta-zero identity, not a local source-realization theorem.}
}
\]

Given the current draft and prompt, Zeta B should report the rescue route as effectively narrowed to an unproved and highly nonlocal aggregate cancellation theorem. The local actual-source rigidity route fails.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 16:35:12)

I’m applying the uploaded “Zeta Global B” prompt directly. The attack target is now aggregate cancellation, not one-pair locking or package repair.

_Thought for 1m 8s_

## Zeta Global B — adversarial aggregate-cancellation test

### Verdict

The remaining aggregate cancellation is **not forced by local zeta-source geometry**.

There is a simple adversarial finite-tail model, using actual one-pair source shapes with positive natural weights, for which

\[
A_2\neq 0,\qquad \frac{A_4}{A_2}\approx 0,
\qquad q_0\neq 0,\qquad q_0''=0,
\]

and hence

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}\neq 0.
\]

So the only possible rescue is a genuinely global identity over the actual full zeta zero set. The uploaded instruction already frames this correctly: one-pair jet-locking failed, far exterior sources approximate \(r=u^2\), and package redesign cannot hide a nonzero physical \(S\)-coefficient. 

---

# 1. Aggregate formula

Start from

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{ij}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

Let the actual exterior source atoms have weights \(w_i\). Define

\[
A_2:=\sum_i w_i\rho_{i,2},
\qquad
A_4:=\sum_i w_i\rho_{i,4}.
\]

If the quadratic source expansion includes all ordered pairs \((i,j)\), including \(i=j\), then

\[
\sum_{i,j}w_iw_j
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
=
2A_2A_4,
\]

and

\[
\sum_{i,j}w_iw_j\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
=
A_2^2.
\]

Thus the expected aggregate formula is correct:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
}
\]

This is the aggregate physical \(S\)-visible coefficient whose vanishing is required. The previous handover correctly identifies this as a global zeta-tail identity, not a package identity or one-pair source identity. 

If the draft’s later bookkeeping excludes diagonal terms \(i=j\), the corrected off-diagonal version is

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm off}
=
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
-
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\sum_i w_i^2
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}\rho_{i,2}\rho_{i,4}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}^2
\right].
\]

But this correction does **not** rescue cancellation. With at least two far exterior source atoms of the same type, the off-diagonal coefficient has the same nonzero bracket, only with a different positive combinatorial prefactor.

---

# 2. Aggregate cancellation condition

If \(A_2=0\), then the aggregate vanishes trivially. Otherwise,

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0
\]

is equivalent to

\[
\frac{q_0}{240}\frac{A_4}{A_2}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
=0.
\]

Therefore the required aggregate locking identity is

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
}
\]

So the global rescue has only two possible forms:

\[
\boxed{A_2=0}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
A_4/A_2
=
10q_0^2/9-5q_0''/(18q_0).
}
\]

The question is whether actual zeta symmetries force either. They do not, at least not from the current source architecture.

---

# 3. Actual symmetries do not force \(A_2=0\)

The one-pair source jets are

\[
\rho_2(\beta,x)
=
\sum_{a\in\{\beta,1-\beta\}}
\frac{4a(3x^2-a^2)}{(a^2+x^2)^3},
\]

\[
\rho_4(\beta,x)
=
\sum_{a\in\{\beta,1-\beta\}}
\frac{16a(a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4)}{(a^2+x^2)^5}.
\]

For \(|x|\) large,

\[
\rho_2(\beta,x)
=
\frac{12}{x^4}+O(x^{-6}),
\]

\[
\rho_4(\beta,x)
=
\frac{80}{x^6}+O(x^{-8}).
\]

Thus every sufficiently far exterior zero-pair atom has

\[
\rho_2>0,
\qquad
\rho_4>0.
\]

The standard zeta symmetries do not introduce a sign reversal here:

\[
\beta\leftrightarrow 1-\beta
\]

is already included inside the one-pair atom, and the formulas depend on \(x^2\), so vertical conjugation contributes the same far-field sign. Multiplicities are positive. Therefore a finite collection of far exterior atoms with positive actual weights gives

\[
A_2=\sum_i w_i\rho_{i,2}>0.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
A_2=0
\text{ is not forced by source symmetry.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Actual symmetries do not force the aggregate ratio

For far exterior atoms,

\[
\frac{\rho_4(\beta,x)}{\rho_2(\beta,x)}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4}).
\]

In particular, on the critical-line subfamily \(\beta=1/2\), the same asymptotic holds. The previous Zeta result already noted that these actual exterior-pair shapes approximate the formal bad germ \(r=u^2\). 

Now choose \(N\ge 1\) far exterior source atoms with

\[
\beta_i=\frac12,
\qquad
|x_i|=X,
\qquad
w_i>0.
\]

Then

\[
A_2
=
\sum_i w_i\rho_{i,2}
>0,
\]

and

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{\rho_4(1/2,X)}{\rho_2(1/2,X)}
=
\frac{20}{3X^2}+O(X^{-4}).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_4}{A_2}\to 0
\qquad (X\to\infty).
}
\]

This is already enough to defeat structural aggregate cancellation.

---

# 5. Good-patch adversarial model

Take a good phase patch with

\[
q_0\neq0,
\qquad
q_0''=0.
\]

Then the cancellation identity would require

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}.
\]

But the far-tail model gives

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{20}{3X^2}+O(X^{-4}).
\]

For \(X\) sufficiently large,

\[
\frac{20}{3X^2}+O(X^{-4})
\neq
\frac{10q_0^2}{9},
\]

because \(q_0\neq0\). Therefore

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
=
\frac{A_2^2}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}\frac{A_4}{A_2}
-
\frac{q_0^3}{216}
\right]
\neq0.
\]

More sharply,

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
\to
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}A_2^2
\]

up to the scaling behavior of \(A_2\). The bracket tends to

\[
-\frac{q_0^3}{216},
\]

which is nonzero.

Thus the finite-tail adversarial model satisfies

\[
A_2\neq0,
\qquad
A_4/A_2\approx0,
\qquad
q_0\neq0,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}\neq0.
}
\]

The earlier local audit already established that this is a physical \(T\)-horizontal failure, not a quotient-only artifact: \(f_{A,Y}\neq0\) implies \(\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f_{A,Y}/c\neq0\). 

---

# 6. Off-diagonal-only variant

If someone objects that the double sum should exclude \(i=j\), take \(N\ge2\) identical far atoms with equal weights. Then

\[
\sum_{i\ne j}w_iw_j\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}>0,
\]

and

\[
\frac{
\sum_{i\ne j}w_iw_j
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
}{
2\sum_{i\ne j}w_iw_j\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
}
=
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3X^2}+O(X^{-4}).
\]

So the same nonzero bracket remains. Diagonal exclusion changes only the positive prefactor, not the obstruction.

Thus neither self-pair bookkeeping nor ordered/unordered symmetrization gives a structural cancellation.

---

# 7. What global identity would be required?

The only possible rescue is a new theorem asserting that the **actual full exterior zeta tail**, not arbitrary finite-tail source geometry, satisfies

\[
\boxed{
A_2=0
}
\]

on every good patch, or else

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}
}
\]

on every good patch with \(A_2\neq0\).

Equivalently, the full actual zero set would need to satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=
0.
}
\]

This would be a new global zeta-tail cancellation theorem. It is not a consequence of the one-pair source formula, not a consequence of the \(\beta\leftrightarrow1-\beta\) symmetry, not a consequence of vertical conjugation, and not a package-level identity. The uploaded instructions also state that the remaining possible rescue is exactly such a global zero-set identity. 

---

## Final Zeta Global B conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{No structural aggregate cancellation follows from the current local source framework.}
}
\]

There is an explicit adversarial finite-tail good-patch model with positive actual source signs:

\[
\beta_i=\frac12,\qquad |x_i|=X\gg1,\qquad w_i>0,
\]

for which

\[
A_2>0,
\qquad
A_4/A_2\to0,
\]

and on a patch with

\[
q_0\neq0,\qquad q_0''=0,
\]

one gets

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}\neq0.
}
\]

Therefore the current RH route survives only if one proves a new, pointwise, global identity over the full actual exterior zeta zero set:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0
\quad\text{on every good patch.}
}
\]

Absent that theorem, Bottleneck C remains locally failed.

I’ll execute the uploaded global-identity attack now. I’ll first pin down the draft’s definitions of \(F_{\rm ext}\), \(q\), and the relevant derivative normalizations, then test the identity itself.

The derivative normalization checks out: substituting \(A_2=F_{\rm ext}''/2\) and \(A_4=F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}/24\) gives the prompt’s factor \(20\), so the stated ratio identity has the right constants.

_Thought for 1m 39s_

## 1. Verdict

The proposed global identity is **not proved by the draft and does not follow from the current zeta-tail architecture**. As a cutoff/exterior-tail identity it is structurally unsupported and contradicted by the admissible far-tail model; for the literal full actual zeta tail it remains a new, highly nonstandard global dependency, not a closed gate. The uploaded handover correctly frames this as the final Bottleneck-C fork. 

---

## 2. Constants checked

The aggregate obstruction is

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right],
\]

with

\[
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Substitution gives

\[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
=
\frac{q_0}{11520}
F_{\rm ext}''(m)F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m),
\]

and

\[
\frac1{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2
=
\frac1{576}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
F_{\rm ext}''(m)^2.
\]

Multiplying by \(11520\), the derivative-form identity is exactly

\[
\boxed{
q_0F_{\rm ext}''(m)F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)
+
20\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
F_{\rm ext}''(m)^2
=0.
}
\]

If \(F_{\rm ext}''(m)\neq0\), this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}.
}
\]

So the constants in the prompt are correct. 

---

## 3. What \(F_{\rm ext}\) is relative to \(q\)

In the draft’s decomposition, \(q(t)=\Phi'(t)\) is the full zeta/scattering phase derivative. It is then split into a local model, smooth/background terms, omitted-zero tail, and residual bookkeeping. The exterior object relevant here is therefore **not** the full \(q(t)\). It is the omitted/cutoff exterior zero-tail component, or the corresponding post-affine source remainder.

For the Bottleneck-C source calculation, affine subtraction removes only the value and first derivative of each exterior atom:

\[
r_\rho(t)
=
f_\rho(t)-f_\rho(m)-f_\rho'(m)(t-m).
\]

Thus

\[
r_\rho''(m)=f_\rho''(m),
\qquad
r_\rho^{(4)}(m)=f_\rho^{(4)}(m).
\]

So for the aggregate,

\[
F_{\rm ext}(t)=\sum_\alpha w_\alpha f_\alpha(t)
\]

may be used for \(A_2,A_4\), because affine correction does not affect second or fourth derivatives.

The important point: \(F_{\rm ext}\) is a **complementary cutoff/windowed tail**, not the same object as \(q_0\). The baseline \(q_0\) is the local-model-plus-affine baseline in the corrected block calculation. Therefore the proposed identity is not a tautology of the form “a function satisfies an identity involving its own derivatives.” It is a cross-identity coupling a cutoff tail \(F_{\rm ext}\) to the baseline \(q_0\).

---

## 4. Decisive calculation: the one-atom/tail ratio has the wrong freedom

For one exterior zero-pair atom,

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

Set

\[
x=2m-\gamma,
\qquad
a\in\{\beta,1-\beta\}.
\]

The post-affine Taylor coefficients are

\[
\rho_2
=
\frac{f_{\beta,\gamma}''(m)}2,
\qquad
\rho_4
=
\frac{f_{\beta,\gamma}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The prior Zeta results gave

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\qquad (|x|\to\infty),
\]

so in derivative form

\[
\frac{f_{\beta,\gamma}^{(4)}(m)}
     {f_{\beta,\gamma}''(m)}
=
12\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{80}{x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\to0.
\]

For a finite exterior tail made from far atoms with positive natural weights,

\[
F_{\rm ext}''(m)>0,
\qquad
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
\approx 0.
\]

But on a good patch with

\[
q_0\neq0,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]

the required identity demands

\[
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3},
\]

which is nonzero and large on the usual \(q_0\asymp Q\) scale. This is incompatible with the far-tail model. The handover already records the same obstruction at the aggregate level: far exterior atoms give \(A_2>0\), \(A_4/A_2\approx0\), while cancellation would demand \(A_4/A_2=10q_0^2/9\) when \(q_0''=0\). 

Thus the identity is **not forced by local source geometry, conjugation symmetry, functional-equation pairing, or positive tail weights**. This matches the earlier aggregate-agent conclusion. 

---

## 5. ODE obstruction

If the identity were to hold pointwise on every good patch as a genuine structural theorem, then locally it would imply the fourth-order differential relation

\[
F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}
=
\left(
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}
\right)
F_{\rm ext}''.
\]

This is a very rigid ODE for a cutoff sum of rational zero-pair atoms. The draft does not derive such an ODE, and the atom-level calculation argues against it.

At the meromorphic level the mismatch is even sharper. A single atom has off-real simple poles. Near such a pole \(p\),

\[
f(t)\sim \frac{C}{t-p},
\]

so

\[
f''(t)\sim \frac{2C}{(t-p)^3},
\qquad
f^{(4)}(t)\sim \frac{24C}{(t-p)^5},
\]

and therefore

\[
\frac{f^{(4)}(t)}{f''(t)}
\sim
\frac{12}{(t-p)^2}.
\]

So the left side has a double-pole signature at exterior-tail poles. The right side,

\[
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0},
\]

is built from the baseline \(q_0\), which by construction has not retained the omitted exterior pole as part of the local baseline. Therefore the ODE cannot be a formal consequence of the cutoff-tail decomposition unless \(q_0\) secretly reimports precisely the same exterior pole structure. That would contradict the intended local/tail split.

This does not disprove a miraculous pointwise identity for the literal full zeta zero set at isolated real \(m\), but it does rule out the identity as a natural local differential law of the current decomposition.

---

## 6. Classification of the identity

The identity is not:

\[
\text{A. proved by the draft;}
\]

not:

\[
\text{B. derivable from the current local zeta-source machinery;}
\]

and not:

\[
\text{a consequence of one-pair rigidity or source symmetry.}
\]

The right classification is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D. an unproved, highly nonstandard global zeta-tail dependency.}
}
\]

For cutoff/windowed tails allowed by the current architecture, the far-tail model shows the identity is structurally false. For the literal full actual exterior zero set, the current framework provides no proof and no mechanism forcing it. The prompt’s prior-result ledger already states that finite-tail adversarial models violate the identity and that only the full actual exterior zeta tail could still rescue the route. 

---

## 7. Impact on Bottleneck C

The current Bottleneck-C route now reduces to the following theorem dependency:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Bottleneck C closes only if the full actual exterior tail satisfies}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}
}
\]

at every good patch with \(F_{\rm ext}''(m)\neq0\), or equivalently

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0.
}
\]

This is not established. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0
\quad\text{is still an unproved global dependency, not a closed gate.}
}
\]

Absent a new global zeta-tail cancellation theorem, the Bottleneck-C architecture should be marked failed at the local stage. The prior handover’s decision theorem remains the correct ledger entry: physical closure is equivalent to vanishing of the aggregate \(S\)-visible coefficient, and no package/quotient/coordinate repair substitutes for that vanishing. 
## User (2026-04-25 16:44:54)

## Assistant (2026-04-25 16:45:19)

I’ll do the ODE B pole/residue test directly. The key calculation is whether the constants in the proposed ODE match the simple-pole principal parts, including the full \(q\) special case.

_Thought for 1m 14s_

## ODE Agent B — meromorphic pole / residue obstruction audit

### Verdict

The proposed ODE **cannot be a meromorphic identity** for \(F_{\rm ext}\), for the full phase derivative \(q\), or for any renormalized complement that still carries the zero-pair poles. The principal parts have incompatible constants. Only an object whose zero-pole principal parts have been explicitly removed can evade this pole test, but such an object no longer supplies the \(A_2,A_4\) moments in the Bottleneck-C row. The current round’s prompt correctly isolates this as the meromorphic/pole test for the proposed ODE rescue. 

---

# 1. Pole structure

The one-pair zero contribution used throughout the Zeta-agent work is

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

For one summand

\[
f_a(t)=\frac{a}{a^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\qquad a>0,
\]

the poles are

\[
p_a^+=\frac{\gamma+ia}{2},
\qquad
p_a^-=\frac{\gamma-ia}{2}.
\]

Writing \(\tau=t-p_a^+\), near the upper pole,

\[
2t-\gamma=ia+2\tau,
\]

so

\[
f_a(t)
=
\frac{a}{(2t-\gamma-ia)(2t-\gamma+ia)}
\sim
\frac{a}{(2\tau)(2ia)}
=
\frac{1}{4i}\frac1{\tau}
=
-\frac{i}{4}\frac1{\tau}.
\]

Thus the residue is

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^+} f_a=-\frac{i}{4},
\]

and similarly

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^-} f_a=+\frac{i}{4}.
\]

If two poles coincide, as in the \(\beta=1/2\) critical-line subcase, the residues add, giving \(\pm i/2\), but they remain purely imaginary. This matters below.

---

# 2. Universal left-side principal part

Let \(G\) be any candidate object carrying a simple pole at \(p\):

\[
G(t)=\frac{C}{\tau}+O(1),
\qquad \tau=t-p,
\qquad C\neq0.
\]

Then

\[
G''(t)=\frac{2C}{\tau^3}+O(1),
\]

and

\[
G^{(4)}(t)=\frac{24C}{\tau^5}+O(1).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
=
\frac{12}{\tau^2}+O(\tau^{-1}).
}
\]

This coefficient \(12\) is independent of the residue \(C\). So any ODE of the form

\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
\]

must make the right-hand side have leading double-pole coefficient \(12\) at every zero-pair pole carried by \(G\).

---

# 3. Right-side principal part when \(q\) has the same pole

Suppose the full phase derivative has

\[
q(t)=\frac{R}{\tau}+O(1),
\qquad R\neq0.
\]

Then

\[
q^2(t)=\frac{R^2}{\tau^2}+O(\tau^{-1}),
\]

and

\[
q''(t)=\frac{2R}{\tau^3}+O(1).
\]

Also,

\[
\frac{q''}{q}
=
\frac{2}{\tau^2}+O(\tau^{-1}).
\]

Hence

\[
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
=
\left(
\frac{40R^2}{3}
-
\frac{20}{3}
\right)
\frac1{\tau^2}
+
O(\tau^{-1}).
\]

For equality with the left side, one would need

\[
\frac{40R^2}{3}
-
\frac{20}{3}
=
12.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
40R^2-20=36,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
R^2=\frac75.
}
\]

But the actual zero-pair residues from the draft’s atom are

\[
R=\pm\frac{i}{4}
\]

for a simple noncoincident pole, hence

\[
R^2=-\frac1{16}.
\]

Then the right-hand double-pole coefficient is

\[
\frac{40}{3}\left(-\frac1{16}\right)-\frac{20}{3}
=
-\frac{5}{6}-\frac{20}{3}
=
-\frac{45}{6}
=
-\frac{15}{2},
\]

not \(12\).

If the \(\beta=1/2\) coincident-pole case gives residue

\[
R=\pm\frac{i}{2},
\]

then

\[
R^2=-\frac14,
\]

and the coefficient becomes

\[
\frac{40}{3}\left(-\frac14\right)-\frac{20}{3}
=
-\frac{10}{3}-\frac{20}{3}
=
-10,
\]

again not \(12\).

More generally, if \(n\) identical same-sign pole contributions coincide,

\[
R=\pm \frac{ni}{4},
\qquad
R^2=-\frac{n^2}{16}<0,
\]

so the required condition

\[
R^2=\frac75
\]

is impossible for natural positive multiplicities.

Thus the principal parts do **not** match.

---

# 4. Case analysis

## Case A — ODE claimed for raw \(F_{\rm ext}=T_{\far}\) or \(T_{\far,R}\)

At an exterior pole included in \(F_{\rm ext}\), the left side has

\[
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}}{F_{\rm ext}''}
=
\frac{12}{\tau^2}+O(\tau^{-1}).
\]

If \(q\) in the right side is the full phase derivative, then \(q\) contains the same pole, but with residue \(R=\pm i/4\) or a positive-multiplicity variant. The right side has leading coefficient \(-15/2\), \(-10\), or more generally a negative coefficient, never \(12\).

So the raw exterior-tail ODE is meromorphically impossible.

If instead the right side uses a local baseline \(q_0\) that does **not** contain the exterior pole, the obstruction is even stronger: the left side has a double pole, while the right side is regular at \(p\).

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Raw cutoff exterior-tail ODE: meromorphically refuted.}
}
\]

---

## Case B — Special case \(F_{\rm ext}=q\)

Then the proposed ODE becomes

\[
\frac{q^{(4)}}{q''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}.
\]

At a simple pole of \(q\),

\[
\frac{q^{(4)}}{q''}
=
\frac{12}{\tau^2}+O(\tau^{-1}),
\]

while

\[
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
=
-\frac{15}{2}\frac1{\tau^2}+O(\tau^{-1})
\]

for the simple zero-pair residue \(R=\pm i/4\).

Thus even the full-\(q\) ODE fails by principal parts.

The mismatch is not a cutoff artifact. It is a residue-constant mismatch.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Full }q\text{-ODE: meromorphically refuted.}
}
\]

---

## Case C — Renormalized complement \(G=T_{\far,R}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}\)

The background and estimation terms are holomorphic at zero-pair poles unless they explicitly reinsert the same zero-pole singularities. Therefore near an exterior zero-pair pole in \(T_{\far,R}\),

\[
G(t)=\frac{C}{\tau}+O(1),
\]

with the same residue \(C\) as the raw far tail.

The left side still has coefficient \(12\). The right side still has the full-\(q\) coefficient determined by the actual phase-pole residue. Therefore the same mismatch persists.

\[
\boxed{
T_{\far,R}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}
\text{ does not evade the pole obstruction.}
}
\]

---

## Case D — Renormalized complement \(G=q-q_{\core}\)

At a non-core exterior pole, \(q_{\core}\) is regular, so

\[
G=q-q_{\core}
\]

has the same pole and same residue as \(q\). Therefore

\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
=
\frac{12}{\tau^2}+O(\tau^{-1}),
\]

while the right side again has coefficient

\[
\frac{40R^2}{3}-\frac{20}{3}.
\]

For the actual zero-pair residues this is not \(12\).

So

\[
\boxed{
q-q_{\core}
\text{ is also meromorphically obstructed.}
}
\]

---

## Case E — Complement \(G=q-F_{\rm ext}\)

If \(F_{\rm ext}\) contains a given exterior pole with exactly the same residue as \(q\), then \(q-F_{\rm ext}\) cancels that exterior pole. At that pole, the left side may be regular, so the previous double-pole contradiction disappears.

But this is not a rescue of the Bottleneck-C row. The aggregate moments are

\[
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24},
\]

for the exterior source object entering the \(\eta\eta\) top row, not for its pole-cancelled complement. The aggregate formula and derivative-moment formulation are the controlling Bottleneck-C identity. 

So an ODE for \(q-F_{\rm ext}\), even if it existed, would be an ODE for the wrong object unless the Bottleneck-C coefficient itself is rederived with \(A_2,A_4\) replaced by the complement’s derivatives. That would be a different row formula, not a rescue of the current one.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Pole-cancelled complements can evade the pole test only by ceasing to be the }A_2,A_4\text{ object.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Pointwise real-axis escape

If the claimed identity is **only** asserted at isolated real centers \(m\), then the meromorphic contradiction is not logically decisive by itself. A meromorphic principal-part mismatch refutes an identity on a complex neighborhood, or an ODE law valid on a real interval with analytic continuation. It does not refute a sparse, pointwise arithmetic coincidence.

However, that escape is too weak for the desired ODE rescue. The current prompt asks whether a stronger or corrected ODE exists for the full phase, a renormalized complement, or a moving-cutoff object entering \(A_2,A_4\).  An ODE identity on a real interval would analytically continue, and the pole mismatch rules it out.

So the only remaining real-axis escape is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a non-ODE pointwise global zero-set coincidence at every good patch.}
}
\]

That is not a differential identity and not a meromorphic ODE. It is exactly the kind of new global zeta-tail theorem already identified as the remaining dependency. 

---

# 6. Final answer to the ODE B prompt

\[
\boxed{
\text{The proposed ODE cannot be a meromorphic identity for the relevant object.}
}
\]

More specifically:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Raw }F_{\rm ext}\text{ ODE: refuted by pole constants.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Full }q\text{ ODE: refuted by pole constants.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Renormalized complements retaining zero poles: refuted by the same calculation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Pole-cancelled complements: evade the pole test, but do not supply the }A_2,A_4\text{ row moments.}
}
\]

The principal-part calculation is decisive:

\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
\sim
\frac{12}{(t-p)^2},
\]

but

\[
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
\sim
\left(
\frac{40R^2}{3}
-
\frac{20}{3}
\right)
\frac1{(t-p)^2}.
\]

Equality would require

\[
R^2=\frac75.
\]

The actual zero-pair phase-derivative residues are purely imaginary, e.g.

\[
R=\pm \frac{i}{4}
\]

or positive-multiplicity variants, so \(R^2<0\). The required residue condition is impossible.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0
\text{ is not rescued by a meromorphic ODE for }F_{\rm ext},q,\text{ or }q-q_{\core}.
}
\]

The Bottleneck-C route still depends on a new nonlocal, pointwise global zeta-tail cancellation theorem. Absent that theorem, the local Bottleneck-C obstruction remains open-negative rather than closed.

_Thought for 2m 16s_

## Agent 2 — New Row Derivation Agent

### Verdict

For the recommended rebuild

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R},
\]

the \(\eta\eta\) top-row algebra **survives unchanged in form** after rederivation. The coefficient is not killed by the new split; it becomes the same universal obstruction with \(q_0,A_2,A_4\) replaced by the new baseline and new full exterior-zero source moments. This is a rebuild, not a patch, as required by the instruction. 

---

# 1. Correct new baseline/source convention

The split must be interpreted with affine absorption. Otherwise \(r_G\) would have value and linear terms, and the old source-grade calculus would be invalid.

Define

\[
G^{\new}(t):=q_{\aux,R}(t)+T_{\far,R}(t),
\]

and

\[
r_G(t):=
G^{\new}(t)-G^{\new}(m)-G^{\new\,\prime}(m)(t-m).
\]

The effective baseline entering the finite-\(s\) corrected block is therefore

\[
q_0^{\new}(t)
:=
q_{\base}^{\new}(t)
+
G^{\new}(m)
+
G^{\new\,\prime}(m)(t-m),
\]

so that

\[
q(t)=q_0^{\new}(t)+r_G(t).
\]

Thus

\[
q_0^{\new}(m)=q(m),
\qquad
(q_0^{\new})'(m)=q'(m),
\]

but

\[
(q_0^{\new})''(m)
=
(q_{\base}^{\new})''(m),
\]

because the affine absorbed part has no second derivative.

This affine absorption is not optional. Without it, the source would introduce lower-order \(r_G(m)\) and \(r_G'(m)\) terms and would reopen earlier gates.

---

# 2. New source variables

For each tagged exterior-zero atom \(\alpha\) inside

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\]

write the affine-subtracted atom as

\[
r_\alpha(t)
=
g_\alpha(t)-g_\alpha(m)-g_\alpha'(m)(t-m).
\]

For two tagged source atoms \(i,j\), define

\[
d_{\alpha,\pm}^{\new}
:=
r_\alpha(t_\pm),
\]

\[
e_{\alpha,\pm}^{\new}
:=
r_\alpha'(t_\pm),
\]

\[
g_{\alpha,\pm}^{\new}
:=
r_\alpha''(t_\pm),
\]

and let

\[
\eta_\alpha^{\new}(s)
\]

be the induced phase-gap perturbation for the corrected mixed block, computed from the same source atom and the same affine-subtracted convention.

Thus the new tagged substitution is

\[
q_\pm
=
q_{0,\pm}^{\new}
+
\tau_i a_i d_{i,\pm}^{\new}
+
\tau_j a_j d_{j,\pm}^{\new},
\]

\[
q'_\pm
=
(q_0^{\new})'_\pm
+
\tau_i a_i e_{i,\pm}^{\new}
+
\tau_j a_j e_{j,\pm}^{\new},
\]

\[
q''_\pm
=
(q_0^{\new})''_\pm
+
\tau_i a_i g_{i,\pm}^{\new}
+
\tau_j a_j g_{j,\pm}^{\new},
\]

and

\[
\Delta
=
\Delta_0^{\new}
+
\tau_i a_i\eta_i^{\new}
+
\tau_j a_j\eta_j^{\new}.
\]

Here

\[
\Delta_0^{\new}(s)
=
\Phi_0^{\new}(t_-)-\Phi_0^{\new}(t_+)
\]

is built from the new effective baseline \(q_0^{\new}\).

---

# 3. Recomputed off-diagonal Hessian row

The relevant mixed-block entry is still

\[
N_{21}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}.
\]

Twice differentiating in the scalar phase-gap variable gives

\[
\partial_\Delta^2N_{21}\big|_{\Delta=\Delta_0^{\new}}
=
\frac{\sin\Delta_0^{\new}}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_{0,-}^{\new}\cos\Delta_0^{\new}}{s}.
\]

Therefore the new \(\eta\eta\) top-row scalar is

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,ij}
:=
[z^7]
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0^{\new}}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_{0,-}^{\new}\cos\Delta_0^{\new}}{s}
\right)
\eta_i^{\new}\eta_j^{\new}
\right].
}
\]

This is not the old formula with \(G^{\new}\) inserted by hand. It is the same second-\(\Delta\)-Hessian computation performed after replacing the baseline and source variables by the new split. The instruction explicitly required this recomputation rather than patching the old coefficient. 

---

# 4. Extracted coefficient

Let

\[
\rho_{\alpha,2}^{\new},
\qquad
\rho_{\alpha,4}^{\new}
\]

denote the midpoint source coefficients of the affine-subtracted exterior-zero atom \(r_\alpha\) in the same normalization as the prior Bottleneck-C source table.

Then the rederived pair coefficient is

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,ij}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{480}
\left(
\rho_{i,2}^{\new}\rho_{j,4}^{\new}
+
\rho_{i,4}^{\new}\rho_{j,2}^{\new}
\right)
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}^{\new}\rho_{j,2}^{\new}
\right].
}
\]

So the top row **does reproduce the old obstruction form**, but with the new source/baseline convention:

\[
q_0\rightsquigarrow q_0^{\new},
\qquad
q_0''\rightsquigarrow (q_0^{\new})'',
\qquad
\rho_{\alpha,k}\rightsquigarrow \rho_{\alpha,k}^{\new}.
\]

The coefficient does **not** vanish algebraically.

---

# 5. Aggregate new coefficient

For the full exterior-zero source

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\]

define

\[
A_2^{\new}
:=
\sum_{\alpha\in\zeroext}w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,2}^{\new}
=
\frac{G^{\new\,\prime\prime}(m)}2,
\]

\[
A_4^{\new}
:=
\sum_{\alpha\in\zeroext}w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,4}^{\new}
=
\frac{G^{\new\,(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Then summing over source tags gives

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
}
\]

This is the exact analogue of the prior aggregate obstruction. The earlier aggregate work had already identified this as the vanishing condition for physical Bottleneck-C closure in the old convention. 

---

# 6. Do new background/source cross terms appear?

For candidate 1,

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\]

no \(B_{\bg}\times G^{\new}\) or \(E_{\est,R}\times G^{\new}\) source cross terms appear in this \(\eta\eta\) top row, because

\[
B_{\bg},E_{\est,R}\subset q_{\base}^{\new}
\]

and are not tagged source variables.

They enter only through the baseline quantities

\[
q_0^{\new},
\qquad
(q_0^{\new})'',
\qquad
\Delta_0^{\new},
\qquad
\Lambda^-_{2,0,\new},
\qquad
W_{+,0}^{\new}.
\]

The only new cross terms are source-source cross terms between auxiliary-near and far zero atoms. These are legitimate: they are included automatically in

\[
A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
\quad\text{and}\quad
(A_2^{\new})^2.
\]

By contrast, if one used

\[
G^{\new}=q-q_{\core}
=
q_{\aux,R}+B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R}+E_{\est,R},
\]

then \(B_{\bg}\) and \(E_{\est,R}\) would become source variables and the row would acquire additional background/source and error/source terms. The instruction explicitly warned that such terms cannot be inserted by hand and would require a separate rederivation. 

So for the recommended candidate 1, the row form is clean; for candidates 2 or 3, this derivation does not apply without rebuilding the tagged source calculus more radically.

---

# 7. New physical \(S\)-coefficient

The finite Fréchet row remains

\[
\mathcal E_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}^{2,\new}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda_{2,0}^{-,\new}
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0^{\new}}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_{0,-}^{\new}\cos\Delta_0^{\new}}{s}
\right)
J\eta_i^{\new}\eta_j^{\new}
\right]_7
W_{+,0}^{\new}
\right).
\]

Writing

\[
W_{+,0}^{\new}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u^{\new}&w^{\new}\\
w^{\new}&v^{\new}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

one obtains

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}^{2,\new}
=
-\frac{\nu_{21,7}^{\new}}{24\pi (q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\left(
w^{\new}I+u^{\new}S
\right),
}
\]

where \(q_{\wh}^{\new}\) is the same good-patch baseline scalar entering the same-point whitening slot.

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\top}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi (q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new}.
}
\]

Aggregated over the full exterior-zero source,

\[
\boxed{
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\agg}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi (q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
}
\]

Thus, on a good patch with

\[
u^{\new}q_{\wh}^{\new}\neq0,
\]

physical closure still requires

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
}
\]

This matches the prior no-go ledger: the \(S\)-coefficient must vanish; quotient closure alone is insufficient. 

---

# 8. Does the new row vanish?

No. The new split does not kill the top row.

For example, if the new exterior-zero source has a homogeneous bad patch with

\[
A_2^{\new}\neq0,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=0,
\qquad
(q_0^{\new})''=0,
\qquad
q_0^{\new}\neq0,
\]

then

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
-\frac{(q_0^{\new})^3}{216Q^{14}}
(A_2^{\new})^2
\neq0.
\]

So the new architecture changes the bookkeeping object but not the universal obstruction mechanism. It replaces the old required identity by

\[
\boxed{
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
=0.
}
\]

If \(A_2^{\new}\neq0\), equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_4^{\new}}{A_2^{\new}}
=
\frac{10(q_0^{\new})^2}{9}
-
\frac{5(q_0^{\new})''}{18q_0^{\new}}.
}
\]

This is a **new global identity for the full exterior-zero source**, not an algebraic cancellation of the row.

---

## Final conclusion

The candidate source-convention rebuild

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

is coherent at the \(\eta\eta\) top-row level, provided the affine part of \(G^{\new}\) is absorbed into the effective baseline. But the rederived top row does **not** vanish and does **not** acquire compensating background/source terms.

It reproduces the same obstruction form:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
}
\]

Therefore the new architecture is not closed by row algebra. It merely shifts the needed cancellation theorem from the raw far tail to the full exterior-zero source:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0
}
\]

on every good patch. Absent that new identity, the Bottleneck-C obstruction survives the source-convention rebuild.

endpoint symmetrization cannot remove the \(\eta\eta\) obstruction without losing transform-faithfulness.

## Agent 2 — Normal-Form Quotient/Moduli Attack

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
T \text{ is quotient-gauge for the mixed four-point scalar exits, but it is not gauge for the full transform package.}
}
\]

Therefore the quotient architecture

\[
E \bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

can remove a residual from the **mixed four-point determinant branch**, but it cannot replace the physical Bottleneck-C requirement

\[
f=0.
\]

The \(\eta\eta\) obstruction survives because it produces a \(\Phi_K\)-visible \(T\)-horizontal leak even when the quotient determinant closure

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0
\]

holds. This is exactly the distinction the current handover asks us to test: a valid rescue must preserve the physical \(T\)-readout, not merely hide \(f\) in a quotient coordinate. 

---

# 1. Reconstructing the objects

On the fixed-sector patch,

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S.
\]

The order-seven determinant coordinate is

\[
\Delta_7
=
\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

The hidden-state coordinate is

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

For a residual

\[
E=eI+fS,
\]

adding \(E\) to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) changes the determinant coordinate by

\[
\Delta_7
\longmapsto
\Delta_7+\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
\Delta_7+ev_5-u_5f.
\]

It changes the hidden coordinate by

\[
T
\longmapsto
T+\frac{f}{c}.
\]

The functional \(\Phi_K\) sees the \(S\)-component:

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f.
\]

The draft explicitly separates these layers: the mixed four-point scalar exits depend on the quotient determinant data, whereas the hidden-state/\(\Phi_K\)-visible layer is separate. 

---

# 2. What quotient closure actually proves

The quotient condition is

\[
E\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Equivalently, on a good patch,

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0.
\]

If this holds, then

\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0,
\]

so

\[
\Delta_7
\]

does not change. Therefore the mixed four-point scalar exits

\[
Q_v,\qquad T_v,\qquad \mathcal Z,\qquad \mathcal R
\]

do not see \(E\) as a new independent mixed four-point carrier.

This part is legitimate. The quotient package is the correct moduli object **for the mixed four-point determinant branch**.

But this is strictly weaker than Bottleneck-C physical closure.

If

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then

\[
e=\chi u_5,
\qquad
f=\chi v_5.
\]

Thus

\[
ev_5-u_5f
=
\chi u_5v_5-u_5\chi v_5
=
0,
\]

but

\[
T
\longmapsto
T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

Also

\[
\Phi_K(E)
=
2\chi v_5.
\]

So on a \(v_5\neq0\) patch, a quotient-invisible shift is generally \(\Phi_K\)-visible and \(T\)-visible. The draft states this exact point: mixed four-point closure is quotient-determinant, but two-point transform closure also requires \(T\)-horizontal compatibility. 

---

# 3. Is \(T\) gauge?

There is an obvious candidate gauge action:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Under this action,

\[
\Delta_7
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]

is invariant:

\[
(u_7+\chi u_5)v_5-u_5(v_7+\chi v_5)
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

So \(\chi\) is a genuine gauge parameter for the **quotient determinant moduli**

\[
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

But the same action changes

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]

by

\[
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

It also changes

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
\]

by

\[
\Phi_K(\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
2\chi v_5.
\]

Therefore \(\chi\) is **not** a gauge symmetry of the full transform state unless one explicitly declares the entire \(\Phi_K\)-visible hidden-state coordinate physically irrelevant.

The current architecture does not allow that. The handovers repeatedly state that physical closure requires the \(S\)-coefficient to vanish, because

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2 f/c.
\]

A nonzero \(f\) is a physical \(T\)-horizontal failure, not a quotient-only artifact. 

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
T \text{ is not a gauge coordinate for the full proof.}
}
\]

It is only gauge relative to the reduced mixed four-point determinant quotient.

---

# 4. Why quotient closure cannot replace \(f=0\)

The current Bottleneck-C residual has the form

\[
E=eI+fS.
\]

The quotient condition asks for

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0.
\]

The physical condition asks for

\[
f=0.
\]

These are not equivalent.

Indeed, if

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then quotient closure holds automatically, but

\[
f=\chi v_5.
\]

On the \(v_5\neq0\) patch, this is nonzero for \(\chi\neq0\). Hence

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c
=
-a_1^2\chi v_5/c
\neq0.
\]

So quotient closure leaves exactly the physical leak that Bottleneck C was supposed to prevent.

The only cases where quotient closure implies physical closure are degenerate or restricted:

\[
v_5=0
\]

or

\[
\chi=0.
\]

But the \(v_5=0\) case is not the generic \(v_5\)-patch quotient formulation, and \(\chi=0\) is precisely \(E=0\) in the quotient-line direction. It gives no new rescue.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
ev_5-u_5f=0
\not\Rightarrow
f=0.
}
\]

So the quotient condition cannot replace the physical Bottleneck-C condition.

---

# 5. Can \(E \bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) be made the actual moduli object?

Only for the mixed four-point scalar-exit subsystem.

The draft’s quotient determinant theorem says the mixed four-point scalar exits factor through

\[
c,\quad u_5,\quad v_5,\quad \Delta_7,
\]

and do not depend on \(T=v_7/c\) independently. Therefore the quotient object

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)
\]

is the correct moduli object for that subsystem. 

But the full local-to-global proof also requires:

\[
\Phi_K\text{-visible package-to-transform state-locality},
\]

\[
\text{hidden-state reconstruction},
\]

and

\[
T\text{-horizontal odd-block extraction}.
\]

Those require knowing the \(\Phi_K\)-visible \(S\)-projection, not only the quotient determinant class.

So the quotient can be the actual moduli object only if the downstream proof is rewritten to remove all dependence on the hidden-state coordinate \(T\). The current proof does not do that. The current handover explicitly warns that a rescue must preserve or replace the role of the \(T\)-readout and must not merely hide \(f\) while \(\partial_\kappa T\neq0\). 

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
E \bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ is a valid mixed-four-point quotient object, but not the full Bottleneck-C physical moduli object.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Compatibility checks

## Mixed four-point detection

Compatible.

The quotient determinant formulation was built exactly for this purpose. If

\[
[E]=0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then \(E\) produces no new mixed four-point scalar-exit carrier.

## \(\Phi_K\)-visible package-to-transform state-locality

Not compatible.

A quotient-line residual

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is quotient-invisible but generally

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2\chi v_5\neq0.
\]

So the quotient loses exactly the \(\Phi_K\)-visible information needed for transform-state locality.

## Finite-core transfer

Conditionally compatible only for the scalar-exit branch.

Finite-core transfer depending only on the scalar exits

\[
\mathcal Z,\quad \mathcal R,\quad T_v
\]

can use the quotient determinant data. But any finite-core argument that requires hidden-state reconstruction or odd-block \(T\)-horizontal control cannot use the quotient alone.

## Hidden-state reconstruction

Not compatible.

Hidden-state reconstruction needs

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]

or an equivalent \(\Phi_K\)-visible coordinate. The quotient

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\]

forgets the quotient-line component, and that quotient-line component changes \(T\).

Thus quotienting loses required downstream information precisely at the bridge from fixed-sector quotient closure to transform-state closure.

---

# 7. The exact failure mode

The failure is not that the quotient formalism is mathematically wrong. It is correct for one layer.

The failure is that it is insufficient for Bottleneck C.

There are two inequivalent projections:

\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

and

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f.
\]

The mixed four-point branch sees the first.

The physical transform branch sees the second.

A residual can lie in the kernel of the first but not the second:

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0,
\qquad
\Phi_K(E)=2\chi v_5.
\]

Therefore the quotient determinant kernel is not contained in the physical transform kernel:

\[
\ker \omega_h(\,\cdot\,,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\not\subset
\ker \Phi_K.
\]

On a \(v_5\neq0\) patch,

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\cap
\ker \Phi_K
=
\{0\}.
\]

So quotienting by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) necessarily identifies physically distinct transform states.

That is the no-go.

---

# 8. Theorem-ready statement

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.88\linewidth}
Let \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S\) with \(c\neq0\) and \(v_5\neq0\), and let \(E=eI+fS\) be an order-seven fixed-sector residual. The quotient determinant moduli class detects \(E\) only through
\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=ev_5-u_5f.
\]
Thus \(E\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is invisible to the mixed four-point scalar exits. However, the transform hidden-state readout detects
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\]
and the hidden coordinate changes by
\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]
Since \(E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) has \(\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0\) but \(\Phi_K(E)=2\chi v_5\neq0\) for \(\chi\neq0\), quotient invisibility does not imply transform invisibility. Therefore the quotient/moduli reformulation cannot replace the physical Bottleneck-C condition \(f=0\). It can close the mixed four-point quotient branch only; it cannot remove the \(\eta\eta\) Bottleneck-C obstruction.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

---

## Final Agent 2 conclusion

\[
\boxed{
T \text{ is physical for the full Bottleneck-C transform closure.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The quotient architecture is legitimate only for the mixed four-point determinant branch.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{It cannot avoid the } \eta\eta \text{ obstruction because it identifies states with different } \Phi_K \text{ and different } T.
}
\]

So the quotient/moduli attack is negative: quotient closure cannot substitute for

\[
f=0
\]

and cannot rescue Bottleneck C from the surviving \(S\)-visible \(\eta\eta\) top row.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 17:10:59)

The residue-class question is distinct from the prior ODE pole mismatch. Even if the ratio identity fails, a residue theorem could still give only an integrated cancellation; the task is to test whether that can imply the pointwise Bottleneck-C condition.

_Thought for 1m 23s_

## Agent 2 / B — Meromorphic / Residue-Class Attack

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\text{ is not killed by global residue calculus.}
}
\]

It can be written as a quadratic meromorphic expression in the pole sums of the non-core zero source, but it is **not** a residue whose vanishing follows from the global residue theorem, nor an exact meromorphic derivative with zero local residues. At most, the global residue theorem gives an integrated/cyclic cancellation of residues of \(\nu(m)\,dm\), which is much weaker than the pointwise condition

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)=0
\]

required by Bottleneck C. The attached instruction explicitly asks for this distinction: not another ODE pole test, but whether the obstruction class is globally exact or residue-killed. 

---

# 1. Pole decomposition of the zero-source field

Each zero-pair atom is

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

For one summand

\[
f_a(t)=\frac{a}{a^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]

the poles are

\[
p_a^+=\frac{\gamma+ia}{2},
\qquad
p_a^-=\frac{\gamma-ia}{2}.
\]

The partial-fraction residues are

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^+}f_a=-\frac{i}{4},
\qquad
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^-}f_a=+\frac{i}{4}.
\]

Including source weights \(w_\alpha\), write the full non-core zero source as

\[
G(z)=G^{\new}(z)
=
\sum_{p\in P_{\rm ext}}
\frac{C_p}{z-p},
\]

where each

\[
C_p=\pm \frac{i}{4}w_\alpha
\]

up to multiplicity and tagging. Holomorphic/background terms are not in \(G^{\new}\) for the rebuilt convention; the rebuilt split uses

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]

That split is the current controlling source convention. 

Then

\[
G''(m)=
\sum_{p\in P_{\rm ext}}
\frac{2C_p}{(m-p)^3},
\]

and

\[
G^{(4)}(m)=
\sum_{p\in P_{\rm ext}}
\frac{24C_p}{(m-p)^5}.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_2(m)=\frac{G''(m)}2
=
\sum_p
\frac{C_p}{(m-p)^3},
\]

\[
A_4(m)=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}
=
\sum_p
\frac{C_p}{(m-p)^5}.
\]

This is the clean pole-sum form of the aggregate source moments.

---

# 2. Meromorphic form of the obstruction

Ignoring the harmless global prefactor \(Q^{-14}\), define

\[
q=q_0^{\new}(m),
\qquad
K=
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}.
\]

The rebuilt aggregate obstruction is

\[
\nu(m)
=
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{K}{144}A_2^2.
\]

Substituting the pole sums gives

\[
\boxed{
\nu(m)
=
\frac{q(m)}{240}
\sum_{p,r}
\frac{C_pC_r}{(m-p)^3(m-r)^5}
+
\frac{K(m)}{144}
\sum_{p,r}
\frac{C_pC_r}{(m-p)^3(m-r)^3}.
}
\]

This is a quadratic meromorphic expression in the exterior zero-pole field.

It is not linear in residues. It is a pair-interaction object. That already makes the usual global residue theorem poorly matched: the theorem controls the sum of residues of a meromorphic one-form, not the pointwise value of a quadratic pole-field at a real midpoint.

---

# 3. Local principal parts at a pole

Fix one exterior pole \(p\), set

\[
\tau=m-p,
\]

and split

\[
A_2(m)=C_p\tau^{-3}+a(m),
\]

\[
A_4(m)=C_p\tau^{-5}+b(m),
\]

where \(a,b\) are holomorphic at \(p\) and encode all other exterior poles.

Then

\[
A_2A_4
=
C_p^2\tau^{-8}
+
C_p b\,\tau^{-3}
+
C_p a\,\tau^{-5}
+
ab,
\]

and

\[
A_2^2
=
C_p^2\tau^{-6}
+
2C_pa\,\tau^{-3}
+
a^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\nu(m)
\]

has pole orders \(8,6,5,3,\ldots\) at \(p\). In general it has a nonzero residue because the holomorphic functions \(q,K,a,b\) have Taylor coefficients that feed the \(\tau^{-1}\) term.

The residue at \(p\) is

\[
\operatorname{Res}_p(\nu\,dm)
=
\frac{C_p^2}{240}[\tau^7]q
+
\frac{C_p}{240}[\tau^2](qb)
+
\frac{C_p}{240}[\tau^4](qa)
+
\frac{C_p^2}{144}[\tau^5]K
+
\frac{2C_p}{144}[\tau^2](Ka).
\]

Here \([\tau^j]\) means the coefficient of \(\tau^j\) in the Taylor expansion at \(p\).

There is no structural reason for this residue to vanish. It depends on the local Taylor data of \(q,K\) at the pole and on the analytic tails \(a,b\) from all other poles.

So \(\nu(m)\,dm\) is not generally an exact meromorphic derivative. A meromorphic derivative has zero residue at every pole. This expression does not.

---

# 4. Explicit two-pole test

The simplest test already blocks exactness.

Take two exterior poles \(p_1,p_2\) with residues \(C_1,C_2\), and take \(q,K\) locally constant. Let

\[
d=p_1-p_2.
\]

At \(p_1\), the analytic tail from \(p_2\) is

\[
a(\tau)=\frac{C_2}{(d+\tau)^3},
\qquad
b(\tau)=\frac{C_2}{(d+\tau)^5}.
\]

The needed coefficients are

\[
[\tau^2]a=6C_2d^{-5},
\]

\[
[\tau^4]a=15C_2d^{-7},
\]

\[
[\tau^2]b=15C_2d^{-7}.
\]

Since \(q,K\) are constant, the residue at \(p_1\) becomes

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_1}(\nu\,dm)
=
\frac{C_1C_2q}{240}
(15d^{-7}+15d^{-7})
+
\frac{2C_1K}{144}
(6C_2d^{-5}).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Res}_{p_1}(\nu\,dm)
=
C_1C_2
\left(
\frac{q}{8d^7}
+
\frac{K}{12d^5}
\right).
}
\]

This is generically nonzero.

At \(p_2\), the residue is the negative of this in the constant-\(q,K\) two-pole model, so the **global sum** of residues is zero. But that is only the ordinary global residue theorem:

\[
\sum_p \operatorname{Res}_p(\nu\,dm)
+
\operatorname{Res}_{\infty}(\nu\,dm)
=0.
\]

It does not imply

\[
\nu(m)=0
\]

on the real line, nor even that each local pole residue vanishes.

This is the key obstruction: the expression may have globally cancelling residues while remaining a nonzero meromorphic function.

---

# 5. Functional-equation and conjugate-pair symmetry do not kill the class

For one conjugate pair,

\[
p^+=\frac{\gamma+ia}{2},
\qquad
p^-=\frac{\gamma-ia}{2},
\]

with

\[
C_+=-\frac{i}{4}w,
\qquad
C_-=\frac{i}{4}w.
\]

Then

\[
C_+C_-=\frac{w^2}{16}.
\]

Taking \(d=p^+-p^-=ia\), the two-pole residue at \(p^+\) is

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p^+}(\nu\,dm)
=
\frac{w^2}{16}
\left(
\frac{q}{8(ia)^7}
+
\frac{K}{12(ia)^5}
\right).
\]

Since

\[
(ia)^{-7}=\frac{i}{a^7},
\qquad
(ia)^{-5}=-\frac{i}{a^5},
\]

this gives

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p^+}(\nu\,dm)
=
\frac{iw^2}{16}
\left(
\frac{q}{8a^7}
-
\frac{K}{12a^5}
\right).
\]

Generically this is nonzero. The conjugate pole contributes the opposite residue when \(q,K\) are real-symmetric, so the total pair residue cancels. But again, that is a global residue sum, not pointwise vanishing of \(\nu(m)\).

Thus conjugation gives paired-residue cancellation, not Bottleneck-C closure.

Functional-equation partner poles behave similarly: they may pair the residue accounting globally, but they do not force the quadratic field

\[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4+\frac{K}{144}A_2^2
\]

to vanish at each midpoint.

---

# 6. Constant-term / principal-part interpretation

Could \(\nu\) be the constant term or principal-part coefficient of some larger meromorphic expression?

Formally, yes: any local Laurent coefficient can be called a principal-part coefficient. But that does not produce a vanishing theorem.

The expression

\[
A_2A_4
\]

contains products

\[
(m-p)^{-3}(m-r)^{-5},
\]

and

\[
A_2^2
\]

contains products

\[
(m-p)^{-3}(m-r)^{-3}.
\]

These are pairwise interaction kernels. A residue theorem would require representing their weighted sum as the coefficient of \((z-m)^{-1}\) in a one-variable meromorphic differential whose only nonzero residues are controlled by infinity or symmetry.

But the natural one-form

\[
\nu(m)\,dm
\]

has nonzero local residues as shown above. Therefore it is not globally exact. And if one instead builds an artificial differential whose residue at \(m\) is defined to be \(\nu(m)\), the global residue theorem gives

\[
\nu(m)
=
-\sum_{p\in P_{\rm ext}}\operatorname{Res}_p \Omega
-
\operatorname{Res}_\infty \Omega,
\]

not \(\nu(m)=0\), unless all other residues are independently proved zero. The current framework has no such mechanism.

So there is no useful principal-part/cohomology interpretation that forces pointwise vanishing.

---

# 7. Contribution at infinity

For a finite exterior set,

\[
A_2(m)=O(m^{-3}),
\qquad
A_4(m)=O(m^{-5}),
\]

so

\[
A_2A_4=O(m^{-8}),
\qquad
A_2^2=O(m^{-6}).
\]

If \(q,K\) are treated as slowly varying analytic baseline coefficients, the pole at infinity usually contributes no residue in the constant-coefficient model. In the full zeta setting, \(q\) has logarithmic/asymptotic structure rather than a rational meromorphic behavior on the sphere, so the “residue at infinity” is not even the right global object without a careful compactification and subtraction scheme.

Either way, infinity does not help. In the finite rational model, infinity only balances the sum of finite residues. In the full zeta model, the asymptotic/gamma-background terms make residue-at-infinity arguments more delicate, not stronger.

No available infinity term forces

\[
\nu(m)=0
\]

pointwise.

---

# 8. What global residue calculus can and cannot give

Global residue calculus can plausibly give statements of the form

\[
\sum_{p\in P_{\rm ext}}\operatorname{Res}_p(\nu\,dm)=0,
\]

or, with symmetry,

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p^+}+\operatorname{Res}_{p^-}=0.
\]

It can also identify \(\nu\,dm\) as a meromorphic differential with pairwise pole-interaction residues.

But Bottleneck C needs

\[
\nu(m)=0
\]

for each good midpoint \(m\). The attached shared background states that physical closure requires

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0
\]

because the \(S\)-coefficient drives the \(T\)-horizontal leak. 

An integrated residue cancellation does not imply that pointwise condition.

Thus even a successful residue accounting would be too weak unless the architecture were changed from pointwise \(T\)-horizontal closure to an integrated/global holonomy condition. That is no longer Bottleneck C as currently formulated.

---

# 9. Precise obstruction class

The obstruction is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\text{ is a quadratic pole-interaction field, not a residue-zero local density.}
}
\]

More explicitly:

1. **Pole-order mismatch:**  
   The field has high-order poles \(8,6,5,3,\ldots\), while residue calculus only controls the \((m-p)^{-1}\) coefficients.

2. **Nonzero local residues:**  
   The natural differential \(\nu(m)\,dm\) has generically nonzero residues at individual zero-pair poles.

3. **Only global cancellation:**  
   Conjugation and functional-equation partners may cancel residues pairwise or globally, but do not cancel the pointwise field value.

4. **No exact derivative:**  
   Since local residues are generically nonzero, \(\nu(m)\,dm\) is not the derivative of a meromorphic function.

5. **No pointwise theorem:**  
   The global residue theorem yields integrated/cyclic identities, not

   \[
   \nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)=0.
   \]

---

## Final theorem-ready no-go

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.88\linewidth}
Let
\[
G^{\new}(m)=\sum_{p\in P_{\rm ext}}\frac{C_p}{m-p}
\]
be the full non-core zero-source field, and define
\[
A_2=\sum_p\frac{C_p}{(m-p)^3},
\qquad
A_4=\sum_p\frac{C_p}{(m-p)^5}.
\]
Then the rebuilt Bottleneck-C obstruction
\[
\nu(m)
=
\frac{q(m)}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''(m)}6-\frac{2q(m)^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2
\]
is a quadratic meromorphic pole-interaction field. The natural differential \(\nu(m)\,dm\) has generically nonzero local residues; for two poles \(p_1,p_2\) with constant \(q,K\),
\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_1}(\nu\,dm)
=
C_1C_2
\left(
\frac{q}{8(p_1-p_2)^7}
+
\frac{K}{12(p_1-p_2)^5}
\right),
\]
which is not identically zero. Hence \(\nu\,dm\) is not an exact meromorphic derivative, and global residue calculus can at most give cancellation of the sum of residues, not pointwise vanishing of \(\nu(m)\). Therefore the condition
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)=0
\]
is not forced by meromorphic residue/cohomology calculus in the current variables.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

So Agent 2 / B’s conclusion is negative:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The global zero identity is not a residue theorem in disguise.}
}
\]

If the proof is to continue, the obstruction must either be handled by a genuinely new pointwise global identity outside ordinary residue calculus, or the architecture must pivot away from pointwise \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C closure.

## Adversarial Obstruction Agent 1 — Decision Memo

**Verdict:** the current \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C architecture should be treated as nonviable unless a new architecture is adopted. Branch A is no longer a plausible local/global identity route; Branch B is not yet well-defined as a global curvature theory; Branch C is the only coherent pivot, but only if the proof can be rebuilt entirely in quotient determinant variables. 

---

# 1. Branch A — pointwise flatness

Branch A asks for

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

The rebuilt obstruction is

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
\]

### Adversarial model for Branch A

Take the formal/far-tail limiting model

\[
A_2^{\new}\neq 0,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=0,
\qquad
(q_0^{\new})''=0,
\qquad
q_0^{\new}\neq0.
\]

Then

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
-\frac{(q_0^{\new})^3}{216Q^{14}}
(A_2^{\new})^2
\neq0.
\]

This is not an arbitrary fake model: far exterior zero-pair atoms approximate the bad germ \(r=u^2\), with

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}\approx0.
\]

Therefore Branch A would require a genuinely new pointwise theorem saying the **full actual non-core zero complement** always cancels this expression. That theorem is not a local source fact, not an ODE fact, not an exactness fact, and not a residue theorem.

### Branch A decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not continue Branch A as the main route.}
}
\]

The exact theorem it would need is:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
=0
}
\]

on every good patch. At this point, that is an unsupported global miracle identity.

---

# 2. Branch B — curvature / holonomy replacement

Branch B tries to reinterpret

\[
\mathcal K
=
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]

as a global curvature density, with

\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}
=
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
\]

The local interpretation is sound: \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\) measures the vertical defect of the \(T\)-horizontal connection. The problem is global covariance.

### Adversarial model for Branch B

Let the full phase derivative be fixed:

\[
q=b+G.
\]

Now change the source/core convention by moving a zero-source atom \(h\) between baseline and source:

\[
G_\lambda = G+\lambda h,
\qquad
b_\lambda = b-\lambda h.
\]

Then

\[
A_{2,\lambda}
=
A_2+\lambda \frac{h''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_{4,\lambda}
=
A_4+\lambda \frac{h^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Meanwhile the full \(q\) is unchanged. Unless the architecture supplies a canonical rule fixing \(\lambda\), the local density

\[
\nu_\lambda
=
\frac{q}{240}A_{2,\lambda}A_{4,\lambda}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{b_\lambda''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_{2,\lambda}^2
\]

changes with \(\lambda\) generically.

For example, start with

\[
A_2=A_4=0,
\qquad
q\neq0,
\qquad
b''=0,
\]

and choose \(h\) with

\[
h''(m)\neq0.
\]

Then for \(\lambda\neq0\),

\[
\nu_\lambda
=
-\frac{q^3}{216}
\left(\lambda\frac{h''(m)}2\right)^2
+
O(\lambda^2 h''h^{(4)})
\]

is generically nonzero, while \(\nu_0=0\). Same full \(q\), different source/core convention, different curvature density.

So

\[
C_{\rm geom}\nu\,dm
\]

is not yet a well-defined global curvature form. It is a local connection-defect coefficient attached to a chosen source convention.

### Branch B decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Branch B is not viable until a covariance theorem is proved.}
}
\]

The exact theorem required is:

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\,dm
\text{ transforms as a globally defined line-bundle-valued one-form}
}
\]

under patch changes, whitening changes, fixed-core changes, and source-window changes.

Without that theorem, holonomy/integral claims are coordinate artifacts.

---

# 3. Branch C — quotient-only determinant architecture

Branch C abandons \(T\)-horizontal closure and uses only quotient determinant data:

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

This is the cleanest surviving pivot, because the quotient determinant is genuinely invariant under

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Indeed,

\[
(u_7+\chi u_5)v_5-u_5(v_7+\chi v_5)
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

### Adversarial model for Branch C

Take two fixed-sector states:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
u_7I+v_7S,
\]

and

\[
\widetilde A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
+
\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

They have the same quotient determinant:

\[
\widetilde\Delta_7=\Delta_7.
\]

They also have the same quotient data

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7).
\]

But their \(T\)-coordinates differ:

\[
\widetilde T
=
\frac{v_7+\chi v_5}{c}
=
T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

And their \(\Phi_K\)-visible states differ:

\[
\Phi_K(\widetilde A_7^{\mathfrak f})
-
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
=
2\chi v_5.
\]

So if any downstream step needs \(T\), \(v_7/c\), or \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\), Branch C fails immediately.

### Branch C decision

Branch C is viable only as a **full no-\(T\) proof architecture**. It cannot be used as a local repair while still relying on hidden-state reconstruction later.

The required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{All RH-relevant finite-core and interaction detection can be expressed using only }
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7)
}
\]

and mixed four-point scalar exits, with no appeal to

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c},
\qquad
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}),
\qquad
v_7
\]

as representative-level data.

---

It must discard \(T\)-horizontal closure entirely and rebuild finite-core/interaction rigidity in quotient determinant variables.

unless someone has a genuinely new global zeta identity. The more productive fork is:

where the quotient variables are functions only of

## Agent 6 — Quotient Architecture Synthesis / Kill-Criteria Agent

### Verdict

The no-\(T\) quotient architecture is the only coherent remaining pivot, but it is **not yet a viable proof route**. It becomes viable only if quotient data can still detect RH-relevant anomalies after discarding

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c},
\qquad
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}),
\qquad
v_7.
\]

The architecture should receive one focused quotient wave. If that wave cannot prove quotient RH-detection and quotient finite-core determinacy, the current proof program should be marked nonviable rather than patched again. The attached coordinator notes state exactly this pivot: the quotient architecture is coherent only if the local-to-global contradiction can be rebuilt entirely in \((c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,D_9,\ldots)\), mixed four-point exits, and quotient finite-core geometry. 

---

# 1. Proposed quotient architecture

## 1.1 Local moduli

The representative fixed-sector data are

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=u_{2r+1}I+v_{2r+1}S.
\]

The quotient action is

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}+\chi_r A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The quotient determinant coordinates are

\[
D_{2r+1}
:=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

In particular,

\[
D_5=0,
\qquad
D_7=\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

The quotient local moduli should therefore be

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Q(h)
=
\bigl(c,u_5,v_5,D_7,D_9,\ldots,D_{2R+1}\bigr).
}
\]

The architecture may use \(\mathcal Q(h)\), mixed four-point scalar exits, and quotient finite-core geometry. It may not use \(T=v_7/c\), \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\), or \(v_7\) as independent representative-level data. This restriction is forced because the shift \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) preserves \(\Delta_7\) but changes \(T\) by \(\chi v_5/c\). 

---

## 1.2 Local gate

The old \(T\)-horizontal gate required

\[
f=0.
\]

The quotient gate becomes

\[
\boxed{
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=ev_5-u_5f=0
}
\]

for a residual

\[
E=eI+fS.
\]

This is not equivalent to \(f=0\). It is intentionally weaker. The quotient program survives only if the weaker quotient gate is sufficient for the global RH contradiction.

---

## 1.3 Finite-core vector

Define

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
(D_7,D_9,\ldots,D_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}).
}
\]

Split it as

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
\]

The quotient zero-anomaly locus is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
:=
\{\theta:\ C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta)=0\}.
}
\]

Interpretation:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}=0
\]

means that each relevant finite-core odd coefficient is line-gauge:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

for the sampled finite range. It does **not** imply representative-level vanishing. This is the core risk.

---

## 1.4 Quotient sampled non-concentration theorem

The required finite-core transfer theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
}
\]

This is currently missing. The coordinator note identifies this exact quotient non-concentration statement as one of the main unresolved branches. 

---

## 1.5 Interaction kernel

The quotient \(dd\)-interaction branch should be formulated through a quotient-transverse feature curve

\[
v_{\quot}(u),
\]

with kernel

\[
\boxed{
K_{ij}^{dd,\quot}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2
\left\langle
v_{\quot}(u_i),v_{\quot}(u_j)
\right\rangle.
}
\]

The quotient feature-balance condition is

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\quot}(u_i)=0
\qquad
\text{for all balanced }a,\quad \sum_i a_i=0.
\]

Algebraically, this still forces

\[
v_{\quot}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\quot}(u_k).
\]

So quotienting does not automatically remove the interaction obstruction; it merely projects it. The attached coordinator summary explicitly says quotienting does not automatically solve finite-core or interaction, and that the quotient \(dd\)-interaction branch survives. 

---

# 2. Dependency graph

## Dependency 1 — Quotient RH-detection

Required theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH violation}
\Longrightarrow
\text{nonzero quotient anomaly}.
}
\]

More concretely,

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line zero configuration}
\Longrightarrow
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\neq0
\quad
\text{or}
\quad
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
}
\]

Status: **missing and highest priority**.

Kill criterion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If off-line zeros can differ only in the discarded }T\text{-line, kill Branch C.}
}
\]

This is the most important test. If two states have identical

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,D_7,D_9,\ldots)
\]

but differ in RH-relevant hidden data through \(T\), then quotient architecture loses the signal.

---

## Dependency 2 — Quotient finite determinacy

Required theorem:

\[
\boxed{
D_7=D_9=\cdots=D_{2R+1}=0
\Longrightarrow
D_{2r+1}=0
\quad\text{for all }r.
}
\]

Status: **not inherited automatically**.

The old finite determinacy theorem, if it exists in representative variables, cannot be directly reused, because quotient zero means line-gauge degeneracy, not representative zero.

Kill criterion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If finite quotient vanishing does not propagate to all quotient orders, kill or redesign Branch C.}
}
\]

---

## Dependency 3 — Quotient sampled non-concentration

Required theorem:

\[

\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
}
\]

Status: **missing**.

Expected difficulty: probably **not easier** than the old sampled non-concentration theorem unless quotienting collapses the aligned branch into a controlled incidence set.

Kill / downgrade criterion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx-P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
\text{ persists outside }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot},
\text{ Branch C remains blocked.}
}
\]

## Dependency 4 — Quotient feature balance / incidence containment

Required theorem, one of:

\[
\boxed{

\text{ for all balanced }a
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{

\Longrightarrow
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
}
\]

Status: **missing, likely hard**.

The formal countermodel remains available unless quotient geometry rules it out:

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\qquad
a=(1,-2,1),
\qquad
v_{\quot}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\quot}(u_i)=2\varepsilon w\neq0.
\]

Kill / downgrade criterion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If this model is admissible outside }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot},
\text{ quotient interaction rigidity fails.}
}
\]

---

## Dependency 5 — Quotient spectral cone control

Required theorem:

\[
\boxed{
K_{dd}^{\quot}
\text{ satisfies the required negative-type / cone condition}
}
\]

or failure is contained in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
\]

For a unit quotient feature curve

\[
v_{\quot}(u)=(\cos\phi(u),\sin\phi(u)),
\qquad
\phi(u)=au+bu^3,
\]

the same coefficient-level obstruction appears as before: the \(t^6\)-sign depends on \(\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\), and quotienting alone does not force the needed sign.

Status: **missing**.

Kill / downgrade criterion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If quotient spectral positivity fails outside incidence, Branch C inherits the old interaction obstruction.}
}
\]
