Required theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{mixed four-point scalar exits factor through quotient determinant data.}
}
\]

Status: **plausible / partially inherited**.

This is the strongest reason to pursue Branch C. The quotient determinant is naturally invariant under

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

But mixed four-point closure alone is insufficient; it must be paired with quotient finite-core and quotient interaction detection.

---

# 3. Comparison with abandoned branches

## Branch A — pointwise flatness

Branch A requires

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

Status: **do not continue as main line**.

The exactness, residue, ODE, finite-tail, and source-rebuild attacks all failed to produce this identity. The attached coordinator note says Branch A is now a low-probability “miracle global identity” route. 

## Branch B — curvature / holonomy

Branch B tries to use

\[
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\,dm
\]

as a curvature or holonomy density.

Status: **diagnostic, not viable yet**.

The obstruction is not globally covariant under representative gauge shifts:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

This changes

\[
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c},
\]

so \(\partial_\kappa T\) acquires an additive gauge defect. The coordinator note says no scalar normalization removes this defect. 

## Branch C — no-\(T\) quotient determinant architecture

Status: **best remaining pivot, but unproved**.

It has one genuine advantage: the quotient determinant data are cleanly invariant under the line shift. It has one decisive risk: it may discard exactly the RH-relevant hidden-state signal.

---

# 4. Kill criteria

## Kill Criterion 1 — lost RH signal

Kill Branch C if there exist two admissible fixed-sector states

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{and}\quad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}+\chi_r A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

with identical quotient data

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,D_7,D_9,\ldots)
\]

but different RH-relevant transform states.

Equivalent practical criterion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If a downstream theorem needs }T,\ v_7,\ \Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}),
\text{ kill no-}T\text{ architecture.}
}
\]

---

## Kill Criterion 2 — quotient finite determinacy fails

Kill or redesign Branch C if

\[
D_7=\cdots=D_{2R+1}=0
\]

does not imply all higher quotient determinants vanish, or if all quotient determinants vanish while an RH-relevant anomaly remains in the discarded representative line.

---

## Kill Criterion 3 — sampled non-concentration remains unchanged

Downgrade Branch C if the quotient aligned branch

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
\]

persists outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
\]

If quotienting merely projects the old obstruction without simplifying it, Branch C is blocked at the same place as the full architecture.

---

## Kill Criterion 4 — quotient interaction countermodels survive

Downgrade or kill Branch C if the quotient feature countermodel

\[
v_{\quot}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\]

or the unit spectral curve countermodel

\[
v_{\quot}(u)=(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3))
\]

is admissible outside the quotient incidence set.

---

## Kill Criterion 5 — mixed four-point exits require representative data

Kill Branch C if mixed four-point scalar exits require

\[
T,\quad v_7,\quad \Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
\]

rather than only quotient determinant data.

---

# 5. Decision recommendation

Proceed with Branch C, but with strict termination conditions.

The next wave should prioritize:

1. **Quotient RH-detection / lost-\(T\)**  
   This is the first kill switch. If quotient data cannot detect off-line zeros, the branch dies.

2. **Quotient finite determinacy**  
   Define \(\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\) and prove or refute finite propagation of quotient determinant vanishing.

3. **Quotient sampled non-concentration**  
   Determine whether the aligned branch is simpler in quotient variables or merely projected.

4. **Quotient interaction rigidity**  
   Test feature balance and spectral cone control in quotient variables.

I would not return to Branch A unless a new zeta identity appears from outside the current local machinery. I would not return to Branch B until there is a canonical gauge or a quotient curvature object.

---

\[
\boxed{
\text{No-}T\text{ quotient architecture viable}
}

only if all of the following hold:

# 1. Proposed no-\(T\) quotient architecture

## 1.1 Local moduli

Use only quotient-invariant fixed-sector data:

\[

\qquad

\]

Define

\[

:=

=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.

So

\[

\qquad

\[
\boxed{

=

\mapsto

\[

but changes

So \(T\) is not quotient-invariant.

This is acceptable only if the whole downstream proof is rewritten in quotient variables. It cannot be used while still relying on \(T\), \(v_7\), or \(\Phi_K\).

The attached prompt frames exactly this test: pure quotient lost line anomalies, so the proposed object is the split readout \((H_m^{\quot},H_m^{\parallel})\), not \(H_m^{\quot}\) alone.

# 1. What the split architecture is supposed to fix

The pure quotient scalar was

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
).
\]

It detects transverse motion relative to the line

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

But it misses pure line anomalies:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Indeed,

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
0.
\]

Yet such an anomaly is generally visible to the old transform readout:

\[
\Phi_K(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f})
=
2\lambda_{2r+1}v_5,
\]

and to the hidden coordinate:

\[
T_{2r+1}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

So the split architecture adds a longitudinal component:

\[
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
=
\frac{
\left\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\left\langle
A_5^{\mathfrak f},
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
H_m^{\quot}(s),
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
\right).
\]

This is the minimal completion of the failed quotient scalar.

---

# 2. Algebraic detection test

Let

\[
A=A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
g=A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Define

\[
D(A)=\omega_h(A,g),
\]

and

\[
\lambda(A)=\frac{\langle A,g\rangle_{\wh}}{\langle g,g\rangle_{\wh}}.
\]

Assume a good patch where

\[
g\neq0,
\qquad
\langle g,g\rangle_{\wh}\neq0,
\]

and where the area form \(\omega_h\) is nondegenerate on \(\mathfrak f_h\). Then the pair

\[
(D(A),\lambda(A))
\]

recovers \(A\) in the two-dimensional fixed sector.

Indeed, write

\[
A=A^\perp+\lambda g,
\qquad
\langle A^\perp,g\rangle_{\wh}=0.
\]

The scalar \(D(A)\) determines the perpendicular coefficient, since

\[
D(A)=\omega_h(A^\perp,g)
\]

and \(\omega_h(\cdot,g)\) is nonzero on the one-dimensional \(\wh\)-orthogonal complement of \(g\). Thus:

\[
\boxed{
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1})
\text{ is complete for the fixed-sector vector }A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
}
\]

provided the whitening metric is canonical and nondegenerate.

This is the main positive result.

---

# 3. Adversarial model 1 — pure line anomaly

Take

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Then

\[
D_{2r+1}=0.
\]

Pure quotient fails.

But

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}
=
\frac{
\langle \lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}.
\]

So the split readout detects the anomaly.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Split readout fixes the pure quotient blind spot.}
}
\]

This is a genuine improvement over the no-\(T\) quotient scalar.

---

# 4. Adversarial model 2 — pure quotient anomaly

Take

\[
\lambda(A)=0,
\qquad
D(A)\neq0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
A\perp_{\wh} A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

but not area-collinear with \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

Then

\[
H_m^{\parallel}
\]

does not see the anomaly, but

\[
H_m^{\quot}
\]

does.

So the split readout also detects transverse quotient anomalies.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Split readout detects both line and transverse fixed-sector anomalies.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Adversarial model 3 — mixed finite-core cancellation

Now take the split finite-core vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots).
\]

A pair/interaction split would have the form

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}.
\]

The old sampled non-concentration obstruction can reappear as

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
\approx
-P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}.
\]

A formal aligned model is immediate:

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}=p\neq0,
\]

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}=-p+\epsilon w,
\]

so

\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}+J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}\|_\infty
=
\epsilon\|w\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\mathrm{split}}.
\]

Unless the split structure forces this alignment into an incidence set, the finite-core obstruction survives.

Thus the split architecture solves the **lost-\(T\) detection problem**, but not automatically the **sampled non-concentration problem**.

---

# 6. Bottleneck-C stress test

Let the bad row be

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=eI+fS.
\]

The split components are

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})
=
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

and

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
\frac{
\langle eI+fS,\ u_5I+v_5S\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle u_5I+v_5S,\ u_5I+v_5S\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

The old obstruction was that \(f\neq0\) gives

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c\neq0.
\]

The pure quotient condition

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})=0
\]

does not imply \(f=0\). This is why quotient failed.

The split readout now also sees

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta}).
\]

But there is a critical fork:

## Case 1 — \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\) must vanish pointwise

If the split architecture requires

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\qquad
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\]

then, on a good patch, the full fixed-sector residual vanishes:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

This is at least as strong as the old condition \(f=0\). In particular, it still requires killing the \(\eta\eta\) row pointwise.

Then the split readout has only repackaged the Bottleneck-C obstruction.

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\text{-flatness pointwise}
\Rightarrow
\text{old obstruction returns.}
}
\]

## Case 2 — \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\) is allowed as transported line motion

If the split architecture allows

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\neq0
\]

but treats it as canonical line transport along

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then Bottleneck C is no longer a pointwise flatness gate. It becomes a line-bundle connection problem.

The required replacement is a transport law:

\[
\nabla^L \lambda
=
\text{controlled source term},
\]

or a holonomy/index theorem:

\[
\operatorname{Hol}(L,\nabla^L)
=
\text{global invariant}.
\]

This is the only way the split readout can genuinely evade the old obstruction.

So the split architecture lives or dies on:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the longitudinal component be transported, rather than killed?}
}
\]

---

# 7. Canonicity stress test

The split uses

\[
\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\wh}.
\]

If this whitening metric changes under normalization, source-window changes, or patch changes, then

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}
=
\frac{
\langle A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}
\]

is not canonical.

Then the split readout becomes another gauge choice, not a geometric invariant.

The precise kill criterion is:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{2r+1}
\text{ gauge-dependent}
\Rightarrow
\text{kill split architecture.}
}
\]

The weaker outcome is that \(\lambda\) is not invariant but is connection-covariant. In that case, the split architecture must become a line-bundle connection architecture.

---

# 8. Is \(\lambda\) just \(T\) in disguise?

On coordinates,

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=u_{2r+1}I+v_{2r+1}S,
\]

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

The old \(T\)-coordinate uses

\[
T_{2r+1}=\frac{v_{2r+1}}{c}.
\]

The new \(\lambda\) is a metric projection onto

\[
u_5I+v_5S.
\]

Unless \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is aligned with \(S\), \(\lambda\) is not literally \(T\). It mixes \(u_{2r+1}\) and \(v_{2r+1}\).

However, for a pure line anomaly,

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

one has

\[
T_{2r+1}
=
\lambda\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

So \(\lambda\) is the canonical replacement for the discarded \(T\)-line coordinate.

This is acceptable only if the proof no longer requires \(T\)-horizontal flatness and instead uses canonical line transport.

If the proof still demands that the \(T\)-visible direction vanish, \(\lambda\) is functionally equivalent to \(T\) for obstruction purposes.

---

# 9. Finite-core and interaction implications

The split vector is stronger than the pure quotient vector:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots).
\]

It is essentially equivalent to the full fixed-sector odd vector, assuming canonicity and good-patch nondegeneracy.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z_k^{\mathrm{split}}
\approx
\mathcal Z_k
}
\]

rather than

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}.
\]

This fixes the quotient zero-locus being too large.

But it also means the old full-vector difficulties likely return:

\[
\boxed{
\text{split non-concentration is probably no easier than full non-concentration.}
}
\]

Similarly, the interaction feature curve becomes

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)
=
\bigl(v_{\quot}(u),v_{\parallel}(u)\bigr).
\]

Feature balance now requires constancy of a larger feature vector:

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_k).
\]

This is stronger, but not automatically true. The same countermodel survives in the larger feature space:

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)
=
v_0+\varepsilon u^2w.
\]

So the split architecture restores detection but inherits the full interaction/non-concentration problem.

---

# 10. Kill criteria

## Kill 1 — noncanonical \(\lambda\)

If

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}
\]

depends on arbitrary whitening, basis, patch, or source-window choices and no connection law repairs this, kill the split architecture.

## Kill 2 — \(\lambda\) requires pointwise flatness

If Bottleneck-C closure demands

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0
\]

pointwise, then the old \(\eta\eta\) obstruction returns.

This is the most likely failure mode.

## Kill 3 — split finite-core no easier than full vector

If

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
\]

is just the full fixed-sector vector in different coordinates, then the architecture has not simplified the finite-core problem. It may still be viable, but it is no longer a quotient rescue.

## Kill 4 — interaction countermodels survive

If

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\]

is admissible outside incidence, then split interaction rigidity remains open.

## Kill 5 — no line-bundle transport theorem

If nonzero longitudinal motion is allowed but no canonical connection/holonomy law controls it, then the split readout has no proof gate.

---

# 11. Decision recommendation

## Continue only if Agent 1 or Agent 4 succeeds

The split architecture is worth continuing only if at least one of these is established:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Agent 1: }\lambda\text{ is canonical under whitening/patch/source changes.}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{Agent 4: }\lambda\text{ is connection-covariant and controlled by a canonical }L\text{-connection.}
}
\]

Without one of these, the split is just a gauge-dependent coordinate choice.

## Then require Agent 3 to succeed

Even if \(\lambda\) is canonical, Agent 3 must show that the Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) row becomes controlled line transport rather than pointwise flatness.

If Agent 3 finds that

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0
\]

is required pointwise, kill or downgrade the split architecture.

## Expect Agents 5–6 to find old obstructions returning

The split vector likely recovers full fixed-sector information. That is good for detection, but it probably revives full sampled non-concentration and interaction rigidity. So the split architecture may be **complete but not simplifying**.

---

# 12. Final decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{The split readout is the correct next object to test, but not yet a rescue.}
}
\]

It improves on pure quotient because it detects pure line anomalies:

\[
H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\quad\not\Rightarrow\quad
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}\equiv0.
\]

But it risks collapsing back to the original obstruction because the longitudinal component is precisely where the old \(T\)-visible failure lives.

So the decision is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue one split-readout wave.}
}
\]

with the following kill condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }\lambda\text{ is noncanonical, or if }\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\text{ must vanish pointwise, declare the current proof program nonviable.}
}
\]

The only positive continuation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{build a canonical }A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{-line connection and show Bottleneck-C line motion is transported, not killed.}
}
\]

## Agent 6 — Architecture Synthesis / Final Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The split-readout / line-bundle architecture is coherent as a diagnostic object, but not yet viable as a proof architecture.}
}
\]

It solves the pure quotient blind spot by recording both transverse and longitudinal fixed-sector data. But unless the longitudinal component \(\lambda\) is governed by a canonical line-bundle transport law, the architecture merely reintroduces the original \(T\)-visible Bottleneck-C obstruction in new coordinates. The attached coordinator prompt correctly frames the decisive question: can \(\lambda\) be transported rather than killed pointwise? 

---

# 1. Proposed architecture

The new scalar package is vector-valued:

\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
H_m^{\quot}(s),
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
\right),
\]

where

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h\!\left(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right),
\]

and

\[
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
=
\frac{
\left\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\left\langle
A_5^{\mathfrak f},
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

For fixed-sector coefficients

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
u_{2r+1}I+v_{2r+1}S,
\]

the split coordinates are

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1},
\]

and

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}
=
\frac{
\langle A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots,D_{2R+1},\lambda_{2R+1}).
}
\]

The line bundle is

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

with candidate connection

\[
\alpha_L
=
\frac{
\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
},
\]

and for a section

\[
s=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

\[
\nabla^L s
=
(d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L)A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

---

# 2. What this architecture fixes

The pure quotient architecture failed because

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

implies

\[
D_{2r+1}=0,
\]

while still giving

\[
\Phi_K(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f})
=
2\lambda_{2r+1}v_5,
\qquad
T_{2r+1}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

The split readout fixes this. A pure line anomaly is now detected by \(\lambda\). A pure transverse anomaly is detected by \(D\). On a good patch, assuming the whitening metric is canonical and nondegenerate, the pair

\[
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1})
\]

recovers the full fixed-sector coefficient

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The split readout is complete for fixed-sector detection.}
}
\]

This is its main advantage over the pure quotient scalar.

---

# 3. Where Bottleneck C returns

The active Bottleneck-C row has the form

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

Its split components are

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
(wv_5-u u_5),
\]

and

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Generically, if

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}\neq0,
\]

then at least one of

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta}),
\qquad
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
\]

is nonzero.

Therefore, if the split architecture imposes pointwise closure

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\qquad
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\]

then it requires

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

That returns the same obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pointwise split-flatness forces the old Bottleneck-C cancellation.}
}
\]

So the split architecture only helps if the longitudinal component is **not** required to vanish pointwise.

---

# 4. The only possible rescue: line-bundle transport

The positive route is:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\neq0
\text{ is allowed as covariant longitudinal transport.}
}
\]

Then Bottleneck C is no longer a local flatness gate. It becomes a transport equation on

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The needed replacement theorem would have the form

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa \lambda
=
F_{\eta\eta}
\]

with

\[
F_{\eta\eta}
\]

a controlled, globally meaningful forcing term, or else a holonomy/index statement such as

\[
\operatorname{Hol}(L,\nabla^L)
=
\text{prescribed global invariant}.
\]

But this theorem is not currently present.

Thus the architecture is viable only if one proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{longitudinal Bottleneck-C motion is globally transported, not locally killed.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Theorem dependencies

## Dependency 1 — Canonical whitening metric

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\wh}
\text{ is canonical on good patches.}
}
\]

It must be stable under:

\[
I,S\text{ basis changes},
\quad
\text{Gram normalization},
\quad
\text{positive square-root choices},
\quad
\text{patch changes},
\quad
\text{source/core changes}.
\]

If not, \(\lambda\) is gauge-dependent.

### Kill criterion

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\text{ noncanonical}
\Longrightarrow
\text{kill split architecture.}
}
\]

---

## Dependency 2 — Canonical line connection

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^L=d+\alpha_L
}
\]

must transform correctly under

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto \mu A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The expected law is

\[
\alpha_L\mapsto \alpha_L+d\log\mu,
\]

or the appropriate Hermitian analogue, so that

\[
d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L
\]

is covariant.

### Kill criterion

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^L\text{ not gauge-covariant}
\Longrightarrow
\text{kill line-bundle architecture.}
}
\]

---

## Dependency 3 — Longitudinal Bottleneck-C transport law

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
\text{ enters as controlled transport, not as pointwise defect.}
}
\]

If the proof still requires

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0
\]

pointwise, then split readout fails to improve on the old route.

### Kill criterion

\[
\boxed{
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\text{ must vanish pointwise}
\Longrightarrow
\text{kill or downgrade split architecture.}
}
\]

---

## Dependency 4 — Global holonomy / boundary theorem

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Hol}_L(\Gamma)
\text{ or endpoint transport of }\lambda
\text{ is globally constrained by zeta geometry.}
}
\]

Without this, allowing nonzero longitudinal forcing is just deferring the obstruction.

### Kill criterion

\[
\boxed{
\text{No canonical path/cycle/boundary law}
\Longrightarrow
\text{no line-bundle proof gate.}
}
\]

---

## Dependency 5 — Split finite-core non-concentration

Because \((D,\lambda)\) recovers the full fixed-sector vector, split finite-core is essentially full finite-core in new coordinates:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
\sim
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{full}}.
\]

So the old aligned branch may return:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
\approx
-P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}.
\]

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\theta\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\mathrm{split}}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\mathrm{split}}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}+J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\mathrm{split}}.
}
\]

### Downgrade criterion

\[
\boxed{
\text{split non-concentration no easier than full non-concentration}
\Longrightarrow
\text{architecture remains blocked downstream.}
}
\]

---

## Dependency 6 — Split interaction control

The split feature curve is

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)
=
(v_{\quot}(u),v_{\parallel}(u)).
\]

Feature balance still requires

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_k)
\]

for all balanced amplitudes.

The standard countermodel still threatens:

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w.
\]

Spectral cone control also still faces the usual obstruction

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

### Downgrade criterion

\[
\boxed{
\text{feature/spectral countermodels survive outside incidence}
\Longrightarrow
\text{split interaction remains blocked.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Comparison with previous architectures

## Old \(\Phi_K\)-scalar architecture

Pros:

\[
\text{detects }S\text{-visible transform data.}
\]

Cons:

\[
\text{forces }T\text{-horizontal Bottleneck-C closure and exposes }\nu_{\eta\eta}.
\]

## Pure quotient architecture

Pros:

\[
\text{gauge-invariant under }A_7\mapsto A_7+\chi A_5.
\]

Cons:

\[
\text{misses pure }A_5\text{-line anomalies.}
\]

## Split readout architecture

Pros:

\[
\text{detects both transverse and line anomalies.}
\]

Cons:

\[
\text{risks becoming full fixed-sector vector architecture with old obstructions.}
\]

## Line-bundle transport architecture

Pros:

\[
\text{only route that could avoid pointwise }\lambda=0.
\]

Cons:

\[
\text{requires new canonical connection/holonomy theorem.}
\]

---

# 7. Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue only as a line-bundle transport attack.}
}
\]

Do **not** continue merely with split readout as a pointwise closure condition. That gives no improvement.

The immediate next target is:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda_{\eta\eta}
=
\text{controlled covariant forcing}
}
\]

or a holonomy statement:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Hol}(L,\nabla^L)
=
\text{global zeta invariant}.
}
\]

If neither can be formulated, then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{declare the current architecture nonviable.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Final recommendation

The current architecture should be classified as follows:

\[
\boxed{
\text{split readout: algebraically complete, not a proof gate.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{line-bundle transport: only possible positive continuation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{pointwise split closure: failed, because it returns to }E_{\eta\eta}=0.
}
\]

So the next wave should be narrow:

1. Prove or refute canonicity of \(\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\wh}\).
2. Prove or refute covariance of \(\nabla^L\).
3. Compute \(\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda_{\eta\eta}\).
4. Determine whether the result is a controlled transport term or a fatal local defect.

If that fails, the present RH proof program should be marked nonviable rather than redirected into another local package repair.

## Agent 6 — Final Synthesis and Kill Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The line-bundle transport architecture is coherent as a final diagnostic, but not yet viable as a proof architecture.}
}
\]

It can remain alive only if one proves a concrete theorem making the longitudinal Bottleneck-C forcing an allowed covariant transport term. Without that theorem, the architecture collapses back to pointwise vanishing of

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta}),
\]

which generically forces the old obstruction

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

This wave is correctly scoped: do not revisit source splitting, pure quotienting, or direct \(\nu=0\); the only live question is whether the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line component can be transported rather than killed. 

---

# 1. Candidate final architecture

The proposed architecture has six pieces.

## 1.1 Split readout

\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
H_m^{\quot}(s),
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
\right),
\]

with

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h\!\left(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right),
\]

and

\[
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
=
\frac{
\left\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\left\langle
A_5^{\mathfrak f},
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

For coefficients,

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
u_{2r+1}I+v_{2r+1}S,
\]

the split coordinates are

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

and

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}
=
\frac{
\langle A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

On a good patch, \((D,\lambda)\) recovers the full fixed-sector vector. So the split readout fixes the pure quotient blind spot.

---

## 1.2 Line bundle

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

A longitudinal anomaly is represented as a section

\[
s=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

---

## 1.3 Candidate connection

\[
\alpha_L
=
\frac{
\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Then

\[
\nabla^L s
=
(d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L)A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Under

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto \mu A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

the required transition behavior is

\[
\alpha_L\mapsto \alpha_L+d\log\mu,
\]

and

\[
\nabla^L\lambda\mapsto \mu^{-1}\nabla^L\lambda.
\]

This must be proved globally, not only locally.

---

## 1.4 Bottleneck-C transport gate

The bad row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

Its longitudinal component is

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

The old local gate would demand

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0.
\]

The new architecture must instead supply a transport gate, e.g.

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda
=
F_{\eta\eta},
\]

where \(F_{\eta\eta}\) is a covariant, globally controlled forcing term.

---

## 1.5 Transported finite-core vector

Possible options:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots),
\]

or

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\nabla}
=
(D_7,\nabla^L\lambda_7,D_9,\nabla^L\lambda_9,\ldots),
\]

or a holonomy/endpoint version

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{Hol}}.
\]

The architecture must decide which of these is the actual finite-core object.

---

## 1.6 Transported interaction branch

The interaction feature could be

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)
=
(v_{\quot}(u),v_{\parallel}(u)),
\]

or, if line transport replaces pointwise \(\lambda\),

\[
v_{\nabla}(u)
=
(v_{\quot}(u),\nabla^L v_{\parallel}(u)).
\]

This replacement must preserve anomaly detection while improving or controlling the old feature-balance and spectral-cone obstructions.

---

# 2. Theorem dependencies

## Dependency 1 — global covariance of whitening metric

Needed:

\[
\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\wh}
\]

must be canonical up to conformal rescaling on \(\mathfrak f_h\). If allowed patch/source/core/whitening changes act by non-conformal positive operators, then \(\lambda\) is not invariant and \(\alpha_L\) acquires uncontrolled defects.

Required theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Allowed good-patch transitions preserve the whitened fixed-sector metric conformally.}
}
\]

---

## Dependency 2 — line connection transition law

Needed:

\[
\alpha_{L,j}
=
\alpha_{L,i}+d\log g_{ij}
\]

on overlaps, where

\[
A_{5,j}^{\mathfrak f}=g_{ij}A_{5,i}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

If this transition law fails, \(L\) is not a usable transport object.

---

## Dependency 3 — covariant Bottleneck-C forcing equation

Needed:

\[
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda
=
F_{\eta\eta}
\]

or

\[
\nabla_\kappa^L s_{\eta\eta}
=
F_{\eta\eta}A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

with \(F_{\eta\eta}\) tensorial under

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto \mu A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The key issue is whether

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
\]

is an allowed forcing term or a local defect that must vanish.

---

## Dependency 4 — exactness, boundary, or holonomy control

Nonzero forcing is useful only if controlled by something like

\[
F_{\eta\eta}=\nabla^L\Psi,
\]

or

\[
\operatorname{Hol}_L(\Gamma)
=
\exp\int_\Gamma \alpha_L
\]

with a canonical \(\Gamma\), or a boundary law

\[
\lambda(b)-\operatorname{PT}_{a\to b}\lambda(a)
=
\int_a^b F_{\eta\eta}.
\]

Without a canonical path, cycle, boundary condition, or global invariant, “transport” is just renaming the obstruction.

---

## Dependency 5 — transported finite-core non-concentration

Needed:

\[
\theta\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\mathrm{transport}}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\mathrm{transport}}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{transport}}+J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{transport}}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\mathrm{transport}}.
\]

If using \(\nabla^L\lambda\) loses constant line anomalies, boundary data must recover them. Otherwise transported finite-core loses detection.

---

## Dependency 6 — transported interaction rigidity

Needed: feature-balance or cone-control for the transported feature curve.

If

\[
v_{\nabla}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\]

or the unit curve spectral countermodel still survives outside incidence, the interaction branch remains blocked.

---

# 3. Hard kill criteria

## Kill 1 — \(\lambda\) noncanonical

If \(\lambda\) depends on arbitrary whitening, patch, source/core, or normalization choices with no covariant correction, kill the line-bundle architecture.

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\text{ noncanonical}
\Rightarrow
\text{kill.}
}
\]

---

## Kill 2 — \(\nabla^L\) non-covariant

If

\[
\alpha_L\mapsto \alpha_L+d\log\mu
\]

fails under legitimate transitions, kill.

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^L\text{ non-covariant}
\Rightarrow
\text{kill.}
}
\]

---

## Kill 3 — pointwise vanishing still required

If the proof still needs

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0
\]

pointwise, then generically it requires

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

That is the old Bottleneck-C obstruction.

\[
\boxed{
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\text{ pointwise flatness required}
\Rightarrow
\text{kill/downgrade.}
}
\]

---

## Kill 4 — no canonical path or boundary

If there is no canonical path/cycle \(\Gamma\), no endpoint condition, and no holonomy invariant, then transport cannot replace local closure.

\[
\boxed{
\text{no canonical global transport object}
\Rightarrow
\text{kill.}
}
\]

---

## Kill 5 — forcing not exact and not globally controlled

If

\[
F_{\eta\eta}
\]

is neither covariantly exact nor globally constrained, nonzero line forcing is uncontrolled.

\[
\boxed{
F_{\eta\eta}\text{ uncontrolled}
\Rightarrow
\text{kill.}
}
\]

---

## Kill 6 — transported finite-core loses anomaly detection

If replacing \(\lambda\) by \(\nabla^L\lambda\) loses constant line anomalies and no boundary data recovers them, the transported finite-core vector is incomplete.

\[
\boxed{
\text{transported finite-core loses detection}
\Rightarrow
\text{kill.}
}
\]

---

## Kill 7 — interaction countermodels survive

If transported/split feature or spectral countermodels survive outside incidence, the architecture remains blocked downstream.

\[
\boxed{
\text{interaction countermodels survive}
\Rightarrow
\text{blocked.}
}
\]

---

# 4. What would count as a positive result

A genuinely positive result must be one concrete theorem of the following type:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.88\linewidth}
On the good-patch atlas, \(L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) carries a canonical connection \(\nabla^L\). The Bottleneck-C longitudinal contribution satisfies a covariant transport equation
\[
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda = F_{\eta\eta},
\]
where \(F_{\eta\eta}\) is globally controlled by a canonical boundary, holonomy, or exactness law. Therefore nonzero \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\) is not a local obstruction; it is the prescribed transport of the line coordinate. This transport data still detects RH-relevant anomalies and feeds a finite-core/interaction theorem.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

Anything weaker does not rescue the architecture.

In particular:

\[
\text{“}\lambda\text{ exists”}
\]

is not enough.

\[
\text{“}\nabla^L\text{ is locally defined”}
\]

is not enough.

\[
\text{“}\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\text{ is a forcing term”}
\]

is not enough unless the forcing is globally controlled.

---

# 5. Comparison with prior architectures

## Old \(\Phi_K\)-scalar architecture

Complete for transform visibility, but fatal because it forces pointwise \(T\)-horizontal closure.

## Pure quotient architecture

Gauge-invariant, but incomplete because it loses pure \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line anomalies.

## Split readout

Complete locally, but if used as a pointwise gate it returns to the old obstruction.

## Line-bundle transport

Only possible continuation. It may allow nonzero longitudinal forcing, but only with a canonical global transport theorem.

---

# 6. Final decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue only if the line-bundle transport theorem can be made precise.}
}
\]

The next action should be extremely narrow:

1. Prove or refute global covariance of \(\nabla^L\).
2. Compute the exact covariant forcing equation for \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\).
3. Test covariant exactness or holonomy/boundary control.
4. Check that transported data remain detection-complete.

If any of the first three fail, stop.

\[
\boxed{
\text{If no canonical, globally controlled line-bundle transport law exists, declare the current proof architecture nonviable.}
}
\]

At present, the architecture is not closed. It is a final plausible diagnostic route, with one necessary theorem: **nonzero longitudinal Bottleneck-C forcing must be globally transportable rather than locally fatal.**

## Agent 6 — Architecture Synthesis / Next-Route Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The next viable attack should be the rank-two fixed-sector connection route.}
}
\]

The scalar, quotient, split, and line-bundle architectures all fail because they either lose fixed-sector information or force pointwise Bottleneck-C flatness. A rank-two connection on the full fixed-sector bundle

\[
\mathcal F_m=\mathfrak f_h(m)=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S
\]

is the best remaining candidate because it does **not** require the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line to be globally preserved. It can absorb line rotation, scalarization defects, and split-coordinate gauge dependence into a full bundle connection. The attached prompt explicitly frames this wave as a move away from scalar/quotient/split/line-bundle repairs and toward rank-two connection, projective index, vector-valued germ, or energy invariants. 

---

# 1. Candidate assessment

## Candidate 1 — Rank-two fixed-sector connection

### Object

\[
\mathcal F\to \mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_m=\mathfrak f_h(m)=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S.
\]

Construct a connection

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}
\]

on the full fixed-sector bundle, rather than on the line

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

### What it fixes

The line-bundle route failed because \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) may not transform by scalar transition functions across patch/source/core/whitening changes. A full rank-two bundle can remain well-defined even when the \(A_5\)-line rotates.

This route avoids the central line-bundle defect:

\[
A_{5,j}^{\mathfrak f}
\not\in
\mathbf C A_{5,i}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

does not kill a rank-two bundle, but it does kill a line-bundle architecture.

### Main theorem dependencies

\[
\boxed{
\text{A canonical good-patch fixed-sector bundle }\mathcal F\text{ exists.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Patch transitions act by }GL(\mathfrak f_h)\text{ and preserve the relevant structure.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\text{ is induced canonically by Gram/whitening/jet transport.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta}
\text{ becomes a connection/curvature/second-fundamental-form component, not a scalar defect.}
}
\]

### Kill criteria

Kill this route if:

\[
\mathfrak f_h
\]

does not transform as a coherent rank-two bundle across good patches, or if every natural \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\) depends on arbitrary whitening/source-window choices.

### Current judgment

\[
\boxed{
\text{Best next route.}
}
\]

It directly addresses the failure mode of the line-bundle architecture.

---

## Candidate 2 — Rank-two curvature / holonomy invariant

### Object

\[
F_{\nabla^{\mathfrak f}},
\qquad

\qquad
\operatorname{tr}F,
\qquad
\det F.
\]

### What it fixes

Earlier curvature attempts failed because the \(T\)-coordinate and \(A_5\)-line were not globally covariant. A full rank-two curvature may be globally meaningful even when individual scalar or line coordinates are not.

### Main theorem dependencies

\text{A rank-two connection exists first.}
}

\[

### Kill criteria

Kill if no canonical cycles exist, or if curvature/holonomy cannot be tied to off-line zero geometry.

### Current judgment

Do not run holonomy first. Construct \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\) first.

## Candidate 3 — Projective spectral-flow / Maslov index

### Object

\[
\ell_{2r+1}(m)
=
[A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)]
\in
\mathbf P(\mathfrak f_h).
\]

In particular,

\[
\ell_5(m)=[A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)],
\qquad
\ell_7(m)=[A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)].
\]

The quotient determinant is the projective incidence detector:

\[
D_{2r+1}=0
\iff
\ell_{2r+1}=\ell_5.
\]

### What it fixes

It avoids scalar pointwise flatness and turns the problem into a path/intersection/winding problem in \(\mathbf P^1\).

### Main theorem dependencies

\[

\text{Projective fixed-sector curves are globally defined.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Off-line zeros force projective winding/intersection.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

### Weakness

Projective data still ignore scale. Pure line anomalies satisfy

\[
[A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_5^{\mathfrak f}]
\]

and may be projectively invisible except as incidence/multiplicity.

Therefore projective data probably need to be paired with either:

\[
\|A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}
\]

or an energy/scale invariant.

### Current judgment

\[
\boxed{
\text{Promising as an index companion to the rank-two connection, not sufficient alone.}
}
\]

---

## Candidate 4 — Vector-valued fixed-sector germ

### Object

\in
\mathfrak f_h.

It avoids premature scalarization. It is complete for fixed-sector data.

}

\[

Use it as the natural section of \(\mathcal F\), not as the final invariant.

}

The failed step is the downstream fixed-sector local-to-global readout.

does not form a globally coherent rank-two bundle, or if all candidate connections depend on arbitrary whitening/source/core choices.

Kill if projective data cannot detect RH-relevant pure line/scale anomalies, and no scale companion exists.

Kill as a proof route if vector-valued non-concentration is exactly the old full-vector obstruction with no new mechanism.

Kill if the bad row contributes indefinite sign or if the energy has no global contradiction mechanism.

## Agent 6 — Rank-Two Architecture Synthesis / Route Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The rank-two fixed-sector architecture is the best remaining route, but it is still only a candidate architecture.}
}
\]

It is better than the scalar, quotient, split, and line-bundle attempts because it stops privileging one defective coordinate and instead treats

\[
\mathfrak f_h(m)=\mathbf C I_m\oplus \mathbf C S_m
\]

as the primary object. However, it becomes a viable proof route only if the fixed-sector planes form a canonical rank-two analytic bundle and the Bottleneck-C row becomes a tensorial affine forcing term with global transport control. The attached prompt correctly frames this as a move away from proving \(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\) and toward affine transport on the full fixed-sector bundle. 

---

# 1. Candidate architecture

The proposed replacement architecture is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
}
\]

The local fixed-sector odd germ becomes a section:

\[
\mathcal A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}(s;m)
=
\sum_{r\ge0}A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)s^{2r+1}
\in \Gamma(\mathcal F).
\]

The Bottleneck-C row is no longer scalarized as \(\Phi_K\), quotiented by \(A_5\), or split into \((D,\lambda)\). It is treated directly as a vector-valued section:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in \Gamma(\mathcal F).
\]

The hoped-for local replacement gate is an affine transport equation:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
}
\]

This is the correct formal shape. It avoids saying \(E_{\eta\eta}=0\) pointwise and instead asks whether the row is a controlled forcing term.

---

# 2. Role of Gate A and Gate B

Gate A and Gate B should be retained, but demoted.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A remains a local aggregate-cancellation lemma.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate B remains a conditional local quotient/fixed-sector algebra lemma.}
}
\]

They are not proof-closing gates. They are local algebraic reductions that feed the vector-valued fixed-sector transport equation. The failed step is downstream: no scalar, quotient, split, or line-bundle readout gave a viable local-to-global mechanism.

---

# 3. Theorem dependencies

## Dependency 1 — Fixed-sector bundle theorem

Required:

\[
\boxed{
\{\mathfrak f_h(b)\}_{b\in\mathcal B}
\text{ forms a canonical rank-two analytic bundle }\mathcal F\to\mathcal B.
}
\]

This requires transition maps

\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
\]

on good-patch overlaps.

This is the first kill switch. If source/core/whitening changes do not act by canonical \(GL_2\)-transitions on the same fixed-sector object, the rank-two route fails.

---

## Dependency 2 — Connection covariance theorem

Required:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F
\text{ carries a canonical connection }\nabla^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

The natural candidate is projection of ambient corrected jet/kernel-state differentiation:

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}\widetilde A).
\]

In a local frame \(E=(I,S)\),

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A
=
d
\begin{pmatrix}
a_I\\
a_S
\end{pmatrix}
+
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
\begin{pmatrix}
a_I\\
a_S
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If \(E=E^{\rm raw}W\), then formally

\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
=
W^{-1}dW+W^{-1}\Gamma^{\rm raw}W.
\]

It must satisfy the usual transition law:

\[
\Gamma_j
=
G_{ij}^{-1}\Gamma_iG_{ij}
+
G_{ij}^{-1}dG_{ij}.
\]

If this fails, the connection is just a local coordinate artifact.

---

## Dependency 3 — Affine forcing tensor theorem

Required:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta}
\text{ transforms tensorially as a section of }\mathcal F.
}
\]

More strongly, one needs an equation of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
}
\]

where \(E_{\rm lower}\) consists only of already-controlled Gate A/Gate B/connection-correction terms.

This theorem must show that \(E_{\eta\eta}\) is not a pointwise defect but an allowed inhomogeneous term in an affine transport system.

If the local gate still becomes

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]

then the rank-two architecture has failed and the old obstruction has merely been rewritten.

---

## Dependency 4 — Global affine transport theorem

Even if the local equation exists, one needs global control:

\[
A(b)
=
U_{\Gamma}A(a)
+
\int_{\Gamma}U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt.
\]

A proof gate would require one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical boundary values for }A(a),A(b),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{path-independent affine displacement,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical holonomy/monodromy constraint,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{global index/spectral-flow theorem.}
}
\]

Without this, nonzero \(E_{\eta\eta}\) remains uncontrolled forcing.

---

## Dependency 5 — Off-line-zero detection theorem

The architecture must still connect to RH:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line zero}
\Longrightarrow
\text{nontrivial rank-two affine transport / index / displacement}.
}
\]

And the global zeta structure must force the opposite condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{global zeta symmetry}
\Longrightarrow
\text{transport/index/displacement constrained}.
}
\]

Without this pair, the rank-two construction is descriptive rather than contradictory.

---

## Dependency 6 — Finite-core and interaction status

The rank-two route does not automatically solve finite-core sampled non-concentration or \(dd\)-interaction rigidity. It may repackage them as vector-valued transport problems.

Remaining dependencies:

\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\vec f}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\vec f}
\Rightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}+J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\vec f}(m,Q).
\]

And an interaction theorem controlling the vector-valued feature branch. If these remain unchanged, the rank-two route may still block downstream.

---

# 4. Derived projective and energy tools

Projective and energy invariants should be treated as **derived tools**, not primary replacements.

## Projective/Maslov

The projective line

\[
[A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)]
\in
\mathbf P(\mathcal F_m)
\]

may yield spectral-flow or Maslov-type invariants. But projective data alone miss pure scale/line anomalies, so they are incomplete unless paired with rank-two transport.

## Energy

Energies such as

\[
\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2
\]

or

\[
\sum_r\omega_r\|A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2
\]

may help if the affine forcing has a sign or monotonicity. But prior energy tests showed sign-indefinite first variation. Energy is not yet a proof gate.

---

# 5. Kill criteria

## Kill 1 — no canonical bundle

If \(\mathfrak f_h(b)\) does not form a canonical rank-two bundle across good patches:

\[
\boxed{
\text{kill rank-two route.}
}
\]

## Kill 2 — no canonical connection

If every \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\) depends on arbitrary whitening/source/core choices:

\[
\boxed{
\text{kill rank-two route.}
}
\]

## Kill 3 — row remains pointwise defect

If the affine equation reduces to:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]

then the old Bottleneck-C obstruction returns:

\[
\boxed{
\text{kill/downgrade rank-two route.}
}
\]

## Kill 4 — no global transport object

If there is no canonical path, boundary, holonomy, displacement, or index:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two route remains diagnostic only.}
}
\]

## Kill 5 — no RH detection

If off-line zeros do not force a rank-two transport anomaly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{kill rank-two route.}
}
\]

## Kill 6 — downstream obstructions unchanged

If finite-core and interaction problems remain exactly the old full-vector non-concentration/feature-balance problems with no new mechanism:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two route is blocked downstream.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue with the rank-two affine transport route for one focused wave.}
}
\]

The next exact theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-sector bundle + connection theorem:}
\quad
\mathcal F=\{\mathfrak f_h(b)\}
\text{ is a canonical rank-two analytic bundle carrying a canonical }
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

If that theorem fails, stop.

If it succeeds, immediately attack:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Affine forcing theorem:}
\quad
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
}
\]

and then:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Global affine transport theorem:}
\quad
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}E_{\eta\eta}(t)\,dt
\text{ is globally constrained or index-detecting.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Final route recommendation

Do **not** return to:

\[
\Phi_K\text{-scalar Bottleneck C},
\quad
\text{pure quotient},
\quad
(D,\lambda)\text{ split closure},
\quad
L=\mathbf C A_5\text{ line transport},
\quad
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\text{ identity attacks}.
\]

The next route is:

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

If this also fails, the current proof family should be marked nonviable rather than repaired again.

## Agent 6 — Coordinator / Decision Agent for the Fixed-Sector Atlas Theorem

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Atlas theorem status: conditional, not proved.}
}
\]

The rank-two route can proceed **only under a restricted fixed-convention atlas**: fixed source/core convention, fixed endpoint orientation, fixed raw jet basis, and canonical whitening branch. Under those restrictions, the fixed-sector planes behave like a local analytic rank-two bundle. But the **global** atlas theorem is still unproved because source/core changes may alter the corrected kernel object rather than merely change coordinates. That is the first hard kill switch. The attached prompt correctly identifies the missing theorem as canonical \(GL_2\)-transition maps satisfying a cocycle condition across good-patch overlaps. 

---

# 1. Candidate fixed-sector bundle

The desired object is

\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
\]

On a fixed good patch with fixed conventions, this is fine:

\[
(I_b,S_b)
\]

vary analytically, and

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad E_{\eta\eta}
\]

are local analytic sections. This matches the prior rank-two wave: the local rank-two bundle exists, but global transition laws remain the issue. 

The required global atlas theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
}
\]

This must hold for all admissible good-patch transitions.

---

# 2. Dependency ledger

## 2.1 Fixed-sector frame definition

The frame

\[
(I,S)
\]

appears to be canonical only **relative to a chosen corrected/whitened local model**. It depends on:

\[
\text{midpoint chart},\quad
t_\pm\text{ ordering},\quad
\text{raw jet basis},\quad
\text{whitening branch},\quad
\text{Gram normalization},\quad
\text{source/core convention},\quad
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\text{ convention}.
\]

Endpoint ordering and raw jet-basis changes are probably internal \(GL_2\)-changes. Whitening and source/core transitions are more dangerous.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The frame is canonical up to }GL_2\text{ only after local conventions are fixed.}
}
\]

---

## 2.2 Whitening / Gram transition

If

\[
E_i=(I_i,S_i)=E_i^{\rm raw}W_i,
\qquad
E_j=E_j^{\rm raw}W_j,
\]

and

\[
E_j^{\rm raw}=E_i^{\rm raw}R_{ij},
\]

then the natural candidate transition is

\[
G_{ij}=W_i^{-1}R_{ij}W_j.
\]

This is acceptable if:

1. \(W_i,W_j\) are canonically chosen, e.g. by a positive square-root branch on a connected good patch;
2. \(R_{ij}\) is a canonical raw-frame transition;
3. whitening does not mix the fixed-sector plane with non-fixed-sector directions.

If whitening changes only by a \(GL_2\)-gauge inside \(\mathfrak f_h\), the atlas survives.

If whitening changes through noncanonical choices or depends on source/core bookkeeping, then \(G_{ij}\) becomes bookkeeping, not geometry.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Whitening gives conditional }GL_2\text{ transitions, not yet canonical global transitions.}
}
\]

---

## 2.3 Source/core window transition

This is the sharpest obstruction.

Changing

\[
q=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}+q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

can do two different things:

### Harmless case

It merely changes the local representation of the same corrected kernel state. Then

\[
\mathfrak f_{h,j}=T_{ij}\mathfrak f_{h,i}
\]

for a canonical transition \(T_{ij}\), and the induced transition on frames is \(GL_2\).

### Fatal case

It changes which terms are treated as source and which are baseline, thereby changing the corrected kernel state and the fixed-sector projection itself. Then

\[
\mathfrak f_{h,i}
\]

and

\[
\mathfrak f_{h,j}
\]

are not two charts of one object. They are different local objects.

The previous source-rebuild audits show source conventions can preserve lower gates while still changing the active Bottleneck-C bookkeeping. That does **not** imply fixed-sector plane invariance. It only means the local algebra survives. 

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source/core transitions are the main unresolved atlas obstruction.}
}
\]

---

## 2.4 Ambient projection functoriality

The future connection wants

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}\widetilde A).
\]

For this to be well-defined, the ambient corrected jet/kernel-state bundle \(\mathcal J\) must have transitions \(T_{ij}\) satisfying:

\[
T_{ij}\mathfrak f_{h,i}=\mathfrak f_{h,j},
\]

and

\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}
=
T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}.
\]

Also, the projection-defined derivative must be independent of the ambient lift \(\widetilde A\). That requires compatibility of the projection kernel under \(d_X^{\mathcal J}\), or a canonical horizontal lift.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Projection functoriality is required before any global }\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\text{ exists.}
}
\]

---

## 2.5 Cocycle consistency

Even if pairwise transitions exist, they must satisfy

\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

Potential failures:

\[
\text{endpoint swaps with signs},
\]

\[
\text{noncanonical whitening branches},
\]

\[
\text{source-window moves performed in different orders},
\]

\[
\text{affine correction terms rather than linear transitions}.
\]

If a transition produces

\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij}+B_{ij},
\qquad B_{ij}\neq0,
\]

then it is not a vector-bundle atlas. It is affine, and the whole rank-two route must be reformulated as an affine bundle.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cocycle consistency is unproved and source/core path-dependence is the main risk.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Gate A / Gate B compatibility

Gate A and Gate B should survive only as **local algebraic lemmas**.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A: local aggregate-cancellation lemma.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate B: conditional local quotient/fixed-sector algebra lemma.}
}
\]

They do not prove the atlas theorem. They are tied to a local convention unless the \(GL_2\)-transition theorem is proved.

So the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B are valid inside each good patch; global transport across patches remains unproved.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Hard kill criteria

## Kill 1 — source/core changes alter the object

If moving a zero atom between core/source changes the corrected kernel state or \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\), rather than merely changing coordinates, then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{global rank-two bundle fails.}
}
\]

This is the primary kill condition.

---

## Kill 2 — whitening mixes sectors noncanonically

If different admissible whitening choices mix \(\mathfrak f_h\) with non-fixed-sector directions, or depend on arbitrary branch choices not fixed by good-patch analyticity, then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{atlas fails or is only gauge-bookkeeping.}
}
\]

---

## Kill 3 — projection not functorial

If

\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}
\neq
T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i},
\]

then fixed-sector coefficients are not tensorial.

\[
\boxed{
\text{no global }\mathcal F.
}
\]

---

## Kill 4 — transition maps are path-dependent

If source-window or whitening transitions depend on the order of moves, so that

\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}\neq G_{ik},
\]

then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cocycle fails.}
}
\]

---

## Kill 5 — only a fixed local convention works

If the only way to define \(\mathcal F\) is to freeze all conventions globally by fiat, then the object is not canonical enough for a proof unless that frozen convention is itself mathematically forced.

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed-convention local theory is not a global proof architecture.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Atlas theorem: conditional.}
}
\]

The rank-two route may proceed **only in a restricted form**:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\{\text{midpoint/collision/finite-core parameters with fixed source/core convention, fixed endpoint orientation, fixed raw jet basis, and canonical whitening branch}\}.
}
\]

On this reduced base, the fixed-sector bundle is plausible.

But the full good-patch atlas theorem remains unproved because source/core and whitening transitions may not be canonical chart changes.

---

# 6. Exact next theorem to attack

The next theorem should be **not** the connection theorem yet. First attack source/core invariance:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source/Core Functoriality Theorem:}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Changing admissible source/core windows induces a canonical ambient transition }
T_{ij}
\text{ satisfying }
T_{ij}\mathfrak f_{h,i}=\mathfrak f_{h,j}
\text{ and }
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}=T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}.
}
\]

If this theorem fails, the global rank-two route fails.

If it succeeds, then attack whitening/Gram transitions:

\[
\boxed{
G_{ij}=W_i^{-1}R_{ij}W_j,
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
}
\]

Only after both are proved should we proceed to:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}\widetilde A).
}
\]

---

# 7. Final recommendation

Do **not** proceed immediately to affine transport or holonomy. The atlas is not ready.

The next wave should focus on exactly one issue:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do source/core and whitening changes define canonical }GL_2\text{ transitions on }\mathfrak f_h?
}
\]

If yes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{proceed to constructing }\nabla^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

If no:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two route is only local and the current proof family should be marked nonviable.}
}
\]

At present, the most honest status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two atlas theorem is plausible locally, conditional globally, and blocked by source/core functoriality.}
}
\]

## Agent 6 — Source/Core Functoriality Coordinator

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{source/core functoriality is conditional, not proved.}
}
\]

The rank-two route can proceed only on a **reduced fixed-convention base** where the fixed core, endpoint orientation, raw jet basis, source convention, and whitening branch are fixed. Near/far cutoff changes inside the non-core complement are plausibly functorial. But moving zero atoms into or out of the fixed core appears to change the corrected local object, not merely its coordinates. If such core moves are unavoidable, the global rank-two vector-bundle atlas fails. The attached instruction identifies this as the current bottleneck: source/core transitions must induce canonical ambient transitions preserving \(\mathfrak f_h\) and commuting with \(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\). 

---

# 1. Required source/core functoriality theorem

The needed theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
T_{ij}\mathfrak f_{h,i}=\mathfrak f_{h,j}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}
=
T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}.
}
\]

Equivalently, for local fixed-sector frames,

\[
\boxed{
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C).
}
\]

If this holds with cocycle compatibility, the rank-two fixed-sector bundle exists globally. If not, the rank-two construction is local bookkeeping only.

---

# 2. Case classification

## Case A — near/far cutoff changes with fixed core

This is the most plausible functorial case.

If the fixed core is unchanged and only the split between

\[
q_{\aux,R}
\]

and

\[
T_{\far,R}
\]

changes, then the full non-core source

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

should be invariant, at least formally. In that case, changing \(R\) is bookkeeping, not a change of the corrected object.

The risk is the estimation/error term:

\[
E_{\est,R}.
\]

If

\[
E_{\est,R_2}-E_{\est,R_1}
\]

is a functorial correction and does not alter the fixed-sector projection except by a canonical transition, then near/far cutoff changes are safe.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{near/far cutoff changes are conditionally linear/functorial if }G^{\new}\text{ is held fixed and }E_{\est,R}\text{ is functorial.}
}
\]

Status: **conditional**.

---

## Case B — moving atoms into or out of fixed core

This is the hard obstruction.

A move of one zero-pair atom

\[
q_\rho
\]

from source to core changes

\[
q_{\core},
\]

the local core model, the baseline phase, the corrected residual decomposition, the source labels, and likely the finite-sector coefficients

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad E_{\eta\eta}.
\]

This is not naturally a \(GL_2\)-frame change. It is a different local model.

The transition would have to satisfy

\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

for all relevant \(r\). But moving a zero into the core changes the actual Taylor/source decomposition, so one expects an additive correction:

\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{\rho,2r+1}.
\]

That is affine, not linear.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{core moves are object-changing unless a nontrivial affine/torsor theorem is proved.}
}
\]

Status: **not functorial as a vector-bundle transition**.

---

## Case C — changing background/error handling

Moving terms between

\[
B_{\bg}
\]

and

\[
E_{\est,R}
\]

is safe only if those terms are smooth/background bookkeeping terms with canonical update rules and if their fixed-sector contributions transform functorially.

But if background/error handling changes the corrected kernel state or fixed-sector projection, then it is not a coordinate change.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{background/error changes are conditionally functorial only with a canonical error-update law.}
}
\]

Status: **conditional**.

---

## Case D — changing finite-core cluster

Changing the cluster itself is generally a change of local model. It affects:

\[
q_{\core},
\]

the local same-scale geometry, the fixed-core Taylor coefficients, and the source/residual decomposition.

Unless cluster changes are confined to a controlled incidence or patch-boundary set, they do not define transitions inside one bundle.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-core cluster changes are object-changing except across controlled patch boundaries.}
}
\]

Status: **avoid or treat as incidence**.

---

## Case E — fixed canonical core convention

This is the most viable practical route.

Choose a canonical rule, for example:

\[
\text{fixed }k\text{ nearest same-scale zeros},
\]

or a spacing/window rule tied to \(S(m)\) or \(Q\). Then avoid comparing different core choices except across boundaries where the rule changes.

The proof base becomes

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\{
\text{good patches with fixed canonical core, fixed source convention, fixed endpoint orientation, fixed raw jet basis, fixed whitening branch}
\}.
\]

Transitions involving core changes are not part of the vector-bundle atlas; they are treated as patch-boundary/incidence events.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a reduced fixed-convention base is viable if core-rule failures are placed in }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
}
\]

Status: **best current option**.

---

# 3. Linear, affine, or object-changing?

| Transition type | Classification | Current status |
|---|---:|---|
| Endpoint swap / raw basis change | Linear \(GL_2\) | likely safe |
| Whitening/Gram change after raw plane identified | Linear \(GL_2\) | conditionally safe |
| Near/far cutoff with fixed \(G^{\new}\) | Linear/bookkeeping | conditional on \(E_{\est,R}\) |
| Background/error reshuffle | Linear or affine | conditional |
| Move atom source \(\leftrightarrow\) core | Affine/object-changing | unsafe |
| Change finite-core cluster | Object-changing | treat as incidence |
| Fixed canonical core convention | Avoids transition | viable reduced-base route |

---

# 4. Does an affine/torsor atlas help?

If core moves produce

\[
A_j^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_i^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{ij},
\]

then one could attempt an affine torsor

\[
\mathcal T\to \mathcal B
\]

modeled on the rank-two vector bundle

\[
\mathcal F.
\]

The affine cocycle would need:

\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik},
\]

and

\[
B_{ik}=G_{jk}^{-1}B_{ij}+B_{jk}
\]

up to convention.

But for source/core moves, \(B_{ij}\) depends on which zero atoms are moved and in which order. That creates a path-dependence risk. Without a canonical single-zero transfer formula and affine cocycle proof, the torsor route is speculative.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{affine/torsor atlas is a possible fallback, but it requires a new single-zero transfer cocycle theorem.}
}
\]

It should not be assumed.

---

# 5. Gate A/B compatibility

Gate A and Gate B survive only locally under a fixed convention.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B are convention-local algebraic lemmas.}
}
\]

They may be transported across the atlas only after source/core functoriality is proved. At present, they do not imply fixed-sector plane invariance under core changes.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B remain useful on }\mathcal B_{\rm red},
\text{ but they do not solve source/core functoriality.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Hard kill criteria

The rank-two route dies if any of the following hold:

\[
\boxed{
\text{core moves are unavoidable and object-changing.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{no canonical fixed core convention exists.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E_{\est,R}\text{ cutoff corrections are non-functorial.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{single-zero transfer produces path-dependent affine corrections.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B depend on source convention in a nontransportable way.}
}
\]

The most immediate kill switch is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{moving atoms into/out of }q_{\core}\text{ cannot be avoided or controlled as incidence.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{source/core functoriality: conditional on reduced fixed-convention base.}
}
\]

The global rank-two vector-bundle atlas is **not proved**.

The recommended next route is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Proceed on }\mathcal B_{\rm red}\text{ with a fixed canonical core convention.}
}
\]

Then prove that failures of the convention lie in a controlled incidence set:

\[
\boxed{
\text{core-rule changes}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
}
\]

Only after that should we build

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}
\]

on the reduced base.

---

# 8. Exact next theorem to attack

The next theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Core Convention Theorem}
}
\]

There exists a canonical fixed-core rule such that, away from a controlled incidence set

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core},
\]

the decomposition

\[
q=q_{\core}+q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}
\]

is locally stable, and all allowed remaining transitions induce canonical \(GL_2\)-changes on

\[
\mathfrak f_h.
\]

Formally:

\[
\boxed{
b\in \mathcal B_{\rm red}
\Longrightarrow
\mathfrak f_h(b)
\text{ is a canonical rank-two analytic bundle fibre,}
}
\]

and on overlaps inside \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\),

\[
\boxed{
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
}
\]

Boundary failures must satisfy:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

---

# 9. Final recommendation

Do **not** attack affine transport yet.

First run a narrow **canonical core convention wave**:

1. Define the core-selection rule.
2. Prove local stability of the selected core.
3. Show core changes occur only on controlled incidence/boundary sets.
4. Prove near/far cutoff functoriality with fixed core.
5. Prove Gate A/B are invariant under the remaining reduced-base transitions.

If that succeeds, continue to the rank-two connection theorem.

If it fails:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the rank-two global route is nonviable, and the current proof family should be marked failed.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:52:12)

_Thought for 8s_

## Agent 6 — Canonical-Core Coordinator / Decision Agent

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical core convention: conditionally viable, but not yet proved.}
}
\]

The reduced-base strategy is the only plausible way to keep the rank-two fixed-sector route alive. Arbitrary source/core transitions are not functorial, so the architecture must freeze a canonical core rule and work only on strata where that rule is stable. The next theorem is therefore **not** affine transport yet; it is the **Canonical Core Convention Theorem**. 

---

# 1. Proposed canonical core convention

The best candidate is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the canonical symmetric same-scale }k\text{-core nearest }m.
}
\]

More explicitly, choose the finite cluster of zero-pair atoms satisfying:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale relative to }m,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{symmetric under conjugation / functional-equation partners as required by the draft,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{nearest to }m\text{ under the local distance/radius ordering,}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m)
}
\]

so the selected \(k\)-core is locally stable.

The rule should be **label-stable** on each reduced stratum. That means the members of \(\mathcal C_k(m)\) do not change under small perturbations of \(m\), and their ordering/endpoint assignment remains fixed.

---

# 2. Reduced base and exceptional set

Define

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

Here \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\) is the locus where all of the following hold:

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

\[
\text{same-scale bounds hold for the selected core,}
\]

\[
\text{endpoint gaps remain nonzero,}
\]

\[
\text{no zero collision or label swap occurs,}
\]

\[
\text{symmetry closure is unambiguous,}
\]

\[
\text{Gram/whitening is nonsingular,}
\]

\[
\text{the finite-core cluster size is locally constant,}
\]

and the source convention is fixed:

\[
q
=
q_{\core}
+
q_{\aux,R}
+
T_{\far,R}
+
B_{\bg}
+
E_{\est,R},
\]

with

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

treated as the full non-core source.

The exceptional set is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm core\ boundary}.
}
\]

The new core-boundary part includes:

\[
d_k=d_{k+1},
\]

nearest-neighbor ties,

equal-spacing degeneracies,

zero collisions,

endpoint-gap collapse,

symmetry-closure ambiguity,

cluster-size jumps,

Gram/whitening singularities,

and patch-boundary failures.

---

# 3. Required theorem dependencies

## Theorem 1 — Canonical core-selection theorem

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_k(m)
\text{ is uniquely determined by zeta/local-zero data on }
\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
}
\]

This theorem must prove that the chosen core is not an arbitrary modeling convention. It must be forced by the same-scale, symmetry, and strict-gap rules.

---

## Theorem 2 — Local core-stability theorem

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
m\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\Longrightarrow
\mathcal C_k(m)
\text{ is locally constant as a labeled symmetric zero cluster.}
}
\]

This follows if all strict inequalities defining the reduced stratum persist under small perturbation.

---

## Theorem 3 — Boundary/incidence containment theorem

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

This is essential. If core-selection failures happen in ordinary good patches, the reduced-base strategy is not global enough.

---

## Theorem 4 — Reduced-base fixed-sector atlas theorem

On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\), source/core membership is fixed. Therefore one can hope for genuine \(GL_2\)-transitions:

\[
\boxed{
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
}
\]

The key point is that no additive source/core transfer term

\[
B_{\rho,2r+1}
\]

should appear inside \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\), because no zero atom moves into or out of the core there.

---

## Theorem 5 — Gate A/B compatibility theorem

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A and Gate B remain valid local lemmas on }\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
}
\]

Since the source labels and core convention are frozen on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\), this is plausible. But it must be stated carefully:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B are stable under reduced-base transitions, not arbitrary core changes.}
}
\]

They do not prove source/core functoriality; they survive only after the canonical core rule freezes the decomposition.

---

## Theorem 6 — RH-relevant good-patch existence theorem

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH-relevant/off-line-zero configuration}
\Longrightarrow
\exists b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
}
\]

If all RH-relevant configurations are forced onto core-boundary strata, the reduced-base proof cannot apply. This is a major kill switch.

---

# 4. Kill criteria

The rank-two route dies if any of the following hold.

## Kill 1 — no canonical core rule

If there is no rule selecting \(\mathcal C_k(m)\) from zeta/local-zero data without arbitrary choices, then

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two reduced-base route fails.}
}
\]

## Kill 2 — core rule changes outside controlled incidence

If \(\mathcal C_k(m)\) changes in ordinary good patches, not just on

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core},
\]

then the reduced-base atlas is not stable.

## Kill 3 — \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\) too small

If RH-relevant configurations do not admit reduced good patches, then the route has no global reach.

## Kill 4 — Gate A/B fail under the fixed convention

If freezing the core convention breaks Gate A or Gate B, then the reduced base destroys the local algebra it was meant to preserve.

## Kill 5 — fixed-sector atlas still fails on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\)

If even with fixed core/source membership the transitions fail to be \(GL_2\)-linear, then the rank-two bundle does not exist.

## Kill 6 — near/far cutoff errors are non-functorial

If varying \(R\) changes fixed-sector coefficients through non-tensorial error terms, then either \(R\) must also be frozen canonically or the route fails.

---

# 5. Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical core convention: viable only conditionally.}
}
\]

The best rule is the **fixed \(k\)-nearest symmetric same-scale core with strict gap and nondegeneracy conditions**.

The best base is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

The best immediate theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Core Convention Theorem:}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
m\in \mathcal B_{\rm red}
\Longrightarrow
\mathcal C_k(m)
\text{ is uniquely selected, locally stable, and source/core membership is fixed.}
}
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Reduced-Base Atlas Theorem:}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak f_h(b)
\text{ forms a canonical rank-two analytic bundle over }
\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
}
\]

Only after those are proved should we proceed to the connection theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
}
\]

as a canonical connection on

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

---

# 6. Next route recommendation

Proceed in this order:

\[
\boxed{
1.\ \text{Prove canonical core selection and local stability.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
2.\ \text{Show core-rule failures lie in }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
3.\ \text{Prove RH-relevant good-patch existence in }\mathcal B_{\rm red}.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
4.\ \text{Prove reduced-base }GL_2\text{ fixed-sector atlas.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
5.\ \text{Only then construct }\nabla^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

If steps 1–3 fail, the rank-two global route is not viable. If they succeed, the rank-two architecture has a legitimate base on which affine transport can finally be tested.
