## Agent 6 — Reduced-Good-Patch Existence Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH-relevant reduced good-patch existence is conditionally plausible, but not proved.}
}
\]

The rank-two route can proceed only under a generic/nondegenerate existence theorem: every RH-relevant off-line packet must admit a midpoint/core choice outside the enlarged exceptional set

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

The current framework gives a plausible reduced base, but not yet a theorem that all RH-relevant configurations enter it. This is now the main kill switch for the rank-two architecture. 

---

# 1. Target theorem

The required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\Longrightarrow
\exists b\in \mathcal B_{\rm red}
}
\]

or, more carefully,

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every RH-relevant/off-line-zero configuration either admits }b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ or lies in a controlled exceptional incidence case.}
}
\]

Here

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core},
\]

with

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm core\ boundary}.
\]

The intended canonical core is

\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale, \(k\)-atom zero cluster nearest }m.
\]

---

# 2. RH-relevant configuration

The minimal RH-relevant packet is an off-critical zero

\[
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,
\qquad
\beta\ne\frac12,
\]

together with its symmetry packet

\[
\rho,\quad \bar\rho,\quad 1-\rho,\quad 1-\bar\rho.
\]

A configuration is RH-relevant only if it can influence the fixed-sector odd germ:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},
\]

or equivalently the rank-two local state

\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S.
\]

Degenerate configurations already lying in collision, endpoint-collapse, Gram-singularity, or patch-boundary incidence should be classified into

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core},
\]

not treated as ordinary reduced-base configurations.

So the working definition is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
=
\{\text{off-line symmetry packets producing a nontrivial local fixed-sector anomaly outside known incidence}\}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Strict core-gap condition

The reduced base requires

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m).
\]

Let

\[
\Delta_k(m)=d_{k+1}(m)-d_k(m).
\]

The strict-gap failure set is

\[
\{\Delta_k(m)=0\}.
\]

Under ordinary local zero geometry, this should be a codimension-one tie wall: two candidate zero packets have equal selection score. Such a wall should be avoidable by perturbing \(m\), unless the off-line packet is trapped by exact symmetry or a degeneracy.

Thus the conditional statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_k(m)>0
\text{ exists near every nondegenerate RH-relevant packet, unless the packet lies on a tie/incidence stratum.}
}
\]

Missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\{\Delta_k=0\}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\quad\text{and does not contain an open RH-relevant family.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Same-scale, endpoint, and symmetry closure

The canonical core must be same-scale:

\[
c_1S(m)\le d_\alpha(m)\le c_2S(m)
\qquad
(\alpha\in\mathcal C_k(m)).
\]

It must also be symmetry closed:

\[
\rho\in\mathcal C_k(m)
\Rightarrow
\bar\rho,\ 1-\rho,\ 1-\bar\rho\in\mathcal C_k(m).
\]

This may force the core size to jump if the nearest \(k\)-cluster is not already symmetry closed. Therefore the reduced-base rule should choose \(k\) as a symmetry-packet count, not a raw zero count.

Endpoint failures include

\[
t_+=t_-,
\]

or endpoint collision with a zero/source atom. These should be placed in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm endpoint}^{\core}.
\]

Conditional result:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-scale and endpoint conditions are plausible on nondegenerate packets, but symmetry closure may force extra exceptional strata.}
}
\]

Required theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm same\ scale}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm sym}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm endpoint}^{\core}
\text{ is controlled and does not swallow }\mathcal R_{\rm RH}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Gram/whitening nondegeneracy

The reduced base requires

\[
\det G_{\core}(m)\ne0
\]

and a canonical whitening branch.

The singularity set is

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram}^{\core}
=
\{m:\det G_{\core}(m)=0\}.
\]

Since the Gram determinant is analytic or semianalytic in the local zero/core parameters, its zero set should be controlled unless it vanishes identically on the RH-relevant family.

Conditional result:

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}\ne0
\text{ should be avoidable generically, but the draft needs a non-identical-vanishing theorem.}
}
\]

Missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}
\not\equiv0
\text{ on every RH-relevant off-line packet family.}
}
\]

If this fails, the rank-two reduced base has no reach.

---

# 6. Exceptional-set control

The enlarged exceptional set is

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm tie}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm scale}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm sym}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm endpoint}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm patch}^{\core}.
\]

Each component is plausibly either:

\[
\text{analytic equality},
\]

\[
\text{semianalytic boundary},
\]

or

\[
\text{finite-core incidence condition}.
\]

But the essential non-swallowing theorem is still missing:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

The stronger needed form is:

\[
\boxed{
\forall R\in\mathcal R_{\rm RH},
\quad
\exists b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ associated to }R,
}
\]

unless \(R\) is already handled by controlled incidence.

---

# 7. Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Reduced-good-patch existence: conditionally proved under generic/nondegenerate hypotheses.}
}
\]

It is **not** proved unconditionally.

The theorem currently depends on these missing pieces:

\[
\boxed{
\text{strict core-gap non-swallowing;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{symmetry-closed same-scale packet stability;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gram determinant non-identical-vanishing;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{exceptional-set non-swallowing of RH-relevant packets.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Kill criteria

The rank-two reduced-base route fails if any of the following occur:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No canonical \(k\)-core can be defined from local zero data.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
d_k<d_{k+1}
\text{ cannot be achieved near RH-relevant packets.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Symmetry closure forces unstable core size on an open RH-relevant family.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}=0
\text{ identically on an RH-relevant family.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\text{ swallows all RH-relevant off-line configurations.}
}
\]

If any of these is true, the reduced-base route cannot support a global proof.

---

# 9. Next theorem to attack

The next theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Exceptional Non-Swallowing Theorem}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

Stronger form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet admits a nearby midpoint }m
\text{ with}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),\quad
\text{same-scale},\quad
\text{symmetry closure},\quad
\text{endpoint separation},\quad
\det G_{\core}(m)\ne0.
}
\]

Only after this theorem is proved should the project proceed to the rank-two connection construction:

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).
\]

---

# 10. Final recommendation

Proceed with the rank-two route **only conditionally**.

The next wave should not construct

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}
\]

yet. It should prove the reduced-good-patch existence theorem, specifically the exceptional non-swallowing result.

If that succeeds:

\[
\boxed{
\text{construct }\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ and then }\nabla^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

If it fails:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the rank-two global route has no reach, and the current proof family should be marked nonviable.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:01:17)

_Thought for 6s_

## Agent 6 — Exceptional Non-Swallowing Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exceptional non-swallowing is conditionally plausible, but not proved.}
}
\]

The reduced-base rank-two route can continue only under a **generic/nondegenerate off-line packet hypothesis**. The current machinery does not yet prove the required universal theorem

\[
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}\not\subseteq \mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

The strongest defensible statement is conditional: if the off-line packet is not trapped on tie walls, same-scale failure, symmetry-closure boundary, endpoint collapse, Gram singularity, or fixed-sector invisibility, then one can choose a nearby \((m,s)\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}\). The attached instruction correctly identifies this as the current kill switch before constructing \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\). 

---

# 1. Target theorem

The target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet admits a nearby reduced good patch.}
}
\]

More explicitly, for an off-line symmetry packet

\[
\mathcal P(\rho)=\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\},
\qquad
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \beta\ne \frac12,
\]

we need some local choice

\[
b=(m,s,\mathcal C_k(m))
\]

such that:

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

same-scale conditions hold,

symmetry closure is stable,

endpoint separation holds,

\[
\det G_{\core}(m,s)\ne0,
\]

and

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(m,s)\ne0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

---

# 2. Parameter-avoidance status

The local free parameters are at least:

\[
m,
\qquad
s,
\]

and possibly finite-core chart parameters \(\theta\).

The relevant bad conditions are equations or boundary inequalities in these parameters:

\[
d_k(m)=d_{k+1}(m),
\]

same-scale boundary,

symmetry-closure boundary,

endpoint collision,

\[
t_\pm=m\pm s/2
\]

hitting a forbidden zero/source location,

and

\[
\det G_{\core}(m,s)=0.
\]

A finite union of proper analytic or semianalytic walls cannot cover a local \((m,s)\)-neighborhood unless one of the bad conditions is identically forced.

Thus we have the conditional theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If no exceptional equation is identically forced, then there exists }(m,s)\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
}
\]

Missing piece:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No exceptional condition is identically forced on every RH-relevant off-line packet family.}
}
\]

That is the precise non-swallowing gap.

---

# 3. Symmetry-packet status

The core must be selected by **symmetry packets**, not raw individual zeros. Otherwise forced internal equalities from

\[
\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho
\]

can look like artificial nearest-neighbor ties.

Define packet-level distance scores

\[
D_P(m)
\]

for symmetry packets \(P\). Then the core rule should be:

\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the nearest \(k\)-packet symmetry-closed same-scale core.}
\]

Under packet-level ordering, internal conjugation/functional-equation ties are harmless. Dangerous ties are only between distinct packets:

\[
D_P(m)=D_Q(m).
\]

These are boundary walls and should be placed in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm tie}^{\core}.
\]

Conditional result:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Symmetry closure does not swallow off-line packets if packet-level ordering is used.}
}
\]

Remaining risk: symmetry closure can force a core-size jump if a required partner lies outside the same-scale window. That must be included in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm sym}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm scale}^{\core}.
\]

---

# 4. Same-scale status

Same-scale requires:

\[
c_1S(m)\le d_\alpha(m)\le c_2S(m)
\qquad
(\alpha\in\mathcal C_k(m)).
\]

For a nondegenerate symmetry packet, same-scale is plausible after choosing \(m\) near the packet center and choosing \(k\) by symmetry-packet count.

But it is not automatic. Surrounding zeros can force the nearest \(k\)-core to mix scales. If that happens only on boundary strata, it is controlled. If it happens on an open RH-relevant family, the reduced-base strategy fails or the core rule must be changed.

Current conditional statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-scale non-swallowing holds unless off-line packets are forced into open scale-mixing families.}
}
\]

Missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm scale}^{\core}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Gram determinant status

The key missing Gram theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}(m,s)\not\equiv0
\text{ on every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet family.}
}
\]

The Gram determinant should be analytic or semianalytic in the local parameters. If it is not identically zero, then its nonzero locus is open and dense, so \((m,s)\) can be chosen outside

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram}^{\core}.
\]

Likely causes of identically zero Gram determinant are already exceptional:

zero collision,

duplicate labels from symmetry closure,

endpoint collapse,

multiplicity,

overlarge \(k\) relative to available jet dimension,

or parity-forced dependence.

Thus the conditional theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}\ne0
\text{ is generically available outside known incidence.}
}
\]

But the proof still needs a concrete local independence lemma, for example:

\[
\boxed{
\text{distinct Cauchy/kernel jet functions for a nondegenerate symmetry packet are linearly independent.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Fixed-sector visibility status

The reduced patch is useful only if the off-line packet is visible to the rank-two fixed-sector odd germ:

\[
\exists r\le R_{\Theta_k}
\quad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m,s)\ne0.
\]

If all such coefficients vanish,

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(m,s)=0,
\]

then the off-line packet is invisible to this architecture.

Define the invisibility locus:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}.
\]

The desired result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A genuine off-line packet produces nonzero fixed-sector data outside controlled incidence.}
}
\]

This is not yet proved. It is a serious dependency because scalar/quotient/split failures already showed that “visibility” depends strongly on the readout. The rank-two germ is complete once constructed, but it still needs a theorem connecting off-line packets to nonzero rank-two data.

Conditional status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-sector visibility is plausible, but must be proved as an off-line packet detection lemma.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Enlarged exceptional set

The current exceptional set should be enlarged to include the remaining non-swallowing dependencies:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram,id}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm forced\ scale}^{\core}.
\]

Where:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\},
\]

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram,id}^{\core}
=
\{\det G_{\core}\equiv0\text{ on the local packet family}\},
\]

and

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm forced\ scale}^{\core}
\]

captures open same-scale failure.

This enlargement is legitimate only if these sets are controlled incidence sets and do **not** swallow all RH-relevant off-line packets.

So the final non-swallowing theorem becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exceptional non-swallowing: conditional, still open.}
}
\]

It is conditionally true under the following hypotheses:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-level core ordering has strict gap off tie walls;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale and symmetry closure fail only on controlled boundaries;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}\not\equiv0
\text{ on nondegenerate off-line packet families;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\not\equiv0
\text{ on nondegenerate off-line packet families.}
}
\]

Without those, we cannot proceed to the rank-two connection theorem.

---

# 9. Kill criteria

The rank-two reduced-base route fails if any of these occur:

\[
\boxed{
\text{all admissible }(m,s)\text{ near an RH packet lie on core tie walls;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale failure is open on an RH-relevant packet family;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{symmetry closure forces unstable core size on an open RH-relevant family;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}\equiv0
\text{ on a nondegenerate RH-relevant family;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0
\text{ for a genuine off-line packet outside incidence;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}
\text{ swallows }\mathcal R_{\rm RH}.
}
\]

---

# 10. Exact next theorem to attack

The next theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Packet Visibility and Independence Theorem}
}
\]

For every nondegenerate off-line symmetry packet \(\mathcal P(\rho)\), there exists a nearby \((m,s)\) such that:

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

the packet-level core is same-scale and symmetry stable,

\[
\det G_{\core}(m,s)\ne0,
\]

and

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(m,s)\ne0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}.
}
\]

This theorem combines Gram non-identical-vanishing and fixed-sector visibility. It is the last prerequisite before constructing

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
\]

on

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

---

# 11. Final recommendation

Do **not** construct the rank-two connection yet.

Run one more narrow wave on:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet Visibility and Independence.}
}
\]

Specifically:

1. Prove distinct packet source/jet functions are independent.
2. Prove \(\det G_{\core}\not\equiv0\).
3. Prove \(C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\not\equiv0\) for off-line packets.
4. Show tie/scale/symmetry/endpoint failures are proper boundary strata.

If that wave succeeds, the rank-two architecture finally has a real base. If it fails, the current proof family should be marked nonviable.

## Agent 6 — Packet Visibility Synthesis Agent

\[

\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}.
}

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

The attached prompt identifies this exactly as the current target before constructing \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\). 

---

# 1. Off-line packet jet expansion status

For a paired source atom,

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]

set

\[
\delta=\beta-\frac12,
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\qquad
x_m=2m-\gamma.
\]

The derivatives of \(f_{\beta,\gamma}\) are rational functions of \(\delta\) and \(x_m\). For \(\delta\ne0\), the packet has genuinely different pole geometry from the critical-line case. In particular, the local jet sequence is not identically the critical-line jet sequence unless a symmetry or projection kills the difference.

So the likely statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\delta\ne0
\Rightarrow
\text{some local source jet changes nontrivially.}
}
\]

But this is not yet enough. We need that a changed source jet reaches the fixed-sector odd vector

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Thus Agent 1’s result should be treated as positive but insufficient:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line packets have nontrivial source jets, but fixed-sector visibility is not automatic.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Fixed-sector projection non-annihilation status

The dangerous failure is:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(\text{off-line packet contribution})\equiv0.
\]

The Bottleneck-C row itself gives strong evidence that the packet class is not generically annihilated by \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\), since the active obstruction has the fixed-sector shape

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in\mathfrak f_h.
\]

If

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}\ne0,
\]

then this is visibly nonzero in the fixed sector.

However, this is evidence from a particular row, not yet a universal projection theorem. The missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(\text{nondegenerate off-line packet contribution})
\not\equiv0
}
\]

outside controlled incidence.

Potential projection-killing cases remain:

\[

\]

\[
\text{endpoint symmetry},
\]

\[
\text{anti-fixed-sector cancellation},
\]

\[
\text{Gram/whitening singularity},
\]

\[
\text{special midpoint or sample choices}.
\]

These should be included in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\]

only if they are proper incidence conditions, not open RH-relevant families.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projection non-annihilation is plausible, but unproved.}
}
\]

---

# 3. First nonzero finite-order coefficient status

The visibility theorem requires a finite order:

\[
\exists r\le R_{\Theta_k}
\quad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

The most likely candidates are

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\quad
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\quad
A_{11}^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots
\]

The prior Bottleneck-C work shows that order \(7\) is already highly sensitive to source geometry. But there are two caveats:

1. \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) may be a reference/line coordinate rather than a visibility witness.
2. Gate A/B cancellations may erase some low-order rows.

Thus the needed finite-order theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad
(3\le r\le R_{\Theta_k})
\Longrightarrow
\text{the off-line packet is incidence-degenerate or invisible globally.}
}
\]

This is essentially a finite-determinacy plus visibility statement. It is not yet proved.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-order visibility is open.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Analytic invisibility-locus status

Define

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}.
\]

On a reduced stratum, each coefficient

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

should be analytic or semianalytic in the local parameters

\[
(\beta,\gamma,m,s,\theta).
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\]

is an analytic or semianalytic incidence set.

The critical question is whether it is proper. If

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0
\]

on an open set with

\[
\beta\ne\frac12,
\]

then the rank-two route loses RH-detection power.

The desired analytic-continuation argument is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0\text{ on an open off-line packet family,}
}
\]

then the same identities would force vanishing in formal/source models where we already have nonzero fixed-sector rows, contradicting the Bottleneck-C obstruction computations.

This argument is promising but not yet formal, because it requires identifying the same analytic family and the same projection conventions.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\text{ is controlled as an analytic set if non-identical-vanishing is proved.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Adversarial countermodel status

The main adversarial possibility is an off-line packet whose contribution lies entirely in the anti-fixed or fibre-complement sector:

\[

\qquad

}

No explicit open-family countermodel is currently available from the prompt history. Therefore:

\[

}
\]

\Longrightarrow

A concrete way to prove it:

2. Exhibit one nondegenerate parameter choice \((\beta,m,s)\) with \(\beta\ne1/2\) where that coefficient is nonzero.
3. Conclude by analyticity that invisibility is a proper incidence set.

## Agent 6 — Coefficient Witness Synthesis / Go-No-Go

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet visibility is conditionally proved at the formal coefficient-witness level.}
}
\]

There is a clean order-7 witness showing the fixed-sector coefficient is **not identically zero** in the off-line packet parameter family, provided the order-7 Bottleneck-C row is accepted as an actual reduced-packet coefficient and the good-patch nondegeneracies \(wI+uS\neq0\), \(q\neq0\), \(Q\neq0\) hold. The remaining gap is no longer “generic visibility”; it is the **realization bridge**: verify that the computed source-moment witness belongs to the actual reduced core packet family, not only the source-perturbative row family. The attached prompt makes this exact witness computation the current bottleneck. 

---

# 1. Order-7 coefficient witness

Use the paired packet source atom

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

Let

\[
\delta=\beta-\frac12,
\qquad
a=\frac12-\delta,
\qquad
b=\frac12+\delta.
\]

At the centered point

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0,
\]

the post-affine source moments are

\[
A_2
=
-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

\[
A_4
=
16(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

Take the concrete off-line value

\[
\delta=\frac14,
\qquad
\beta=\frac34,
\qquad
a=\frac14,
\qquad
b=\frac34.
\]

Then

\[
A_2
=
-4\left(4^3+\left(\frac43\right)^3\right)
=
-\frac{7168}{27}
\neq0,
\]

and

\[
A_4
=
16\left(4^5+\left(\frac43\right)^5\right)
=
\frac{3997696}{243}
\neq0.
\]

Thus the source moments are explicitly nonzero.

---

# 2. Septic coefficient at a clean model point

The expected order-7 scalar coefficient is

\[
\nu
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
\]

Use the clean good-patch normalization

\[
q=1,\qquad q''=0,\qquad Q=1.
\]

Then

\[
\nu
=
\frac1{240}A_2A_4
-
\frac1{216}A_2^2.
\]

Substituting the above values gives

\[
\boxed{
\nu
=
-\frac{1823080448}{98415}
\neq0.
}
\]

So the order-7 fixed-sector row

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]

is nonzero whenever

\[
wI+uS\neq0.
\]

This gives a concrete finite fixed-sector witness at order 7.

---

# 3. Septic locking check

The septic locking condition is

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q''}{18q}.
\]

For the chosen values,

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
-\frac{3904}{63}.
\]

But with

\[
q=1,\qquad q''=0,
\]

the right-hand side is

\[
\frac{10}{9}.
\]

Therefore

\[
-\frac{3904}{63}
\neq
\frac{10}{9}.
\]

So the witness is not on the septic locking hypersurface.

\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ is nonzero at this witness point.}
}
\]

No \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) fallback is needed for this witness.

---

# 4. Analytic non-identity consequence

On a reduced stratum, the finite vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f})
\]

is analytic or meromorphic-analytic in local packet/sample parameters, away from the already-excluded exceptional set.

Since we have exhibited one parameter value with

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
\]

we get:

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\not\equiv0
}
\]

on the connected analytic component containing this witness, provided the witness is an actual reduced off-line packet point.

Therefore

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}
\]

is a proper analytic incidence set on that component.

---

# 5. Remaining adversarial gaps

The nonzero witness is strong, but it is still conditional on four realization assumptions.

## Gap 1 — actual packet realization

We used the packet source moments

\[
A_2=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

This proves non-identity for the source-moment row. To close packet visibility, we still need:

\[
\boxed{
\text{these source moments enter the actual reduced-core }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ coefficient with the displayed constants.}
}
\]

If core absorption changes the coefficient before it becomes \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\), the witness must be recomputed in the fully reduced-core convention.

## Gap 2 — good-patch normalization

The choice

\[
q=1,\qquad q''=0,\qquad Q=1
\]

is a clean local model normalization. It is enough to show non-identity in the formal analytic coefficient family if these values are permitted. If actual zeta packet families impose a constraint forbidding this local jet combination, then the witness is not yet actual.

The weaker but still useful conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the coefficient is not algebraically forced to vanish by the packet source moments alone.}
}
\]

## Gap 3 — full symmetry packet inclusion

The paired atom already includes the \(\beta\) and \(1-\beta\) horizontal partners. But a fully reduced packet may also impose additional conjugation/functional-equation bookkeeping. We still need to verify that adding all partners does not cancel the fixed-sector row.

The prior symmetry-packet analysis suggests this should be packet-internal bookkeeping, not open cancellation, but it must be checked at the coefficient level.

## Gap 4 — fixed-sector vector nondegeneracy

The row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

Even with \(\nu\neq0\), visibility also requires

\[
wI+uS\neq0.
\]

This is a good-patch nondegeneracy condition. If

\[
w=u=0
\]

or the whitening projection degenerates, the point lies in the exceptional set.

---

# 6. Status of the packet visibility theorem

The theorem

\[
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\]

is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{conditionally proved on any reduced off-line packet component containing the above witness.}
}
\]

The exact condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the order-7 row formula is realized by the actual reduced packet coefficients.}
}
\]

If that realization bridge is accepted, then the invisibility locus is proper incidence, and the reduced-base rank-two route can proceed.

If not, the theorem remains open with one missing formula:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ directly in the actual reduced-core convention.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Go / no-go decision

## Go, conditionally

Proceed to the rank-two connection theorem **only if** the following bridge is certified:

\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ contains the computed order-7 source-moment row in the actual reduced-packet model.}
}
\]

Then the next theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ admits a canonical connection }
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).
}
\]

## Hold, if strict proof is required

If the actual reduced-core convention may absorb this row into baseline/reference data, then do **not** proceed yet. Run one more micro-attack:

\[

}
\]

That micro-attack should check core absorption, full symmetry closure, whitening projection, and \(wI+uS\neq0\).

---

# 8. Final decision memo

\[

## Agent 6 — Realization Bridge Synthesis / Final Go-No-Go

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual reduced-core packet visibility remains conditional, not proved.}
}
\]

The order-7 source-moment witness is strong, but the realization bridge is still the unresolved step:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-moment }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{actual reduced-core }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
}
\]

That implication has not yet been derived. The attached instruction correctly narrows the task to this micro-bridge: determine whether the nonzero source-moment row survives when the packet is moved into the canonical reduced core. 

---

# 1. What is already established

The source-moment witness is explicit.

For

\[
\delta=\frac14,\qquad
a=\frac14,\qquad
b=\frac34,
\]

at

\[
x_m=0,
\]

the source moments are

\[
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{3997696}{243}.
\]

With the clean normalization

\[
q=1,\qquad q''=0,\qquad Q=1,
\]

the order-7 scalar coefficient

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\]

is nonzero. Equivalently, the septic locking relation fails:

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
-\frac{3904}{63}
\ne
\frac{10}{9}
=
\frac{10q^2}{9}-\frac{5q''}{18q}.
\]

Thus the source-moment row

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]

is nonzero whenever

\[
wI+uS\ne0.
\]

So the coefficient is not formally or algebraically forced to vanish.

---

# 2. What remains unproved

The reduced-base rank-two architecture puts the packet into

\[
q_{\core},
\]

not into the non-core source object. Therefore the actual coefficient is

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_{\zeta}^{\corr,\core}(s;m).
\]

The required bridge is:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ contains the same }(A_2,A_4)\text{-driven row}
}
\]

possibly plus controlled correction terms that do **not** cancel it identically.

The current state does **not** yet rule out:

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
+
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\]

with

\[
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

by some baseline/core absorption mechanism.

That cancellation seems unlikely, but it has not been excluded by a direct reduced-core derivation.

---

# 3. Agent-by-agent synthesis

## Agent 1 — direct reduced-core \(A_7\)

Needed theorem:

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
+
\text{controlled lower/core terms}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{not yet derived.}
}
\]

This is the principal missing formula.

---

## Agent 2 — core/source comparison

Needed comparison:

\[
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
-
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The key question is whether moving the packet into \(q_{\core}\) merely changes representation or actually absorbs the order-7 witness.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{open; no structural cancellation theorem has been shown.}
}
\]

---

## Agent 3 — full symmetry-packet cancellation

The paired atom already includes the horizontal pair

\[
\beta\leftrightarrow1-\beta.
\]

The remaining concern is whether conjugation / ordinate partners cancel the row in the actual reduced core.

Given that the row is built from even moments like

\[
A_2,\quad A_4,
\]

full-packet cancellation is not expected generically. But it still needs a direct packet-level check.

## Agent 6 — Order-7 Channel Independence Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order-7 channel independence is conditionally proved at the structural level.}
}
\]

The live one-whitening-slot channel

\[
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}
\]

has a nonzero fixed-sector projection

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(\cdots)=-2yBr\,I
\]

under explicit good-patch conditions. The remaining cancellation risk is not generic; it would require a new exact identity forcing the \(K_1\)-transport slice to vanish or to be cancelled by a sector known to be either quotient-line, projected away, or pure odd-germ zero. No such identity is present in the current material. The attached update correctly reframes the task: visibility has a nonzero corrected-whitening channel; the remaining issue is exact cross-channel cancellation. 

---

# 1. Full order-7 convolution structure

The corrected-whitened coefficient is

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\sum_{a+g+b=7}
X_{-,a}N_gX_{+,b}.
\]

The direct raw off-diagonal channel is

\[
X_{-,0}N_7^{\off}X_{+,0}.
\]

At a centered packet,

\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J,
\qquad
X_{-,0}=X_{+,0}=X_0,
\]

so

\[
X_0N_7^{\off}X_0
=
C_7(\det X_0)J.
\]

Since \(J\) is skew,

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_7^{\off}X_0)=0.
\]

So the raw \(N_7\) term is not the witness.

The first live channel is instead

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

Writing

\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\qquad
Y=yJ,
\]

gives

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})=-2yBr\,I.
}
\]

This is the established nonzero channel.

---

# 2. Jet-monomial independence

The channel factors are:

\[
B=
\frac{q''}{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\]

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}),
\]

and

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]

At the centered off-line packet,

\[
q''=2A_2,
\qquad
A_2\ne0.
\]

Thus the live monomial contains

\[
q_0A_2^2q''\,r\,I,
\]

or after using \(q''=2A_2\),

\[
q_0A_2^3r\,I.
\]

The channel can vanish only on the explicit incidence set

\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,\qquad r=0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
y=0,\qquad A_2=0,\qquad g=h.
\]

For the clean off-line witness, none holds. Therefore the live monomial is not zero by packet symmetry, centering, or fixed-sector projection.

Any cancellation by another order-7 summand would need another term with the same fixed-sector \(I\)-direction and the same jet-monomial content. That is not supplied by the raw \(N_7\) skew channel, by pure same-point septic terms, or by the \(K_3\)-shadow sector.

---

# 3. Sector and parity separation

The relevant matrix sectors are

\[
I,\quad S,\quad D,\quad J.
\]

The direct raw channel remains in the \(J\)-sector and is killed:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(J)=0.
\]

The one-whitening-slot channel converts the skew mixed block into fixed sector because

\[
S J=-D,
\qquad
J S=D,
\]

and the commutator-like expression

\[
X_1JX_0-X_0JX_1
\]

has an \(I\)-component when \(X_0\) is anisotropic:

\[
r\ne0.
\]

This is the essential mechanism:

\[
\boxed{
\text{skew mixed block}+\text{odd whitening variation}
\Longrightarrow
\text{fixed-sector }I\text{-component}.
}
\]

So cancellation cannot come from sector-incompatible terms. It can only come from another \(I\)-sector, same-grade, same-monomial term.

---

# 4. Cross-channel cancellation audit

The plausible cancellation sources are:

\[
\text{diagonal }N_7,
\]

\[
X_{-,2}N_5X_{+,0}\ \text{and companions},
\]

\[
X_{-,1}N_5X_{+,1},
\]

\[
\text{normalization shadows},
\]

\[
K_5\text{-line terms},
\]

\[
K_3\text{-shadow terms},
\]

and

\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}.
\]

The septic decomposition described in the attached material is decisive:

\[
A_7
=
A_{7,K_1}
+
A_{7,K_5}
+
A_{7,K_3}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}.
\]

Known reductions:

\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

\[
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad\text{or vanishes after fixed-sector projection},
\]

and

\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad\text{in the odd two-point germ}.
\]

The live one-whitening-slot channel is a \(K_1\)-transport contribution. Therefore the only possible full-vector cancellation would have to cancel the \(K_1\) component itself.

But if the \(K_1\)-component is nonzero in the quotient

\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then no \(K_5\)-line term can cancel it. \(K_3\) and pure sectors are already projected away. Thus cross-channel cancellation would require a new identity inside the \(K_1\)-transport sector, not cancellation by the other septic sectors.

No such identity is present.

---

# 5. \(K_1\)-transport isolation

The live channel belongs to the \(K_1\)-transport slice because it has exactly the structural form:

\[
\text{one same-point whitening slot}
+
\text{quadratic mixed block}.
\]

This is the channel repeatedly isolated by the Bottleneck-C audits.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad
\text{in }
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

If

\[
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]\ne0,
\]

then

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]

as a full rank-two vector.

The live channel gives a nonzero \(I\)-component. If that component were entirely in the \(A_5\)-line, quotient detection could miss it, but the rank-two route does not quotient. Full-vector visibility only requires

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

So even the line case is not fatal for rank-two visibility. It would matter only for quotient-only detection, which has already been abandoned.

---

# 6. Decision on channel independence

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order-7 channel independence: conditionally proved.}
}
\]

The condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the live }K_1\text{ one-whitening-slot channel is not killed by an internal }K_1\text{ identity.}
}
\]

Given the computed nonzero channel

\[
-2yBr\,I,
\]

the only vanishing conditions are explicit incidence conditions:

\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,\qquad g=h.
\]

For the clean centered off-line packet,

\[
A_2\ne0,
\qquad
q''=2A_2\ne0,
\qquad
y_{\rm lead}=-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}\ne0,
\qquad
g\ne h.
\]

Therefore the live channel is nonzero. Cross-sector cancellation by \(K_5,K_3,\mathrm{pure}\) is structurally excluded. Remaining same-\(K_1\) cancellation would be a new analytic identity, not a consequence of the known architecture.

---

# 7. Visibility theorem

On the reduced visibility-positive base

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}
\supset
\{y=0\}\cup\{q''=0\}\cup\{g=h\}
\]

and, for the non-centered route,

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}
\supset
\{q^{(7)}=0\}\cup\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\},
\]

we have

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\ne0.
}
\]

In particular,

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv0
}
\]

on the reduced off-line packet family.

This is enough to move packet visibility from “open” to “closed modulo explicit incidence.”

---

# 8. Remaining caveat

The only caveat is formal: a full printed proof should still include the order-7 convolution table, or cite the septic decomposition proving

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\]

and the nonzero \(K_1\)-slice. Without that table in the paper, this remains a theorem dependency.

But mathematically, based on the provided derivations, the obstruction is now narrowed to a standard analytic-incidence exclusion.

---

The next theorem is no longer packet visibility. It is the affine forcing equation:

=
E_{\eta\eta}
+

}

as a tensorial equation on

\[

\]

This theorem must identify \(E_{\eta\eta}\) as the symmetric source-Hessian / affine forcing term in the rank-two connection language, with \(E_{\rm lower}\) consisting only of Gate A/Gate B/connection-correction terms already controlled locally.

## Final go/no-go

\[

Packet visibility is now sufficiently certified for the rank-two route, provided the explicit incidence set includes the channel-vanishing walls and the final write-up records the \(K_1\)-transport isolation.

---

# 1. Connection theorem status

On

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\]

the fixed core is stable, packet visibility is positive, and arbitrary source/core transfers are excluded. The rank-two fixed-sector bundle is

\[

\qquad

\]

The proposed connection is

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\bigl(d_X^{\mathcal J}A\bigr).
}
\]

This is conditionally valid under the standing atlas assumptions:

\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik},
\]

and functoriality of the ambient projection:

\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}
=
T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}.
\]

In a local frame

\[
E=(I,S),
\qquad
A=Ea,
\]

the connection has the form

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A
=

\]

If

\[

\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
=
W^{-1}\Gamma^{\rm raw}W+W^{-1}dW.
}
\]

So the connection theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{conditionally established on }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
}
\]

The condition is that the reduced-base frame/projection functoriality is accepted.

is precisely what should absorb frame, whitening-gauge, and projection-gauge variation. After this absorption, the remaining non-gauge part should split as

Thus the affine forcing equation is not an optional interpretation. It is the covariant form of the old Bottleneck-C variation after moving from scalar \(T\)-flatness to rank-two fixed-sector transport.

It is not an antisymmetric curvature two-form. It is the tensorial remnant of the \(\eta_i\eta_j\) second-source Hessian, now interpreted as an inhomogeneous forcing term in rank-two transport.

E_{\rm bg/core}
=
\text{fixed analytic baseline terms on }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
}
\]

A complete row table should list each row by:

\[
\text{row label},
\quad
\text{source},
\quad
\text{sector},
\quad
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\text{-output},
\quad
\text{classification},
\quad
\text{controlled?}
\]

This table is still the missing written artifact.

---

# 3. Gate A/B closure

Gate A and Gate B remain valid on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\) only as **fixed-convention local algebraic lemmas**.

On this base:

\[
\text{fixed source/core convention},
\]

\[
\text{stable source labels},
\]

\[
\text{stable endpoint orientation},
\]

\[
\text{same finite-core patch},
\]

\[
\text{no source/core transition}.
\]

Therefore the hypotheses needed for Gate A/B are preserved.

Thus the expected closure is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm GateA}=0,
\qquad
E_{\rm GateB}=0
}
\]

under the already accepted Gate A/B assumptions.

Caveat: if any Gate B row depends on a source-grade reflection or mixed-block swap that was proved only in a narrower centered setting, it must be restated on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\). No such failure is currently identified.

---

# 4. Septic sector decomposition

The order-7 decomposition is:

\[
A_7
=
A_{7,K_1}
+
A_{7,K_5}
+
A_{7,K_3}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}.
\]

The live visibility and forcing channel belongs to the \(K_1\)-transport sector.

The lower sectors behave as follows:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

These are line/normalization-shadow terms.

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0
}
\]

after fixed-sector projection, or belongs to a projected-away shadow sector.

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
}
\]

in the odd two-point germ.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad
\text{mod } \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

This supports the conclusion that no \(K_5/K_3/\mathrm{pure}\) sector cancels the \(K_1\) source-Hessian forcing in quotient. In full rank-two space, \(K_5\)-line terms remain part of the transported vector but are not scalar defects.

---

# 5. Connection-correction absorption

The connection was chosen precisely so that frame, whitening, and projection gauge variation are not misclassified as physical forcing.

If

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=Ea_7,
\qquad
E=(I,S),
\]

then

\[
\partial_\kappa(Ea_7)
=
E\,\partial_\kappa a_7
+
(\partial_\kappa E)a_7.
\]

The second term is absorbed by

\[
E\Gamma_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}a_7.
\]

If

\[
E=E^{\rm raw}W,
\]

then

\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
=
W^{-1}\Gamma^{\rm raw}W
+
W^{-1}dW.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm conn}=0
}
\]

after passing from ordinary derivative to

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Potential issue: if \(\partial_\kappa\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\) produces a genuine tensorial term not absorbed by the connection, it must be listed separately. Under the functorial projection hypothesis, it is absorbed into \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\).

---

# 6. Line and background terms

## Line terms

Terms in

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

are not invisible in the rank-two architecture. They are transported as part of the vector. They are acceptable as part of \(E_{\rm lower}\) provided they are known/controlled analytic line forcing terms.

They cannot cancel the quotient-nonzero \(K_1\)-transport component. In full rank-two space, line terms can affect \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\), but they do not reintroduce the old scalar \(T\)-flatness obstruction. They become part of the affine forcing vector.

So:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm line}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ is acceptable for rank-two transport.}
}
\]

## Background/core baseline terms

These are fixed analytic baseline data on

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\]

because source/core convention is frozen.

They are not functorial source/core transition defects. They should be included in the total affine forcing:

\[
E=
E_{\eta\eta}
+
E_{\rm lower}.
\]

They are acceptable if they are explicitly known analytic functions. They become part of the later global transport integral.

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm bg/core}
\text{ is acceptable as fixed analytic forcing, not a local obstruction.}
}
\]

## Agent 6 — Global Affine Transport Synthesis / Route Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{global affine transport route: conditional, with transported finite-core non-concentration as the least-bad next target.}
}
\]

The local rank-two equation

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]

is now coherent, but it does not yet produce a global contradiction. The natural path, holonomy, exactness, and projective-index routes all remain underdetermined. The only route that still interfaces with the existing proof machinery is a **transported finite-core non-concentration theorem**. The attached prompt correctly frames this as the first global step after local affine forcing. 

---

# 1. Candidate global routes

## 1.1 Path / boundary route

The affine transport formula is

\[
A(b)
=
U_{a\to b}A(a)
+
\int_a^b U_{t\to b}
(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower})(t)\,dt.
\]

A path/boundary proof would require a canonical path

\[
\Gamma:a\to b
\]

and known endpoint data such as

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a)=0,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)=0,
\]

or some prescribed relation between them.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No canonical endpoint conditions are known.}
}
\]

Midpoint intervals, \(\kappa\)-paths, and finite-core parameter paths are locally natural, but none yet carries a boundary theorem strong enough to constrain the affine displacement. So this route is not ready.

---

## 1.2 Affine holonomy / loop route

A loop route would use

\[
\operatorname{AffHol}_\Gamma
=
\left(
U_\Gamma,
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower})(t)\,dt
\right).
\]

This would be useful if there were a canonical loop around a zero-packet, core-boundary wall, Gram wall, or visibility incidence wall.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No canonical loop with a zeta-imposed affine holonomy constraint is known.}
}
\]

There are plausible loops around incidence walls, but without a theorem saying the affine holonomy is zero, integral, quantized, or forced by the functional equation, this is diagnostic only.

---

## 1.3 Exactness / path-independence route

A strong positive result would be

\[
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
=
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\Psi.
\]

Then the affine displacement would be endpoint-controlled.

But earlier scalar exactness attempts already failed, and rank-two covariantization does not automatically remove the bulk term. In current notation, the forcing still contains the same non-exact source-Hessian structure that originally produced

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no covariant exactness theorem is available.}
}
\]

So path-independence is not the next route unless a new potential \(\Psi\) is explicitly found.

---

## 1.4 Projective / Maslov / spectral-flow route

A projective route would study

\[
b\mapsto [A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)]\in \mathbf P(\mathcal F_b)
\]

or

\[
d\log \omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

This may detect crossings, winding, or Maslov-type indices.

The weakness is unchanged from the quotient phase: projective data can miss scale/line information. A pure line anomaly can be projectively invisible unless paired with a scale/energy invariant.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective index is useful as a diagnostic, but incomplete as the primary gate.}
}
\]

It may become a derived invariant after finite-core transport is understood.

---

## 1.5 Transported finite-core non-concentration route

This route keeps the existing finite-core proof skeleton but upgrades the finite vector to include transport data:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots).
\]

Since

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
\]

the forcing gives additional information beyond the static finite-core vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots).
\]

The possible theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
}
\]

This is still hard, but it is the only candidate that directly reuses:

\[
\text{Gate A/B},
\quad
\text{packet visibility},
\quad
\text{rank-two transport},
\quad
\text{finite-core machinery}.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{best next target, but still conditional.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Hard kill criteria

The rank-two global route fails if any of the following occur.

## Kill 1 — no canonical path or finite-core sampling path

If no canonical local parameter path or sampled finite-core path can be associated to the RH-relevant packet, affine transport has no global object to constrain.

## Kill 2 — no endpoint or incidence control

If the transported vector can always absorb the forcing by arbitrary endpoint data, then the affine equation is descriptive, not contradictory.

## Kill 3 — forcing not exact and no replacement lower bound

Exactness is not required if transported non-concentration works. But if forcing is non-exact and no lower bound theorem uses it, the route stalls.

## Kill 4 — transported finite-core aligned branch survives unchanged

If one can still arrange

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\]

outside incidence, then the transport upgrade does not improve the old finite-core obstruction.

## Kill 5 — projective index misses scale data

If the route falls back to projective winding alone, pure scale/line anomalies may remain invisible.

---

# 3. Recommended next theorem

The next theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Transported Finite-Core Non-Concentration Theorem.}
}
\]

Define

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots)
\]

or the minimal version

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots).
\]

Then prove or refute:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
}
\]

More specifically, test whether adding the derivative/forcing component kills the old aligned branch:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}.
\]

## Agent 6 — Global Affine Transport Synthesis / Route Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global affine transport remains the right next architecture, but no proof gate is closed yet.}
}
\]

The local rank-two machinery is now coherent: packet visibility is closed modulo explicit incidence; the rank-two connection is conditionally available on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\); and the Bottleneck-C row has been reinterpreted as tensorial affine forcing. But the attached Agent 5 results show that **none** of the obvious global replacements—quotient scalar, split readout, energy, projective index, transported finite-core, or affine torsor—currently closes the proof. The next target should be a **canonical affine path/boundary theorem**, with vector-valued differential non-concentration as the backup route. 

---

# 1. Current local equation

We are now working with

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
}
\]

The forcing row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in \Gamma(\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}),
\]

and it is no longer treated as a scalar \(T\)-flatness defect. It is an inhomogeneous rank-two forcing section.

The transport formula is

\[
A(b)
=
U_{a\to b}A(a)
+
\int_a^b U_{t\to b}
\left(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\right)(t)\,dt.
\]

So the remaining question is global:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the affine displacement be constrained?}
}
\]

---

# 2. Route assessment

## 2.1 Quotient scalar route

The quotient scalar

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h\!\left(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right)
\]

is analytically coherent. Its coefficients are

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

It preserves holomorphy, odd sampling, and quotient determinacy.

But it loses line anomalies:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
D_{2r+1}=0.
\]

Those same line anomalies can be \(T\)- and \(\Phi_K\)-visible. Therefore quotient scalarization cannot replace the old \(H_m=\Phi_K(\cdots)\) pipeline unless one proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH-relevant anomalies cannot be pure }A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{-line anomalies.}
}
\]

That theorem is missing.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Decision: do not return to pure quotient as the main route.}
}
\]

---

## 2.2 Split readout route

The split vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots)
\]

is complete on a good patch. It repairs the quotient lost-\(T\) problem.

But completeness brings back the full fixed-sector difficulty. Split non-concentration is essentially full-vector non-concentration in better coordinates, and the \(dd\)-interaction feature/spectral obstructions survive:

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\]

still gives feature-balance failure, and the unit-curve spectral obstruction still has

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac1{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Decision: split is diagnostic/coordinate-complete, but not a proof gate.}
}
\]

---

## 2.3 Energy / positivity route

Natural energies such as

\[
\mathcal E_7
=
\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2
\]

detect the bad row. But their first variation is sign-indefinite:

\[
\delta\mathcal E_7
=
2\operatorname{Re}
\langle A_7^{\mathfrak f},E_{\eta\eta}\rangle_{\wh},
\]

and second variation is only tautologically positive:

\[
\delta^2\mathcal E_7
=
2\|E_{\eta\eta}\|_{\wh}^2\ge0.
\]

No global theorem forces the energy to vanish, be monotone, or satisfy endpoint constraints.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Decision: energy is descriptive, not proof-closing.}
}
\]

---

## 2.4 Projective / Maslov / spectral-flow route

Projective data

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in \mathbf P(\mathcal F)
\]

and determinants

\[
\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\]

are useful for incidence/crossing diagnostics. But projective data miss scale and pure line anomalies unless paired with norm/scale information. Once that scale is restored, the route is just split/full-vector transport again.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Decision: projective index may be derived later, but cannot be primary.}
}
\]

---

## 2.5 Transported finite-core route

Adding transport data gives something like

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},\nabla A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots).
\]

This is coherent, but the old aligned branch survives:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\approx
-P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

Transport adds coordinates; it does not by itself impose sign, convexity, monotonicity, or incidence containment. The \(dd\)-interaction feature and spectral-cone countermodels also survive in transported variables.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Decision: transported finite-core is the best finite-core formulation, but not yet a theorem.}
}
\]

It should be pursued **after** path/boundary structure is clarified, or in parallel only as a secondary route.

---

## 2.6 Affine torsor route

If source/core transitions are allowed, the natural transition is likely affine:

\[
A_j^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_i^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{ij}.
\]

That suggests a rank-two affine torsor rather than a vector bundle.

But the affine cocycle

\[
B_{ik}
=
G_{jk}^{-1}B_{ij}+B_{jk}
\]

is unproved. Therefore source/core transitions remain object-changing unless the affine cocycle theorem is established.

Since the current route already restricts to fixed source/core convention on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), the torsor route should not be the main immediate target.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Decision: torsor is fallback only if fixed-convention base becomes insufficient.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Main decision

The current proof family should proceed with:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Affine Path / Boundary Theorem.}
}
\]

The target is to find a canonical path, interval, or loop

\[
\Gamma\subset \mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\]

such that the affine displacement

\[
\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}
=
\int_\Gamma
U_{t\to b}
\left(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\right)(t)\,dt
\]

is constrained by boundary, holonomy, index, or zeta symmetry.

The minimal useful theorem would be one of:

\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)-U_{a\to b}A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a)
\text{ is known or constrained;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{AffHol}_\Gamma
\text{ is prescribed on a canonical loop;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}
\text{ is nonzero for off-line packets but globally forced to vanish;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{transported finite-core non-concentration follows from path control.}
}
\]

Without one of these, the local affine equation is only descriptive.

Run a **Canonical Affine Path / Boundary Wave**.

```latex
\subsection{Rank-two fixed-sector remaining language}
\subsection{The \(\eta\eta\) row as rank-two affine forcing}
\subsection{Global affine transport dependency}
```

The edits below fill the main remaining gaps: the **last-chance pointwise-flatness \(Q=b+G\) no-go**, the **ODE/pole principal-part no-go**, the **order-7 packet visibility/K\(_1\) one-whitening-slot positive result**, the **reduced visibility-positive base**, the **\(E_{\rm lower}\) closure ledger**, and the **global affine-transport decision**. These are exactly the structural results reflected in the latest agent outputs: packet visibility is now closed modulo explicit incidence walls via the \(K_1\)/one-whitening-slot mechanism, while the global proof gate remains open and likely must be an affine transport/path-boundary theorem.

## Edit 1 — Add a last-chance pointwise-flatness subsection

**Where:** In `proof_of_rh(479).tex`, insert this **after**:

```latex
\end{remark}
```

ending the subsection:

```latex
\subsection{Meromorphic residue no-go for the rebuilt obstruction}
\label{subsec:meromorphic-residue-no-go-rebuilt-obstruction}
```

and **before**:

```latex
\subsection{Connection-defect interpretation and possible architecture pivot}
\label{subsec:connection-defect-interpretation-bc}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Last-chance pointwise flatness in full phase variables}
\label{subsec:last-chance-pointwise-flatness-full-phase-variables}

The preceding exactness and residue checks rule out the most natural local
conservation-law interpretations of
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}.
\]
There remains one final possible escape: perhaps the full phase derivative
itself, together with the exact decomposition into rebuilt baseline and full
non-core complement, forces the required identity.  This subsection records
that this is not a formal consequence of the decomposition.

Write
\[
Q(t):=q(t)
\]
for the full phase derivative, and decompose
\[
Q(t)=b(t)+G(t),
\]
where
\[
b(t):=q_{\base}^{\new}(t)=q_{\core}(t)+B_{\bg}(t)+E_{\est,R}(t),
\]
and
\[
G(t):=G^{\new}(t)=q_{\aux,R}(t)+T_{\far,R}(t).
\]
At the midpoint \(m\), put
\[
b_0:=b(m),\qquad b_2:=b''(m),
\]
and
\[
A_2:=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4:=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]
Then
\[
A_2=\frac{Q''(m)-b''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{Q^{(4)}(m)-b^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The rebuilt flatness condition is
\[
\frac{b_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{b_2}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=0.
\]
Substituting the full decomposition gives
\[
\frac{b_0}{11520}
\bigl(Q''-b''\bigr)
\bigl(Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}\bigr)
+
\frac{1}{576}
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
\bigl(Q''-b''\bigr)^2
=0,
\]
with all derivatives evaluated at \(m\).  Equivalently, if
\[
D_2:=Q''-b''=G'',
\qquad
D_4:=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}=G^{(4)},
\]
then the condition is
\[
D_2
\left[
b_0D_4
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
D_2
\right]
=0.
\]

\begin{proposition}[The rebuilt flatness equation is an extra fourth-order constraint]
\label{prop:rebuilt-flatness-extra-fourth-order-constraint}
The identity
\[
Q=b+G
\]
does not imply
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]
On a good patch with \(G''(m)\ne0\), pointwise flatness is equivalent to the
additional derivative-ratio constraint
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{G''(m)}
=
\frac{40b(m)^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b(m)}.
\]
Equivalently, as an equation for the baseline jet,
\[
b^{(4)}(m)
=
Q^{(4)}(m)
-
\left(
\frac{40b(m)^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b(m)}
\right)
\bigl(Q''(m)-b''(m)\bigr).
\]
Thus the desired flatness is not a consequence of the tautological full-phase
decomposition.  It is an extra nonlinear fourth-order pointwise condition on
the selected baseline/source split.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The displayed factorization shows that, if \(D_2=G''(m)\ne0\), the vanishing
condition is precisely
\[
b_0D_4
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
D_2
=0.
\]
Dividing by \(b_0D_2\) gives
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{G''(m)}
=
\frac{40b_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b_0}.
\]
The equivalent formula for \(b^{(4)}\) follows from
\[
G^{(4)}=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}.
\]
The decomposition \(Q=b+G\) supplies only the two identities
\[
G''=Q''-b'',
\qquad
G^{(4)}=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}.
\]
It supplies no relation fixing \(G^{(4)}/G''\) in terms of \(b,b''\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why defining the baseline by flatness is circular]
\label{rem:baseline-by-flatness-is-circular}
One could formally choose \(b\) by requiring the fourth-order equation in
Proposition~\ref{prop:rebuilt-flatness-extra-fourth-order-constraint}.  Such a
choice would kill the Bottleneck-C row by definition.  It is not a proof
unless an independent zeta-side principle selects exactly this baseline, for
example through the functional equation, a canonical scattering law, a
zero-counting conservation principle, or a functorial fixed-core construction.
No such principle is currently present.  A core or window choice that forces
\(G''=0\), or forces the ratio \(G^{(4)}/G''\), is therefore a
Bottleneck-C-tuned source convention unless it is justified independently.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Asymptotic scale is not enough]
\label{rem:asymptotic-scale-not-enough-for-flatness}
If \(b\) is dominated by the smooth phase/background, one expects roughly
\(b(t)\sim \frac12\log(t/2\pi)\).  Then the required ratio is on the scale
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
\sim
\frac{40}{3}b^2
\asymp
\log^2 t.
\]
A non-core zero complement with pole distances of order \(1/\log t\) can have
the same dimensional scale.  This is not enough: the identity requires the
exact constant and sign
\[
\frac{40b^2}{3}-\frac{10b''}{3b}
\]
pointwise.  Local one-pair and finite-tail tests show that source geometry can
produce different fourth-to-second derivative ratios.  Thus a proof of
flatness would have to be a genuinely new global zero-complement rigidity
theorem.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 2 — Add the meromorphic ODE/principal-part no-go

**Where:** Immediately after **Edit 1**, still before:

```latex
\subsection{Connection-defect interpretation and possible architecture pivot}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Meromorphic ODE principal-part no-go}
\label{subsec:meromorphic-ode-principal-part-no-go}

A related failed repair is to seek a meromorphic differential equation for the
source complement or for the full phase derivative.  The local flatness
condition would be implied by an equation of the form
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q},
\]
or by the same equation with \(G=q\).  This is incompatible with the principal
parts of the actual zero-pair pole fields.

Let
\[
H(t)=\frac{C}{t-p}+O(1)
\]
have a simple pole.  Then
\[
H''(t)=\frac{2C}{(t-p)^3}+O(1),
\qquad
H^{(4)}(t)=\frac{24C}{(t-p)^5}+O(1),
\]
so
\[
\frac{H^{(4)}}{H''}
=
\frac{12}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]

On the other hand, if the full phase derivative has
\[
q(t)=\frac{R}{t-p}+O(1),
\]
then
\[
q^2(t)=\frac{R^2}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right),
\qquad
\frac{q''}{q}
=
\frac{2}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]
Hence
\[
\frac{40q^2}{3}-\frac{10q''}{3q}
=
\left(
\frac{40R^2}{3}
-
\frac{20}{3}
\right)
\frac1{(t-p)^2}
+
O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]
Matching the left-hand double-pole coefficient \(12\) would require
\[
R^2=\frac75.
\]

\begin{proposition}[Zero-pair residues rule out the meromorphic ODE repair]
\label{prop:zero-pair-residues-rule-out-meromorphic-ode}
The flatness-forcing ODE
\[
\frac{H^{(4)}}{H''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
\]
cannot hold as a meromorphic identity for the raw non-core zero source, for the
full phase derivative, or for any complement retaining the zero-pair poles.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For a zero-pair summand
\[
f_a(t)=\frac{a}{a^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]
the upper and lower poles are
\[
p_a^\pm=\frac{\gamma\pm ia}{2},
\]
with residues
\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^+} f_a=-\frac{i}{4},
\qquad
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^-} f_a=\frac{i}{4}.
\]
Thus the phase-pole residues are purely imaginary, and for a simple pole
\(R=\pm i/4\).  Hence \(R^2=-1/16\), not \(7/5\).  If several same-sign pole
contributions coincide, then \(R=\pm ni/4\), so \(R^2<0\) remains impossible.
Therefore the principal double-pole coefficient of the right-hand side cannot
match the coefficient \(12\) of \(H^{(4)}/H''\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Pole-cancelled complements are the wrong object]
\label{rem:pole-cancelled-complements-wrong-object}
A complement such as \(q-G\) may cancel an exterior pole and thereby evade the
principal-part contradiction at that pole.  But the Bottleneck-C coefficient is
built from the source moments
\[
A_2=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]
An ODE for a pole-cancelled complement is therefore an ODE for the wrong
object, unless the entire order-seven source-row calculation is rederived with
different moments.
\end{remark}
```

This fills an explicit no-go not currently visible in the draft. It matters because the rank-two pivot should not be read as “we forgot to try a meromorphic ODE”; that ODE was ruled out by residue constants in the agent work.

---

## Edit 3 — Add a precise packet-visibility / \(K_1\) one-whitening-slot subsection

The draft already has a “rank-two remaining language” subsection, but the latest work sharpened packet visibility substantially. The direct raw \(N_7\) channel is **not** the witness; the \(K_1\) one-whitening-slot channel is. The latest updates explicitly say packet visibility is now closed modulo incidence walls through this channel. 

**Where:** Insert this **immediately before**:

```latex
\subsection{Rank-two fixed-sector remaining language}
\label{subsec:rank-two-fixed-sector-remaining-language}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Reduced-core packet visibility through the \(K_1\) one-whitening-slot channel}
\label{subsec:reduced-core-packet-visibility-k1-one-whitening}

The rank-two route must have actual RH-detection reach: an off-line packet
must give nonzero fixed-sector odd data on the reduced base.  The first naive
reduced-core witness is misleading.  At a centered even packet, the raw
off-diagonal order-seven numerator has the form
\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J,
\qquad
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
-1&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Since the leading endpoint whitenings agree,
\[
X_{-,0}=X_{+,0}=X_0,
\]
one has
\[
X_0N_7^{\off}X_0
=
C_7(\det X_0)J,
\]
which remains skew.  Therefore
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_7^{\off}X_0)=0.
\]
Thus the raw lower-left \(s^7\)-coefficient is not itself a fixed-sector
visibility witness.

The live centered channel is instead the one-whitening-slot term
\[
T_7^{(1)}
:=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\]
where the quadratic mixed block is skew,
\[
Y=yJ.
\]
At centered parity,
\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]
Write
\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\]
where
\[
D=
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&-1
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_0-X_0YX_{-,1}.
\]
Using
\[
SJ=-D,
\qquad
JS=D,
\]
one obtains
\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yB(pD+rI).
\]
Consequently
\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})
=
-2yBr\,I.
}
\]

\begin{lemma}[First whitening coefficient at a centered packet]
\label{lem:first-whitening-coefficient-centered-packet}
Let the same-point Gram block at the centered packet be
\[
G_0=
\begin{pmatrix}
g&0\\
0&h
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
g,h>0,
\]
and put
\[
X_0=G_0^{-1/2}=pI+rD,
\qquad
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]
For the phase-kernel value/first-jet Gram block
\[
G(t)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q(t) & \frac12 q'(t)\\
\frac12 q'(t) & \frac13 q(t)^3+\frac16q''(t)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
the centered even packet has \(q'(m)=q'''(m)=0\), and
\[
G_{-,1}
=
-\frac{q''(m)}{4\pi}S.
\]
Therefore
\[
X_{-,1}=D(G_0^{-1/2})[G_{-,1}]
=
B S,
\]
where
\[
B=
\frac{q''(m)}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}
\]
up to the harmless sign convention of the first-jet basis.  In particular,
\[
X_{-,1}\ne0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''(m)\ne0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Since \(t_-=m-s/2\),
\[
G_{-,1}=-\frac12G'(m).
\]
At a centered even packet,
\[
G'(m)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
0&\frac12q''(m)\\
\frac12q''(m)&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Hence
\[
G_{-,1}
=
-\frac{q''(m)}{4\pi}S.
\]
For \(f(x)=x^{-1/2}\), the off-diagonal divided difference at
\(\operatorname{diag}(g,h)\) is
\[
\frac{g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}}{g-h}
=
-\frac{1}{\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}.
\]
Substitution gives the displayed formula for \(B\), with the sign depending
only on the convention for the oriented first-jet basis.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Nonvanishing of the quadratic mixed-block coefficient]
\label{lem:nonvanishing-quadratic-mixed-block-coefficient}
Let a centered off-line packet have post-affine leading even source jet
\[
r(u)=A_2u^2+O(u^4),
\qquad
A_2\ne0.
\]
Then its phase-gap variation satisfies
\[
\delta\Delta(s)=\frac{A_2}{12}s^3+O(s^5).
\]
The pure second-\(\Delta\)-Hessian quadratic mixed-block coefficient has
leading scalar
\[
y_{\lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]
In particular, on a good patch with \(q_0\ne0\),
\[
y_{\lead}\ne0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For
\[
N_{12}
=
\frac{\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\qquad
N_{21}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\]
the second \(\Delta\)-Hessian at centered parity is skew:
\[
D_\Delta^2N
=
-\frac{F}{s^2}J,
\qquad
F=\sin\Delta+q_s s\cos\Delta.
\]
Since
\[
\Delta=q_0s+O(s^3),
\qquad
F=2q_0s+O(s^3),
\]
and
\[
\delta\Delta(s)=\frac{A_2}{12}s^3+O(s^5),
\]
the quadratic channel has leading scalar
\[
-\frac{2q_0}{s}\left(\frac{A_2}{12}s^3\right)^2
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}s^5.
\]
This is the displayed coefficient, up to the common order bookkeeping
normalization used in the \(K_1\)-transport table.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Centered \(K_1\) one-whitening-slot visibility]
\label{prop:centered-k1-one-whitening-slot-visibility}
At a centered reduced-core off-line packet, the one-whitening-slot
\(K_1\)-transport channel has fixed-sector projection
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]
It is nonzero outside the explicit incidence walls
\[
y=0,
\qquad
q''(m)=0,
\qquad
g=h.
\]
For the packet source
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\qquad
a=\frac12-\delta,\quad b=\frac12+\delta,
\]
at \(x_m=2m-\gamma=0\) one has
\[
A_2=-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]
so \(q''(m)=2A_2\ne0\) whenever \(0<|\delta|<1/2\).  Thus centered packet
visibility holds on the generic centered patch modulo the displayed incidence
walls.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The formula for \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})\) follows from the computation
above.  The three factors are \(y\), \(B\), and \(r\).  By
Lemma~\ref{lem:first-whitening-coefficient-centered-packet}, \(B=0\) exactly
when \(q''(m)=0\).  By definition \(r=0\) exactly when \(g=h\).  By
Lemma~\ref{lem:nonvanishing-quadratic-mixed-block-coefficient}, \(y\ne0\) on a
good off-line packet with \(q_0A_2\ne0\).  The explicit packet formula gives
\(A_2\ne0\) for \(0<|\delta|<1/2\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the direct raw term was not the witness]
\label{rem:direct-raw-n7-not-visibility-witness}
The nonzero raw lower-left \(s^7\)-coefficient is real information, but at
centered parity it occurs in a skew matrix \(C_7J\).  Leading whitening
preserves the skew sector, so fixed-sector projection kills it.  The
visibility mechanism is subtler: an odd endpoint whitening variation converts
the skew quadratic mixed block into a fixed-sector \(I\)-component.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Order-seven channel independence modulo explicit incidence]
\label{prop:order-seven-channel-independence-mod-incidence}
The one-whitening-slot channel of
Proposition~\ref{prop:centered-k1-one-whitening-slot-visibility} belongs to
the septic \(K_1\)-transport sector.  The order-seven decomposition has the
form
\[
A_7
=
A_{7,K_1}
+
A_{7,K_5}
+
A_{7,K_3}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}},
\]
with
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\]
after fixed-sector projection, and
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\]
in the odd two-point germ.  Hence
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad
\text{in }
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
In particular, if
\[
\omega_h(A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})\ne0,
\]
then
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]
For the centered one-whitening-slot channel this quotient nonvanishing is
\[
-2yBr\,v_5\ne0.
\]
Thus \(K_5\)-line, \(K_3\)-shadow, and pure same-point sectors cannot cancel
the live \(K_1\)-visibility channel outside the incidence set
\[
\{y=0\}\cup\{q''=0\}\cup\{g=h\}\cup\{v_5=0\}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Non-centered \(q^{(7)}\) visibility route]
\label{rem:noncentered-q7-visibility-route}
The centered route above is not the only order-seven visibility mechanism.
The finite-\(s\) construction uses a free sampling midpoint
\[
t_\pm=m\pm\frac{s}{2}.
\]
It does not force \(m\) to be the ordinate center of a zero packet.  For the
same packet,
\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3),
\qquad
x_m=2m-\gamma.
\]
Thus \(x_m=0\) is a simple zero of the \(q^{(7)}\)-channel, and every
sufficiently small nonzero midpoint perturbation activates it.  The direct
septic \(K_1\)-transport slice then gives an actual reduced-core order-seven
visibility channel outside
\[
\{x_m=0\}\cup\{q^{(7)}=0\}\cup\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}.
\]
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Visibility-positive reduced base]
\label{def:visibility-positive-reduced-base}
Define
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
:=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7},
\]
where, for the centered one-whitening-slot route, the exceptional set includes
\[
\{y=0\}\cup\{q''=0\}\cup\{g=h\}\cup\{v_5=0\},
\]
and, for the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\)-route, includes
\[
\{x_m=0\}\cup\{q^{(7)}=0\}\cup\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}.
\]
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\) the finite fixed-sector vector
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots)
\]
is nonzero for the reduced off-line packet family, modulo the stated
incidence exclusions and the order-seven channel-independence assumption.
\end{definition}
```

## Edit 4 — Strengthen the rank-two connection subsection with the reduced-base caveat

**Where:** In:

```latex
\subsection{Rank-two fixed-sector remaining language}
\label{subsec:rank-two-fixed-sector-remaining-language}
```

find the paragraph beginning:

```latex
The best remaining local language is the full rank-two fixed-sector
object.
```

After the first paragraph defining the rank-two object, insert:

```latex
The rank-two language is only meaningful on a fixed-convention reduced base.
Source/core transfers are not currently known to be functorial \(GL_2\)
changes of coordinates.  Moving a zero atom into or out of the core may change
the corrected local object by an additive fixed-sector term rather than by a
linear frame transition.  Thus the present rank-two bundle is to be understood
over \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), where the core rule, source convention,
endpoint orientation, raw jet frame, and whitening branch are fixed and stable.
If source/core changes must be compared, the correct fallback object is likely
a rank-two affine torsor with transitions
\[
A_j^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_i^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{ij},
\]
and one would need the affine cocycle
\[
B_{ik}=G_{jk}^{-1}B_{ij}+B_{jk}.
\]
No such source/core affine cocycle theorem is currently proved.
```

This captures the source/core functoriality issue that the current draft only partially covers.
