## Edit 5 — Add an \(E_{\rm lower}\) row-table dependency as a theorem-like lemma

**Where:** In:

```latex
\subsection{The \(\eta\eta\) row as rank-two affine forcing}
\label{subsec:etaeta-row-rank-two-affine-forcing}
```

after the paragraph ending:

```latex
The remaining table dependency is to verify that no additional uncontrolled
same-grade \(K_1\) source-Hessian companion survives outside the already
identified \(E_{\eta\eta}\) row.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{definition}[Lower-row closure table]
\label{def:lower-row-closure-table}
In the rank-two affine equation
\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
\]
write the lower remainder as
\[
E_{\rm lower}
=
E_{\rm GateA/B}
+
E_{\rm conn}
+
E_{\rm line}
+
E_{\rm shadow}
+
E_{\rm bg/core}.
\]
Here
\[
E_{\rm GateA/B}=E_{\rm GateA}+E_{\rm GateB}
\]
collects rows closed by Gate~A and Gate~B under the fixed-convention
hypotheses;
\[
E_{\rm conn}
\]
collects frame, whitening, and projection derivative terms absorbed by the
covariant derivative \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\);
\[
E_{\rm line}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
collects \(K_5\)-line and normalization-shadow terms;
\[
E_{\rm shadow}
\]
collects \(K_3\)-shadow and pure same-point septic rows killed by
\(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\) or by odd two-point parity; and
\[
E_{\rm bg/core}
\]
collects fixed analytic background and core-baseline forcing on
\(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\).
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Conditional local closure of \(E_{\rm lower}\)]
\label{prop:conditional-local-closure-e-lower}
Assume the reduced-base atlas is fixed, the projection \(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\)
is functorial, Gate~A and Gate~B hold in the fixed source convention, and the
septic decomposition has no additional uncontrolled \(K_1\)-source-Hessian
companion besides \(E_{\eta\eta}\).  Then \(E_{\rm lower}\) is locally
controlled in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:lower-row-closure-table}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Gate~A and Gate~B close their assigned rows by the accepted local algebraic
hypotheses.  Frame, whitening, and projection derivatives are absorbed by
\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A=\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A),
\]
so they contribute no separate physical row after covariantization.  The
\(K_3\)-shadow sector is projected away, and pure same-point septic terms
vanish in the odd two-point germ.  The \(K_5\)-sector lies in
\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
so it is a transported line component rather than a scalar Bottleneck-C
defect.  Finally, on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), the background and core
convention is fixed, so \(E_{\rm bg/core}\) is fixed analytic forcing.  The
only excluded possibility is a further same-grade \(K_1\)-source-Hessian row
not equivalent to \(E_{\eta\eta}\), which is exactly the stated hypothesis.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Line terms are transported, not discarded]
\label{rem:line-terms-transported-not-discarded}
Unlike the quotient-only architecture, the rank-two architecture does not
discard
\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Thus \(E_{\rm line}\) is not invisible.  It is part of the transported
rank-two vector.  It cannot cancel a quotient-nonzero \(K_1\)-component, and
if it aligns with the \(K_1\)-forcing in full vector space, that alignment is
a separate analytic incidence condition rather than a scalar closure theorem.
\end{remark}
```

This makes the local affine equation more self-contained and records the “local close modulo row-table” status.

C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=

J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}

\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\left\|
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))
\right\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q),

\left\|
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))
\right\|_\infty.

rank-two affine-transport architecture.

## Edit 2 — Add the missing full-phase \(Q=b+G\) flatness no-go

**Where:** Insert immediately after:

```latex
\subsection{Local Bottleneck-C ledger after repair attempts}
\label{subsec:local-bottleneck-c-ledger-after-repairs}
```

and before:

```latex
\subsection{Global obstruction-class interpretation of the Bottleneck-C defect}
\label{subsec:global-obstruction-class-bottleneck-c-defect}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Last-chance pointwise flatness in full phase variables}
\label{subsec:last-chance-pointwise-flatness-full-phase-variables}

The rebuilt source convention removes the unstable-cutoff objection by using
the full non-core zero complement
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
\]
A final possible escape is that the exact decomposition of the full phase
derivative into rebuilt baseline and non-core complement might itself force
the Bottleneck-C flatness identity.  This subsection records that it does not.

Write
\[
Q(t):=q(t)
\]
for the full phase derivative, and decompose
\[
Q(t)=b(t)+G(t),
\]
where
\[
b(t):=q_{\base}^{\new}(t)
      =q_{\core}(t)+B_{\bg}(t)+E_{\est,R}(t),
\]
and
\[
G(t):=G^{\new}(t)=q_{\aux,R}(t)+T_{\far,R}(t).
\]
At the midpoint \(m\), put
\[
b_0:=b(m),
\qquad
b_2:=b''(m),
\]
and
\[
A_2:=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4:=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]
Then
\[
A_2=\frac{Q''(m)-b''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{Q^{(4)}(m)-b^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The rebuilt Bottleneck-C flatness condition is
\[
\frac{b_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{b_2}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=0.
\]
Substitution gives
\[
\frac{b_0}{11520}
\bigl(Q''-b''\bigr)
\bigl(Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}\bigr)
+
\frac{1}{576}
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
\bigl(Q''-b''\bigr)^2
=0,
\]
with all derivatives evaluated at \(m\).  Equivalently, if
\[
D_2:=Q''-b''=G'',
\qquad
D_4:=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}=G^{(4)},
\]
then the condition is
\[
D_2
\left[
b_0D_4
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
D_2
\right]
=0.
\]

\begin{proposition}[The rebuilt flatness equation is an extra fourth-order constraint]
\label{prop:rebuilt-flatness-extra-fourth-order-constraint}
The identity
\[
Q=b+G
\]
does not imply
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]
On a good patch with \(G''(m)\ne0\), pointwise flatness is equivalent to the
additional derivative-ratio constraint
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{G''(m)}
=
\frac{40b(m)^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b(m)}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
b^{(4)}(m)
=
Q^{(4)}(m)
-
\left(
\frac{40b(m)^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b(m)}
\right)
\bigl(Q''(m)-b''(m)\bigr).
\]
Thus the desired flatness is not a consequence of the tautological full-phase
decomposition.  It is an extra nonlinear fourth-order pointwise condition on
the selected baseline/source split.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The displayed factorization shows that, if \(D_2=G''(m)\ne0\), the vanishing
condition is precisely
\[
b_0D_4
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
D_2
=0.
\]
Dividing by \(b_0D_2\) gives
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{G''(m)}
=
\frac{40b_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b_0}.
\]
The equivalent formula for \(b^{(4)}\) follows from
\[
G^{(4)}=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}.
\]
The decomposition \(Q=b+G\) supplies only
\[
G''=Q''-b'',
\qquad
G^{(4)}=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}.
\]
It supplies no relation fixing \(G^{(4)}/G''\) in terms of \(b,b''\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why defining the baseline by flatness is circular]
\label{rem:baseline-by-flatness-is-circular}
One could formally choose \(b\) by requiring the fourth-order equation in
Proposition~\ref{prop:rebuilt-flatness-extra-fourth-order-constraint}.  Such a
choice would kill the Bottleneck-C row by definition.  It is not a proof
unless an independent zeta-side principle selects exactly this baseline, for
example through the functional equation, a canonical scattering law, a
zero-counting conservation principle, or a functorial fixed-core construction.
No such principle is currently present.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Asymptotic scale is not an identity]
\label{rem:asymptotic-scale-not-identity}
If \(b\) is dominated by the smooth phase/background, one expects roughly
\[
b(t)\sim \frac12\log(t/2\pi).
\]
Then the required ratio has scale
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
\sim
\frac{40}{3}b^2
\asymp
\log^2 t.
\]
A non-core zero complement with pole distances of order \(1/\log t\) can have
the same dimensional scale.  This is not enough: the identity requires the
exact constant and sign
\[
\frac{40b^2}{3}-\frac{10b''}{3b}
\]
pointwise.  Local one-pair and finite-tail tests show that source geometry can
produce different fourth-to-second derivative ratios.  Thus a proof of
flatness would have to be a genuinely new global zero-complement rigidity
theorem.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** The latest draft has exactness and residue no-gos, but it still does not record the clean \(Q=b+G\) algebra showing flatness is an extra fourth-order constraint. That is a useful final nail in the coffin for pointwise-flatness rescue.

## Edit 3 — Add the meromorphic ODE principal-part no-go

**Where:** Insert after the current subsection:

```latex
\subsection{Meromorphic residue no-go for the rebuilt obstruction}
\label{subsec:meromorphic-residue-no-go-rebuilt-obstruction}
```

before the next subsection.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Meromorphic ODE principal-part no-go}
\label{subsec:meromorphic-ode-principal-part-no-go}

A related failed repair is to seek a meromorphic differential equation for the
source complement or for the full phase derivative.  The local flatness
condition would be implied by an equation of the form
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q},
\]
or by the same equation with \(G=q\).  This is incompatible with the principal
parts of the actual zero-pair pole fields.

Let
\[
H(t)=\frac{C}{t-p}+O(1)
\]
have a simple pole.  Then
\[
H''(t)=\frac{2C}{(t-p)^3}+O(1),
\qquad
H^{(4)}(t)=\frac{24C}{(t-p)^5}+O(1),
\]
so
\[
\frac{H^{(4)}}{H''}
=
\frac{12}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]

On the other hand, if the full phase derivative has
\[
q(t)=\frac{R}{t-p}+O(1),
\]
then
\[
q^2(t)=\frac{R^2}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right),
\qquad
\frac{q''}{q}
=
\frac{2}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]
Hence
\[
\frac{40q^2}{3}-\frac{10q''}{3q}
=
\left(
\frac{40R^2}{3}
-
\frac{20}{3}
\right)
\frac1{(t-p)^2}
+
O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]
Matching the left-hand double-pole coefficient \(12\) would require
\[
R^2=\frac75.
\]

\begin{proposition}[Zero-pair residues rule out the meromorphic ODE repair]
\label{prop:zero-pair-residues-rule-out-meromorphic-ode}
The flatness-forcing ODE
\[
\frac{H^{(4)}}{H''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
\]
cannot hold as a meromorphic identity for the raw non-core zero source, for the
full phase derivative, or for any complement retaining the zero-pair poles.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For a zero-pair summand
\[
f_a(t)=\frac{a}{a^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]
the poles are
\[
p_a^\pm=\frac{\gamma\pm ia}{2},
\]
with residues
\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^+} f_a=-\frac{i}{4},
\qquad
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^-} f_a=\frac{i}{4}.
\]
Thus the phase-pole residues are purely imaginary.  For a simple pole,
\[
R=\pm \frac{i}{4},
\]
so
\[
R^2=-\frac1{16},
\]
not \(7/5\).  If several same-sign pole contributions coincide, then
\[
R=\pm \frac{ni}{4},
\]
and still \(R^2<0\).  Therefore the right-hand double-pole coefficient cannot
match the coefficient \(12\) of \(H^{(4)}/H''\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Pole-cancelled complements are the wrong object]
\label{rem:pole-cancelled-complements-wrong-object}
A pole-cancelled complement can evade the principal-part contradiction at the
cancelled pole.  But Bottleneck-C uses the source moments
\[
A_2=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]
An ODE for a pole-cancelled complement is therefore an ODE for the wrong
object, unless the entire order-seven row is rederived with different moments.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** The draft’s residue section rules out residue-killing, but not the nearby ODE/principal-part rescue. This insertion is short and prevents a stale “maybe the ODE works” branch. The agent transcript contains the pole calculation and residue mismatch.

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Global rank-two affine transport gate]
\label{hyp:global-rank-two-affine-transport-gate}
There exists a canonical path, loop, boundary condition, index, or transported
finite-core non-concentration theorem on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\) that
controls
\[
\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}
=
\int_\Gamma
U_{t\to b}
\left(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\right)(t)\,dt.
\]
Equivalently, the rank-two affine forcing equation must be coupled to a global
law that distinguishes RH-compatible configurations from off-line-packet
configurations.  Without such a law, the rank-two architecture is locally
coherent but globally non-closing.
\end{hypothesis}
```

**Why:** This promotes the main remaining dependency from prose to a named hypothesis, making it easier to reference downstream.

## Agent 6 — Interaction / Feature-Balance / Global Synthesis Attack

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }dd\text{-interaction branch does not currently supply the missing cone or positivity input.}
}
\]

The transported/rank-two feature formalism is coherent, but it inherits the same algebraic obstruction as the split and quotient interaction branches: ordinary amplitude balance

\[
\sum_i a_i=0
\]

does **not** imply feature balance

\[
\sum_i a_i v_i=0.
\]

Nor does unit normalization force the required spectral sign: the local coefficient

\[
\kappa_6=-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
\]

remains sign-indefinite. Therefore the \(dd\)-interaction branch cannot yet provide the coercive cone theorem Agent 5 needs for transported finite-core non-concentration. This matches the attached instruction’s warning that the global gate is now the hard problem, not local formalization. 

The only viable output from this branch is a sharper missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{feature-balance failure or spectral-cone failure must be forced into incidence,}
}
\]

or else one needs a genuinely new arithmetic/zero-geometry input.

---

# 1. Feature-balance algebra

Let the transported interaction feature be a vector-valued curve

\[
v(u)\in V,
\]

where \(V\) is whichever finite-dimensional feature space the current global route uses:

\[
V=V_{\rm tr},
\qquad
v=v_{\rm tr},
\]

or, in split notation,

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)
=
(v_{\quot}(u),v_{\parallel}(u)).
\]

The \(dd\)-interaction kernel has the schematic form

\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2
\langle v(u_i),v(u_j)\rangle.
\]

For a finite core \(u_1,\ldots,u_k\), feature balance asks:

\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\qquad
\text{for all }a\in \mathbf 1^\perp,
\]

where

\[
\mathbf 1^\perp=\left\{a:\sum_i a_i=0\right\}.
\]

This condition is equivalent to sampled constancy.

\[
\boxed{
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\ \forall a\in\mathbf 1^\perp
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
v(u_1)=\cdots=v(u_k).
}
\]

Proof: If all \(v(u_i)\) are equal, the balanced sum vanishes. Conversely, take \(a=e_i-e_j\). Then

\[
0=\sum_\ell a_\ell v(u_\ell)=v(u_i)-v(u_j),
\]

so all sampled features coincide.

This is already too strong to expect from ordinary amplitude balance. Amplitude balance only says

\[
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]

It imposes no constraint on

\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i).
\]

So the interaction branch needs a new theorem, not a rephrasing of balance.

---

# 2. Basic countermodel survives transport

The standard three-point countermodel works for quotient, split, and transported feature spaces.

Take

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\qquad
a=(1,-2,1),
\]

so

\[
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]

Let

\[
v(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w,
\qquad
w\neq0.
\]

Then

\[
v(-1)=v_0+\varepsilon w,
\qquad
v(0)=v_0,
\qquad
v(1)=v_0+\varepsilon w.
\]

Therefore

\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)
=
(v_0+\varepsilon w)-2v_0+(v_0+\varepsilon w)
=
2\varepsilon w\neq0.
\]

This is a regular local feature variation. It does not by itself force collision, endpoint collapse, Gram singularity, quotient degeneracy, or line degeneracy. Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{feature-balance failure can occur outside known incidence in the formal local model.}
}
\]

To kill this branch, the proof needs one of:

\[
\boxed{
v(u_1)=\cdots=v(u_k)
\text{ by actual zeta geometry,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
v(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\text{ is inadmissible outside a named incidence set.}
}
\]

At present neither is proved.

---

# 3. Spectral expansion

Now test whether spectral cone control can replace exact feature balance.

Define the transported \(dd\)-kernel near a midpoint \(m\):

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle.
\]

Write the Taylor expansion

\[
v(m+h)
=
v_0+h v_1+\frac{h^2}{2}v_2+\frac{h^3}{6}v_3+\frac{h^4}{24}v_4+O(h^5).
\]

Then

\[
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right)
=
v_0+\frac t2v_1+\frac{t^2}{8}v_2+\frac{t^3}{48}v_3+\frac{t^4}{384}v_4+O(t^5),
\]

and

\[
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
=
v_0-\frac t2v_1+\frac{t^2}{8}v_2-\frac{t^3}{48}v_3+\frac{t^4}{384}v_4+O(t^5).
\]

Taking the inner product gives

\[
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle
=
\kappa_2+\kappa_4t^2+\kappa_6t^4+O(t^6),
\]

with

\[
\kappa_2=\langle v_0,v_0\rangle,
\]

\[
\kappa_4
=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right),
\]

and

\[
\kappa_6
=
\frac{1}{192}\langle v_0,v_4\rangle
-\frac{1}{48}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
+\frac{1}{64}\langle v_2,v_2\rangle.
\]

Under unit normalization,

\[
\langle v(u),v(u)\rangle=1,
\]

we have, after differentiating twice,

\[
\langle v_1,v_1\rangle+\langle v_0,v_2\rangle=0,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\kappa_4=-\frac12\langle v_1,v_1\rangle\le0.
}
\]

After differentiating four times,

\[
2\langle v_0,v_4\rangle
+
8\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
+
6\langle v_2,v_2\rangle
=0,
\]

hence

\[
\langle v_0,v_4\rangle
=
-4\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
-3\langle v_2,v_2\rangle.
\]

Substitute into \(\kappa_6\):

\[
\kappa_6
=
\frac{1}{192}
\left(
-4\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
-3\langle v_2,v_2\rangle
\right)
-\frac{1}{48}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
+\frac{1}{64}\langle v_2,v_2\rangle.
\]

The \(v_2\)-terms cancel:

\[
-\frac{3}{192}+\frac{1}{64}=0.
\]

The \(v_1,v_3\)-terms combine:

\[
-\frac{4}{192}-\frac{1}{48}
=
-\frac{1}{48}-\frac{1}{48}
=
-\frac{1}{24}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\kappa_6
=
-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
}
\]

Thus unit normalization gives a good sign at order \(t^4\), but leaves the order \(t^6\) sign open.

---

# 4. Unit-curve spectral countermodel

Take a two-dimensional feature subspace and define a unit curve

\[
v(u)=(\cos\phi(u),\sin\phi(u)),
\qquad
\phi(u)=au+bu^3.
\]

At \(u=0\),

\[
v_0=(1,0),
\]

\[
v_1=(0,a),
\]

and

\[
v_3=(-3a^2,6b-a^3).
\]

Therefore

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
=
a(6b-a^3).
\]

For \(a>0\), this is positive exactly when

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6}.
\]

Then

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac{1}{24}a(6b-a^3).
\]

Depending on the sign convention required for the \(dd\)-cone, this gives the bad sixth-order sign. In particular, unit normalization alone does not force the needed spectral sign.

This countermodel is smooth, unit-normalized, and lives in a two-dimensional transported/split feature subspace. It does not automatically trigger geometric incidence.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{spectral cone control is not a formal consequence of the transported feature setup.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Can actual zeta symmetry force feature balance?

The only possible positive route is to show that the actual zeta finite-core feature curve is much more rigid than an arbitrary smooth vector curve.

Possible sources of extra rigidity:

\[
\text{functional equation symmetry,}
\]

\[
\text{conjugation symmetry,}
\]

\[
\text{same-scale packet closure,}
\]

\[
\text{Gram/whitening normalization,}
\]

\[
\text{rank-two affine transport equation,}
\]

or

\[
\text{finite-core source identities.}
\]

But none of these currently implies

\[
v(u_1)=\cdots=v(u_k)
\]

on an admissible finite core. Functional equation and conjugation symmetries create paired/packet symmetries, not sampled constancy across all core points. Whitening normalizes the metric, not the curve’s derivatives. The affine equation controls \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) as a section, but it does not currently impose a curvature sign or constancy condition on the transported feature curve.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual zeta symmetry is not yet strong enough to force feature balance.}
}
\]

A proof would need a new statement of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale finite-core admissibility}
\Longrightarrow
v_{\rm tr}(u_i)\text{ is constant up to controlled incidence.}
}
\]

That is currently unsupported and likely too strong.

---

# 6. Can incidence containment save the branch?

The more realistic target is incidence containment:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
}
\]

or spectral-incidence containment:

\[
\boxed{
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\text{ has bad sign}
\Longrightarrow
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}.
}
\]

But the local countermodels above show this cannot be a purely formal algebraic theorem. It must use actual zeta geometry, not merely rank-two/split/transported linear algebra.

A plausible incidence list would have to include:

\[
\det G_{\core}=0,
\quad
\text{core tie walls},
\quad
\text{visibility walls},
\quad
\text{feature-rank degeneracy},
\quad
\text{transport curvature walls},
\quad
\text{interaction alignment walls}.
\]

The problem is that adding “feature-balance failure” or “bad spectral sign” to the exceptional set would be circular unless those sets are independently controlled and shown not to swallow RH-relevant packets.

So incidence containment is a legitimate target only if it comes with a non-swallowing theorem.

---

# 7. Can the \(dd\)-interaction branch supply the cone input for Agent 5?

Not currently.

Agent 5’s transported finite-core lower bound would need some coercive statement such as:

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}
\]

outside incidence. The \(dd\)-branch could help if it showed:

\[
\text{interaction vector lies in a cone transverse to the pair vector,}
\]

or

\[
\text{interaction quadratic form has one sign on balanced amplitudes,}
\]

or

\[
\text{near-cancellation forces feature-balance failure incidence.}
\]

But the feature-balance countermodel and the spectral \(\kappa_6\) countermodel show that no such cone theorem follows from the present transported feature formalism alone.

Thus the \(dd\)-interaction branch cannot yet supply the missing coercivity for Agent 5.

The needed additional input is external to the current local linear algebra. It would have to be one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a zeta-specific feature rigidity theorem,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{an arithmetic lower bound on feature variation,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{a same-scale source geometry cone theorem,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{a controlled-incidence theorem for all bad feature/spectral loci.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Final gate table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|l}
\text{gate} & \text{status} & \text{reason}\\
\hline
\text{Gate A/B local lemmas} & \text{local closed} & \text{accepted fixed-convention algebra}\\
\text{packet visibility} & \text{local conditional closed} & K_1\text{ one-slot channel/non-centered }q^{(7)}\text{ outside incidence}\\
\text{rank-two bundle/connection} & \text{local conditional} & \text{needs fixed core and functorial atlas}\\
E_{\eta\eta}\text{ affine forcing} & \text{local conditional} & \text{tensorial forcing; }E_{\rm lower}\text{ row table pending}\\
\text{path/boundary transport} & \text{global open} & \text{no canonical endpoint or holonomy law}\\
\text{transported finite-core lower bound} & \text{global open-negative} & \text{aligned branch survives formally}\\
dd\text{-feature balance} & \text{global open-negative} & \sum a_i v_i=0\Leftrightarrow v_i\text{ constant}\\
dd\text{-spectral cone} & \text{global open-negative} & \kappa_6=-\frac1{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\text{ sign uncontrolled}\\
\text{energy/projective diagnostics} & \text{diagnostic only} & \text{miss scale or lack boundary theorem}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 9. Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }dd\text{-interaction branch does not currently close the global gate.}
}
\]

It gives a precise obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary amplitude balance is too weak; feature balance is sampled constancy.}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{unit feature normalization controls }\kappa_4\text{ but not }\kappa_6.
}
\]

Therefore the next global theorem cannot be a purely formal transported \(dd\)-cone theorem. It must use new input.

---

# 10. Exact next mathematical target

The best next target is a **zeta-specific transported interaction incidence theorem**:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{dd}^{\rm bad}
:=
\left\{
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)\neq0
\ \text{or}\ 
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\text{ has bad sign}
\right\}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
}
\]

together with a non-swallowing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}.
}
\]

If that theorem is unavailable, the more honest route is a transported finite-core lower-bound theorem with an explicit arithmetic input:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q)
}
\]

where the lower bound cannot come from smooth local feature algebra alone.

---

## Final conclusion

The rank-two local architecture is still the best current language. But the \(dd\)-interaction branch does not yet supply the missing positivity or cone input. The global proof now requires a genuinely new theorem: either zeta-specific feature rigidity/incidence containment, or an arithmetic transported finite-core non-concentration lower bound.

## Agent 6 — Global Falsifier / Model-Builder

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current rank-two local framework is too flexible to prove RH by itself.}
}
\]

I can build clean local and semiglobal models satisfying the present local axioms:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\ne\varnothing,
\qquad
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\text{ rank two},
\qquad
\nabla A_7=E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
\qquad
A_7\ne0,
\]

while still allowing transported finite-core near-cancellation:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

So the present framework cannot close RH without an additional **zeta-specific quantitative input**: incidence-distance, cone separation, arithmetic non-concentration, or a true global path/boundary law. This matches the attached instruction’s strategic conclusion: the live risk is no longer local formalization; it is that the local rank-two story becomes a polished but non-closing framework. 

---

# 1. Minimal local model satisfying the rank-two axioms

Let the reduced base be a small interval

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}=(-1,1),
\]

with coordinate \(t\). Let

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(-1,1)\times \mathbf C^2
\]

with fixed frame

\[
I=(1,0),
\qquad
S=(0,1),
\]

and take the flat connection

\[
\nabla=\frac{d}{dt}.
\]

This satisfies the rank-two bundle and connection axioms in the strongest possible way.

Choose a visible order-seven section

\[
A_7(t)=\varepsilon I+tS,
\qquad
\varepsilon\ne0.
\]

Then

\[
A_7(t)\ne0
\]

on a neighborhood of \(0\), so packet visibility holds.

Define forcing

\[
E(t):=\nabla A_7(t)=S.
\]

Declare

\[
E_{\eta\eta}(t)=S,
\qquad
E_{\rm lower}(t)=0.
\]

Then the affine forcing equation holds exactly:

\[
\nabla A_7=E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

This model satisfies the local rank-two architecture perfectly. It has a visible fixed-sector packet and a nonzero affine forcing row. But it has no RH contradiction. There is no boundary condition, no holonomy constraint, no sign contradiction, and no finite-core lower bound.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local rank-two affine forcing is not, by itself, a proof gate.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Local transported finite-core cancellation model

Now add a transported finite-core vector. Let

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7,\nabla A_7,A_9,\nabla A_9,\ldots)
\]

take values in some finite-dimensional vector space \(V\).

Let the pair and interaction parts be

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)=p(t),
\]

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)=-p(t)+\delta w(t),
\]

where

\[
p(t)\ne0,
\qquad
w(t)\ne0,
\]

and \(0<|\delta|\ll1\).

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)
=
\delta w(t).
\]

Thus

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)\ne0
\]

for \(\delta\ne0\), so qualitative visibility remains true. But for any proposed lower bound \(\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q)\), choose

\[
|\delta|<\frac{\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q)}{\|w(t)\|_\infty}.
\]

Then

\[
0<
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
\]

This explicitly realizes the bad aligned branch:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{visibility plus affine forcing does not imply transported non-concentration.}
}
\]

The missing theorem must forbid this alignment using actual zeta geometry.

---

# 3. Incidence-distance failure model

A qualitative incidence statement says only

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)\ne0
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}.
\]

But the proof needs a quantitative lower bound. Without arithmetic separation from the zero set, analytic nonvanishing is too weak.

Let

\[
\theta_Q=e^{-Q},
\]

and let the transported finite-core coordinate be

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)=\theta.
\]

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta_Q)=e^{-Q}\ne0.
\]

So \(\theta_Q\) is outside the zero set. But for every fixed \(B>0\),

\[
e^{-Q}<Q^{-B}
\]

for all large \(Q\). Thus no polynomial lower bound

\[
|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta_Q)|\ge Q^{-B}
\]

follows from analytic nonvanishing alone.

This proves the exact point in the attached instruction: the real missing theorem is not

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\ne0,
\]

but something like

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Only after such a distance bound can a Łojasiewicz/Remez argument yield

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative incidence separation is essential.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Semiglobal affine transport model with zero displacement

Let

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}=[0,1],
\]

with flat connection. Let the forcing be

\[
E(t)=
\begin{cases}
B, & 0\le t\le \frac12,\\
-B, & \frac12<t\le1,
\end{cases}
\]

smoothed near \(t=1/2\) if desired.

Then the pointwise forcing is nonzero on most of the interval:

\[
E(t)\ne0.
\]

But the affine displacement is

\[
\Delta^{\rm aff}_{[0,1]}
=
\int_0^1 E(t)\,dt
=
0.
\]

Thus nonzero local Bottleneck-C forcing does not imply nonzero global affine displacement. Conversely, if the integral were nonzero, that alone would not contradict anything without endpoint data.

This model satisfies:

\[
\nabla A=E,
\]

with

\[
A(1)=A(0)
\]

if the total integral vanishes.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{nonzero forcing requires path/boundary/holonomy control to become contradictory.}
}
\]

The local affine equation is descriptive unless the paper supplies a global constraint.

---

# 5. Feature-balance countermodel compatible with transport

Let the transported feature curve be

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w,
\qquad
w\ne0.
\]

For the three-point core

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\]

take the balanced amplitude

\[
a=(1,-2,1).
\]

Then

\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]

but

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)
=
(v_0+\varepsilon w)-2v_0+(v_0+\varepsilon w)
=
2\varepsilon w\ne0.
\]

So ordinary amplitude balance does not imply transported feature balance.

This model is compatible with a smooth rank-two transported feature curve and does not force a local singularity. It is exactly the branch that blocks \(dd\)-interaction positivity.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
dd\text{-interaction cannot provide a cone theorem from formal balance alone.}
}
\]

A zeta-specific theorem is required.

---

# 6. Spectral-cone countermodel compatible with transport

Take a unit feature curve in a two-dimensional transported feature subspace:

\[
v(u)=(\cos\phi(u),\sin\phi(u)),
\qquad
\phi(u)=au+bu^3.
\]

At \(u=0\),

\[
v_1=(0,a),
\]

\[
v_3=(-3a^2,6b-a^3).
\]

Hence

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
=
a(6b-a^3).
\]

The normalized \(dd\)-kernel has sixth-order coefficient

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac1{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

For \(a>0\) and

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6},
\]

we get

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle>0,
\]

so \(\kappa_6\) has the bad sign in the relevant convention.

Thus unit normalization gives no full spectral cone control.

\[
\boxed{
\text{formal spectral positivity fails at order }t^6.
}
\]

Again, only a zeta-specific rigidity or incidence theorem could rescue this.

---

# 7. Model satisfying all local axioms but not closing RH

Combine the pieces.

Take:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}=(-1,1),
\qquad
\mathcal F=\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\times\mathbf C^2,
\qquad
\nabla=d.
\]

Let

\[
A_7(t)=I+tS,
\qquad
E_{\eta\eta}=S,
\qquad
E_{\rm lower}=0.
\]

Then

\[
\nabla A_7=E_{\eta\eta}.
\]

Visibility holds:

\[
A_7(t)\ne0.
\]

Let transported finite-core data split as

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=p,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=-p+\delta w.
\]

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=\delta w,
\]

which is nonzero but arbitrarily small.

Let the transported interaction feature be

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w.
\]

Then feature balance fails for balanced amplitudes.

This model satisfies:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\ne\varnothing,
\]

\[
\mathcal F\text{ rank two},
\]

\[
\nabla A_7=E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
\]

\[
A_7\text{ visible},
\]

but it allows:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

Therefore it is a countermodel to the proposition that the current local rank-two axioms alone imply RH-closing non-concentration.

\[
\boxed{
\text{The framework needs a genuinely zeta-specific global theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 8. What kind of theorem is now required?

The model-building attack narrows the missing input.

A viable next theorem must be one of the following.

## Option A — Quantitative incidence separation

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Together with a Łojasiewicz/Remez inequality, this could yield

\[
\boxed{
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

## Option B — Zeta-specific feature rigidity

\[
\boxed{
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}.
}
\]

This must use actual zeta/zero-packet geometry, not abstract feature algebra.

## Option C — Cone separation from actual source geometry

\[
\boxed{
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\in\mathcal C_P,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\in\mathcal C_J,
\qquad
\mathcal C_P\cap(-\mathcal C_J)=\{0\}.
}
\]

The cones must be derived from the actual phase/zero geometry.

## Option D — Boundary/holonomy law

\[
\boxed{
A(b)-U_{a\to b}A(a)
=
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt
}
\]

must be constrained by global zeta symmetry or endpoint data.

No current local axiom supplies any of these.

---

# 9. Gate table after falsifier attack

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|l}
\text{component} & \text{status} & \text{reason}\\
\hline
\text{local rank-two bundle} & \text{conditional} & \text{fixed reduced atlas needed}\\
\text{packet visibility} & \text{conditional-positive} & K_1\text{ channel/noncentered }q^{(7)}\\
\text{affine forcing equation} & \text{conditional-positive} & E_{\eta\eta}\text{ as tensorial forcing}\\
E_{\rm lower}\text{ closure} & \text{conditional} & \text{row table dependency}\\
\text{path/boundary} & \text{open-negative} & \text{no endpoint constraints}\\
\text{transported finite-core lower bound} & \text{open-negative} & \text{aligned branch model survives}\\
dd\text{-interaction cone} & \text{open-negative} & \text{feature/spectral countermodels survive}\\
\text{global RH gate} & \text{missing} & \text{needs zeta-specific quantitative theorem}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 10. Final decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{The rank-two architecture is locally coherent but globally underdetermined.}
}
\]

The adversarial models show that the following implication is false:

\[
\text{local rank-two affine forcing}
\Longrightarrow
\text{transported finite-core non-concentration}.
\]

Therefore the next mathematical attack should not be another local repair. It should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative incidence separation / zeta-specific transported non-concentration.}
}
\]

A precise target is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or a direct lower bound

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\|_\infty
\ge \Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
}
\]

Without such a theorem, the present proof family remains a coherent local framework but not an RH proof.

## Agent 6 — Zeta-Like Falsifier

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Even after imposing zeta-like symmetry, positivity, same-scale structure, }q_0>0,\text{ and Gram positivity, near-cancellation remains possible.}
}
\]

The current local rank-two axioms plus the standard packet symmetries still do **not** imply a transported finite-core lower bound. I can build finite “zeta-like” packet models satisfying the structural constraints but allowing

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\]

to be arbitrarily small outside the formal zero set. Therefore the next theorem really must be **quantitative and arithmetic/zeta-specific**, not formal local geometry. This matches the current strategic state in the attached instruction: the local architecture should be frozen, and the central obstruction is quantitative incidence separation or transported non-concentration. 

---

# 1. Zeta-like packet model

Use the standard off-line symmetry packet

\[
\mathcal P(\rho)
=
\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\},
\qquad
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,
\qquad
\beta\ne\frac12.
\]

Set

\[
\delta=\beta-\frac12,
\qquad
a=\frac12-\delta,
\qquad
b=\frac12+\delta,
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma.
\]

The real phase-derivative contribution of the horizontal pair is

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2}.
\]

This already imposes:

\[
\beta\leftrightarrow1-\beta,
\qquad
\bar\rho\text{ symmetry},
\qquad
a,b>0.
\]

So the source kernel is positive and has the right functional-equation/conjugation packet structure.

Now build a finite zeta-like source model

\[
q_{\rm model}(t)
=
q_{\rm bg}(t)
+
\sum_{j=1}^N
\left[
\frac{a_j}{a_j^2+(2t-\gamma_j)^2}
+
\frac{b_j}{b_j^2+(2t-\gamma_j)^2}
\right],
\]

where

\[
a_j=\frac12-\delta_j,
\qquad
b_j=\frac12+\delta_j,
\qquad
0<|\delta_j|<\frac12.
\]

Choose \(q_{\rm bg}(m)>0\) large enough that

\[
q_0=q_{\rm model}(m)>0,
\]

and choose the packet ordinates \(\gamma_j\) so that all offsets

\[
x_j=2m-\gamma_j
\]

are same-scale and lie in the selected finite core. Add outside packets far enough away to create a strict core gap

\[
d_k<d_{k+1}.
\]

This model satisfies all the requested zeta-like constraints at the local level:

\[
\boxed{
\text{functional equation symmetry, conjugation symmetry, positive source kernels, same-scale core, }q_0>0.
}
\]

For Gram positivity, use the same-point block

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right).
\]

Taking \(q_{\rm bg}\) sufficiently large gives

\[
g>0,
\qquad
h>0,
\]

and generically

\[
g\ne h.
\]

Thus the whitening/Gram good-patch constraints can also be satisfied.

---

# 2. Sign reversal survives positivity

For one packet, near the centered point

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0,
\]

we have the seventh derivative channel

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m
+
O(x_m^3).
\]

Since

\[
a,b>0,
\]

the coefficient

\[
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})
\]

is strictly positive.

Therefore changing the packet from

\[
x_m=+\varepsilon
\]

to

\[
x_m=-\varepsilon
\]

reverses the sign of the \(q^{(7)}\) visibility channel while keeping:

\[
a,b>0,
\qquad
q_0>0,
\qquad
\text{functional-equation packet symmetry},
\qquad
\text{same-scale admissibility}.
\]

This is the key falsifier.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Positive zeta-like packets can still contribute opposite rank-two directions by moving across the sampling midpoint.}
}
\]

So any cone theorem that tries to put all actual packet contributions in a pointed cone already fails at the local packet level unless it introduces a canonical orientation convention or an arithmetic sign theorem.

---

# 3. Two-packet cancellation model

Take two off-line packets with the same \(\delta\), same scale, and ordinates

\[
\gamma_1=2m-\varepsilon,
\qquad
\gamma_2=2m+\varepsilon.
\]

Then

\[
x_1=2m-\gamma_1=\varepsilon,
\qquad
x_2=2m-\gamma_2=-\varepsilon.
\]

Their leading \(q^{(7)}\)-channels are opposite:

\[
q^{(7)}_1(m)
=
C\varepsilon+O(\varepsilon^3),
\]

\[
q^{(7)}_2(m)
=
-C\varepsilon+O(\varepsilon^3),
\]

where

\[
C=5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})>0.
\]

The aggregate leading \(K_1\) transported channel cancels to order

\[
O(\varepsilon^3).
\]

If the two packets are slightly unequal, say

\[
\delta_2=\delta_1+\eta,
\qquad
x_2=-\lambda x_1,
\]

then by choosing \(\lambda\) as a smooth function of \(\eta\), we can make the leading channel cancel exactly:

\[
C(\delta_1)x_1+C(\delta_2)x_2=0.
\]

All constraints remain zeta-like:

\[
a_j,b_j>0,
\qquad
\mathcal P(\rho_j)\text{ closed under }\rho\mapsto1-\rho,\bar\rho,
\qquad
q_0>0,
\qquad
g,h>0,
\qquad
\text{same-scale core}.
\]

This gives a concrete same-scale symmetric packet ensemble with arbitrarily small transported order-seven forcing.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale packet symmetry does not prevent near-cancellation.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Transported finite-core near-cancellation

Let the transported finite-core vector be

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots).
\]

In the finite packet model, each packet contributes analytically to this vector:

\[
V_j=V(\delta_j,x_j,\ldots).
\]

Near \(x_j=0\), the order-seven transported component has the form

\[
V_j
=
x_j V_1(\delta_j)+O(x_j^2)
\]

for the \(q^{(7)}\)-route, plus even centered channels from the one-whitening-slot mechanism.

Because \(x_j\) can have either sign while preserving all zeta-like packet constraints, the image contains both directions

\[
V_1
\quad\text{and}\quad
-V_1
\]

to first order.

Now split packets into a “pair” subset and an “interaction” subset. Define

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
\sum_{j\in P} V_j,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
\sum_{j\in J} V_j.
\]

By choosing the offsets and \(\delta\)-parameters in the \(J\)-subset, one can arrange

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
-P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
+
\epsilon W
\]

with \(\epsilon\) arbitrarily small, at least in the formal local packet model.

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
\epsilon W.
\]

So

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\ne0
\]

but can be made smaller than any proposed polynomial lower bound.

This is the transported version of the aligned branch:

\[
\boxed{
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
}
\]

The construction respects functional-equation packet symmetry and positive source kernels.

---

# 5. Why this is not yet a counterexample to zeta

This is an adversarial **zeta-like local model**, not an actual construction of zeta zeros.

The actual zeta zeros are not freely placeable. Their ordinates, spacings, and off-line displacements—if any—are constrained by the global \(\xi\)-function, Hadamard product, explicit formula, and arithmetic structure.

So this falsifier proves only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the current local axioms and packet symmetries are insufficient.}
}
\]

It does **not** prove:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual zeta data can realize the bad alignment.}
}
\]

That distinction is exactly the point. The missing theorem must use actual zeta arithmetic or analytic number theory, not just the local rank-two formalism.

---

# 6. Incidence-distance failure survives zeta-like constraints

Even if the bad locus is a proper analytic set, a zeta-like path may approach it too fast.

Let an incidence function be

\[
\Phi(\theta)=C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta).
\]

Analytic nonvanishing gives only:

\[
\Phi(\theta)\ne0
\]

outside the incidence set. It gives no polynomial lower bound.

A zeta-like local path could satisfy

\[
\Phi(\theta_Q)=e^{-Q},
\]

with

\[
\theta_Q\notin \{\Phi=0\}.
\]

Then for every fixed \(B\),

\[
e^{-Q}<Q^{-B}
\]

for large \(Q\). Thus no lower bound

\[
|\Phi(\theta_Q)|\ge Q^{-B}
\]

follows.

This remains true even if \(\theta_Q\) respects the local positivity, symmetry, and Gram constraints. Those constraints define an admissible semianalytic region, but they do not impose arithmetic separation from the incidence wall.

Therefore the real theorem must be something like:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Only then can Łojasiewicz/Remez-type inequalities yield

\[
\boxed{
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Feature-balance falsifier with zeta-like packet symmetry

The \(dd\)-feature balance obstruction also survives.

Let the transported feature curve be

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w.
\]

This is even in \(u\), so it is compatible with a symmetric same-scale packet model around the midpoint.

For the three-point symmetric core

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\]

take balanced amplitudes

\[
a=(1,-2,1).
\]

Then

\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]

but

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)
=
2\varepsilon w\ne0.
\]

So even parity-compatible feature curves do not satisfy feature balance. Functional-equation and conjugation symmetry do not automatically make

\[
v_{\rm tr}(-1)=v_{\rm tr}(0)=v_{\rm tr}(1).
\]

They may enforce some symmetries, such as

\[
v_{\rm tr}(-u)=v_{\rm tr}(u)
\]

or structured pairings, but sampled constancy is much stronger.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zeta-like parity symmetry does not imply }dd\text{-feature balance.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Spectral-cone falsifier with zeta-like orientation freedom

The unit-curve countermodel also remains compatible with local zeta-like constraints.

Take

\[
v(u)=(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3)).
\]

This is unit-normalized. The spectral coefficient is

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle,
\]

and

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
=
a(6b-a^3).
\]

Choosing

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6}
\]

gives the bad sign.

The zeta-like packet constraints above do not forbid such third-order rotation of the transported feature curve. In particular, the sign reversal of \(q^{(7)}\) across the midpoint already shows local orientation freedom.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{spectral cone positivity requires additional zeta-specific rigidity.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Stronger falsifier: pointed cones cannot contain all local packet contributions

Suppose one seeks cones

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\in \mathcal C_P,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\in \mathcal C_J,
\]

with

\[
\mathcal C_P\cap(-\mathcal C_J)=\{0\}.
\]

The sign-reversal packet calculation already threatens this.

For a single packet,

\[
V(x)=Cx+O(x^3)
\]

in the \(q^{(7)}\)-channel.

Since both

\[
x>0
\]

and

\[
x<0
\]

are legitimate nearby sampling midpoints inside the same zeta-like packet family, any cone containing all such local packet contributions must contain both

\[
V_1
\quad\text{and}\quad
-V_1.
\]

Thus it is not pointed.

So a cone theorem cannot be based merely on positivity of the source kernels or same-scale packet structure. It must either:

1. choose a canonical orientation excluding one sign;
2. prove actual zeta data occupy only one side;
3. use a higher-dimensional invariant where sign reversal is compensated by another constrained coordinate.

None is currently available.

---

# 10. What theorem could defeat this falsifier?

The falsifier leaves exactly three plausible proof inputs.

## A. Arithmetic incidence-distance

Prove

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

for actual zeta data. This would rule out super-polynomial approach to the aligned branch.

## B. Actual zeta feature rigidity

Prove that actual transported features cannot realize the formal variations

\[
v(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\]

or

\[
v(u)=(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3))
\]

outside controlled incidence.

## C. New invariant immune to sign reversal

Find a finite-core invariant not vulnerable to

\[
V(x)\mapsto -V(x)
\]

under midpoint non-centering. Candidates might involve multi-scale determinants, wedge products across asymmetric samples, or an arithmetic phase-orientation invariant. But every candidate must be tested against the two-packet cancellation model.

## Agent 6 — Stronger Zeta-Like Falsifier

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Near-cancellation still survives after imposing finite Hadamard-product, functional-equation, conjugation, positive-kernel, same-scale, }q_0>0,\text{ and Gram-positive constraints.}
}
\]

The current local rank-two framework is not strong enough to yield RH. It remains a good coordinate system for the obstruction, but it does not prevent transported pair/interaction cancellation. The missing theorem is still quantitative and genuinely zeta-specific:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}\!\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or directly

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))
\right\|_\infty
\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

The attached instruction explicitly says the current bottleneck is no longer local geometry, packet visibility, or formal rank-two transport, but quantitative separation of actual zeta finite-core data from transported cancellation incidence. 

---

# 1. Strengthened model: finite \(\xi\)-like Hadamard product

Work in the centered variable

\[
z=s-\frac12.
\]

A \(\xi\)-like finite product should satisfy:

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

so zeros occur in packets

\[
\{\alpha,\bar\alpha,-\alpha,-\bar\alpha\}.
\]

Take off-line packets

\[
\alpha_j=\delta_j+i\gamma_j,
\qquad
\delta_j\ne0.
\]

Define a finite even real entire model

\[
F(z)
=
e^{\mu z^2+\nu}
\prod_{j=1}^N
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\alpha_j^2}\right)
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\bar\alpha_j^2}\right),
\]

with \(\mu,\nu\in\mathbb R\). This imposes the functional equation and conjugation exactly. It is a finite Hadamard-product model with the same quartet symmetry as \(\xi\).

The logarithmic derivative is

\[
\frac{F'(z)}{F(z)}
=
2\mu z
-
\sum_j
\left(
\frac{2z}{\alpha_j^2-z^2}
+
\frac{2z}{\bar\alpha_j^2-z^2}
\right).
\]

Restricting to the critical line \(z=it\) gives a real phase-derivative contribution of the same rational positive-kernel type as the earlier packet model. Thus this is not an arbitrary local vector model; it is generated by a symmetric entire product.

So the falsifier now satisfies:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite Hadamard-product structure, functional equation, conjugation, and real-line reality.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Same-scale packet construction survives

Choose two off-line packets with the same horizontal displacement \(\delta\) and ordinates symmetrically placed around the sampling midpoint:

\[
\gamma_1=2m-\varepsilon,
\qquad
\gamma_2=2m+\varepsilon.
\]

Then the midpoint offsets are

\[
x_1=2m-\gamma_1=\varepsilon,
\qquad
x_2=2m-\gamma_2=-\varepsilon.
\]

Both packets are same-scale if \(|\varepsilon|\) and \(|\delta|\) are chosen within the core window. Add all symmetry partners through the finite product above. Add far packets outside the selected window to create a strict core gap

\[
d_k<d_{k+1}.
\]

This respects packet-level core selection and same-scale symmetry closure.

---

# 3. Positive source kernels still allow sign reversal

For a single packet contribution

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]

with

\[
a=\frac12-\delta,
\qquad
b=\frac12+\delta,
\qquad
a,b>0,
\]

the seventh derivative near the packet center is

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m
+
O(x_m^3),
\qquad
x_m=2m-\gamma.
\]

The coefficient

\[
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})
\]

is strictly positive. Therefore the sign of the \(q^{(7)}\) rank-two visibility/transport channel is controlled by the sign of \(x_m\), not by the positivity of the source kernel.

For the two packets above,

\[
q^{(7)}_1(m)=C\varepsilon+O(\varepsilon^3),
\]

\[
q^{(7)}_2(m)=-C\varepsilon+O(\varepsilon^3),
\]

where

\[
C=5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})>0.
\]

So the leading \(K_1\)-transport contribution cancels.

This cancellation is compatible with:

\[
a,b>0,
\qquad
q_0>0,
\qquad
\text{functional equation},
\qquad
\text{conjugation symmetry},
\qquad
\text{same-scale core}.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{positivity and Hadamard symmetry do not produce a pointed cone.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Gram positivity can be enforced independently

The local Gram scalars have the schematic form

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right).
\]

Add a smooth even background, corresponding to the exponential factor \(e^{\mu z^2+\nu}\), so that \(q_0\) is large positive. Then

\[
g>0,
\qquad
h>0,
\]

and generically

\[
g\ne h.
\]

The same construction preserves the packet cancellation above, because the opposite-offset packet contributions to \(q^{(7)}\) still cancel at leading order.

So the bad near-cancellation survives even on a Gram-positive good patch.

---

# 5. Explicit-formula consistency does not automatically forbid the model

The explicit formula is a global identity connecting zeros and primes/test functions. A finite Hadamard-product model is not the Riemann \(\xi\)-function, but it shows that the **structural symmetries alone** do not prohibit the bad local configuration.

To rule this out for actual zeta, one would need a theorem saying that the Euler product / primes / true explicit formula prevent symmetric same-scale off-line packets from producing near-canceling transported finite-core data.

That theorem would need to be quantitative. A qualitative global identity is not enough because the bad branch is near-cancellation, not exact cancellation.

The necessary shape is:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the actual zeta-induced incidence function \(\Phi_{\rm align}\), or

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),Z_{\rm align})\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

No standard explicit-formula statement gives such a pointwise finite-core incidence separation.

---

# 6. Pair/interaction near-cancellation survives with zeta-like constraints

Let each symmetric packet contribute a transported finite-core vector

\[
V_j=V(\delta_j,x_j,\text{background jets}).
\]

Near \(x_j=0\),

\[
V_j=x_jV_1(\delta_j)+O(x_j^2)
\]

for the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\)-transport channel.

Because \(x_j\) can be positive or negative inside the same legitimate packet family, the attainable local directions include both

\[
V_1
\quad\text{and}\quad
-V_1.
\]

Now choose packets divided into pair-type and interaction-type subsets. Set

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=\sum_{j\in P}V_j,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=\sum_{j\in J}V_j.
\]

By choosing the \(J\)-packet offsets and horizontal displacements slightly, one can arrange

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
-P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
+
\epsilon W
\]

with \(\epsilon\) arbitrarily small in the local finite-product model.

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
\epsilon W.
\]

Thus

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\neq0,
\]

but it can be smaller than any prescribed polynomial threshold.

This is exactly the dangerous aligned branch:

\[
\boxed{
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
}
\]

It survives after imposing the strongest local zeta-like constraints available in this model.

---

# 7. Feature-balance still fails in symmetric packet models

A transported feature curve compatible with packet symmetry can be even:

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w.
\]

For a symmetric three-point core

\[
u=(-1,0,1)
\]

and balanced amplitudes

\[
a=(1,-2,1),
\]

we have

\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]

but

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)
=
(v_0+\varepsilon w)-2v_0+(v_0+\varepsilon w)
=
2\varepsilon w\ne0.
\]

This countermodel is even in \(u\), so it is compatible with conjugation/functional-equation parity. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet symmetry does not imply feature balance.}
}
\]

Feature balance would require sampled constancy:

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\rm tr}(u_k),
\]

which is much stronger than parity.

---

# 8. Spectral cone still fails

The unit feature-curve countermodel also survives.

Let

\[
v(u)=(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3)).
\]

Then

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac1{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle,
\]

and

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
=
a(6b-a^3).
\]

Choosing

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6}
\]

gives the bad sign.

There is no contradiction with local finite-product symmetry, Gram positivity, or source positivity. Therefore spectral positivity is not a formal consequence of zeta-like local constraints.

---

# 9. What would defeat the stronger falsifier?

Only a genuinely arithmetic theorem can now help. The options are:

## A. Polynomial incidence separation

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

## B. Explicit-formula lower bound for a specific incidence function

Construct a test function whose zero-side expression is the transported alignment functional

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr},
\]

then prove

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

unless RH already holds or the packet lies in controlled incidence.

## C. Arithmetic rigidity of zero packets

Prove that actual zeta zero packets cannot realize the opposite-offset cancellation pattern compatible with finite-product symmetry.

This would be a new zero-configuration rigidity theorem.

## D. A new invariant immune to sign reversal

The invariant must survive

\[
V(x)\mapsto -V(x)
\]

and the two-packet cancellation model. Ordinary norm, wedge, projective, and energy candidates tested so far do not do this.

---

# 10. Final decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{The stronger zeta-like falsifier still permits near-cancellation.}
}
\]

The current rank-two local framework plus finite Hadamard-product symmetry is not enough to prove RH.

The next attack should be concentrated on a specific quantitative incidence function:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta),
}
\]

or a low-order scalar component of it, and ask:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can actual zeta constraints prove }
|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))|\ge Q^{-B}?
}
\]

If not, the current proof architecture remains locally coherent but globally non-closing.

## Agent 6 — Strong Falsifier for an Exact Transported Alignment Coordinate

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{For the natural low-order transported alignment coordinates, finite \(\xi\)-like packet models can still tune the coordinate arbitrarily small.}
}
\]

So the next attack cannot stay at the level of “choose a coordinate and hope it is separated.” For any coordinate whose leading term is linear in a signed packet jet such as \(q^{(7)}\), or a linear projection of the \(K_1\)-transport channel, the same opposite-offset packet construction kills polynomial lower bounds unless actual zeta arithmetic forbids that configuration. The attached instruction correctly narrows the next phase to one explicit transported alignment coordinate; this response tests the canonical candidates and finds the same near-cancellation mechanism. 

---

# 1. Candidate coordinate family

The cleanest low-order transported coordinates are:

\[
\Phi_7(\theta)
=
\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

and

\[
\Phi_{\nabla 7}(\theta)
=
\omega_h(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

If the goal is transported finite-core non-concentration, the general scalar coordinate is

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta)
=
\ell\!\left(
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)
\right),
\]

where \(\ell\) is a fixed rank-two transported coordinate functional.

The exact coordinate is not yet fixed by the other agents, so I test the whole natural class:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{\rm align}
\text{ whose first nonzero packet term is a nontrivial linear functional of a signed odd packet jet.}
}
\]

This includes the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\) channel and any determinant/projection coordinate that sees the \(K_1\)-transport slice.

---

# 2. Finite \(\xi\)-like model

Use the centered variable

\[
z=s-\frac12.
\]

Construct a finite even real entire model

\[
F(z)
=
e^{\mu z^2+\nu}
\prod_{j=1}^N
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\alpha_j^2}\right)
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\bar\alpha_j^2}\right),
\]

where

\[
\alpha_j=\delta_j+i\gamma_j,
\qquad
\delta_j\ne0,
\qquad
\mu,\nu\in\mathbb R.
\]

Then

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

so the finite model has functional-equation symmetry and conjugation symmetry. Each off-line packet is

\[
\{\alpha_j,\bar\alpha_j,-\alpha_j,-\bar\alpha_j\}.
\]

Along the critical line, the phase derivative has packet contributions of the usual positive-kernel form

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]

with

\[
a=\frac12-\delta,
\qquad
b=\frac12+\delta,
\qquad
a,b>0.
\]

By choosing \(\mu\) large enough, we force

\[
q_0>0,
\qquad
g>0,
\qquad
h>0,
\]

and generically

\[
g\ne h.
\]

Thus the model satisfies the local zeta-like constraints: quartet symmetry, positive kernels, same-scale packet structure, \(q_0>0\), and Gram positivity.

---

# 3. Leading signed packet channel

For one packet,

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3),
\qquad
x_m=2m-\gamma.
\]

Set

\[
C(\delta):=5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})>0.
\]

Then

\[
q^{(7)}(m)=C(\delta)x_m+O(x_m^3).
\]

Thus the leading \(K_1\)-transport contribution to any coordinate detecting the \(q^{(7)}\) channel has the schematic form

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}^{(j)}
=
\lambda(\delta_j)\,x_j+O(x_j^2),
\]

where

\[
\lambda(\delta_j)\ne0
\]

on the visibility-positive patch.

The crucial fact is that

\[
x_j
\]

can have either sign without violating the zeta-like packet constraints.

---

# 4. Two-packet cancellation for the exact coordinate

Take two packets with

\[
\delta_1,\delta_2\ne0,
\]

same scale, and offsets

\[
x_1=\varepsilon,
\qquad
x_2=-\lambda\varepsilon.
\]

Their coordinate contributions are

\[
\Phi_1
=
\lambda_1\varepsilon+O(\varepsilon^2),
\]

\[
\Phi_2
=
-\lambda_2\lambda\varepsilon+O(\varepsilon^2).
\]

Choose

\[
\lambda=\frac{\lambda_1}{\lambda_2}.
\]

Then

\[
\Phi_1+\Phi_2=O(\varepsilon^2).
\]

By allowing a second small adjustment in either \(\delta_2\), \(x_2\), or a third packet offset, the implicit function theorem gives an exact local solution

\[
\Phi_1+\Phi_2=0
\]

provided the derivative with respect to the tuning parameter is nonzero. In the generic visibility-positive case, that derivative is nonzero because the coordinate already sees the \(K_1\)-transport channel.

Hence the finite \(\xi\)-like model admits exact cancellation of the tested scalar coordinate while maintaining the symmetry and positivity constraints.

If we do not tune exactly, we can make

\[
|\Phi_{\rm align}|<Q^{-B}
\]

for any fixed \(B\), simply by choosing

\[
\varepsilon\ll Q^{-B/2}
\]

or by tuning to residual size \(e^{-Q}\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No polynomial lower bound for this coordinate follows from local zeta-like constraints.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Application to \(\Phi_7=\omega_h(A_7,A_5)\)

On a visibility-positive patch, the \(K_1\)-transport contribution gives a nonzero rank-two vector. In the non-centered channel, it is \(q^{(7)}\)-driven. Therefore

\[
\Phi_7
=
\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\]

has leading packet contribution

\[
\Phi_7^{(j)}
=
c_7(\delta_j)\,x_j+O(x_j^2),
\]

unless the selected coordinate lies on the quotient-invisible incidence wall.

Using two opposite-offset packets,

\[
x_1=\varepsilon,
\qquad
x_2=-\frac{c_7(\delta_1)}{c_7(\delta_2)}\varepsilon,
\]

gives

\[
\Phi_7^{(1)}+\Phi_7^{(2)}=O(\varepsilon^2).
\]

Further tuning gives exact cancellation or arbitrarily small nonzero value.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
}
\]

is not separated by formal packet symmetry.

---

# 6. Application to \(\Phi_{\nabla7}=\omega_h(\nabla A_7,A_5)\)

The affine equation gives

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

The leading active forcing component is a transported \(K_1\)-source/Hessian term. For the non-centered packet, the same odd jet sign reversal appears in the forcing coordinate unless the coordinate is chosen to kill that channel.

Thus generically

\[
\Phi_{\nabla7}^{(j)}
=
c_{\nabla7}(\delta_j)x_j+O(x_j^2).
\]

The same two-packet cancellation applies.

If instead the coordinate is centered and sees the one-whitening-slot channel

\[
-2yBr\,I,
\]

then it is even in the centered offset, but it can still be cancelled by choosing two packets with different \(\delta\)-values and adjusting their amplitudes/effective weights through same-scale geometry or background normalization. In the finite product model, packet multiplicity or nearby packet duplication can tune the coefficient continuously.

So neither the value coordinate nor the derivative/forcing coordinate currently has a formal anti-cancellation property.

---

# 7. Why replacement invariants do not escape

Suppose the coordinate is replaced by an invariant such as

\[
|\Phi|^2,
\qquad
|\Phi(x)|^2+|\Phi(-x)|^2,
\qquad
\omega(P,J),
\qquad
|P|^2-|J|^2,
\qquad
\det(C,\nabla C).
\]

The adversarial pair model can be written

\[
P=V,
\qquad
J=-V+\eta W.
\]

Then

\[
C=P+J=\eta W.
\]

So

\[
|C|^2=|\eta|^2|W|^2
\]

is still arbitrarily small.

Projective data lose scale. Wedge data detect nonparallelity but fail when the cancellation is nearly collinear:

\[
J=-V+\eta V+\eta^2 W.
\]

Then

\[
\omega(P,J)=O(\eta^2).
\]

Energy differences such as

\[
|P|^2-|J|^2
\]

can also be tuned small by taking

\[
J=-(1+\eta)P+O(\eta^2).
\]

So no obvious scalar invariant bypasses the need for quantitative anti-alignment.

---

# 8. What would be needed to defeat this falsifier?

The finite \(\xi\)-like model shows that local symmetries and positive kernels are insufficient. A successful theorem must use a property not built into this model.

Possible missing inputs:

## 8.1 Euler-product / prime-side arithmetic

A theorem that the actual zeta zeros cannot be arranged in the opposite-offset packet pattern while preserving the prime-side explicit formula.

This would need to produce a lower bound for a concrete alignment statistic:

\[
|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

## 8.2 Quantitative zero-configuration rigidity

A theorem that same-scale off-line packets cannot satisfy the analytic cancellation equations to better than polynomial accuracy unless they lie in exact controlled incidence.

Formally:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),Z_{\rm align})\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

## 8.3 A new orientation invariant

A coordinate that does not change sign under

\[
x_m\mapsto -x_m
\]

but also does not lose scale under

\[
P+J\approx0.
\]

The standard candidates tested so far do not meet both requirements.

---

# 9. Result for the selected-coordinate program

The selected-coordinate program remains valuable, but the target must be sharpened.

For any proposed coordinate \(\Phi_{\rm align}\), the next proof attempt must do three things:

1. **Write the coordinate explicitly** in packet jets, Gram terms, and projection data.
2. **Test the two-packet opposite-offset model**:
   \[
   x_1=\varepsilon,\qquad x_2=-\lambda\varepsilon.
   \]
3. **Identify the first non-cancellable term**.

If every low-order coordinate has a tunable leading cancellation, then the proof must either move to a multi-scale/global statistic or import arithmetic separation from the explicit formula.

---

# 10. Final gate table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c}
\text{candidate coordinate} & \text{falsifier status}\\
\hline
\omega_h(A_7,A_5) & \text{two-packet cancellation survives}\\
\omega_h(\nabla A_7,A_5) & \text{two-packet cancellation survives}\\
|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}|^2 & \text{small when }C=P+J\text{ is small}\\
\omega(P,J) & \text{small under near-collinear cancellation}\\
|P|^2-|J|^2 & \text{tunable to zero}\\
\text{projective class }[C] & \text{loses scale}\\
dd\text{-feature balance} & \text{requires sampled constancy}\\
dd\text{-spectral cone} & \kappa_6\text{ sign remains free}
\end{array}
\]

---

# Final conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{The stronger finite-\(\xi\)-like falsifier defeats the natural explicit transported alignment coordinates.}
}
\]

The current architecture now needs a truly arithmetic quantitative theorem.

The most precise next target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{For an explicitly chosen coordinate }\Phi_{\rm align},
\text{ prove }
|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta_\zeta(m))|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

using actual zeta constraints, not local rank-two formalism.

Without that, the proof remains locally coherent but globally non-closing.
