## Agent 6 — Exact-Coordinate Explicit-Formula Attack

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The explicit formula can represent the linear ingredients of }
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)},
\text{ but it does not presently give a lower bound for the full scalar.}
}
\]

The first obstruction is not visibility of the ingredients. It is the **nonlinear product/ratio structure**, especially the Gram-anisotropy factor

\[
g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
h-g.
\]

A one-level explicit formula sees \(q_0\), \(q''\), and \(A_2\)-type linear zero statistics. A tensorized explicit formula can formally expand products such as \(A_2^2q''\). But neither gives sign, cone separation, or polynomial non-cancellation for

\[
q_0A_2^2q''(h-g).
\]

So the explicit formula currently **rewrites** the alignment problem; it does not solve it. This matches the instruction’s warning that the next phase must lock to the exact scalar

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}=-2yBr
\]

rather than drift to \(D_7\), \(\Phi_{\rm lock}\), or generic transported coordinates. 

---

# 1. Exact coordinate

The locked scalar is

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-2yBr,
\]

where

\[
B=
\frac{q''}{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\]

and

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-y\,
\frac{q''(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2})}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}.
}
\]

Using

\[
g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}
=
\frac{h-g}{\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\]

we get the more useful form

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-y\,
\frac{q''(h-g)}
{4\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
}
\]

The leading channel has

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^2q''(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2})}
{288\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^2q''(h-g)}
{288\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
}
\]

At a centered distinguished packet,

\[
q''=2A_2,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^3(h-g)}
{144\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
}
\]

The coordinate is therefore controlled by four factors:

\[
q_0,
\qquad
A_2^2,
\qquad
q'',
\qquad
h-g.
\]

The denominator is harmless only under explicit good-patch bounds for \(g,h\).

---

# 2. Explicit-formula visibility of each factor

The Gram scalars are

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\]

and

\[
h=
\frac1\pi
\left(
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''
\right).
\]

Hence

\[
h-g
=
\frac1\pi
\left(
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''-q_0
\right).
\]

So the leading scalar may be written entirely in terms of

\[
q_0,\qquad q'',\qquad A_2,
\]

as

\[
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^2q''}{288\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}
\cdot
\frac1\pi
\left(
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''-q_0
\right).
\]

Thus the numerator is schematically

\[
\boxed{
q_0A_2^2q''
\left(
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''-q_0
\right).
}
\]

Expanding,

\[
\boxed{
\text{numerator}
=
\frac13 q_0^4A_2^2q''
+
\frac16 q_0A_2^2(q'')^2
-
q_0^2A_2^2q''.
}
\]

Each of \(q_0\), \(q''\), and \(A_2\) is explicit-formula visible as a linear statistic after fixing the local convention. But the coordinate itself is a nonlinear polynomial/rational expression in those statistics.

---

# 3. Factor table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{factor} & \text{meaning} & \text{explicit-formula visible?} & \text{lower-bound status}\\
\hline
q_0 & \text{phase value / baseline local slope} & \text{yes, linear zero/background statistic} & q_0>0\text{ plausible; polynomial lower depends on good-patch assumptions}\\
q'' & \text{second local phase/source curvature} & \text{yes, linear statistic} & \text{no general lower bound away from }0\\
A_2 & \frac12G''(m)\text{ source-complement curvature} & \text{yes, after fixed source convention} & \text{no general anti-cancellation lower bound}\\
A_2^2 & \text{quadratic source curvature} & \text{requires two-level/tensored formula} & \text{nonnegative only if real; still can be tiny}\\
y_{\lead}=-q_0A_2^2/72 & \text{quadratic mixed-block coefficient} & \text{composite} & \text{depends on }q_0,A_2\\
g & q_0/\pi & \text{yes through }q_0 & \text{positive on good patch}\\
h & \pi^{-1}(q_0^3/3+q''/6) & \text{composite} & \text{positive on good patch, but tunable}\\
h-g & \pi^{-1}(q_0^3/3+q''/6-q_0) & \text{composite} & \boxed{\text{main missing lower bound}}\\
(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^{-2}(gh)^{-1} & \text{Gram denominator} & \text{composite} & \text{controlled only if }g,h\asymp Q^{O(1)}\text{ and bounded from }0
\end{array}
\]

The first serious obstruction is:

\[
\boxed{
|h-g|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or equivalently

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''-q_0
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Without this, the scalar can approach the Gram-isotropy wall

\[
g=h
\]

faster than any fixed power of \(Q\).

---

# 4. One-level explicit formula

A standard explicit formula can represent linear statistics of zeros. In this setting, it can see objects like

\[
q_0,
\qquad
q'',
\qquad
G''(m),
\qquad
A_2=\frac12G''(m),
\]

once the source/core convention is fixed.

For example, \(q''\) and \(G''\) are derivatives of log-derivative-type kernels and can be represented by zero-side sums paired with suitable test functions.

So a one-level explicit formula can address questions such as:

\[
q''=0?
\]

\[
A_2=0?
\]

\[
q_0>0?
\]

But the target scalar is not linear. It contains

\[
q_0A_2^2q''(h-g),
\]

and \(h-g\) itself contains

\[
q_0^3
\]

and \(q''\).

Therefore a one-level explicit formula cannot directly produce

\[
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It can only express or bound individual factors.

\[
\boxed{
\text{One-level explicit formula: useful for ingredients, insufficient for the product.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Two-level or tensorized explicit formula

A two-level explicit formula could formally expand products such as

\[
A_2^2,
\qquad
q_0A_2^2,
\qquad
A_2^2q'',
\qquad
q_0A_2^2q''(h-g).
\]

For instance, if

\[
A_2=\sum_\rho K_2(\rho;m),
\]

then

\[
A_2^2
=
\sum_{\rho_1,\rho_2}
K_2(\rho_1;m)K_2(\rho_2;m).
\]

Similarly, the full leading numerator becomes a multiple zero sum.

But this does not solve the lower-bound problem. It merely rewrites

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
\]

as a multi-zero statistic. The prime side of a tensorized explicit formula would contain complicated convolutions of test functions, and there is no evident positivity or sign.

The same cancellation problem reappears as cancellation among multiple zero tuples or prime convolutions.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Tensorization expands the scalar but does not produce anti-cancellation.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Tailored test function possibility

Could one design a test function whose zero-side statistic is directly

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}?
\]

Only partially.

The linear pieces \(q_0\), \(q''\), \(A_2\) can be generated by differentiating kernels. But the factors

\[
A_2^2,
\qquad
q_0^3,
\qquad
(gh)^{-1},
\qquad
(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^{-2}
\]

depend on the zero configuration itself. A standard explicit formula uses fixed test functions independent of the zero set. To encode these nonlinear denominators, the test function would have to depend on the same local zero configuration it is trying to bound.

That becomes circular unless one proves uniform stability estimates allowing the denominator to be frozen.

A possible route is to split:

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{
N_{\Phi}
}{
D_{\Phi}
},
\]

where

\[
N_{\Phi}
=
q_0A_2^2q''(h-g),
\]

and

\[
D_{\Phi}
=
288\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2.
\]

If the good patch gives

\[
Q^{-d}\le g,h\le Q^d,
\]

then

\[
D_{\Phi}\le Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Then it suffices to prove

\[
|N_{\Phi}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But

\[
N_{\Phi}
=
q_0A_2^2q''
\left(
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''-q_0
\right)/\pi.
\]

Thus one still needs polynomial lower bounds for all four factors:

\[
|q_0|,
\qquad
|A_2|,
\qquad
|q''|,
\qquad
|h-g|.
\]

The explicit formula does not currently provide these simultaneous lower bounds.

---

# 7. The Gram-anisotropy obstruction

The weakest factor is

\[
h-g
=
\frac1\pi
\left(
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''-q_0
\right).
\]

The wall

\[
g=h
\]

is

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

This is not obviously forbidden by zeta structure. It is a relation between a local slope and a local curvature. Neither functional equation symmetry nor positivity of source kernels prevents this relation from being approached.

A finite \(\xi\)-like model with adjustable background parameter \(\mu\) can tune \(q_0\) and \(q''\) while preserving:

\[
q_0>0,
\qquad
g,h>0,
\qquad
\text{quartet symmetry}.
\]

Thus \(g-h\) can plausibly be made arbitrarily small in the local model. To rule this out for actual zeta, one needs a new theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

on the reduced visibility-positive patches.

This is a highly nonstandard local phase-jet separation statement.

---

# 8. Lower-bound reduction

Assume good-patch scale bounds:

\[
Q^{-d}\le g,h\le Q^d.
\]

Then

\[
\sqrt g+\sqrt h\le 2Q^{d/2},
\]

and

\[
gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2\le 4Q^{3d}.
\]

Using

\[
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^2q''(h-g)}
{288\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2},
\]

we get

\[
|\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}|
\ge
c Q^{-3d}
|q_0|\,|A_2|^2\,|q''|\,|h-g|.
\]

Thus a polynomial lower bound follows from assumptions of the form:

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-a},
\]

\[
|A_2|\ge Q^{-b},
\]

\[
|q''|\ge Q^{-c},
\]

\[
|h-g|\ge Q^{-e}.
\]

Then

\[
|\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}|
\ge
Q^{-(3d+a+2b+c+e+O(1))}.
\]

This reduction is clean. But the real work is proving those four factor lower bounds for actual zeta data.

Among them, the first is plausible under good-patch slope positivity. The last three are not currently proved, and

\[
|h-g|\ge Q^{-e}
\]

looks like the sharpest obstruction.

---

# 9. Does explicit formula offer a real path?

For this exact coordinate, my classification is:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c}
\text{question} & \text{status}\\
\hline
\text{Can explicit formula express }q_0,q'',A_2? & \text{yes}\\
\text{Can it express }A_2^2q''q_0(h-g)? & \text{formally via tensorization}\\
\text{Does one-level explicit formula give positivity?} & \text{no}\\
\text{Does tensorization give positivity?} & \text{no}\\
\text{Can a fixed test function encode the nonlinear denominator?} & \text{no, not directly}\\
\text{Can good-patch bounds reduce to numerator only?} & \text{yes}\\
\text{Can standard explicit formula prove numerator lower bound?} & \text{not currently}\\
\text{First serious obstruction} & \boxed{\text{Gram anisotropy }h-g}
\end{array}
\]

So the explicit formula offers a way to **expand** the scalar, and possibly to search for prime-side identities, but it does not presently yield the required lower bound.

---

# 10. Final conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{For the exact scalar }\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)},\text{ the explicit formula sees the ingredients but not the anti-cancellation.}
}
\]

The scalar reduces to a nonlinear rational expression in explicit-formula-visible jets:

\[
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^2q''(h-g)}
{288\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
\]

The missing lower bound is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0A_2^2q''(h-g)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Given good-patch bounds on \(g,h\), this reduces to polynomial lower bounds for

\[
q_0,\quad A_2,\quad q'',\quad h-g.
\]

The first may be plausible. The last three, especially

\[
\boxed{
|h-g|
=
\frac1\pi
\left|
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''-q_0
\right|
\ge Q^{-A},
}
\]

are not supplied by the standard explicit formula.

Therefore this coordinate does not yet close the proof. The next mathematical target should be a direct attack on the Gram-anisotropy separation:

\[
\boxed{
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or a proof that the actual zeta zero configuration cannot simultaneously make

\[
A_2,\quad q'',\quad h-g
\]

super-polynomially small or mutually canceling on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\).

## Agent 6 — Escape-Route / Alternative Coordinate Agent

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Inside the centered order-7 rank-two fixed-sector scalar, } |g-h|\ge Q^{-A}\text{ is unavoidable.}
}
\]

The weak factor \(g-h\) is not an artifact of notation. It is the algebraic price of converting the skew mixed block \(Y=yJ\) into a fixed-sector \(I\)-component through one odd whitening slot. If \(g=h\), the leading whitening is isotropic and the one-slot centered channel lands in the anti-fixed \(D\)-sector, not in \(\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S\).

So the locked scalar

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-2yBr
=
-y\frac{q''(h-g)}{4\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}
\]

cannot be rescued by a different normalization, ratio, or projection without changing the architecture. The attached instruction correctly identifies \(g-h\) as the current failure point. 

The only plausible escapes are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{leave the rank-two fixed sector and use an ambient/anti-fixed coordinate,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{move to another actual fixed-sector coefficient, probably }A_9^{\mathfrak f}\text{ or non-centered }q^{(7)}.
}
\]

Both are new attacks, not repairs of \(\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}\).

---

# 1. Matrix reason \(g-h\) appears

The centered one-whitening-slot channel is

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

Write

\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

Then

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_0-X_0YX_{-,1}.
\]

Using

\[
SJ=-D,
\qquad
JS=D,
\]

we get

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yB(pD+rI).
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})
=
-2yBr\,I.
}
\]

The fixed-sector part is exactly the \(rI\)-piece. Since

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}),
\]

the fixed-sector channel vanishes when \(g=h\).

The anti-fixed part is

\[
\boxed{
-2yBp\,D,
}
\]

where

\[
p=\frac12(g^{-1/2}+h^{-1/2}).
\]

This remains nonzero at \(g=h\), provided \(yB\ne0\). Thus the **full ambient channel does not vanish at \(g=h\)**. Only the fixed-sector projection does.

That proves the core point:

\[
\boxed{
g-h\text{ is structural for the centered order-7 fixed-sector scalar.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Candidate table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{candidate coordinate} & \text{contains }g-h\text{?} & \text{new obstruction}\\
\hline
\ell_I(A_7^{\mathfrak f})=\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)} & \text{yes} & \text{needs }|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}\\
D_7=\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}) & \text{often yes for this channel if }A_5\text{ has }S\text{-part} & \text{line/quotient cancellation and lost-line issues}\\
\Phi/(g-h) & \text{divides it out} & \text{non-holomorphic/unbounded at }g=h;\text{ no lower bound for original signal}\\
\partial_\tau\Phi\text{ transverse to }g=h & \text{not necessarily} & \text{needs lower bound for }\partial_\tau(g-h)\text{ and canonical }\tau\\
(\Phi,g-h) & \text{yes, explicitly} & \text{still requires quantitative }|g-h|\\
(yq'',g-h) & \text{yes, as second coordinate} & \text{requires lower bounds for }yq''\text{ and }g-h\\
\text{anti-fixed }D\text{-component }-2yBpD & \text{no} & \text{leaves rank-two fixed sector; requires ambient/rank-four architecture}\\
\|T_7^{(1)}\|_{\rm ambient} & \text{no} & \text{ambient energy; global proof gate missing}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\text{ centered} & \text{unknown} & \text{must compute actual order-9 row at }g=h\\

\end{array}
\]

# 3. Candidate-by-candidate analysis

## 3.1 \(D\)-component before fixed-sector projection

The anti-fixed component is

\[
\Phi_D:=-2yBp.
\]

Since

\[
p=\frac12(g^{-1/2}+h^{-1/2}),
\]

we have

\[
p>0
\]

whenever \(g,h>0\). Thus

\[
\Phi_D
=
-2yB p
\]

does **not** contain \(g-h\). It only needs

\[
y\ne0,
\qquad
q''\ne0,
\qquad
g,h>0.
\]

This is the cleanest escape from Gram anisotropy.

But it is not in the rank-two fixed sector. It lies in the anti-fixed \(D\)-sector. Therefore using it requires expanding the architecture from

\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S
\]

to at least an ambient sector including \(D\), e.g.

\[
\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S\oplus \mathbf C D
\]

or the full four-dimensional block algebra

\[
\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S\oplus\mathbf C D\oplus\mathbf C J.
\]

This would require redoing:

\[
\text{visibility,}
\quad
\text{finite-core vector,}
\quad
\text{transport,}
\quad
\text{interaction/cone analysis,}
\quad
\text{global proof gate.}
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The anti-fixed coordinate is a real escape from }g-h,\text{ but only by leaving rank-two fixed-sector geometry.}
}
\]

It is not a repair of the locked scalar.

---

## 3.2 Different fixed-sector projection

One could try to define a projection that maps the anti-fixed \(D\)-piece into the fixed sector. But that breaks the symmetry meaning of

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The fixed sector is the \(I/S\) sector determined by the swap/fixed decomposition. A projection that sees \(D\) is not a fixed-sector projection. It is an ambient projection or a new readout.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Changing }\pi_{\mathfrak f}\text{ to see }D\text{ is a new architecture, not a coordinate tweak.}
}
\]

---

## 3.3 Dividing by \(g-h\)

Consider

\[
\frac{\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}}{g-h}
=
-y\frac{q''}{4\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
\]

This removes the weak factor. But it does not lower-bound the original physical coordinate. If \(g-h=e^{-Q}\), then the ratio can be large while

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
\]

is exponentially small.

It also becomes singular or noncanonical on the wall

\[
g=h.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Dividing by }g-h\text{ hides the obstruction rather than solving it.}
}
\]

It is acceptable only as a diagnostic for the remaining factors \(yq''\).

---

## 3.4 Transverse derivative through the wall

Let \(\tau\) be a parameter and differentiate:

\[
\partial_\tau \Phi
=
-\partial_\tau\!\left(
y\frac{q''(h-g)}
{4\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}
\right).
\]

On \(g=h\), the leading term is

\[
\partial_\tau \Phi
\sim
-yq''\,\partial_\tau(h-g)\,
\frac{1}{4\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
\]

This can be nonzero even when \(\Phi=0\). So a transverse derivative coordinate could detect crossing of the Gram-isotropy wall.

But it requires:

1. a canonical transverse parameter \(\tau\);
2. a lower bound
   \[
   |\partial_\tau(h-g)|\ge Q^{-A};
   \]
3. a global proof gate using derivative data rather than value data.

If \(\partial_\tau(h-g)\) is also small, or if the path is tangent to the wall, the same issue returns at higher order.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transverse derivatives replace }|g-h|\text{ by a higher-jet non-tangency theorem.}
}
\]

This may be useful, but it does not avoid quantitative Gram separation. It upgrades it to quantitative transversality.

---

## 3.5 Two-coordinate vectors

A vector such as

\[
(\Phi,g-h)
\]

has norm bounded below only if

\[
|g-h|
\]

is bounded below or \(\Phi\) is. But

\[
\Phi
\propto g-h,
\]

so this vector is effectively controlled by

\[
|g-h|.
\]

A vector such as

\[
(yq'',g-h)
\]

is better diagnostically. It separates the source factor from the Gram factor. But a lower bound requires:

\[
|yq''|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

or

\[
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is not the original fixed-sector order-seven coordinate. It is an expanded incidence vector.

Such a vector can be useful for defining a stronger good-patch condition, but it does not prove the original scalar is large.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-coordinate vectors help diagnose which factor fails; they do not by themselves lower-bound }\Phi.
}
\]

---

## 3.6 Higher-order \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\)

This is the best possible escape **within the rank-two fixed sector**.

At \(g=h\), the order-seven centered one-slot fixed-sector channel dies because the leading whitening is isotropic. But a higher order may have other anisotropy sources, for example:

\[
\partial_s^2G_\pm,
\quad
q^{(4)},
\quad
A_4,
\quad
A_6,
\quad
\text{higher mixed-block carriers},
\]

which could produce a fixed-sector component not proportional to \(g-h\).

The key test is:

\[
\boxed{
\left.
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\right|_{g=h,\; yq''\ne0}
\stackrel{?}{\ne}0.
}
\]

If yes, then the rank-two route can replace the order-seven scalar with an order-nine coordinate on the Gram-isotropy wall.

If no, and if the same symmetry keeps every centered odd fixed-sector channel proportional to a Gram anisotropy factor, then \(|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}\) is unavoidable for the centered route.

So:

\[
\boxed{
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\text{ is the main intra-rank-two escape route.}
}
\]

But it requires an actual order-nine row computation. It cannot be assumed.

---

## 3.7 Non-centered \(q^{(7)}\) route

The non-centered route avoids the centered one-slot \(g-h\) factor because it uses midpoint freedom:

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3).
\]

This channel is activated by \(x_m\ne0\), not by Gram anisotropy.

However, it introduces another weak factor:

\[
x_m.
\]

It is vulnerable to midpoint sign reversal and two-packet cancellation:

\[
x_1=\varepsilon,
\qquad
x_2=-\varepsilon.
\]

So the obstruction changes from Gram anisotropy to midpoint-orientation / packet-cancellation separation.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The non-centered route avoids }g-h\text{ but not quantitative non-concentration.}
}
\]

It may still be preferable if \(x_m\) is easier to control than \(g-h\).

---

## 3.8 Full vector \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7\)

The rank-two vector equation

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]

does not itself require choosing \(\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}\). In principle, one can use the whole vector.

But if the only live order-seven fixed-sector component at centered parity is proportional to \(g-h\), then the whole rank-two order-seven vector is small near \(g=h\). The full-vector formulation cannot recover the anti-fixed \(D\)-component because \(D\notin\mathfrak f_h\).

Thus full rank-two transport does not evade \(g-h\) at centered order 7. It only avoids selecting a particular scalar after the vector is already available.

---

# 4. Main conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{Within centered order-seven rank-two fixed-sector visibility, Gram anisotropy is structural.}
}
\]

The factor

\[
g-h
\]

appears because:

\[
\text{skew }J
+
\text{one }S\text{-whitening slot}
\]

produces

\[
pD+rI,
\]

and only the

\[
rI
\]

piece lies in the fixed sector.

When \(g=h\), \(r=0\), and the live information is anti-fixed:

\[
-2yBpD.
\]

Therefore there is no scalar or normalization inside the same rank-two fixed-sector channel that removes \(g-h\).

---

# 5. Viable next choices

There are three serious options.

## Option A — Prove quantitative Gram anisotropy

Attack directly:

\[
\boxed{
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\left|
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This keeps the centered \(K_1\) scalar.

## Option B — Compute \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) at \(g=h\)

Test whether the next odd rank-two coefficient survives the Gram-isotropy wall:

\[
\boxed{
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{g=h}\ne0.
}
\]

This is the best intra-rank-two escape.

## Option C — Enlarge to ambient anti-fixed transport

Use the nonzero anti-fixed channel

\[
-2yBpD.
\]

This avoids \(g-h\), but requires a new ambient/rank-four architecture.

---

# 6. Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{No viable escape from }|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}\text{ exists inside the locked centered order-seven rank-two scalar.}
}
\]

The exact next mathematical target should be one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove quantitative Gram anisotropy,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute and test }A_9^{\mathfrak f}\text{ on }g=h,
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{upgrade to an ambient anti-fixed coordinate.}
}
\]

My recommendation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{First compute }A_9^{\mathfrak f}\text{ on the Gram-isotropy wall.}
}
\]

Reason: proving

\[
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

looks like a genuinely new arithmetic phase-jet separation theorem, while an \(A_9\) computation may reveal whether Gram anisotropy is only an order-seven artifact or a structural fixed-sector obstruction.

## Agent 6 — Synthesis and Next-Fork Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Branch B is now the best next attack: compute the order-9 fixed-sector channel on }g=h.
}
\]

The centered order-7 scalar is dead as a protected proof gate because its fixed-sector component is structurally proportional to

\[
g-h.
\]

Branch A, proving

\[
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

looks like a new arithmetic phase-jet separation theorem and is unsupported by the current framework. Branch C, using the surviving anti-fixed \(D\)-component, is a real escape but requires a larger ambient bundle and a major architecture rebuild.

The most promising move is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\left.
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\right|_{g=h}
\stackrel{?}{\ne}0.
}
\]

There is a concrete order-9 mechanism that can survive at \(g=h\): one odd whitening slot \(X_1\), one second even whitening slot \(X_2\), and the skew mixed block \(Y=yJ\). The key new factor is not \(g-h\), but the **second-order Gram anisotropy**, i.e. the \(D\)-component of \(X_2\). This is exactly the branch the attached instruction identifies as the next fork after the \(g-h\) obstruction became decisive.

# 1. Branch table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{branch} & \text{mathematical status} & \text{main obstruction} & \text{recommendation}\\
\hline
\text{A. Prove }|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}
& \text{unsupported}
& \text{requires new arithmetic phase-jet separation}
& \text{deprioritize}\\

& \text{promising}
& \text{requires actual order-9 row table}
& \text{attack next}\\

& \text{real escape}
& \text{leaves rank-two fixed sector}
& \text{fallback only}
\end{array}

# 2. Why order 7 dies at \(g=h\)

The centered one-whitening-slot term is

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

Write

\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

Then

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_1YX_0-X_0YX_1
=
-2yB(pD+rI).
\]

The fixed-sector projection keeps only

\[
-2yBr\,I,
\]

where

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]

So on

\[
g=h,
\]

we have

\[
r=0,
\]

and the fixed-sector order-7 channel vanishes. The ambient signal remains:

\[
-2yBpD,
\]

but \(D\notin\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{order 7 dies in the fixed sector for structural matrix reasons.}
}
\]

---

# 3. The key order-9 candidate

At \(g=h\), the leading whitening is scalar:

\[
G_0=gI,
\qquad
X_0=g^{-1/2}I.
\]

But the higher whitening coefficients need not be scalar.

At centered parity, the structure is generically:

\[
X_1\in \mathbf C S,
\qquad
X_2\in \mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C D.
\]

Write

\[
X_1=BS,
\qquad
X_2=aI+dD.
\]

Consider the order-9-type channel

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1},
\qquad
X_{+,2}=X_{-,2}.
\]

So

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1.
\]

With \(Y=yJ\),

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
y(X_1JX_2-X_2JX_1).
\]

Compute:

\[
S J=-D,
\qquad
D J S=I,
\qquad
I J S=D.
\]

Then

\[
X_1JX_2
=
B S J(aI+dD)
=
B(-D)(aI+dD)
=
B(-aD-dI),
\]

and

\[
X_2JX_1
=
(aI+dD)JBS
=
B(aD+dI).
\]

Therefore

\[
X_1JX_2-X_2JX_1
=
-2B(aD+dI).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yBd\,I.
}
\]

This is the order-9 analogue of the order-7 one-slot channel, except the fixed-sector leakage is controlled by

\[
d=\text{\(D\)-component of }X_2,
\]

not by

\[
r=\text{\(D\)-component of }X_0.
\]

Thus order 9 can survive on \(g=h\) if

\[
\boxed{
d\ne0.
}
\]

---

# 4. What is \(d\)?

At \(g=h\), since

\[
G_0=gI,
\]

the expansion of

\[
G(s)^{-1/2}
\]

around a scalar matrix is ordinary scalar functional calculus to second order. If

\[
G_\pm(s)=G_0\pm sG_1+s^2G_2+\cdots,
\]

then

\[
X_2
=
-\frac12 g^{-3/2}G_2
+
\frac38 g^{-5/2}G_1^2.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
G_1\in \mathbf C S,
\]

so

\[
G_1^2\in\mathbf C I.
\]

Therefore the \(D\)-component of \(X_2\) comes only from the \(D\)-component of \(G_2\):

\[
\boxed{
d
=
-\frac12 g^{-3/2}(G_2)_D
}
\]

up to the harmless convention-dependent factor in the definition of the \(s^2\)-coefficient.

The same-point Gram matrix is

\[
G(t)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q(t) & \frac12q'(t)\\[2mm]
\frac12q'(t) &
\frac13q(t)^3+\frac16q''(t)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

At a centered even packet,

\[
q'(m)=q'''(m)=0.
\]

Then

\[
G''(m)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q'' &
0\\[2mm]
0 &
q^2q''+\frac16q^{(4)}
\end{pmatrix}_{t=m}.
\]

Thus the raw diagonal anisotropy in the second variation is

\[
\Delta_2
:=
q''-\left(q^2q''+\frac16q^{(4)}\right).
\]

So

\[
(G_2)_D
\propto
\frac1{2\pi}
\left(
q''-q^2q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\right),
\]

again up to the coefficient convention for \(G_2\).

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
d\ne0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}\ne0.
}
\]

On the Gram-isotropy wall,

\[
g=h
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

Substituting gives

\[
\Delta_2
=
(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3)
-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

There is no visible structural reason for this to vanish identically.

So the order-9 candidate survives at \(g=h\) unless one is also on the second-order Gram-anisotropy wall

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)q''
}
\]

with the exact convention-dependent normalization.

---

# 5. Source-jet availability

For a centered off-line packet,

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

the even source jets are nonzero:

\[
A_2=-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

\[
A_4=16(a^{-5}+b^{-5}),
\]

\[
A_6=-64(a^{-7}+b^{-7}).
\]

Thus

\[
q'',
\qquad
q^{(4)},
\qquad
q^{(6)}
\]

are available and generically independent enough to feed an order-9 row.

In particular, even if the order-7 fixed-sector channel vanishes because

\[
g=h,
\]

there is still independent even jet data in

\[
q^{(4)}
\]

and higher. That data enters \(G_2\), hence \(X_2\), hence the candidate

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yBd\,I.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source jets are available for an order-9 fixed-sector escape.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Remaining uncertainty

The computation above identifies a strong **candidate** order-9 survivor. It does not yet prove that the full actual coefficient

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is nonzero on \(g=h\). The missing checks are:

1. confirm the degree bookkeeping: the \(X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1\) term indeed contributes to the \(s^9\) fixed-sector coefficient in the draft’s ordinary-order convention;

2. verify no companion order-9 terms cancel

   \[
   -2yBd\,I
   \]

   identically;

3. check whether \(d=0\) is merely a proper incidence wall, not forced by the Gram-isotropy condition plus centered packet symmetry;

4. compute the actual constants in

   \[
   d\propto (1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
   \]

These are concrete algebraic tasks, not new architecture.

---

# 7. Branch assessment

## Branch A — quantitative Gram anisotropy

Target:

\[
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{hard and unsupported.}
}
\]

Finite \(\xi\)-like models tune

\[
g-h=e^{-Q}
\]

while preserving good-patch conditions. This route requires a new arithmetic phase-jet separation theorem.

Recommendation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{do not prioritize.}
}
\]

---

## Branch B — order-9 fixed-sector signal at \(g=h\)

Target:

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{g=h}\ne0.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{promising.}
}
\]

Candidate channel:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1
\right)
=
-2yBd\,I,
}
\]

with

\[
d=(X_2)_D
\propto
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Recommendation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{attack immediately.}
}
\]

---

## Branch C — ambient \(D\)-sector

Target:

\[
-2yBpD.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{real but major rebuild.}
}
\]

It avoids \(g-h\), but leaves

\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S.
\]

Recommendation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{keep as fallback if order 9 also fails.}
}
\]

---

(X_2)_D
\not\equiv0
\]

on centered off-line packets satisfying

\[
g=h,
\qquad

If this succeeds, the centered fixed-sector route can continue at order 9, replacing the failed order-7 Gram-anisotropy scalar.

If it fails, then the centered fixed-sector architecture likely requires either:

## Agent 6 — Order-9 Fixed-Sector Synthesis / Next-Fork Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue the order-9 fixed-sector route.}
}
\]

The order-9 candidate is real and structurally different from the failed order-7 scalar. At \(g=h\), the order-7 fixed-sector leakage dies because \(X_0\) is scalar. But the order-9 channel can use the \(D\)-component of the **second whitening coefficient** \(X_2\), and that component is governed by the new factor

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
:=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Thus the fixed-sector route is not yet dead on the Gram-isotropy wall. The next theorem should prove or refute:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1}
\right)\bigg|_{g=h}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}\,I
\neq0
}
\]

under the literal coefficient convention

\[
G_-(s)=G_0+sG_1+s^2G_2+\cdots,
\qquad
G_1=-\frac12G'(m),
\qquad
G_2=\frac18G''(m).
\]

The attached instruction correctly identifies this as the highest-value branch after the centered order-7 scalar failed through the \(g-h\) factor. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{question} & \text{answer} & \text{confidence} & \text{next action}\\

T_9^{(1,2)}\in A_9^{\mathfrak f}? 
& \text{yes, conditionally on the same ordinary-degree convention as }T_7^{(1)}

# 2. Degree bookkeeping

The known order-7 live term is

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_1YX_0-X_0YX_1.
\]

The proposed order-9 term is

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1.
\]

This replaces \(X_0\) by \(X_2\). Since \(X_2\) is the second even whitening coefficient, this increases ordinary order by \(2\). Therefore, if

\[
X_1YX_0-X_0YX_1
\]

contributes to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\), then

\[
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1
\]

contributes to \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) under the same convention.

So the degree verdict is:

\[
\boxed{
T_9^{(1,2)}\subset A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{conditional on the draft's accepted }T_7^{(1)}\text{ degree convention.}
}
\]

This should be verified in the order-9 row table, but it is the natural degree shift.

---

# 3. Exact \(X_2\) coefficient

Use

\[
G_-(s)=G(m-s/2)
=
G_0+sG_1+s^2G_2+O(s^3),
\]

so

\[
G_1=-\frac12G'(m),
\qquad
G_2=\frac18G''(m).
\]

At \(g=h\),

\[
G_0=gI,
\]

and

\[
G^{-1/2}
=
g^{-1/2}I
-\frac12g^{-3/2}\Delta
+\frac38g^{-5/2}\Delta^2+\cdots.
\]

Thus

\[
X_2
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}G_2
+\frac38g^{-5/2}G_1^2.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
G_1\in\mathbf C S,
\]

so

\[
G_1^2\in\mathbf C I.
\]

Therefore

\[
(X_2)_D
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}(G_2)_D.
\]

Now

\[
G''(m)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q'' & 0\\
0 & q_0^2q''+\frac16q^{(4)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

For a diagonal matrix \(\operatorname{diag}(A,B)\),

\[
(\operatorname{diag}(A,B))_D=\frac{A-B}{2}.
\]

Hence

\[
(G''(m))_D
=
\frac{1}{2\pi}
\left(
q''-q_0^2q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\right)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi}\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Because

\[
G_2=\frac18G''(m),
\]

we get

\[
(G_2)_D
=
\frac{1}{16\pi}\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{1}{32\pi g^{3/2}}\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Exact order-9 candidate coefficient

At \(g=h\), write

\[
X_1=BS,
\qquad
Y=yJ,
\qquad
X_2=aI+dD,
\]

where

\[
d=(X_2)_D.
\]

Then

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1.
\]

Using

\[
SJ=-D,
\qquad
JS=D,
\qquad
DJS=I,
\]

we compute:

\[
X_1JX_2
=
BSJ(aI+dD)
=
B(-D)(aI+dD)
=
B(-aD-dI),
\]

and

\[
X_2JX_1
=
(aI+dD)JBS
=
B(aD+dI).
\]

Therefore

\[
X_1JX_2-X_2JX_1
=
-2B(aD+dI).
\]

Multiplying by \(y\),

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yB(aD+dI).
\]

The fixed-sector projection keeps the \(I\)-component:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yBd\,I.
}
\]

Substitute

\[
B=\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}}
\]

at \(g=h\), and

\[
d=-\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{32\pi g^{3/2}}.
\]

Then

\[
-2yBd
=
-2y
\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}}
\left(
-\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{32\pi g^{3/2}}
\right)
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''}{128\pi^2g^3}
\left(
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\right)I.
}
\]

This is the exact candidate order-9 fixed-sector survivor, under the stated coefficient convention.

---

# 5. Packet evaluation of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)

For a centered packet

\[
f(t)=\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}+\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

expand at \(x=0\):

\[
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
=
a^{-1}
-
a^{-3}x^2
+
a^{-5}x^4
-
a^{-7}x^6+\cdots.
\]

Since \(x=2(t-m)\),

\[
q_0=a^{-1}+b^{-1},
\]

\[
q''=-8(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}=384(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

Thus

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
-8(1-q_0^2)(a^{-3}+b^{-3})
-
64(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

For the clean packet

\[
a=\frac14,
\qquad
b=\frac34,
\]

we have

\[
q_0=\frac{16}{3},
\]

\[
q''=-\frac{14336}{27},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=\frac{95944704}{243},
\]

and therefore

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac{12449792}{243}\ne0.
\]

This clean packet is not itself on the \(g=h\) wall. But the calculation shows that \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is a genuinely nonzero packet jet expression, not a symmetry-forced zero.

Now impose

\[
g=h,
\qquad
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3)
-
\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

This does **not** vanish identically unless an additional relation forces

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3).
\]

No such relation follows from centered parity or from \(g=h\). So:

\[
\boxed{
g=h\text{ does not force }\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
}
\]

---

# 6. Cancellation audit status

The candidate row is

\[
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

It can fail if:

\[
y=0,
\qquad
q''=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

or if another order-9 \(I\)-sector row cancels it identically.

The likely possible companions are:

\[
X_3YX_0-X_0YX_3,
\]

\[
X_2N_7X_0+X_0N_7X_2,
\]

\[
X_1N_7X_1,
\]

and higher mixed-block carriers \(Y_2,Y_4\).

I do **not** see a structural reason they must cancel

\[
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1.
\]

The candidate contains a distinctive product:

\[
y\,B\,(X_2)_D,
\]

i.e.

\[
y\,q''\,\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Any forced cancellation would need another order-9 \(I\)-sector term with the same jet-monomial content and exact opposite coefficient. That is possible only after a full order-9 row table is computed; it is not implied by parity.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{order-9 success is conditional on a no-cancellation row audit.}
}
\]

But unlike the order-7 \(g-h\) failure, the order-9 candidate is not killed structurally.

---

# 7. New incidence wall

The new wall is

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=0.
}
\]

This is a proper higher-jet wall, not implied by

\[
g=h.
\]

Is it easier than the old wall?

Not necessarily. Quantitative separation

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

would still be an arithmetic phase-jet theorem. But for local visibility, it is enough that \(\Gamma_{G,2}\not\equiv0\), so that one can move from \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\) to an order-9 visibility-positive base excluding

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

The order-9 route is therefore a genuine **local escape**, even if the eventual global quantitative problem remains.

---

# 8. Branch decision

## Branch A: quantitative first Gram anisotropy

\[
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is no longer the best immediate attack. It requires a new arithmetic theorem and is falsified by flexible finite \(\xi\)-like models.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deprioritize.}
}
\]

## Branch B: order-9 fixed-sector survivor

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{g=h}\ne0.
\]

This has a concrete survivor candidate:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue.}
}
\]

## Branch C: ambient \(D\)-sector

This remains a real fallback because

\[
-2yBpD
\]

survives already at order 7. But it requires leaving the rank-two fixed sector.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fallback only.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Proceed with the order-9 fixed-sector route.}
}
\]

The next exact theorem to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Order-9 Gram-isotropy escape theorem.}
}

On a centered reduced good patch with

\[
g=h,
\qquad

\qquad

}

with leading contribution

\right)

}
\]

The next push should be a full order-9 row-table computation to confirm:

1. this term truly lands in \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\);
2. no same-monomial order-9 row cancels it;
3. \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) is a proper incidence wall for centered off-line packets.

If this succeeds, the rank-two fixed-sector visibility base can be enlarged to cover the old \(g=h\) wall by moving from order 7 to order 9.

# Agent 3 — Exact constant and convention audit agent

```text
You are Agent 3: Exact Constant and Convention Audit Agent.

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I

including all factors of \(1/2\), \(\pi\), signs, and coefficient conventions.

\[
G_-(s)=G(m-s/2)
=
G_0+sG_1+s^2G_2+O(s^3).
\]

Then verify:
\[
G_1=-\frac12G'(m),
\qquad
G_2=\frac18G''(m).
\]

2. At \(g=h\), compute:
\[
X_2
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}G_2
+
\frac38g^{-5/2}G_1^2.
\]

3. Verify:
\[
(G_1)^2\in\mathbf C I
\]
at centered parity, so
\[
(X_2)_D=-\frac12g^{-3/2}(G_2)_D.
\]

4. Starting from
\[
G(t)=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q(t) & \frac12q'(t)\\
\frac12q'(t) &
\frac13q(t)^3+\frac16q''(t)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
compute \(G''(m)\) at centered parity \(q'(m)=q'''(m)=0\).

5. Verify:
\[
(G''(m))_D
=
\frac{1}{2\pi}
\left((1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}\right).
\]

6. Therefore verify:
\[
(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{1}{32\pi g^{3/2}}\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

7. Verify:
\[
B=\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}}
\]
at \(g=h\).

8. Multiply:
\[
-2yB(X_2)_D
\]
and confirm or correct:
\[
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

Deliverable:

\[
\boxed{

=
C\cdot yq''\Gamma_{G,2}g^{-3}I.
}
\]

If the constant differs from \(1/(128\pi^2)\), give the corrected value and explain the convention.
```

```text
+
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 21:36:58)

_Thought for 26s_

## Agent 6 — Synthesis / Layered Visibility Theorem

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order-9 fixed-sector escape is conditionally successful.}
}
\]

The centered order-7 channel dies on \(g=h\), but the order-9 channel has a new fixed-sector survivor controlled by the second Gram-anisotropy factor

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}:=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Under the current algebra, the layered visibility statement should be:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\qquad
\bigl(g-h\neq0\ \text{or}\ \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0\bigr)
\Longrightarrow
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\neq0,
}
\]

with visibility occurring at order \(7\) if \(g-h\neq0\), and at order \(9\) if \(g=h\) but \(\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0\). The remaining caveat is a full order-9 row-table / cross-channel cancellation audit. The attached instruction identifies exactly this order-9 survivor as the current target. 

---

# 1. Agent-result synthesis

## Agent 1 — order-9 row-table status

The candidate row is

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1},
\qquad
X_{+,2}=X_{-,2},
\]

so

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1.
\]

Relative degree bookkeeping is consistent:

\[
T_7^{(1)}=X_1YX_0-X_0YX_1
\subset A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\]

and replacing \(X_0\) by \(X_2\) shifts the order by \(2\), giving

\[
\boxed{
T_9^{(1,2)}\subset A_9^{\mathfrak f}
}
\]

under the same ordinary-order convention.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{degree bookkeeping: conditionally passes.}}
\]

---

## Agent 2 — \(K_1\)-sector isolation status

The row

\[
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1
\]

has the same structural character as the live order-7 row: one odd whitening slot, the skew mixed carrier \(Y=yJ\), and a whitening anisotropy slot. Therefore it belongs to the \(K_1\)-transport family, not the \(K_5\)-line, \(K_3\)-shadow, or pure same-point families.

At order 9, the relevant survivor is the \(I\)-component

\[
-2yB(X_2)_D I.
\]

A \(K_5\)-line term could only cancel this in full rank-two space on an additional line-alignment incidence, for example if the reference line \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) aligns with the \(I\)-axis. Otherwise, line terms cannot structurally cancel a quotient-nonzero \(K_1\) row.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{\(K_1\)-sector isolation: conditionally passes modulo line/cross-channel incidence.}}
\]

---

## Agent 3 — exact coefficient status

At \(g=h\),

\[
G_0=gI.
\]

Using the coefficient convention

\[
G_-(s)=G(m-s/2)
=
G_0+sG_1+s^2G_2+O(s^3),
\]

we have

\[
G_1=-\frac12G'(m),
\qquad
G_2=\frac18G''(m).
\]

Since

\[
G^{-1/2}
=
g^{-1/2}I
-\frac12g^{-3/2}\Delta
+\frac38g^{-5/2}\Delta^2+\cdots,
\]

we get

\[
X_2
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}G_2
+
\frac38g^{-5/2}G_1^2.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
G_1\in \mathbf C S,
\qquad
G_1^2\in \mathbf C I,
\]

so

\[
(X_2)_D
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}(G_2)_D.
\]

The same-point Gram model is

\[
G(t)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q(t) & \frac12q'(t)\\[1mm]
\frac12q'(t) &
\frac13q(t)^3+\frac16q''(t)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

At a centered even point,

\[
q'(m)=q'''(m)=0,
\]

so

\[
G''(m)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q'' & 0\\
0 & q_0^2q''+\frac16q^{(4)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Thus

\[
(G''(m))_D
=
\frac{1}{2\pi}
\left(
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\right)
=
\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{2\pi}.
\]

Since \(G_2=\frac18G''(m)\),

\[
(G_2)_D
=
\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{16\pi},
\]

and therefore

\[
\boxed{
(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{32\pi g^{3/2}}.
}
\]

At \(g=h\),

\[
B=\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}}.
\]

Now compute

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yB(X_2)_D I.
\]

Substituting gives

\[
-2y
\left(
\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}}
\right)
\left(
-\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{32\pi g^{3/2}}
\right)I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

So the exact candidate is

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''}{128\pi^2g^3}
\left(
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\right)I.
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{exact coefficient: passes under the stated coefficient convention.}}
\]

---

## Agent 4 — packet / incidence status

For a centered packet

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

one has

\[
q_0=a^{-1}+b^{-1},
\]

\[
q''=-8(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=384(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

Hence

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

For the clean packet

\[
a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34,
\]

we get

\[
q_0=\frac{16}{3},
\]

\[
q''=-\frac{14336}{27},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=\frac{95944704}{243},
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac{12449792}{243}\neq0.
}
\]

This clean packet is not itself constrained to \(g=h\), but it proves that \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is not symmetry-forced to vanish.

The first Gram-isotropy wall is

\[
g=h
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

This condition does **not** imply

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

Indeed, on \(g=h\),

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3)-\frac16q^{(4)},
\]

which vanishes only if the additional fourth-jet relation

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3)
\]

also holds.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\Gamma_{G,2}=0\text{ is a proper higher-jet wall, not forced by }g=h.}
\]

---

## Agent 5 — cancellation audit status

The candidate row is

\[
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

Potential order-9 companions include:

\[
X_3YX_0-X_0YX_3,
\]

\[
X_2N_7X_0+X_0N_7X_2,
\]

\[
X_1N_7X_1,
\]

raw \(N_9\) channels,

higher \(Y_2/Y_4\) carrier terms,

and \(K_5\)-line / normalization shadows.

No matrix-sector identity forces these to cancel the \(X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1\) row. A cancellation would require a genuine analytic identity among order-9 rows with the same \(I\)-sector output and the same source-monomial structure.

Therefore the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no structural cancellation found; candidate survives modulo a cross-channel incidence wall.}
}
\]

Define that wall as

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cross}^{(9)}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{cancellation audit: conditionally positive, full row table still needed.}}
\]

---

# 2. Layered local visibility theorem

The current local visibility theorem should be layered.

At order 7:

\[
g-h\neq0
\]

gives

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\]

through

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]

On the wall

\[
g=h,
\]

order 7 dies in the fixed sector, but order 9 gives

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

Therefore the conditional layered theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,
\qquad
\left(
g-h\neq0
\ \text{or}\
\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\right),
\qquad
\theta\notin\mathcal E_{\rm cross}^{(9)}
\Longrightarrow
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\neq0.
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
g-h\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
}
\]

while

\[
\boxed{
g=h,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
}
\]

modulo the order-9 cross-channel incidence wall.

by excluding:

\quad\text{and}\quad

On this base,

through order \(7\) or order \(9\).

# 4. Main remaining issue

This is still a local visibility theorem, not a global RH proof.

The new wall

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

may also be approachable super-polynomially. The global non-concentration problem remains.

But this order-9 result improves the local architecture: the previous base excluded all of \(g=h\). The new base only excludes the **codimension-two layered wall**

\[
g=h,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

plus cross-channel incidence.

So locally:

\[
\boxed{

The ambient \(D\)-sector remains a fallback if layered fixed-sector visibility fails at all higher orders. For now, order 9 gives an intra-rank-two escape.

## Agent 6 — Layered Visibility Synthesis / Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The order-9 fixed-sector escape is conditionally successful and should be promoted to the next local theorem.}
}
\]

The correct local replacement for the failed centered order-7 scalar is now a **layered visibility theorem**:

\[
\boxed{
g-h\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
}
\]

and, on the Gram-isotropy wall,

\[
\boxed{
g=h,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
}
\]

where

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}:=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The remaining caveat is not conceptual; it is the order-9 row-table audit: verify that no companion order-9 \(I\)-sector row structurally cancels the \(X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1\) contribution. The attached instruction frames exactly this synthesis task. 

---

# 1. Order-7 layer

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

Write

\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_1=BS,
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

The order-7 channel is

\[
T_7^{(1)}=X_1YX_0-X_0YX_1.
\]

Using

\[
SJ=-D,
\qquad
JS=D,
\]

one gets

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yB(pD+rI).
\]

Hence

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]

Since

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}),
\]

this gives the order-7 visibility implication:

\[
\boxed{
yB\neq0,\quad g-h\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
}
\]

modulo the already named order-7 cross-channel incidence.

On \(g=h\), \(r=0\), so the order-7 fixed-sector signal dies. The surviving order-7 signal is anti-fixed:

\[
-2yBpD,
\]

which is outside

\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S.
\]

Thus order 7 is exhausted inside the rank-two fixed sector.

---

# 2. Order-9 layer

Now consider

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1},
\qquad
X_{+,2}=X_{-,2},
\]

so

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1.
\]

At \(g=h\), write

\[
X_1=BS,
\qquad
Y=yJ,
\qquad
X_2=aI+dD.
\]

Then

\[
X_1JX_2
=
BSJ(aI+dD)
=
B(-D)(aI+dD)
=
B(-aD-dI),
\]

and

\[
X_2JX_1
=
(aI+dD)JBS
=
B(aD+dI).
\]

Therefore

\[
X_1JX_2-X_2JX_1
=
-2B(aD+dI).
\]

Multiplying by \(y\),

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yB(aD+dI).
\]

The fixed-sector projection keeps the \(I\)-part:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yBd\,I.
}
\]

So order 9 survives at \(g=h\) exactly when

\[
d=(X_2)_D\neq0.
\]

---

# 3. Exact second-anisotropy coefficient

Use

\[
G_-(s)=G(m-s/2)=G_0+sG_1+s^2G_2+O(s^3),
\]

so

\[
G_1=-\frac12G'(m),
\qquad
G_2=\frac18G''(m).
\]

At \(g=h\),

\[
G_0=gI.
\]

The whitening expansion is

\[
G^{-1/2}
=
g^{-1/2}I
-\frac12g^{-3/2}\Delta
+\frac38g^{-5/2}\Delta^2+\cdots.
\]

Therefore

\[
X_2
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}G_2
+
\frac38g^{-5/2}G_1^2.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
G_1\in\mathbf C S,
\qquad
G_1^2\in\mathbf C I.
\]

Thus

\[
(X_2)_D
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}(G_2)_D.
\]

The centered Gram model is

\[
G(t)=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q(t) & \frac12q'(t)\\[1mm]
\frac12q'(t)&
\frac13q(t)^3+\frac16q''(t)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

At a centered even point,

\[
q'(m)=q'''(m)=0.
\]

So

\[
G''(m)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
q'' & 0\\
0 & q_0^2q''+\frac16q^{(4)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

For a diagonal matrix \(\operatorname{diag}(A,B)\), the \(D\)-coefficient is

\[
\frac{A-B}{2}.
\]

Hence

\[
(G''(m))_D
=
\frac1{2\pi}
\left(
q''-q_0^2q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\right)
=
\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{2\pi}.
\]

Since

\[
G_2=\frac18G''(m),
\]

we get

\[
(G_2)_D
=
\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{16\pi}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{32\pi g^{3/2}}.
}
\]

At \(g=h\),

\[
B=\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}}.
\]

Thus

\[
-2yBd
=
-2y
\left(
\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}}
\right)
\left(
-\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{32\pi g^{3/2}}
\right)
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

So the order-9 survivor is

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
}
\]

---

# 4. Packet-level non-forcing of \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\)

For a centered off-line packet,

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma.
\]

The centered jets are

\[
q_0=a^{-1}+b^{-1},
\]

\[
q''=-8(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=384(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

Thus

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

For

\[
a=\frac14,
\qquad
b=\frac34,
\]

one gets

\[
q_0=\frac{16}{3},
\]

\[
q''=-\frac{14336}{27},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=\frac{95944704}{243},
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac{12449792}{243}\neq0.
\]

So \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is not symmetry-forced to vanish.

Moreover,

\[
g=h
\]

only gives

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

It does not imply

\[
q^{(4)}=6(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
g=h\not\Rightarrow \Gamma_{G,2}=0.
}
\]

The wall

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

is a new proper higher-jet incidence wall, not the same as the old Gram-isotropy wall.

---

# 5. Conditional layered theorem

Define the order-9 cross-channel incidence wall

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cross}^{(9)}
\]

to contain the locus where the row

\[
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I
\]

is structurally cancelled by companion order-9 \(I\)-sector rows.

Then the local theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad
\theta\notin\mathcal E_{\rm cross}^{(9)},\quad
\left(
g-h\neq0
\ \text{or}\
\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\right)
\Longrightarrow
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\neq0.
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
g-h\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
g=h,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
}
\]

This is currently **conditional**, because the full order-9 row table still needs to verify that

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cross}^{(9)}
\]

is a proper incidence wall rather than a structural identity.

But as a local architecture, this is a real improvement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{order 9 removes the first Gram-isotropy obstruction.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Updated visibility-positive base

Define

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+,9}
:=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\left(
\{y=0\}
\cup
\{q''=0\}
\cup
\{g-h=0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}=0\}
\cup

\right).
\]

On this base,

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\neq0
\]

through order \(7\) or order \(9\).

This base is strictly better than the previous order-7 visibility base, which had to exclude the whole wall

\[

\]

Now only the layered wall

\[
g=h,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

is excluded.

---

# 7. Next fork

## Continue order-9 local theorem

Yes. The next immediate task should be a full order-9 row-table audit proving:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm cross}^{(9)}
\text{ is a proper incidence wall, not a structural cancellation identity.}
}
\]

## Do not return to quantitative first Gram anisotropy

The need for

\[
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

has been bypassed locally by the order-9 layer. It may return later as part of a global quantitative problem, but it is not the next local target.

## Do not switch to ambient \(D\)-sector

The ambient \(D\)-sector remains a fallback. Since order 9 gives a rank-two fixed-sector survivor, stay in the rank-two architecture.

## Do not jump to order 11

Order 11 is relevant only if the order-9 cross-channel audit structurally cancels the survivor or if the double wall

\[
g=h,
\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

swallows the relevant reduced packets.

---

# Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Proceed with the layered order-7/order-9 fixed-sector visibility theorem.}
}

The exact next theorem is:

imply

with leading row

If this theorem is locked, the local visibility stack becomes:

\qquad

Then the project can return to the larger global problem: quantitative non-concentration away from the layered incidence set.

# 2. The candidate row is structurally real

The candidate row is

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1},
\qquad
X_{+,2}=X_{-,2},
\]

so

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1.
\]

With

\[
X_1=BS,\qquad Y=yJ,\qquad X_2=aI+dD,
\]

we have

\[
X_1JX_2-X_2JX_1
=

\]

hence

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=

At \(g=h\),

=

\]

and

\[

\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
}
\]

This row is not a bookkeeping artifact. It uses the mechanism:

\[
S\cdot J\cdot D-D\cdot J\cdot S
\leadsto I,
\]

so it is precisely the second-anisotropy analogue of the order-7 one-whitening-slot escape.

---

# 3. What must be computed next

Define the total order-9 fixed-sector \(I\)-coordinate at \(g=h\) as

\[

=

+

}
\]

plus any order-9 higher-carrier terms such as

\[

\]

if the draft’s order bookkeeping places them at the same ordinary order.

The most urgent computations are:

\]

and

\]

These are more dangerous than \(N_5\)-family terms because they can plausibly land in the same \(I\)-sector at \(g=h\).

# 4. Expected companion structure

X_0=pI,
\qquad

\qquad

up to the exact centered-parity sign convention.

+

The main audit question is whether the first terms are independent source carriers or whether they contain the same monomial

If they are independent, then cancellation is an analytic incidence condition. If they are the same monomial with forced opposite coefficient, the candidate row fails.

The row-table theorem must prove that

\]

is a proper analytic wall, i.e.

\not\equiv0.

Until that non-identity is proved, the order-9 theorem remains conditional.

Here

so

This is the desired layered visibility theorem through order 9, but it remains conditional on the cross-channel row-table audit.

At \(g=h\),

d=(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{1}{32\pi}g^{-3/2}\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and

\[
B=\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}},
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
}
\]

This is the order-9 fixed-sector survivor.

---

# 3. The dangerous remainder

The remainder has the schematic form

\[
R_9^I
=
R_9^I[N_9]
+
R_9^I[N_7]
+
R_9^I[N_5]
+
R_9^I[N_{\le4}].
\]

The \(N_9\) family appears harmless if the centered raw carrier is skew:

\[
N_9=F_9J.
\]

Then

\[
X_0N_9X_0=g^{-1}F_9J,
\]

and

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_9X_0)=0.
\]

The \(N_7\) family is more dangerous. At \(g=h\), write

\[
X_0=pI,\qquad X_1=BS,\qquad X_2=aI+dD.
\]

Then the \(N_7\)-companion row has expected \(I\)-component

\[
\boxed{
R_9^I[N_7]
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
}
\]

This can share the same \(I\)-coordinate as the candidate row. Therefore \(N_7^I\) and \(N_7^D\) must be computed.

The \(N_5\) family is also relevant. With

\[
X_3=cS,\qquad X_4=eI+fD,
\]

the expected \(I\)-component is

\[
\boxed{
R_9^I[N_5]
=
N_5^I(2pe-2bc+a^2+d^2)
+
N_5^D(2pf+2ad).
}
\]

So \(N_5^I\), \(N_5^D\), and the \(D\)-part \(f=(X_4)_D\) are the next layer of danger.

---

# 4. Cross-channel wall: formal definition is possible, properness is not yet proved

We can define:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm source}^{(9)}
=
\{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}=0\}.
\]

The true cross-channel wall is

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
=
\left\{
R_9^I
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\quad
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\right\}.
\]

And

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cross}^{(9)}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm source}^{(9)}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}.
\]

But to use this in the theorem, we need the non-identity:

\[
\boxed{
R_9^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\not\equiv0.
}
\]

At present, this is not proved.

A single witness with

\[
F_9^I
:=
R_9^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\neq0
\]

would prove properness. But without raw \(N_7\) and \(N_5\) coefficients, that witness cannot be certified.

---

# 5. Can we lock the theorem now?

Not yet.

The theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\ne0,\quad
(\Gamma_G\ne0\ \text{or}\ \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0),
\quad
\theta\notin\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(7)}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
\Longrightarrow
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})\ne0.
}
\]

But the phrase

\[
\theta\notin\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
\]

only becomes meaningful after proving

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
\]

is a proper analytic wall. That requires either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit computation of }R_9^I,
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{one concrete nonzero witness for }F_9^I.
}
\]

Neither is currently available.

---

# 6. Exact next action

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute }N_7^I\text{ and }N_7^D\text{ first.}
}
\]

Reason: the \(N_7\)-family is the closest same-order companion:

\[
R_9^I[N_7]
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
\]

It uses lower raw carrier order than \(N_5\), but combines with \(X_2\) and \(X_1^2\) to land exactly in the \(I\)-sector at order 9. If \(N_7^I=N_7^D=0\), the audit simplifies sharply. If they are nonzero, they define the main cross-channel incidence.

Second priority:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute }N_5^I,\ N_5^D,\text{ and }(X_4)_D.
}
\]

Third priority:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find a witness for }F_9^I\neq0.
}
\]

But a witness is hard until \(N_7/N_5\) are known.

---

# 7. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push should compute }N_7^I\text{ and }N_7^D.
}
\]

If those vanish, compute

\[
N_5^I,\quad N_5^D,\quad (X_4)_D.
\]

If the \(N_7\) terms do not vanish, determine whether

\[
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D
\]

shares the same source monomial as

\[
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

The theorem should be locked only after proving:

\[
\boxed{
F_9^I
=
R_9^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\not\equiv0.
}
\]

So the answer is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }N_7^{I,D}\text{ next; do not yet draft the theorem or move to global non-concentration.}
}
\]

# 1. Centered parity of the raw \(N_7\) carrier

At centered parity, the raw cross block before whitening has two structural facts.

First, the diagonal entries are even in \(s\). Schematically,

\[
N_{11}(s)=N_{11}(-s),
\qquad
N_{22}(s)=N_{22}(-s).
\]

Therefore their odd coefficients vanish:

\[
[N_{11}]_{s^7}=0,
\qquad
[N_{22}]_{s^7}=0.
\]

Hence

\[
N_7^I
=
\frac{N_{11,7}+N_{22,7}}2
=0,
\]

and

\[
N_7^D
=
\frac{N_{11,7}-N_{22,7}}2
=0.
\]

Second, the off-diagonal entries are skew at odd order. In the finite-\(s\) numerator convention used earlier,

\[
N_{12}(s)
=
\frac{\sin\Delta(s)+q_+(s)s\cos\Delta(s)}{s^2},
\]

\[
N_{21}(s)
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta(s)+q_-(s)s\cos\Delta(s)}{s^2}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
q_+(s)=q_-(s),
\]

and

\[
\Delta(s)
\]

is odd in \(s\). Therefore the odd raw coefficient has

\[
N_{21,7}=-N_{12,7}.
\]

Thus

\[
N_7^{\rm off}=F_7J.
\]

So the full raw carrier is

\[

\]

Consequently,

\[

---

# 1. Raw \(N_5\) parity classification

At centered parity,

\[
s\mapsto -s,
\qquad
t_+\leftrightarrow t_-.
\]

The swap action gives

\[
SIS=I,\qquad SSS=S,
\]

and

\[
SDS=-D,\qquad SJS=-J.
\]

The raw quintic carrier is odd under the centered endpoint swap, so it is anti-fixed:

\[
SN_5S=-N_5.
\]

Therefore the only possible sectors are

\[
D,\qquad J.
\]

Parity alone gives

\[
N_5^I=N_5^S=0,
\]

but it leaves open the possibility

\[
N_5^D\neq0.
\]

So we need diagonal parity.

---

# 2. Diagonal raw entries

The diagonal raw entries are same-point / endpoint-self terms. At centered parity they are even in \(s\):

\[
N_{11}(s)=N_{11}(-s),
\qquad
N_{22}(s)=N_{22}(-s).
\]

Hence the quintic coefficients vanish:

\[
N_{11,5}=0,
\qquad
N_{22,5}=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
N_5^I
=
\frac{N_{11,5}+N_{22,5}}2
=0,
\]

and

\[
N_5^D
=
\frac{N_{11,5}-N_{22,5}}2
=0.
\]

Thus diagonal raw terms do **not** produce \(N_5^D\).

If some normalization convention introduces endpoint-asymmetric diagonal correction terms, those are not part of the raw \(N_5\) carrier and must be classified separately in \(R_{\le4}^I\) or in the connection/normalization-shadow ledger.

---

# 3. Off-diagonal raw entries

The off-diagonal raw numerator has the same centered structure used in the \(N_7\) audit. In the usual convention,

\[
N_{12}(s)
=
\frac{\sin\Delta(s)+q_+(s)s\cos\Delta(s)}{s^2},
\]

and

\[
N_{21}(s)
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta(s)+q_-(s)s\cos\Delta(s)}{s^2}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
q_+(s)=q_-(s),
\]

and

\[
\Delta(s)
\]

is odd in \(s\). Therefore the quintic off-diagonal coefficients satisfy

\[
N_{21,5}=-N_{12,5}.
\]

So

\[
N_5^{\rm off}
=
F_5J,
\]

with

\[
N_5^S=0.
\]

Off-diagonal raw data cannot create a \(D\)-component, because \(D\) is diagonal. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
N_5=F_5J.
}
\]

=

# 2. Why raw lower carriers are harmless

At \(g=h\), the whitening sector pattern is

\[
X_{2j}\in \mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C D,
\qquad
X_{2j+1}\in \mathbf C S,
\]

under centered parity.

The raw carrier parity is

\[
N_b=(-1)^b S N_b S.
\]

Thus:

- even \(b\): \(N_b\) is fixed, so potentially \(I,S\);
- odd \(b\): \(N_b\) is anti-fixed, so potentially \(D,J\).

But the raw centered two-point block has additional structure:

\[
\boxed{
\text{odd raw carriers are skew off-diagonal: }N_{2k+1}=F_{2k+1}J;
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{even raw carriers have no off-diagonal symmetric }S\text{-part at centered parity.}
}
\]

So:

\[
N_{2k+1}^D=0,
\qquad
N_{2k}^S=0.
\]

This is exactly what cleared

\[
N_7,\quad N_5,\quad N_9,
\]

and it continues for lower raw carriers.

---

# 3. Sector check for each lower carrier

The order-9 lower-carrier piece has total whitening degree

\[
h=9-b.
\]

## \(b=4\)

Here \(h=5\), odd. One whitening side is odd and one is even.

An \(I\)-sector output from an even fixed carrier would require an \(S\)-component in \(N_4\), because schematically

\[
S\cdot S\cdot I \leadsto I.
\]

But centered raw parity gives

\[
N_4^S=0.
\]

An \(N_4^I\)-component gives \(S\) or \(J\), not \(I\), after one odd whitening slot.

Therefore

\[
\boxed{R_4^I[N_4]=0.}
\]

## \(b=3\)

Here \(h=6\), even. An \(I\)-sector output from an odd anti-fixed carrier could occur if

\[
N_3^D\neq0.
\]

But centered raw odd carriers are skew:

\[
N_3=F_3J.
\]

The \(J\)-sector remains non-\(I\) under the relevant even whitening patterns. Therefore

\[
\boxed{R_3^I[N_3]=0.}
\]

## \(b=2\)

Here \(h=7\), odd. As with \(b=4\), an \(I\)-output would require

\[
N_2^S\neq0.
\]

But centered raw even carriers have no off-diagonal symmetric component:

\[
N_2^S=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{R_2^I[N_2]=0.}
\]

## \(b=1\)

Here \(h=8\), even. An \(I\)-output would require

\[
N_1^D\neq0.
\]

But

\[
N_1=F_1J.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{R_1^I[N_1]=0.}
\]

## \(b=0\)

Here \(h=9\), odd. An \(I\)-output would require an \(S\)-component in the raw fixed carrier:

\[
N_0^S\neq0.
\]

At centered parity, the leading raw carrier has no symmetric off-diagonal \(S\)-part:

\[
N_0^S=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{R_0^I[N_0]=0.}
\]

Combining,

\[
\boxed{
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{raw}}=0.
}
\]

---

# 4. Correction rows are the only remaining risk

The above statement is about **raw pre-whitening lower carriers**.

If the draft’s \(N_b\)-notation folds in any of the following, they must be treated separately:

\[
\text{normalization/subtraction rows},
\]

\[
\text{diagonal endpoint correction rows},
\]

\[
\text{connection/covariantization rows},
\]

\[
\text{Gate A/B residue rows},
\]

\[
\text{line terms},
\]

\[
\text{shadow terms},
\]

\[
\text{background/core baseline rows}.
\]

The prior affine-forcing ledger classifies most of these as:

\[
\text{Gate A/B closed},
\quad
\text{connection absorbed},
\quad
\text{line},
\quad
\text{shadow/projected},
\quad
\text{fixed analytic background/core}.
\]

For the present order-9 visibility theorem, the only dangerous possibility is a correction row with an \(I\)-component satisfying a structural identity

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

No such identity is currently known.

Thus define

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9),\mathrm{corr}}
:=
\left\{
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\quad
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\right\}.
\]

Then the row is controlled modulo this named correction incidence.

---

# 5. Updated order-9 row

Since

\[
N_9,N_7,N_5,N_4,N_3,N_2,N_1,N_0
\]

are raw harmless for the order-9 \(I\)-row, we have

\[
\boxed{
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}.
}
\]

If correction rows are excluded by the fixed-convention affine ledger, then

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}=0
\]

and the theorem locks outright.

If not, then it locks modulo

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9),\mathrm{corr}}.
\]

---

# 6. Theorem-lock status

\[
\boxed{
\text{The raw row-table is now lockable.}
}
\]

The local theorem becomes:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad
\left(\Gamma_G\neq0\ \text{or}\ \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0\right),
\quad
\theta\notin
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(7)}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9),\mathrm{corr}}
\Longrightarrow
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})\neq0.
}
\]

Here

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

---

# 7. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Lock the raw layered visibility theorem.}
}
\]

The next action depends on whether the project accepts the previous correction-row ledger.

## If yes

Proceed to theorem finalization:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Layered fixed-sector visibility through order 9.}
}
\]

## If no

Do one final narrow audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{correction/normalization rows only.}
}
\]

Do **not** compute more raw \(N_b\) carriers. The raw lower-carrier obstruction is cleared.

The exact remaining object, if needed, is:

\[
\boxed{
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}.
}
\]

## Agent 6 — Final Correction-Row Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

The raw order-9 row table is now cleared. The remaining correction classes are either absorbed, closed, projected away, or belong to a residual analytic correction term. I do **not** see a structural reason for that residual term to cancel

\[
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\]

identically. But unless the draft’s correction convention explicitly excludes all background/core and normalization/subtraction rows, the cleanest theorem is conditional modulo

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}.
\]

This is exactly the remaining decision point in the attached instruction: raw rows are done; the final question is whether correction rows are absorbed/zero or become a named incidence wall. 

---

# 1. Correction-class table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{correction class} & \text{status} & \text{effect on theorem}\\
\hline
E_{\rm conn} & \text{absorbed by }\nabla^{\mathfrak f} & \text{no residual row}\\
E_{\rm GateA/B} & \text{closed under fixed-convention Gate A/B hypotheses} & \text{no residual row}\\
E_{\rm shadow} & \text{projected away by }\pi_{\mathfrak f} & \text{no residual row}\\
E_{\rm pure} & \text{zero by centered odd-germ parity} & \text{no residual row}\\
E_{\rm line} & \text{not necessarily zero, but line/cross-channel} & \text{incidence if scalar \(I\)-coordinate cancels}\\
E_{\rm bg/core} & \text{fixed analytic baseline under reduced convention} & \text{possible cross-channel residual}\\
E_{\rm norm/sub} & \text{convention-dependent; mostly absorbed/projected} & \text{possible cross-channel residual}
\end{array}
\]

Thus

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
\]

should be decomposed as

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
=
R_{\rm line}^{I,(9)}
+
R_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}
+
R_{\rm norm/sub}^{I,(9)}
\]

after the connection, Gate A/B, shadow, and pure rows are removed.

If the existing correction ledger proves these three terms vanish or are absorbed, then

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}=0.
\]

If not, they are best treated as a residual analytic correction.

---

# 2. Why the main correction classes are harmless

## 2.1 Connection / covariantization

The rank-two connection is

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).
\]

In a local frame \(E=(I,S)\), with \(A=Ea\),

\[
d_X(Ea)=E\,d_Xa+(d_XE)a.
\]

The frame-motion term is precisely the connection term

\[
E\Gamma_X^{\mathfrak f}a.
\]

Therefore connection, frame-motion, projection-motion, and whitening-gauge correction rows are not physical residual order-9 rows after covariantization:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm conn}^{I,(9)}=0
\quad\text{inside }R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}.
}
\]

## 2.2 Gate A / Gate B rows

Under the fixed reduced convention, Gate A and Gate B remain local algebraic closure hypotheses. Rows assigned to those gates satisfy

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm GateA/B}^{I,(9)}=0.
}
\]

If a row is not covered by Gate A/B, it should not be hidden there; it must be assigned to line, shadow, background/core, or normalization/subtraction.

## 2.3 Shadow and pure rows

For shadow and pure same-point rows, the centered sector logic is:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(D)=0,\qquad \pi_{\mathfrak f}(J)=0,
\]

and pure same-point odd rows vanish by centered parity.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm shadow}^{I,(9)}=0,
\qquad
E_{\rm pure}^{I,(9)}=0.
}
\]

---

# 3. Residual correction term

The only honest residual is

\[
R_{\rm corr}^{I,(9)}
:=
R_{\rm line}^{I,(9)}
+
R_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}
+
R_{\rm norm/sub}^{I,(9)}.
\]

So the total row is

\[
\boxed{
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
R_{\rm corr}^{I,(9)}.
}
\]

Here

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The correction incidence wall is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}
=
\left\{
R_{\rm corr}^{I,(9)}
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\quad
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\right\}.
}
\]

The row-table work supports treating this as a **proper analytic wall**, not a structural identity, because the raw row families

\[
N_9,N_7,N_5,N_4,N_3,N_2,N_1,N_0
\]

are all harmless for the order-9 \(I\)-coordinate. Any remaining cancellation would have to come from correction bookkeeping, not from the raw centered matrix algebra.

---

# 4. The layered theorem

Let

\[
\Gamma_G:=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

so that

\[
g-h=-\frac{\Gamma_G}{6\pi}.
\]

The local theorem should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\ne0,\quad
\left(
\Gamma_G\ne0
\ \text{or}\
\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\right),
\quad
\theta\notin
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(7)}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}
\Longrightarrow
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})\ne0.
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
}
\]

through the order-7 channel

\[
-2yBr\,I,
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0,\quad
\theta\notin\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
}
\]

through

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
}
\]

---

# 5. Final decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{The theorem is lockable modulo correction incidence.}
}

I would not spend another local push on raw \(N_b\) rows. They are cleared. The only optional remaining local check is a narrow correction-convention audit:

R_{\rm line}^{I,(9)},\quad

}

\[

}

## Agent 6 — Synthesis and Next-Strategy Decision

### Verdict

\[

}

The layered theorem gives a genuine local improvement:

\[
\Gamma_G\neq0 \Rightarrow A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0 \Rightarrow A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
\]

modulo the named correction incidence wall. But this is still qualitative. The next proof-closing target is not another local row computation unless the layered incidence set swallows reach. It is the quantitative bound

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The attached instruction correctly frames the next fork: either prove quantitative layered non-concentration, show finite \(\xi\)-like models can defeat it, or move to a higher anisotropy tower if the local wall remains too large. 

---

# 1. Route decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{route} & \text{status} & \text{next action}\\
\hline
\text{direct layered anisotropy separation}
& \text{main proof gate}
& \text{attack quantitatively}\\
\text{quantitative good-patch reach}
& \text{conditional}
& \text{needs Remez/Cartan-style control on admissible intervals}\\
\text{finite \(\xi\)-like falsifier}
& \text{likely dangerous}
& \text{test against the two-layer pair \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\)}\\
\text{explicit formula route}
& \text{not enough at one level}
& \text{only useful if aimed at this exact layered functional}\\

& \text{local fallback}
& \text{defer unless two-layer reach fails}\\
\text{paper integration}
& \text{premature for this round}
& \text{only after deciding global/tower fork}
\end{array}
