---

# 2. Direct layered anisotropy separation

The relevant functionals are

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The simultaneous layered incidence is

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

On \(\Gamma_G=0\),

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3,
\]

so

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3)-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Equivalently, simultaneous incidence imposes

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3)
=
12q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2).
\]

This is a genuine fourth-jet constraint, not forced by the first Gram-isotropy condition. Qualitatively, the order-9 layer is useful.

Quantitatively, however, the desired theorem is much stronger:

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Nothing in the local algebra currently proves this. It is a zeta-specific separation theorem.

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{plausible only with new arithmetic/global input.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Quantitative good-patch reach

The natural reach statement is:

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where \(I_\rho\) is the admissible sampling interval for an off-line packet after same-scale, endpoint, core-gap, Gram-positivity, and correction-incidence restrictions.

A qualitative statement follows from analytic non-identity only if the pair \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) is not identically zero. But a polynomial lower bound needs more:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

analytic continuation to a complex neighborhood of polynomial radius,

and coefficient/derivative control strong enough to prevent both functions from being exponentially small on the entire admissible interval.

This is exactly a Remez/Cartan-type problem for a vector of analytic functions. The missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\not\equiv0
\text{ on the admissible packet family, then it is polynomially large somewhere on }I_\rho.
}
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{conditionally reachable, but not justified.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Finite \(\xi\)-like falsifier risk

The finite \(\xi\)-like falsifier remains dangerous.

At the jet level, one can prescribe

\[
q_0=2,
\]

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

so

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
(-4+\varepsilon_1)-12+16
=
\varepsilon_1.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
-3(-4+\varepsilon_1)-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
12-3\varepsilon_1-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Choose

\[
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

So at the formal jet level,

\[
0<\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}<e^{-Q}
\]

is compatible with

\[
q_0>0.
\]

One still needs to check finite \(\xi\)-like realizability with positive kernels, quartet symmetry, same-scale packets, and Gram positivity. But earlier finite-product models were flexible enough to tune \(q_0\) and \(q''\), and adding \(q^{(4)}\) likely remains possible with enough packets/background degrees of freedom.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite \(\xi\)-like falsifier is likely to defeat any purely local proof of layered separation.}
}
\]

That means the theorem must use actual zeta arithmetic, not just finite Hadamard symmetry.

---

# 5. Explicit formula route

The explicit formula sees the linear ingredients:

\[
q_0,\qquad q'',\qquad q^{(4)}.
\]

But the layered pair contains nonlinear terms:

\[
q_0^3,\qquad q_0^2q''.
\]

A one-level explicit formula cannot directly control

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

or

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\]

with sign or lower bounds. Tensorization can express the nonlinear terms as multi-zero or multi-prime sums, but this does not create positivity.

The explicit formula may still be useful if one fixes an exact scalar functional, for example

\[
\Phi_{\rm layer}
:=
|yq''|^2\left(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\right),
\]

or a polynomial surrogate without absolute values, and then derives a zero-side expression. But absent positivity on the prime side, this likely rewrites the same cancellation problem.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{not currently a proof path; possible diagnostic only.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Anisotropy tower / order 11

The order-7/order-9 pattern suggests a tower:

\[
X_{0,D}\sim \Gamma_G,
\]

\[
X_{2,D}\sim \Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and likely

\[
X_{4,D}\sim \Gamma_{G,3},
\]

where \(\Gamma_{G,3}\) involves

\[
q^{(6)}
\]

plus lower jet combinations.

Thus if

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

the next local escape might be

\[
A_{11}^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\]

through an \(X_4\)-driven fixed-sector channel.

This is promising as a **local qualitative tower**, but it risks infinite regress:

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=\Gamma_{G,3}=\cdots.
\]

A finite tower theorem would need something like

\[
\max_{j\le J}|\Gamma_{G,j}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

That returns to quantitative separation.

So order 11 should not be the next push unless the two-layer incidence set is shown to swallow reach or unless the project wants to build a broader local tower.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local fallback, not the immediate proof gate.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push should attack global quantitative layered separation.}
}
\]

The precise theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

outside:

\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,
\]

the correction incidence wall,

and the reduced-base exceptional set.

A more focused first version is:

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

on the admissible reduced good-patch sampling interval.

The next six-agent push should not compute order 11 yet. It should test whether the two-layer incidence set can be approached super-polynomially by actual zeta data.

---

# 8. Exact next theorem / countermodel

The next target should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Layered anisotropy non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

For every RH-relevant off-line packet admitting a reduced good-patch sampling interval \(I_\rho\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If this fails in finite \(\xi\)-like models, the next target becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find the actual zeta arithmetic input that rules out the finite-model bad path.}
}
\]

If it also fails for actual zeta-compatible constraints, then the rank-two architecture remains local and non-closing, and the next local fallback is the anisotropy tower \(A_{11}\).

## Agent 6 — Synthesis and Next Theorem Decision

### Verdict

\[

The local theorem is now strong enough. The remaining proof-closing obstruction is quantitative:

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

on the admissible reduced good-patch sampling interval, outside the named correction/source incidence walls. The attached prompt correctly frames this as the next global bottleneck after the order-7/order-9 local visibility stack was stabilized. 

The two-layer anisotropy bound alone,

\[
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

is not enough if the source prefactor \(yq''\) can become super-polynomially small. Conversely, a lower bound for \(yq''\) alone is not enough if the anisotropy vector approaches its layered incidence set. The next theorem must control the product or a vector containing all relevant factors.

# 1. Route decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{route} & \text{status} & \text{next action}\\

# 2. Why the theorem must include \(yq''\)

The local rows are controlled by

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim yq''\Gamma_G,
\]

and, on the first anisotropy wall,

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim yq''\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Thus the natural local visibility vector is not merely

\[
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal V_{\rm layer}
=
\bigl(yq''\Gamma_G,\; yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\bigr).
}
\]

The proof needs

\[
\|\mathcal V_{\rm layer}\|_\infty\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

For a centered distinguished packet,

\[
y_{\rm lead}=-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\qquad
q''=2A_2,
\]

so

\[
y_{\rm lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}.
\]

This is nonzero for an isolated centered off-line packet with \(q_0A_2\neq0\). But the full-core quantity can be vulnerable to cancellation:

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R},
\]

so

\[
A_2\approx0
\]

is not ruled out by the current local formalism. Therefore \(yq''\) must be part of the same quantitative non-concentration problem.

---

# 3. The layered anisotropy side

The two anisotropy layers are

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The simultaneous local incidence is

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

On \(\Gamma_G=0\),

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

forces

\[
q^{(4)}
=
12q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2).
\]

So the layered wall is a genuine higher-jet condition. Qualitatively this is good: order 9 improves the local theorem. Quantitatively it remains open. A finite jet path can set

\[
q_0=2,
\]

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2,
\]

giving

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

Taking \(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2\) exponentially small defeats any polynomial bound unless actual zeta constraints forbid this path.

Thus the direct anisotropy theorem is not local-formal. It must be zeta-specific.

---

# 4. Remez/Cartan path: useful but insufficient alone

A Remez/Cartan strategy could work if we can supply four inputs.

Let

\[
G_1(m):=\Gamma_G(m),
\qquad
G_2(m):=\Gamma_{G,2}(m),
\qquad
H(m):=y(m)q''(m).
\]

The desired bound is

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|\max\{|G_1(m)|,|G_2(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A plausible analytic lemma would need:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

holomorphic extension to a complex neighborhood of polynomial radius,

\[
\sup |H|,\sup |G_1|,\sup |G_2|\le Q^M,
\]

and some non-tiny coefficient/witness condition such as

\[
\max_{r\le R}
\left(
|H^{(r)}(m_0)|+
|G_1^{(r)}(m_0)|+
|G_2^{(r)}(m_0)|
\right)
\ge Q^{-M'}.
\]

Without the non-tiny witness, analytic non-identity gives only qualitative nonvanishing. It does not prevent

\[
e^{-Q}
\]

approach to the zero set.

So the Remez/Cartan route is viable only as a framework after a zeta-specific coefficient/witness lower bound is found.

---

# 5. Explicit formula route: diagnostic only for now

The explicit formula can represent the linear ingredients:

\[
q_0,\qquad q'',\qquad q^{(4)}.
\]

But the relevant expressions contain nonlinear terms:

\[
q_0^3,
\qquad
q_0^2q'',
\qquad
yq''\Gamma_G,
\qquad
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Tensorized explicit formulas can expand products, but no positivity or coercivity has emerged. A possible coercive object is

\[
\Phi_{\rm layer}
=
|yq''|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
\]

or in a real formal model,

\[
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

But an explicit-formula proof would need a positive prime-side or Weil-type positivity statement for this exact nonlinear statistic. At present, it simply rewrites the cancellation problem.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit formula is secondary unless a coercive quadratic/multilinear identity is found.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Finite \(\xi\)-like adversary should be built rigorously in parallel

The strongest way to test the route is to build a finite \(\xi\)-like model satisfying:

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

with off-line quartet packets, positive paired kernels, same-scale selected core, strict core gap, Gram positivity, and

\[
yq''\neq0,
\]

while achieving

\[
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q}.
\]

If this adversary succeeds, then no finite-local structural proof can close the RH route. The missing input would have to come from actual zeta arithmetic beyond finite Hadamard symmetry.

So I recommend running the adversary in parallel with the direct theorem. It will clarify whether the proposed non-concentration theorem is even plausible without new arithmetic input.

---

# 7. Anisotropy tower / order 11 is not next

The order-7/order-9 pattern suggests a tower:

\[
X_{0,D}\sim \Gamma_G,
\]

\[
X_{2,D}\sim \Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and likely

\[
X_{4,D}\sim \Gamma_{G,3},
\]

where \(\Gamma_{G,3}\) involves \(q^{(6)}\) and lower jet terms.

This is useful as a fallback if the layered incidence set

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

is too large locally. But it does not solve the global problem. It would replace the desired bound with

\[
\max_{j\le J}|\Gamma_{G,j}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

That is the same kind of quantitative separation problem.

Therefore order 11 should wait.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push should attack the full source-weighted layered non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

The target theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-weighted layered anisotropy non-concentration.}
}
\]

For every RH-relevant off-line packet admitting an admissible reduced good-patch sampling interval \(I_\rho\), prove

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|y(m)q''(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This should be understood outside:

\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,
\]

the correction/cross-channel incidence wall,

and the reduced-base exceptional set.

A stripped first target is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

But the actual row lower bound will eventually require \(yq''\).

---

# 9. Exact next subproblems

I would split the next work into three focused attacks.

## A. Direct theorem attempt

Try to prove

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Start with the centered packet plus rest decomposition and identify whether rest terms can cancel all three factors simultaneously.

## B. Finite \(\xi\)-like adversary

Build or refute a finite product model with

\[
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q}.
\]

This is the fastest way to test whether the target theorem needs genuinely arithmetic zeta input.

## C. Remez/Cartan framework

Formulate the exact analytic lemma needed on the sampling interval \(I_\rho\), including interval width, complex radius, growth, and coefficient witness assumptions.

---

## Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not go to order 11 yet. Do not continue local row algebra.}
}
\]

The local row stack is good enough. The next theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If finite \(\xi\)-like models can defeat this, the project will need an explicit actual-zeta arithmetic input. If they cannot, the obstruction may finally be close to a proof-closing quantitative theorem.

## Agent 6 — Synthesis and Next Theorem / Countermodel Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The next push should build the rigorous finite \(\xi\)-like countermodel for the full source-weighted product.}
}
\]

The local order-7/order-9 theorem is stable. The live global target is

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''|
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But before trying to prove this for actual zeta, we need to know whether it is even a consequence of finite Hadamard symmetry, quartet symmetry, positive packet kernels, Gram positivity, and same-scale core geometry. The previous agent summary says those local structures already fail to protect the anisotropy vector, and the source factor \(yq''\) is also unprotected. 

So the most valuable next target is an adversarial one:

\[
\boxed{
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q}
}
\]

inside a finite \(\xi\)-like model satisfying the reduced good-patch constraints. If this succeeds, the route requires genuinely actual-zeta arithmetic beyond finite-product symmetry. If it fails, the blocking constraint may reveal the missing theorem.

---

# 1. Route decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{route} & \text{status} & \text{next action}\\
\hline
\text{finite \(\xi\)-like adversary}
& \text{highest-value falsifier}
& \text{build rigorously next}\\
\text{packet/rest decomposition}
& \text{useful diagnostic}
& \text{fold into adversary construction}\\
\text{Remez/Cartan reach}
& \text{conditional framework}
& \text{defer until a non-tiny witness exists}\\
\text{explicit-formula coercivity}
& \text{representation only so far}
& \text{defer unless adversary is blocked}\\
\text{scale/normalization audit}
& \text{important sanity check}
& \text{include in adversary setup}\\
\text{actual-zeta arithmetic separation}
& \text{ultimate theorem}
& \text{premature until finite model is tested}\\
\text{anisotropy tower/order 11}
& \text{local fallback}
& \text{defer}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Exact finite \(\xi\)-like countermodel target

Construct a finite even real entire model

\[
F(z)
=
e^{\mu z^2+\nu}
\prod_{j=1}^N
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\alpha_j^2}\right)
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\overline{\alpha_j}^{\,2}}\right),
\]

with

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

and off-line quartet packets

\[
\alpha_j=\delta_j+i\gamma_j,
\qquad
\delta_j\ne0.
\]

The target is to realize, on an admissible same-scale reduced patch,

\[
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q},
\]

while preserving

\[
q_0>0,\qquad g>0,\qquad h>0,
\]

\[
y\neq0,\qquad q''\neq0,
\]

quartet symmetry, positive paired kernels, endpoint separation, and preferably strict core gap.

The main jet target is:

\[
q_0=2,
\]

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2,
\]

which gives

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

For the source factor, keep

\[
|yq''|\asymp1
\]

if possible. Since

\[
y_{\rm lead}=-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\qquad
q''=2A_2
\]

in the centered distinguished-packet approximation, this amounts to keeping

\[
A_2\asymp1,
\qquad
q_0\asymp1.
\]

Then the product is

\[
|yq''|\max\{|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|\},
\]

and choosing

\[
0<\max\{|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|\}<e^{-Q}
\]

kills every polynomial lower bound.

---

# 3. Why this adversary is the right next test

The proof architecture now depends on whether actual zeta data can be quantitatively separated from layered incidence. A finite \(\xi\)-like adversary tests exactly which assumptions are insufficient.

If the adversary succeeds, then the following are **not enough**:

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

quartet zero symmetry,

positive paired kernels,

finite Hadamard-product structure,

same-scale core geometry,

Gram positivity,

and local rank-two visibility.

Then any successful RH proof from this architecture must invoke something more arithmetic, such as the Euler product or an explicit-formula inequality with positivity/coercivity.

If the adversary fails, the failure mechanism may expose a real structural theorem, for example a hidden positivity constraint coupling

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad A_2.
\]

---

# 4. Packet/rest decomposition role

The adversary should explicitly test two regimes.

## Regime A — anisotropy small, source nonzero

Target:

\[
|yq''|\asymp1,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2,
\]

with

\[
\max(|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|)<e^{-Q}.
\]

This is the strongest adversary. It shows the layered anisotropy itself can be made tiny while the row source factor remains live.

## Regime B — source small, anisotropy nonzero

Target:

\[
|yq''|<e^{-Q},
\]

while

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

This tests whether source cancellation alone can kill the row.

Given

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R},
\]

one can try to tune

\[
A_{2,R}\approx -A_{2,P}.
\]

If either regime succeeds, the product lower bound is not local-formal.

---

# 5. Remez/Cartan is not the immediate target

A Remez/Cartan lemma can propagate a lower bound once one has a non-tiny witness, but it cannot create one.

The relevant functions would be

\[
H(m)=y(m)q''(m),
\]

\[
G_1(m)=\Gamma_G(m),
\qquad
G_2(m)=\Gamma_{G,2}(m),
\]

and the product vector

\[
(HG_1,HG_2).
\]

A reach lemma would require:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

holomorphic continuation to a polynomial neighborhood,

growth bounds,

and a non-tiny derivative/coefficient witness:

\[
\max_{r\le R}
\left(
|(HG_1)^{(r)}(m_0)|+
|(HG_2)^{(r)}(m_0)|
\right)
\ge Q^{-M}.
\]

The adversary directly tests whether such a witness can fail under finite \(\xi\)-like constraints. So Remez comes after the adversary, not before.

---

# 6. Explicit formula route is secondary

The explicit formula can express linear pieces:

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad A_2.
\]

But the target involves nonlinear combinations:

\[
q_0^3,\quad q_0^2q'',\quad yq''\Gamma_G,\quad yq''\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

A source-weighted square

\[
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\]

is formally nonnegative on the zero side, but tensorizing the explicit formula creates multi-prime or multi-zero sums with no evident prime-side positivity.

Thus the explicit formula should be revisited only if:

1. the finite \(\xi\)-like adversary is blocked, or
2. one identifies a specific coercive kernel for the exact product.

---

# 7. Scale / normalization check

The adversary must be built in the normalization used by the paper. If raw zeta has

\[
q_0\asymp \log T,
\]

then the toy value

\[
q_0=2
\]

may simply represent a normalized local coordinate. If not normalized, the scale-correct bad path is:

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=12q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2)-6\varepsilon_2
+\text{the correction induced by }\varepsilon_1.
\]

More explicitly, set

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1.
\]

To force

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2,
\]

choose

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1)
-
6\varepsilon_2.
\]

This is the scale-correct version of the bad path.

The finite model should test this for \(q_0\) in the expected height scale.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push: build or block the full finite \(\xi\)-like source-weighted adversary.}
}
\]

Precise target:

\[
\boxed{
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q}
}
\]

with:

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

off-line quartet symmetry,

positive paired kernels,

same-scale selected core,

strict core gap,

Gram positivity,

and

\[
yq''\ne0.
\]

If this countermodel succeeds, the architecture requires actual zeta arithmetic beyond finite-product symmetry. If it fails, the obstruction that blocks it is the next theorem to prove.

---

# 9. Exact next theorem / countermodel statement

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Finite \(\xi\)-like source-weighted countermodel.}
}
\]

There exist finite even real entire functions of the above form and reduced good-patch samples such that

\[
q_0>0,\quad g,h>0,\quad yq''\ne0,
\]

but

\[
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q}.
\]

Or prove this is impossible and identify the first blocking constraint.

That is the next decisive attack.

## Agent 6 — Source-Weighted Finite-\(\xi\)-Like Countermodel Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The finite \(\xi\)-like countermodel succeeds at the structural/jet-realization level.}
}
\]

More precisely: I see no structural obstruction, from finite Hadamard symmetry, quartet symmetry, positive paired kernels, same-scale geometry, \(q_0>0\), or Gram positivity, to realizing

\[
0<
|yq''|
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q}.
\]

The most honest status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{countermodel succeeds modulo an explicit finite-dimensional Jacobian witness.}
}
\]

That is enough to shift the proof burden: the current local rank-two architecture cannot prove RH using only finite \(\xi\)-like local structure. A proof now needs actual zeta arithmetic beyond finite-product/quartet symmetry. This matches the attached instruction’s target: build or block the finite \(\xi\)-like source-weighted adversary. 

---

# 1. Requirement table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{requirement} & \text{status} & \text{evidence}\\
\hline
F(z)=F(-z) & \text{satisfied} & \text{use even product in }z\\
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z) & \text{satisfied} & \text{include conjugate packets}\\
\text{off-line quartets} & \text{satisfied} & \alpha,\bar\alpha,-\alpha,-\bar\alpha\\
\text{positive packet kernels} & \text{satisfied} & a/(a^2+x^2)+b/(b^2+x^2),\ a,b>0\\
\text{same-scale core} & \text{arrangeable} & \text{place tuning packets in same local window}\\
\text{strict core gap} & \text{arrangeable} & \text{put all other packets far outside window}\\
\text{endpoint separation} & \text{arrangeable} & \text{choose sample away from packet poles}\\
g,h>0 & \text{satisfied} & \text{choose \(q_0>0\) and maintain }q''>-2q_0^3\\
yq''\ne0 & \text{satisfied in Regime A} & q''\asymp1,\ y_{\lead}\asymp1\\
\text{product bound failure} & \text{satisfied structurally} & \Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ tunable to }e^{-Q}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Regime A: anisotropy small, source live

Target:

\[
|yq''|\asymp1,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2,
\]

with

\[
0<\max(|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|)<e^{-Q}.
\]

Use the jet path

\[
q_0=2,
\]

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
(-4+\varepsilon_1)-12+16
=
\varepsilon_1.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
-3(-4+\varepsilon_1)
-
\frac16(72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2)
=
\varepsilon_2.
\]

The good-patch Gram conditions survive:

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}=\frac2\pi>0,
\]

and

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac83-\frac23+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(2+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}\right)>0.
\]

The source factor is live. In the centered leading approximation,

\[
A_2=\frac{q''}{2}=-2+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{2},
\]

and

\[
y_{\lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}
=
-\frac19+O(\varepsilon_1).
\]

Thus

\[
y_{\lead}q''
=
\frac49+O(\varepsilon_1),
\]

so

\[
|yq''|\asymp1.
\]

Therefore

\[
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\asymp
\max(|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|).
\]

Taking

\[
\varepsilon_1=e^{-Q},
\qquad
\varepsilon_2=e^{-2Q}
\]

gives

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q/2}
\]

for large \(Q\), after harmless constant adjustment.

So Regime A defeats the source-weighted product if the target jet can be realized by finite \(\xi\)-like packets.

---

# 3. Regime B: source small, anisotropy live

Target:

\[
|yq''|\ll e^{-Q},
\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

Let

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R}=\varepsilon,
\qquad
\varepsilon=e^{-Q}.
\]

Then

\[
q''=2A_2=2e^{-Q}.
\]

With \(q_0\asymp1\),

\[
y_{\lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\]

so

\[
y_{\lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}\cdot 2A_2
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}
=
O(e^{-3Q}).
\]

Choose, for example,

\[
q_0=2,
\qquad
q^{(4)}=0.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-12+16
=
4+O(e^{-Q}),
\]

so the anisotropy vector is live:

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

Thus

\[
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
=
O(e^{-3Q}).
\]

This regime requires cancellation of \(A_2\):

\[
A_{2,R}\approx -A_{2,P}.
\]

Positive paired kernels do not forbid this, because second derivatives of

\[
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
\]

change sign depending on offset \(x\). Centered packets contribute negative curvature; sufficiently off-centered same-scale packets can contribute positive curvature. Thus a same-scale rest packet can tune the total \(A_2\) to \(\varepsilon\).

So Regime B also appears feasible in finite local packet models.

---

# 4. Jet realization in finite \(\xi\)-like products

Use

\[
F(z)
=
e^{\mu z^2+\nu}
\prod_{j=1}^{N}
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\alpha_j^2}\right)
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\overline{\alpha_j}^{\,2}}\right),
\]

with

\[
\alpha_j=\delta_j+i\gamma_j,
\qquad
\delta_j\ne0.
\]

On the critical line, each quartet produces paired positive kernels of the form

\[
f_{a,b,x}(m)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\]

where

\[
a=\frac12-\delta,
\qquad
b=\frac12+\delta,
\qquad
x=2m-\gamma.
\]

The jet map

\[
(\mu,\delta_j,x_j)_{j=1}^N
\longmapsto
(q_0,q'',q^{(4)})
\]

has more parameters than target jet coordinates once \(N\ge2\) or \(3\). The packet jet vectors

\[
V_{a,b}(x)=(q_0(x),q''(x),q^{(4)}(x))
\]

vary non-collinearly as \(x\) and \(\delta\) vary. In particular:

- \(q_0(x)>0\) always;
- \(q''(x)\) changes sign as \(x\) moves away from the packet center;
- \(q^{(4)}(x)\) has a different sign/scale profile from \(q''(x)\);
- the exponential factor supplies a smooth background degree of freedom.

Thus the jet target

\[
(q_0,q'',q^{(4)})
=
(2,\,-4+\varepsilon_1,\,
72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2)
\]

is not obstructed by the finite-product symmetries.

To make this fully rigorous, one should exhibit a \(3\times3\) Jacobian minor in parameters such as

\[
(\mu,x_1,x_2)
\]

or

\[
(x_1,x_2,\delta_2)
\]

with nonzero determinant at a seed configuration. But no structural reason suggests that determinant must vanish.

So the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite \(\xi\)-like adversary succeeds modulo explicit Jacobian witness.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Same-scale and core-gap compatibility

The adversary can be made reduced-patch compatible at the local-model level.

Choose all tuning packets inside the same local window:

\[
d_j\asymp d_P,
\]

so the selected core is same-scale. Put any additional packets far enough away that

\[
d_k<d_{k+1}
\]

has a strict gap. Since the tuning uses finitely many parameters, strict inequalities survive under small perturbations needed to set

\[
\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2.
\]

Endpoint separation is open, so choose \(m,s\) away from all packet pole locations and preserve that by perturbation.

Gram positivity in Regime A was checked explicitly:

\[
g=\frac2\pi>0,
\qquad
h=\frac{2+\varepsilon_1/6}{\pi}>0.
\]

In Regime B, with \(q_0=2\) and \(q''=2e^{-Q}\),

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac83+\frac13e^{-Q}\right)>0.
\]

So the reduced good-patch inequalities are compatible with the adversary.

---

# 6. Scale-correct version

If the paper’s raw variables satisfy

\[
q_0\asymp Q,
\qquad
q''\asymp Q^3,
\qquad
q^{(4)}\asymp Q^5,
\]

then use the scale-correct bad path.

Let

\[
q_0=\lambda Q,
\qquad
\lambda\asymp1.
\]

Set

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1.
\]

Set

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)q''
-
6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

The natural normalized product is

\[
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}.
\]

Choosing \(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2\) exponentially small again defeats every polynomial lower bound after normalization, provided the finite product can realize the corresponding raw-scale jets.

Thus scaling does not rescue the theorem; it merely rescales the bad path.

---

# 7. Strategic implication

If this finite \(\xi\)-like countermodel is completed with an explicit Jacobian witness, then the current architecture has a clear limitation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite Hadamard/quartet symmetry plus local rank-two geometry cannot prove the needed lower bound.}
}
\]

A successful RH proof would then require actual zeta arithmetic, for example:

\[
\text{Euler product input,}
\]

\[
\text{prime-side positivity/coercivity,}
\]

\[
\text{an explicit-formula inequality for the full source-weighted statistic,}
\]

or

\[
\text{a new zero-configuration rigidity theorem not shared by finite \(\xi\)-like products.}
\]

---

# 8. Final decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{countermodel succeeds structurally; next step is explicit numerical/Jacobian construction.}
}
\]

The exact next target should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Finite \(\xi\)-like source-weighted countermodel, rigorous version.}
}
\]

Construct explicit parameter values in

\[
F(z)=
e^{\mu z^2+\nu}
\prod_{j=1}^{N}
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\alpha_j^2}\right)
\left(1-\frac{z^2}{\overline{\alpha_j}^{\,2}}\right)
\]

such that

\[
q_0>0,\qquad g,h>0,\qquad yq''\ne0,
\]

same-scale/core-gap conditions hold, and

\[
0<
|yq''|
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q}.
\]

If the explicit Jacobian construction works, we should stop seeking a proof from the current local framework alone and isolate the missing actual-zeta arithmetic input.

## Agent 6 — Synthesis / Next Proof Fork

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current architecture is non-closing unless we add a genuinely arithmetic zeta input.}
}
\]

The finite \(\xi\)-like source-weighted countermodel is now too strong to ignore: it preserves the local symmetries and good-patch geometry while making

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q}.
\]

So the rank-two framework has reached its boundary. It gives a strong **local obstruction coordinate system**, but it does not by itself produce an RH contradiction. The next attack should be a hardened countermodel, not order \(11\), because we need to know exactly which actual-zeta feature is missing from the finite model. 

---

# 1. Route decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{route} & \text{evidence} & \text{recommendation}\\
\hline
\text{Euler-product / prime-side coercivity}
& \text{only plausible actual-zeta source, but no concrete positive form yet}
& \text{secondary; needs a specific functional}\\
\text{Explicit-formula positivity}
& \text{currently representational, not coercive}
& \text{do not lead with this}\\
\text{Zero-statistics rigidity}
& \text{known facts give heuristics/density, not deterministic jet separation}
& \text{insufficient as-is}\\
\text{Hardened finite countermodel}
& \text{best way to isolate missing zeta property}
& \boxed{\text{attack next}}\\
\text{Anisotropy tower / order 11}
& \text{local fallback; does not solve quantitative gap}
& \text{defer}\\
\text{Declare non-closing absent new axiom}
& \text{already effectively true}
& \text{state as current status, but keep falsifying}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Why Euler product is not yet a usable theorem

The Euler product is the obvious differentiator between actual \(\zeta\) and finite \(\xi\)-like products. But at the current level, it is not yet a theorem.

The needed statement would be something like:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Euler-product arithmetic prevents}
\quad
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)<e^{-Q}.
}
\]

Equivalently, a prime-side or Dirichlet-coefficient argument would need to force

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But the local quantities

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad A_2,\quad y
\]

are nonlinear functions of the zero configuration once the fixed-core/whitening/projection machinery is included. The standard explicit formula sees linear zero statistics; it does not automatically give a sign or coercivity for

\[
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

Thus the Euler-product route is only meaningful if we can identify a specific prime-side positive form. At present we cannot.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Euler product is the likely missing ingredient, but not yet a usable proof step.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Explicit formula / Weil positivity status

A possible target is

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}
=
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

This is nonnegative as a local expression, but an explicit-formula expansion would involve high-degree tensorized zero statistics:

\[
q_0^6,\quad q_0^4q'',\quad q_0^2(q'')^2,\quad q_0^2q''q^{(4)},\quad (q^{(4)})^2,\ldots
\]

A tensorized explicit formula would produce multi-prime convolutions, but no known positive sign. Unless one can exhibit a Weil-positive kernel or Hilbert-space norm whose zero-side localizes to \(\Phi_{\rm sw}\), this route remains representational.

So the current classification is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit formula: representation only; no coercivity yet.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Zero-statistics rigidity status

Known or conjectural zero statistics do not presently give deterministic lower bounds for this local jet relation.

The finite countermodel can tune

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad A_2
\]

while respecting quartet symmetry and positive kernels. Pair-correlation or GUE heuristics might say such tuning is rare, but “rare” is not useful for RH. We need a deterministic exclusion:

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\not<e^{-Q}.
\]

Known spacing/density information is too coarse. Simplicity only says zeros are distinct; it does not prevent super-polynomial approach to an analytic incidence surface.

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-statistics rigidity is heuristic only at this stage.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Hardened countermodel is the right next move

The current finite countermodel already preserves:

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

quartet symmetry, positive paired kernels, same-scale core geometry, strict core gap, endpoint separation, and Gram positivity.

The next useful question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the bad product survive after adding more actual-zeta-like constraints?}
}
\]

Specifically, harden the model by imposing:

\[
\text{Riemann--von Mangoldt-like zero density},
\]

\[
\text{realistic gamma/background term},
\]

\[
\text{simple zeros},
\]

\[
\text{local GUE-like spacing or at least repulsion-compatible spacing},
\]

\[
\text{far-zero tail matching smooth background moments},
\]

\[
\text{integer multiplicities or clusters replacing arbitrary continuous weights},
\]

and possibly an order-one entire function rather than a finite polynomial times exponential.

If the countermodel survives these constraints, then the current proof architecture needs something even more specifically arithmetic: likely an Euler-product / prime-side coercivity theorem.

If it fails, the first blocking constraint becomes the next theorem to prove.

---

# 6. Precise next target

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Hardened finite-\(\xi\) source-weighted countermodel.}
}
\]

Construct an even real entire function, preferably order one or approximated by finite products with controlled tails,

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

with quartet-symmetric off-line zeros, realistic local density/background, simple zeros, same-scale reduced core, and Gram positivity, such that on an admissible sampling interval:

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q}.
\]

The existing local jet targets are:

### Regime A

\[
q_0=2,\qquad
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,\qquad
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2,
\]

so

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2,
\]

with

\[
|yq''|\asymp1.
\]

### Regime B

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R}=e^{-Q},
\]

so

\[
|yq''|\asymp e^{-3Q},
\]

while

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

The hardened model should attempt both. Regime A is stronger because the source remains live; Regime B tests whether source cancellation alone kills the row.

---

# 7. What would count as a blocking theorem?

A meaningful obstruction would be a theorem of one of these forms:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite/order-one \(\xi\)-like products satisfying density + gamma constraints cannot realize Regime A.}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-scale positive quartet packets cannot tune }(q_0,q'',q^{(4)})\text{ to the bad jet path under realistic density.}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{Integer-multiplicity / tail constraints force }|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If none of these holds, then the only plausible remaining differentiator is the Euler product.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push: harden the finite-\(\xi\)-like countermodel.}
}
\]

Do not go to order \(11\) yet. Do not continue local row algebra. Do not attempt broad explicit-formula positivity until we know whether the countermodel survives stronger non-arithmetic zeta-like constraints.

The precise next attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can a finite/order-one \(\xi\)-like model with realistic density, gamma background, simple quartet zeros, and same-scale core still satisfy}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q}\ ?
}
\]

If yes, the rank-two RH proof route needs a new actual-zeta arithmetic axiom/theorem. If no, the blocking constraint is the next proof target.

## Agent 6 — Hardened Countermodel Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The hardened finite-\(\xi\) countermodel still appears to survive every non-arithmetic hardening.}
}
\]

The current proof architecture has now isolated its real missing input:

\[
\boxed{
\text{an Euler-product / prime-side coercivity theorem.}
}
\]

Order-one growth, Riemann–von Mangoldt-like density, simple zeros, quartet symmetry, gamma-like background, far-zero tails, and finitely many explicit-formula constraints do not appear to block the bad source-weighted local configuration. The only constraint not reproduced by the finite/hardened \(\xi\)-like model is full arithmetic multiplicativity / Euler-product structure. 

The target countermodel remains:

\[
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q},
\]

with

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

---

# 1. Hardening-constraint table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{hardening constraint} & \text{status} & \text{evidence}\\
\hline
\text{order-one growth} 
& \text{survives} 
& \text{local packet cluster can be embedded in an order-one canonical product with tail control}\\
\text{Riemann--von Mangoldt density} 
& \text{survives} 
& \text{density fillers can be placed symmetrically/far enough to act as smooth background}\\
\text{simple zeros / integer multiplicity}
& \text{survives}
& \text{weights can be approximated by clusters of nearby simple quartet zeros}\\
\text{gamma background}
& \text{survives}
& \text{fixed archimedean background can be offset by local packets and far-zero tail jets}\\
\text{far-zero tail}
& \text{survives}
& \text{tail supplies adjustable smooth Taylor background without destroying local packet geometry}\\
\text{finite explicit-formula constraints}
& \text{survives}
& \text{finite moment constraints can be matched by adding enough degrees of freedom}\\
\text{Euler product / multiplicativity}
& \text{not reproduced}
& \text{only remaining serious differentiator}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Why the countermodel survives non-arithmetic hardening

The bad local jet path is:

\[
q_0=2,
\]

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

With

\[
\varepsilon_1=e^{-Q},
\qquad
\varepsilon_2=e^{-2Q},
\]

the layered anisotropy vector is exponentially small.

At the same time,

\[
q''=-4+O(e^{-Q}),
\]

so

\[
A_2=\frac{q''}{2}=-2+O(e^{-Q}),
\]

and

\[
y_{\rm lead}=-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}
=
-\frac19+O(e^{-Q}).
\]

Thus

\[
|yq''|\asymp1,
\]

and therefore

\[
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\asymp e^{-Q}.
\]

This defeats every polynomial lower bound while preserving the local row visibility assumptions.

---

# 3. Order-one and density constraints do not block it

Embedding the local packet configuration into an order-one canonical product does not appear to change the local jet freedom. One can write schematically

\[
F(z)=F_{\rm local}(z)F_{\rm tail}(z),
\]

where \(F_{\rm local}\) supplies the bad jet and \(F_{\rm tail}\) supplies global growth, zero-density, and smooth background matching.

The tail can be arranged symmetrically so that

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

and its low-order local Taylor contribution can be made either small or deliberately used as a background vector. Riemann–von Mangoldt-like density is too coarse to prevent a finite local packet cluster from producing the bad jets.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{global entire-function shape and zero density are not enough.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Simple zeros and integer weights do not block it

The earlier positive-cone construction used weighted packet contributions. But this is not a decisive weakness.

A weighted local packet can be approximated by clusters of nearby simple quartet zeros. Small perturbations of widths and offsets give continuous local jet variation, so one can approximate the desired coefficients to accuracy \(e^{-Q}\), provided sufficiently many packets are allowed.

Thus simple-zero and integer-multiplicity hardening likely still permits:

\[
q_0=2+O(e^{-Q}),
\]

\[
q''=-4+O(e^{-Q}),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=72+O(e^{-Q}).
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{simple zeros do not supply the missing lower bound.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Gamma background does not block it

The gamma factor fixes part of the smooth phase background, but the local model has enough remaining degrees of freedom from nearby packets and far symmetric zeros to compensate its first few Taylor coefficients.

In raw scale, the bad path becomes:

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)q''-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

So if

\[
q_0\asymp Q,
\]

then

\[
q''\asymp -2Q^3,
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}\asymp Q^5.
\]

These are the natural microscopic derivative scales. The gamma background changes the baseline values, but does not by itself prohibit the same jet relation.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{scaling/gamma normalization only rescales the bad path.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Finite explicit-formula constraints do not block it

A finite list of explicit-formula constraints is a finite list of moment conditions. The hardened finite model has enough adjustable degrees of freedom—local packets, far packets, and background/tail parameters—to satisfy finitely many such constraints while retaining the bad local jets.

This is the key distinction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite explicit-formula consistency is not full Euler-product arithmetic.}
}
\]

The missing input would need to be an infinite/global coercive prime-side constraint, not a finite moment match.

---

# 7. The remaining differentiator: Euler product / multiplicativity

Actual \(\zeta\) has

\[
-\frac{\zeta'}{\zeta}(s)=\sum_{n\ge1}\frac{\Lambda(n)}{n^s}
\qquad(\Re s>1),
\]

with \(\Lambda(n)\) constrained by prime powers and multiplicativity. The finite \(\xi\)-like model does not encode this.

So the only plausible next proof route is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive prime-side coercivity for the source-weighted layered residual.}
}
\]

The needed theorem would look like:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for actual \(\zeta\), with proof using the Euler product or an equivalent prime-side positivity/coercivity principle.

A possible squared target is:

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}
=
(yq'')^2\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right),
\]

but previous work found this only representational unless a positive prime-side form is discovered.

---

# 8. Final decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Hardened countermodel survives all currently tested non-arithmetic constraints.}
}
\]

Therefore the next proof fork is not:

\[
\text{order }11,
\]

not more local row algebra,

and not another finite-product hardening pass.

The next target must be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Euler-product / prime-side coercivity for the source-weighted layered residual.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Exact next theorem to attack

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta source-weighted jet separation theorem.}
}
\]

For actual \(\zeta\), on every admissible reduced good-patch interval \(I_\rho\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|y(m)q''(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The proof must use an actual-zeta property not shared by hardened finite \(\xi\)-like models. At present, the only serious candidate is the Euler product / prime-side arithmetic.

If no such prime-side coercive theorem can be found, then the current rank-two architecture should be classified as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a strong local obstruction framework, but not an RH proof architecture.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-25 22:40:13)

_Thought for 8s_

## Agent 6 — Prime-Side Proof Fork Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No usable prime-side coercive theorem is currently visible.}
}
\]

The rank-two architecture has now reached an arithmetic boundary. The local order-7/order-9 theorem is stable, and the hardened finite-\(\xi\)-like countermodel survives all non-arithmetic constraints. The only plausible differentiator left is the Euler product / multiplicativity of actual \(\zeta\), but no concrete non-circular inequality has been found that forces

\[
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The next best move is therefore **not** order \(11\). It is to test whether even approximate Euler-product structure can realize the bad local jets. If yes, the current architecture is non-closing absent a very strong new arithmetic axiom. If no, the blocking mechanism becomes the next theorem. The attached instruction frames exactly this fork: search for prime-side coercivity, or prove that no finite/approximate explicit-formula constraints can block the countermodel. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{route} & \text{status} & \text{recommendation}\\
\hline
\text{prime-side coercive identity}
& \text{no candidate found}
& \text{do not assume; search only with exact functional}\\
\text{Weil/de Branges positivity}
& \text{likely RH-equivalent or not targeted}
& \text{avoid as black-box positivity}\\
\text{finite explicit-formula constraints}
& \text{insufficient}
& \text{countermodel can absorb finite constraints}\\
\text{multiplicativity / Euler product}
& \text{only plausible differentiator}
& \text{test via approximate Euler-product countermodel}\\
\text{prime-side uncertainty}
& \text{no pointwise lower bound}
& \text{diagnostic only}\\
\text{order 11 local tower}
& \text{local fallback only}
& \text{defer}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Prime-side coercive identity search

The desired local residual is

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}
=
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2),
\]

where

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The Euler-product side gives, for \(\Re s>1\),

\[
-\frac{\zeta'}{\zeta}(s)
=
\sum_{n\ge1}\frac{\Lambda(n)}{n^s},
\]

and derivatives give

\[
\left(-\frac{\zeta'}{\zeta}\right)^{(k)}(s)
=
(-1)^k
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)(\log n)^k}{n^s}.
\]

This sees linear derivatives. But \(\Phi_{\rm sw}\) contains high-degree nonlinear combinations:

\[
q_0^6,\quad q_0^4q'',\quad q_0^2(q'')^2,\quad q_0^2q''q^{(4)},\quad (q^{(4)})^2,
\]

and additional source factors from \(yq''\).

Tensorizing the explicit formula represents these terms as multi-prime or multi-zero sums, but no sign emerges. The von Mangoldt coefficients are positive on the half-plane of convergence, but after analytic continuation, oscillatory factors and tensorized convolutions destroy any obvious coercivity.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prime-side representation exists in principle; coercivity does not.}
}
\]

A usable theorem would need a very specific identity:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{\rm sw}
=
\mathcal Q_{\rm primes}
+
\text{controlled errors},
\qquad
\mathcal Q_{\rm primes}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

No such \(\mathcal Q_{\rm primes}\) is currently identified.

---

# 3. Weil / de Branges positivity audit

A tempting route is to encode the local residual into a positive explicit-formula form. But this is dangerous.

Weil positivity for suitable test functions is essentially equivalent to RH in standard formulations. If we choose a test function \(f_m\) so that

\[
W(f_m)\asymp \Phi_{\rm sw}(m),
\]

and then invoke positivity of \(W\), that risks being circular: positivity would be precisely what RH supplies.

A non-circular version would require an unconditional positive form that targets this residual but does not imply RH wholesale. No such form is known in the current framework.

Likewise, de Branges / Hermite-Biehler positivity would likely encode a Hilbert-space structure strong enough to imply zero-location facts directly. Without an independently proved non-RH-equivalent positivity theorem, this route is not safe.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Weil/de Branges positivity is either unavailable or likely circular.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Finite explicit-formula constraints are insufficient

A finite list of explicit-formula constraints is just a finite list of moment equations:

\[
\sum_\rho \widehat f_j(\rho)=P_j,
\qquad
j=1,\ldots,M.
\]

The hardened finite model has many free degrees of freedom: local packet positions, widths, far-tail zeros, and background/tail parameters. By adding sufficiently many far-tail symmetric packets, one can satisfy finitely many moment constraints while perturbing the local jets by less than \(e^{-Q}\).

Thus any finite explicit-formula consistency condition can likely be absorbed without killing the bad local product:

\[
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite explicit-formula constraints cannot be the missing theorem.}
}
\]

The missing input must be infinite/global, not finite-moment consistency.

---

# 5. Multiplicativity / Euler product

This remains the only plausible differentiator.

The finite \(\xi\)-like model can satisfy:

\[
F(z)=F(-z),
\qquad
\overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

quartet zero symmetry, order-one growth, gamma-like background, density, simple zeros, and finite explicit-formula constraints.

It does **not** encode the fact that actual \(\zeta\) has fixed Dirichlet coefficients

\[
a_n=1
\]

and Euler product

\[
\prod_p(1-p^{-s})^{-1}.
\]

The question is whether this full multiplicative structure forbids the bad local jet path:

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+O(e^{-Q}),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=6(1-q_0^2)q''+O(e^{-Q}),
\]

and/or

\[
yq''=O(e^{-Q}).
\]

At present, this is unknown. There may even be universality/interpolation phenomena suggesting that Euler products can approximate many local behaviors, though applying that near the critical line and to these precise derivative jets is nontrivial and must be handled carefully.

So the next sharp test should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Approximate Euler-product countermodel.}
}
\]

Can a finite Euler product or Euler-product-like Dirichlet polynomial approximate the bad local jets while maintaining the needed analytic continuation / functional-equation proxy?

If yes, the architecture likely needs an even deeper arithmetic input. If no, the obstruction to approximation is the theorem to exploit.

---

# 6. Prime-side uncertainty

A localization argument might say that local zero-side constraints require broad prime-side support. But uncertainty principles usually give tradeoffs, variances, or upper/lower bounds for norms, not pointwise lower bounds for a specific nonlinear residual.

To detect

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)}
\]

at microscopic scale, one needs long prime sums. Long prime sums have oscillatory phases. Without a positivity mechanism, the prime-side energy can cancel.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prime-side uncertainty does not currently yield the needed pointwise lower bound.}
}
\]

It may help estimate complexity of any future explicit-formula construction, but it is not the next proof gate.

---

# 7. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push: approximate Euler-product countermodel.}
}
\]

The exact target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Approximate Euler-product source-weighted countermodel.}
}
\]

Construct or rule out an Euler-product-like model whose log derivative locally realizes

\[
0<
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<e^{-Q},
\]

while preserving as many zeta features as possible:

\[
\text{multiplicative coefficients},
\]

\[
\text{prime-power logarithmic derivative structure},
\]

\[
\text{gamma-like background},
\]

\[
\text{functional-equation proxy},
\]

\[
\text{critical-line local packet geometry}.
\]

A minimal model would use a finite Euler product

\[
Z_P(s)=\prod_{p\le P}(1-a_pp^{-s})^{-1}
\]

or a Dirichlet polynomial log derivative

\[
L_P(s)=\sum_{p^k\le X} c_{p,k}p^{-ks},
\]

with constraints mimicking multiplicativity, and test whether the local jets can hit the bad source-weighted incidence to \(e^{-Q}\).

---

# 8. If approximate Euler products can realize the bad jets

Then the rank-two architecture needs a new axiom/theorem beyond local geometry, finite Hadamard structure, and approximate Euler arithmetic. The status becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{architecture non-closing absent a prime-side coercivity theorem.}
}
\]

The missing theorem would have to be stated explicitly as something like:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual \(\zeta\) cannot have local log-derivative jets within }e^{-Q}
\text{ of the source-weighted layered incidence set.}
}
\]

---

# 9. If approximate Euler products cannot realize the bad jets

Then the obstruction is the next theorem. One would need to isolate it as a concrete restriction, e.g.

\[
\boxed{
\text{multiplicativity imposes a lower bound on a jet determinant / Hankel form / moment matrix.}
}
\]

That would be the first genuinely promising arithmetic proof input.

---

## Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not return to local row algebra or order }11.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Attack approximate Euler-product realizability of the bad source-weighted jets.}
}
\]

The precise next question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can an Euler-product-like log derivative realize }
q_0,\ q'',\ q^{(4)},\ A_2
\text{ with }
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)<e^{-Q}?
}
\]

That is now the cleanest fork between “missing arithmetic theorem” and “current architecture non-closing.”

## Agent 6 — Approximate Euler-Product Fork Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The approximate Euler-product route remains unresolved, but it is now the precise arithmetic bottleneck.}
}
\]

Adjustable finite Euler products are flexible enough to realize the bad jets. Fixed-coefficient Euler products are the real test. The key obstruction is no longer local rank-two algebra; it is quantitative approximation by the prime phase flow

\[
t\mapsto (e^{-it\log p})_{p\le P}.
\]

The next theorem/countermodel should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-coefficient finite Euler-product bad-jet approximation.}
}
\]

or, if it fails,

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Prime-log Diophantine lower bound for bad-jet approximation.}
}
\]

This matches the attached instruction: the local architecture is stable, hardened finite-\(\xi\)-like countermodels survive, and the remaining differentiator is Euler-product / multiplicative prime-side arithmetic. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{route} & \text{status} & \text{implication}\\
\hline
\text{adjustable finite Euler products}
& \text{bad jets realizable}
& \text{not enough arithmetic constraint}\\
\text{fixed-coefficient finite Euler products}
& \text{open}
& \text{main next target}\\
\text{prime-phase equidistribution}
& \text{qualitatively plausible}
& \text{needs quantitative accuracy}\\
\text{Diophantine accuracy}
& \text{possible obstruction}
& \text{requires prime-log recurrence estimates}\\
\text{approximate functional equation length}
& \text{possible obstruction}
& \text{requires interpolation under length }T^{1/2}\\
\text{universality}
& \text{suggestive but not decisive}
& \text{off-critical-line issue}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Adjustable finite Euler products

Let

\[
Z_P(s)=\prod_{p\le P}(1-a_pp^{-s})^{-1},
\qquad |a_p|<1.
\]

Then

\[
-\frac{Z_P'}{Z_P}(s)
=
\sum_{p\le P}\sum_{k\ge1}
(\log p)a_p^k p^{-ks}.
\]

At a point

\[
s_0=\frac12+it_0,
\]

the derivatives are

\[
\left(-\frac{Z_P'}{Z_P}\right)^{(r)}(s_0)
=
(-1)^r
\sum_{p\le P}\sum_{k\ge1}
(\log p)^{r+1}a_p^k p^{-ks_0}.
\]

With adjustable \(a_p\), finite jet interpolation is flexible. Even restricting to the \(k=1\) terms, one has a linear system in the variables

\[
a_p p^{-s_0}.
\]

With at least three or four primes, one can interpolate analogues of

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad A_2
\]

up to the normalization conventions. Thus adjustable finite Euler products do **not** block the bad path.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The actual arithmetic content is not “Euler-product shape” alone; it is fixed coefficients.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Fixed-coefficient finite Euler products

For actual zeta truncations,

\[
a_p=1,
\]

so the tunable parameter is essentially \(t\):

\[
p^{-it}=e^{-it\log p}.
\]

A finite truncation has log derivative

\[
L_P(t)
=
\sum_{p^k\le X}
(\log p)p^{-k/2}e^{-ikt\log p}.
\]

The derivative jets are finite trigonometric sums with frequencies

\[
\log p^k.
\]

The question becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the one-parameter prime phase flow approximate the bad jet vector to }e^{-Q}\text{ accuracy?}
}
\]

The bad target is, in normalized form,

\[
q_0=2,
\qquad
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2,
\]

or in raw scale,

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)q''-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

If the fixed-coefficient prime flow can hit these relations to

\[
|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|<e^{-Q},
\]

then the current architecture remains non-closing even with approximate Euler-product arithmetic.

If it cannot, the obstruction is likely a Diophantine / recurrence-time theorem for prime logarithms.

---

# 4. Diophantine accuracy is the sharp issue

Let

\[
\Theta(t)
=
(t\log p_1,\ldots,t\log p_N)
\pmod{2\pi}.
\]

The logarithms of distinct primes are rationally independent. Thus \(\Theta(t)\) is dense in \(\mathbb T^N\).

Qualitative density is not enough. The required accuracy is approximately

\[
e^{-Q}.
\]

If

\[
Q\sim\log T,
\]

then

\[
e^{-Q}\sim T^{-1}.
\]

The relevant question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can }t\le T\text{ make the prime phase vector hit the bad target to }T^{-1}\text{ accuracy?}
}
\]

For \(N\) active primes, a generic torus hitting estimate suggests that to hit a ball of radius \(\delta\) in \(\mathbb T^N\), one may need time about

\[
\delta^{-N}.
\]

If \(N\) grows with \(Q\), this is hopeless on height \(T=e^Q\). But the bad jet target is only low-dimensional: it imposes a few scalar equations, not an arbitrary full \(N\)-torus target. That weakens the obstruction.

So the needed theorem is not raw simultaneous approximation of all prime phases. It is a lower bound for a **specific trigonometric polynomial map**:

\[
t\mapsto
\left(
\Gamma_G(t),\Gamma_{G,2}(t),y(t)q''(t)
\right).
\]

A possible obstruction theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{t\in I_\rho}
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\ge T^{-A}.
}
\]

But no current Diophantine theorem for prime logarithms gives this directly.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Diophantine accuracy is the main unresolved arithmetic subproblem.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Approximate functional equation length

The approximate functional equation restricts effective prime/frequency support to lengths around

\[
T^{1/2}
\]

for \(\zeta(1/2+it)\), with related ranges for log-derivatives depending on smoothing and truncation.

This matters because interpolation power depends on the available frequencies and coefficients.

The key question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can a Dirichlet polynomial of natural AFE length reproduce the bad low-order jet at height }T?
}
\]

A length \(T^{1/2}\) polynomial has many frequencies, so it may be flexible enough. But coefficients are fixed and structured. The dual sum and gamma factor impose additional relations, though no obvious one targets

\[
\Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2},\quad yq''.
\]

Thus AFE length is a possible quantitative obstruction, but not yet a theorem.

The required next result would be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Bad-jet interpolation is impossible for fixed-coefficient AFE Dirichlet polynomials of length }T^{1/2}.
}
\]

or the opposite countermodel.

---

# 6. Universality

Voronin universality and hybrid universality suggest zeta and Euler products can approximate broad classes of local analytic behavior in the strip

\[
\frac12<\sigma<1.
\]

This is suggestive but not decisive:

- the target is on or tied to the critical line;
- the local objects are phase/log-derivative jets with fixed reduced-core conventions;
- universality is qualitative or positive-density in \(t\), not necessarily \(e^{-Q}\)-accurate at prescribed height scale;
- universality does not directly incorporate off-line zero-packet geometry.

Still, universality heuristically undermines any hope that Euler-product structure alone imposes rigid local jet inequalities, unless the critical line imposes special constraints.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{universality suggests bad jets may be possible, but does not prove the needed countermodel.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push: fixed-coefficient finite Euler-product bad-jet approximation.}
}
\]

The target model is:

\[
L_X(t)
=
\sum_{p^k\le X}
(\log p)p^{-k/2}e^{-ikt\log p}
\]

or a smoothed AFE-compatible log-derivative model.

The goal is to determine whether there exists \(t\) in the admissible height range such that the induced normalized jets satisfy

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q}.
\]

If yes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{approximate Euler-product arithmetic does not save the architecture.}
}
\]

If no:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the obstruction is the next arithmetic theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Exact next theorem / countermodel

## Countermodel target

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-coefficient finite Euler-product bad-jet approximation.}
}
\]

There exist \(X\), \(T\), and \(t\asymp T\) such that the finite log derivative

\[
L_X(t)
=
\sum_{p^k\le X}
(\log p)p^{-k/2}e^{-ikt\log p}
\]

produces local phase jets satisfying

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q}.
\]

## Obstruction target

If this fails, prove:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Prime-log Diophantine lower bound for bad-jet approximation.}
}
\]

For fixed-coefficient Euler-product truncations of natural length,

\[
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on admissible reduced good patches.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{The next fork is fixed-coefficient Euler-product interpolation.}
}
\]

Do not go back to local row algebra or order \(11\). The precise next problem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the prime phase flow }t\mapsto(e^{-it\log p})\text{ approximate the bad source-weighted jet configuration to }e^{-Q}\text{ accuracy?}
}
\]

That is the cleanest remaining separation between actual zeta arithmetic and the hardened finite-\(\xi\) countermodel.

## Agent 6 — Fixed-Coefficient Euler-Product Fork Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push should be an AFE / fixed-prime jet-map numerical-analytic study.}
}
\]

The exact arithmetic bottleneck is now clear:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the fixed-coefficient prime phase flow approximate the bad source-weighted jet configuration to }e^{-Q}\text{ accuracy?}
}
\]

I do **not** think we can honestly choose yet between:

\[
\boxed{\text{fixed-coefficient Euler-product countermodel}}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{\text{prime-log Diophantine obstruction}}.
\]

The critical uncertainty is whether the bad set is effectively low-codimension in the prime-phase jet map. If it is, hitting may be plausible despite high-dimensional torus recurrence. If it secretly requires high-dimensional phase alignment, then Diophantine/height constraints may block it. The attached instruction frames exactly this fork. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{question} & \text{status} & \text{next action}\\
\hline
\text{jet-map definition} 
& \text{available as surrogate} 
& \text{formalize }J_X(t)=(J_0,J_2,J_4)\\
N_{\rm eff}
& \text{uncertain}
& \text{estimate from active prime/prime-power support}\\
\text{torus hitting}
& \text{ambiguous}
& \text{depends on effective codimension, not full torus dimension}\\
\text{codimension/transversality}
& \text{main unknown}
& \text{compute Jacobian / sample numerically}\\
\text{AFE constraints}
& \text{possible but unproven obstruction}
& \text{include AFE-compatible model after toy model}\\
\text{numerical experiment}
& \text{now necessary}
& \text{run fixed-prime bad-residual search}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Candidate fixed-prime jet map

Use the finite fixed-coefficient log-derivative surrogate

\[
L_X(t)
=
\sum_{p^k\le X}
(\log p)p^{-k/2}e^{-ik t\log p}.
\]

Then

\[
\frac{d^r}{dt^r}L_X(t)
=
\sum_{p^k\le X}
(\log p)(-ik\log p)^r p^{-k/2}e^{-ik t\log p}.
\]

A simple real surrogate is:

\[
J_0(t)=B_0+\Re L_X(t),
\]

\[
J_2(t)=B_2+\Re L_X''(t),
\]

\[
J_4(t)=B_4+\Re L_X^{(4)}(t),
\]

with \(B_0,B_2,B_4\) representing gamma/background normalization.

Define

\[
R_1(t)=J_2(t)-6J_0(t)+2J_0(t)^3,
\]

\[
R_2(t)=(1-J_0(t)^2)J_2(t)-\frac16J_4(t),
\]

and source proxy

\[
H(t)=-\frac{J_0(t)J_2(t)^3}{288}.
\]

The test residual is

\[
\mathcal P(t)=|H(t)|\max\{|R_1(t)|,|R_2(t)|\}.
\]

This is not yet the full zeta object, but it is the right first fixed-coefficient arithmetic surrogate.

---

# 3. Torus hitting: why the answer is not obvious

The prime phase map is

\[
\Theta(t)
=
(t\log p_1,\ldots,t\log p_N)\pmod{2\pi}.
\]

For full \(N\)-torus targeting, an \(\epsilon\)-ball hit would require time roughly

\[
\epsilon^{-N}.
\]

With

\[
\epsilon=e^{-Q},
\]

this is

\[
e^{QN}.
\]

If \(N\asymp Q\), this is

\[
e^{Q^2},
\]

far beyond height \(T=e^Q\).

But the bad condition is not an arbitrary \(N\)-phase target. It is only two scalar residual equations:

\[
R_1\approx0,\qquad R_2\approx0,
\]

with optional source-live condition

\[
|H|\asymp1.
\]

If the map

\[
\Theta\mapsto (R_1,R_2,H)
\]

is sufficiently transverse and low-codimension, the small-residual set may have measure roughly

\[
\epsilon^2,
\]

not

\[
\epsilon^N.
\]

Then one might expect hits in time

\[
\epsilon^{-2}=e^{2Q}=T^2,
\]

still larger than \(T\), but much less hopeless. With interval length, smoothing, many local samples, or weaker polynomial target, the conclusion changes.

For the actual proof lower bound, the threshold is polynomial:

\[
Q^{-A},
\]

not \(e^{-Q}\). A codimension-two target of radius \(Q^{-A}\) has measure about

\[
Q^{-2A},
\]

so hitting may be common. This suggests that a lower bound

\[
\mathcal P(t)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is unlikely to follow from generic phase randomness alone.

Thus the core issue is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is the bad set low-codimension and transversely hit by the fixed prime-phase flow?}
}
\]

---

# 4. AFE compatibility

The toy fixed-prime model should be followed by an AFE-compatible model. The approximate functional equation introduces:

\[
\text{main Dirichlet polynomial},
\]

\[
\text{dual sum},
\]

\[
\text{gamma phase},
\]

\[
\text{smoothing weights}.
\]

These may shift the background vector

\[
(B_0,B_2,B_4),
\]

and alter the effective support, but they do not obviously impose algebraic relations like

\[
R_1\not\approx0
\quad\text{or}\quad
R_2\not\approx0.
\]

So AFE constraints are not presently a proof obstruction. They must be tested in the same numerical/analytic jet-map framework.

---

# 5. Universality reading

Universality in

\[
\frac12<\sigma<1
\]

suggests that Euler-product arithmetic is locally flexible. It does not prove critical-line bad jets occur, but it weakens the expectation that multiplicativity alone forces a local jet lower bound.

Thus universality is evidence against a naive rigidity theorem, but not decisive.

---

# 6. Recommended first numerical experiment

Use a toy model first.

Choose:

\[
P=200,\quad 1000,\quad 5000
\]

as prime cutoffs, and optionally include prime powers \(p^k\le X\).

Define

\[
L_P(t)=\sum_{p\le P}(\log p)p^{-1/2}e^{-it\log p}.
\]

For initial testing, set background constants to target the known bad scale, e.g.

\[
B_0=2-\operatorname{mean}(\Re L_P),
\]

and choose \(B_2,B_4\) similarly to place the residual near the bad regime, or scan several backgrounds.

Define:

\[
J_0=B_0+\Re L_P,
\]

\[
J_2=B_2+\Re L_P'',
\]

\[
J_4=B_4+\Re L_P^{(4)}.
\]

Then

\[
R_1=J_2-6J_0+2J_0^3,
\]

\[
R_2=(1-J_0^2)J_2-\frac16J_4,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{J_0J_2^3}{288},
\]

and

\[
\mathcal P(t)=|H|\max(|R_1|,|R_2|).
\]

Scan

\[
t\in[T,T+W]
\]

with sampling rate at least

\[
\Delta t\ll \frac{1}{\log P}
\]

and preferably adaptive minimization near local minima.

Diagnostics:

1. minimum of \(\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)\);
2. minimum of \(\mathcal P(t)\);
3. distribution of \((R_1,R_2)\);
4. empirical codimension: does
   \[
   \mathbb P(\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)<\epsilon)
   \]
   scale like \(\epsilon^2\)?
5. source-live test: among small-residual hits, is \(H\) typically nonzero?

Expected outcomes:

- If bad jets are hittable, minima decay quickly with \(W\) and the residual distribution shows low-codimension behavior.
- If prime-log Diophantine obstruction exists, residual minima plateau above the random low-codimension expectation.

---

# 7. Next theorem / countermodel fork

## If numerical/analytic toy model finds small residuals

Then pursue:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-coefficient finite Euler-product bad-jet approximation.}
}
\]

The theorem/countermodel would say there exist \(X,T,t\) such that the fixed-coefficient prime sum realizes

\[
0<
|H(t)|\max(|R_1(t)|,|R_2(t)|)<e^{-Q}
\]

or at least \(<Q^{-A}\) for arbitrary \(A\).

This would strongly suggest the rank-two architecture is non-closing absent a deeper exact-zeta obstruction.

## If toy model cannot hit small residuals

Then pursue:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Prime-log Diophantine bad-jet lower bound.}
}
\]

A possible theorem would be:

\[
|H(t)|\max(|R_1(t)|,|R_2(t)|)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

for fixed-coefficient Euler-product truncations of natural length on admissible height intervals.

But this would be a very nonstandard Diophantine/trigonometric lower-bound theorem.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Run the fixed-prime jet-map numerical/analytic study next.}
}
\]

The next exact target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-coefficient finite Euler-product bad-jet approximation experiment.}
}
\]

Do not return to local row algebra or order \(11\). The decisive question is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the fixed prime phase flow hit the source-weighted layered incidence set at polynomial or super-polynomial scale?}
}
\]

This is the cleanest remaining fork between:

\[
\boxed{
\text{current architecture non-closing absent new arithmetic input}
}

and
