## Agent 6 — Corrected Projective Branch Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The clean projective branch does not yet survive as a proof route.}
}
\]

It remains a useful diagnostic: if

\[
A_7=H G_1,\qquad A_9=H G_2,\qquad H=yq'',
\]

then

\[
[A_7:A_9]=[G_1:G_2]=[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}]
\]

formally removes the source factor. But the actual corrected rows contain residual correction terms, and unless those are zero, absorbed, or \(H\)-divisible, the clean ratio is not the true projective coordinate near \(H=0\). The attached instruction correctly identifies this as the decisive audit for the projective branch. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{issue} & \text{status} & \text{decision}\\
\hline
\text{order-7 correction divisibility} 
& \text{not fully certified} 
& \text{must be assumed or audited}\\
\text{order-9 correction divisibility} 
& \text{residual }R_{\rm corr}^{(9)}\text{ remains} 
& \text{clean ratio conditional}\\
\text{line/background/normalization meaning} 
& \text{likely cross-channel/baseline, not packet-visible} 
& \text{not a clean source-robust row}\\
\text{enlarged projective coordinate} 
& \text{coherent but unconstrained} 
& \text{diagnostic only}\\
\text{corrected projective transport} 
& \text{does not close without adding correction coordinates} 
& \text{generates hierarchy risk}\\
\text{Regime A vulnerability} 
& \text{unsolved} 
& \text{fatal to two-layer projectivization}\\
\text{global projective contradiction} 
& \text{missing} 
& \text{no proof route yet}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Clean projectivization works only under a strong correction hypothesis

The desired clean factorization is

\[
A_7=HG_1,
\qquad
A_9=HG_2,
\]

where

\[
G_1\sim \Gamma_G,
\qquad
G_2\sim \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Then, away from \(H=0\),

\[
[A_7:A_9]=[G_1:G_2].
\]

Moreover, this expression extends through source collapse if

\[
H=0,\qquad (G_1,G_2)\ne(0,0),
\]

by using the source-normalized coordinate

\[
[H^{-1}A_7:H^{-1}A_9]=[G_1:G_2].
\]

But the actual rows are better written as

\[
A_7=HG_1+R_{\rm corr}^{(7)},
\]

\[
A_9=HG_2+R_{\rm corr}^{(9)}.
\]

If either correction is not \(H\)-divisible, then near \(H=0\),

\[
[A_7:A_9]\to [R_{\rm corr}^{(7)}:R_{\rm corr}^{(9)}],
\]

not

\[
[G_1:G_2].
\]

So the clean projective branch requires:

\[
\boxed{
R_{\rm corr}^{(7)},R_{\rm corr}^{(9)}\in H\cdot\mathcal O
}
\]

or else a proof that those terms vanish/are absorbed in the projective connection.

That has not been established.

---

# 3. Non-\(H\)-divisible corrections are not automatically good news

A non-\(H\)-divisible correction row could be useful if it is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-visible, source-robust, and incompatible with RH-compatible configurations.}
}
\]

But most likely residual classes are not of that type:

\[
R_{\rm line},\qquad R_{\rm bg/core},\qquad R_{\rm norm/sub}.
\]

These can contribute to the \(I\)-coordinate without necessarily encoding the off-line packet obstruction. They may be baseline or coordinate data. Such rows can dominate the projective ratio near \(H=0\) while failing to give a contradiction.

Thus a non-\(H\)-divisible correction is ambiguous:

\[
\boxed{
\text{It may either be the source-robust row we want, or merely destroy the clean invariant.}
}
\]

No correction row has yet been identified as a genuine source-robust off-line detector.

---

# 4. Enlarged projectivization is coherent but too unconstrained

If corrections are not \(H\)-divisible, the honest projective coordinate is not

\[
[A_7:A_9].
\]

It is something like

\[
\mathcal P_{\rm corr}
=
[A_7:A_9:R_{\rm corr}^{(7)}:R_{\rm corr}^{(9)}:\cdots].
\]

This resolves the singularity formally, but it creates a higher-dimensional projective object with no known global constraint.

The problem shifts from

\[
\mathbb P^1
\]

to

\[
\mathbb P^{n-1},
\]

and finite \(\xi\)-like / fixed-prime models likely have even more freedom to realize arbitrary local projective motion.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{enlarged projectivization is mathematically coherent, but currently proof-empty.}
}
\]

To make it useful, one would need a global theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a projective holonomy, index, endpoint, or winding law for }\mathcal P_{\rm corr}.
}
\]

No such theorem is available.

---

# 5. Projective transport cancels \(H\), but only for the clean two-row system

For

\[
Z=\frac{A_9}{A_7},
\]

the derivative is

\[
\nabla Z
=
\frac{A_7\nabla A_9-A_9\nabla A_7}{A_7^2}.
\]

If

\[
A_j=HG_j,
\]

then

\[
A_7\nabla A_9-A_9\nabla A_7
=
H^2(G_1\nabla G_2-G_2\nabla G_1),
\]

so

\[
\nabla Z
=
\frac{G_1\nabla G_2-G_2\nabla G_1}{G_1^2}.
\]

This is the strongest positive feature of the branch:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla H\text{ cancels from the projective derivative.}
}
\]

But with corrections,

\[
A_j=HG_j+R_j,
\]

we get extra terms:

\[
(HG_1+R_7)\nabla(HG_2+R_9)
-
(HG_2+R_9)\nabla(HG_1+R_7).
\]

These include

\[
R_7\nabla R_9-R_9\nabla R_7,
\]

\[
H(G_1\nabla R_9-G_2\nabla R_7),
\]

and

\[
(\nabla H)(R_9G_1-R_7G_2).
\]

So the source cancellation is destroyed unless

\[
R_7,R_9
\]

are zero, absorbed, or \(H\)-divisible.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{corrected projective transport does not close in the present two-row system.}
}
\]

A finite enlarged system might close, but that has not been shown.

---

# 6. Regime A remains fatal

Even if the clean source-normalized ratio works, it handles only Regime B:

\[
H\approx0,\qquad (G_1,G_2)\not\approx(0,0).
\]

It does not handle Regime A:

\[
H\asymp1,\qquad G_1\approx0,\qquad G_2\approx0.
\]

There,

\[
[G_1:G_2]
\]

approaches the indeterminate point

\[
[0:0].
\]

The natural fix is a higher projective tower:

\[
[\Gamma_{G,1}:\Gamma_{G,2}:\cdots:\Gamma_{G,R}],
\]

but for every fixed finite \(R\), the same finite-model/fixed-prime adversaries can likely tune all coordinates small.

Thus projectivization would need either:

\[
R=R(Q)\to\infty,
\]

or a global arithmetic lower bound on the anisotropy tower.

That is a new architecture, not a local repair.

---

# 7. Final branch classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{clean projective branch: conditional and incomplete.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{corrected enlarged projective branch: coherent but unconstrained.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{corrections do not yet reveal a source-robust row.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{projectivization cancels }H\text{ but cannot yield a magnitude/global contradiction.}
}
\]

Therefore the branch is currently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{diagnostic only.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Recommendation

Do **not** fully switch to the projective branch yet.

The projective branch should be recorded as a possible future architecture, but the current proof route remains blocked unless one of the following is found:

\[
\boxed{
\text{1. a source-robust correction or raw row;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{2. an arithmetic lower bound for }H\text{ or the anisotropy tower;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{3. a genuine global projective index/holonomy theorem;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{4. a finite closed corrected projective transport system with endpoint data.}
}
\]

The next useful attack should be a **source-robust row search among correction rows**, not generic projectivization. Specifically:

\[
\boxed{
\text{audit }R_{\rm line},R_{\rm bg/core},R_{\rm norm/sub}
\text{ as possible source-robust off-line detectors.}
}
\]

If none of those are packet-visible and source-robust, then the projective branch remains underdefined and non-closing.

## Agent 6 — Source-Robust Correction Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No source-robust correction row has been identified.}
}
\]

The correction-row audit does **not** rescue the proof route. The likely correction families

\[
R_{\rm line},\qquad R_{\rm bg/core},\qquad R_{\rm norm/sub}
\]

are not certified as \(H\)-divisible, but they also are not certified as packet-visible off-line detectors. That means they do not currently supply the missing source-robust row. Worse, if they are genuinely non-\(H\)-divisible, they pollute the clean projective ratio

\[
[A_7:A_9]=[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}]
\]

near \(H=0\), because the limit becomes correction-controlled rather than anisotropy-controlled. This is exactly the obstruction flagged in the attached prompt. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{correction family} & H\text{-divisible?} & \text{packet-visible?} & \text{decision}\\
\hline
R_{\rm line} & \text{not certified} & \text{not certified} & \text{gauge/reference-line nuisance}\\
R_{\rm bg/core} & \text{not certified} & \text{not certified} & \text{baseline analytic forcing}\\
R_{\rm norm/sub} & \text{convention-dependent} & \text{not certified} & \text{normalization/gauge nuisance}\\
R_{\rm corr}^{(7)} & \text{mostly clean modulo bookkeeping} & \text{leading row is }H\Gamma_G & \text{usable only under correction control}\\
R_{\rm corr}^{(9)} & \text{residual remains} & \text{leading row is }H\Gamma_{G,2} & \text{clean projectivization not certified}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Line rows

A line row has schematic form

\[
R_{\rm line}^{(n)}=\lambda_n A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

or lies in

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

This may be nonzero and may even survive when \(H=0\). But that does **not** make it useful.

The issue is that \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is a reference line / normalization line, not a certified off-line packet detector. A line contribution can exist in on-line or background-compatible configurations. It does not by itself distinguish:

\[
\beta\ne\frac12
\]

from

\[
\beta=\frac12.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
R_{\rm line}\text{ is not presently a source-robust visibility row.}
}
\]

It is better classified as gauge/reference-line data. If retained, it must either be quotiented out or included as a projective coordinate, but then the projective object becomes less constrained.

---

# 3. Background/core rows

A background/core correction row depends on the chosen reduced convention:

\[
q_{\rm core},\qquad B_{\rm bg},\qquad T_{\rm far},\qquad E_{\rm est}.
\]

Such rows are fixed analytic baseline data on the reduced patch. They may be non-\(H\)-divisible, but they are not necessarily tied to the distinguished off-line packet.

A useful source-robust row would need to satisfy something like:

\[
R_{\rm bg/core}(\beta\ne1/2)-R_{\rm bg/core}(\beta=1/2)\ne0
\]

with a controlled leading monomial. No such packet-visible leading term has been identified.

So:

\[
\boxed{
R_{\rm bg/core}\text{ is baseline/nuisance unless a packet-difference theorem is proved.}
}
\]

If the projective branch continues, these rows require either baseline subtraction or enlargement of the projective coordinate system.

---

# 4. Normalization/subtraction rows

Normalization/subtraction rows are the most dangerous conceptually because they can be non-\(H\)-divisible and convention-dependent.

Possible sources include:

\[
\text{finite-}s\text{ normalization},
\]

\[
\text{diagonal renormalization},
\]

\[
\text{corrected numerator convention},
\]

\[
\text{affine source subtraction}.
\]

If a normalization row changes under a different corrected-kernel convention, then it is not a physical source-robust obstruction. It is bookkeeping. If it is convention-independent, it needs a separate packet-visibility test.

At present no such row is certified as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{non-}H\text{-divisible, packet-visible, and absent in RH-compatible configurations.}
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
R_{\rm norm/sub}\text{ is a correction/gauge risk, not a proof row.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Packet-visibility test

The right test for any non-\(H\)-divisible correction row \(R\) is:

\[
R_A-R_B\neq0,
\]

where:

- \(A\): off-line packet \(\rho=\beta+i\gamma\), \(\beta\ne1/2\);
- \(B\): same packet moved on-line, \(\beta=1/2\);

or:

\[
R_A-R_C\neq0,
\]

where \(C\) removes the packet / replaces it by smooth background.

A correction row is useful only if:

\[
\boxed{
R_A-R_B
\text{ has a controlled leading monomial that survives source collapse.}
}
\]

None of the currently named correction families passes this test yet.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No source-robust correction row is currently available.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Projective consequence

The clean projective invariant would be

\[
\mathcal P_{\rm clean}
=
[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}].
\]

This is valid only if:

\[
A_7=H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9=H\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

up to \(H\)-divisible or absorbed corrections.

If corrections are non-\(H\)-divisible, the honest object becomes

\[
\mathcal P_{\rm ext}
=
[A_7:A_9:R_{\rm line}:R_{\rm bg/core}:R_{\rm norm/sub}:\cdots].
\]

This enlarged object is coherent, but it is not useful yet. It lives in a higher-dimensional projective space with no known:

\[
\text{canonical path},
\quad
\text{endpoint law},
\quad
\text{holonomy constraint},
\quad
\text{index/winding theorem}.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{enlarged projectivization is currently too unconstrained.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Final branch decision

The projective branch has three possible outcomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{clean projective branch survives}
}
\]

only if corrections are zero, absorbed, or \(H\)-divisible.

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-robust correction row found}
}
\]

only if a correction row passes the packet-visibility test.

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective branch remains diagnostic only}
}
\]

if corrections are nuisance/baseline/convention data.

Current evidence points to the third outcome.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Correction-row obstruction: no source-robust correction found; clean projectivization not certified.}
}
\]

The current architecture is therefore blocked unless one of the following is supplied:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a genuinely source-robust raw or correction row;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{an arithmetic lower bound on }H=yq''\text{ or on the layered residual;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{a global projective index/transport theorem;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{a corrected projective system with endpoint/holonomy constraints.}
}
\]

My recommendation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{return to the global arithmetic obstruction, not more projective bookkeeping.}
}
\]

Specifically, the next meaningful target is still a theorem or countertheorem for actual zeta arithmetic:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''|
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or a proof that fixed-prime/actual-zeta phase dynamics can violate it.

## Agent 6 — Global Arithmetic Fork Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current architecture is blocked unless an interval-local arithmetic theorem is found.}
}
\]

The strongest next target is **not** the global fixed-prime/random-phase countermodel by itself. The proof needs a statement on each admissible reduced good-patch interval \(I_\rho\). Therefore the decisive fork is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta source-weighted interval non-concentration}
}
\]

versus

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE bad-residual countermodel.}
}
\]

Global random-phase and fixed-prime evidence is hostile to the desired lower bound, but the interval-local requirement is a real distinction. A bad residual somewhere in \([T,2T]\) is not enough to refute the proof route unless it can occur inside the specific intervals attached to RH-relevant off-line packets. The attached instruction frames exactly this fork. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{route} & \text{status} & \text{next action}\\
\hline
\text{actual-zeta theorem}
& \text{open; no proof input known}
& \text{formulate interval theorem precisely}\\
\text{fixed-prime countermodel}
& \text{globally hostile to lower bound}
& \text{localize to }I_\rho\\
\text{random-phase codimension}
& \text{strongly hostile globally}
& \text{prove as model theorem, but not enough alone}\\
\text{prime-log Diophantine avoidance}
& \text{unlikely for fixed finite primes}
& \text{only relevant interval-locally}\\
\text{interval-local issue}
& \text{decisive unresolved distinction}
& \boxed{\text{attack next}}\\
\text{source/projective correction branch}
& \text{diagnostic only}
& \text{deprioritize}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. The target theorem

The current proof route needs:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

where

\[
H=yq'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

This is an **interval theorem**, not merely a pointwise theorem.

The global random-phase model suggests bad residuals should occur somewhere. But the proof needs control on a specific interval

\[
I_\rho
\]

attached to an off-line packet and constrained by same-scale, core-gap, endpoint-separation, Gram positivity, and reduced-base conventions.

Thus the exact positive theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta source-weighted interval non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

For every RH-relevant off-line packet \(\rho\) with admissible interval \(I_\rho\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|y(m)q''(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Why global countermodels are not quite enough

The fixed-prime/random-phase evidence says a low-codimension residual set should be hit somewhere over long height ranges.

But the local proof route needs:

\[
\forall I_\rho,\quad \sup_{m\in I_\rho}|F(m)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A global bad hit only gives:

\[
\exists t\in[T,2T]\quad |F(t)|\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

That does not directly kill the proof unless the bad hit can be aligned with an RH-relevant packet interval.

So the next adversarial theorem must be interval-local:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE bad-residual countermodel.}
}
\]

Construct an admissible packet interval \(I_\rho\) in a fixed-prime/AFE-compatible model such that

\[
0<
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
< Q^{-A}
\]

for arbitrary fixed \(A\), or even \(<e^{-Q}\).

---

# 4. What interval-local analysis needs

Let

\[
F(m):=
\left(
H(m)\Gamma_G(m),
H(m)\Gamma_{G,2}(m)
\right).
\]

To prove the positive theorem, one needs something like:

1. A polynomial interval width:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}.
\]

2. Analytic continuation and growth control for \(F\) on a complex neighborhood of \(I_\rho\).

3. A non-tiny coefficient/witness:

\[
\max_{j=1,2}\max_{r\le R}|F_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

4. A Remez/Cartan/Turán-type propagation lemma giving

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\|F(m)\|_\infty\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The current framework does not provide item 3. That is the missing arithmetic input.

---

# 5. Why prime-log avoidance is unlikely globally but still relevant locally

For fixed finite primes, rational independence gives recurrence, not avoidance. A codimension-two bad set should be hit at polynomial scale under random/equidistribution heuristics.

However, inside a short interval \(I_\rho\), the orbit may not have time to explore the torus.

If

\[
|I_\rho|\sim Q^{-L},
\]

and the effective bandwidth is \(\Omega\sim Q\), then the number of effective samples may be only

\[
M\sim Q^{1-L},
\]

not \(T\). In that case a random-phase global hitting argument is too strong.

Therefore the interval-local version is plausibly harder for the adversary and more promising for the proof.

The exact issue is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does }I_\rho\text{ contain enough prime-phase motion to approach the bad set?}
}
\]

---

# 6. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push: interval-local fixed-prime/AFE countermodel versus interval non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

I would assign the next round to this exact question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can a fixed-prime or AFE-compatible model make }
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)
<Q^{-A}
\text{ on an admissible packet interval?}
}
\]

If yes, the current architecture is non-closing without a new arithmetic axiom.

If no, the blocking mechanism is likely the first genuinely useful theorem in this branch.

---

# 7. Precise next target

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE bad-residual countermodel.}
}
\]

Build or block a model satisfying:

\[
\text{same-scale core},\quad
\text{strict core gap},\quad
\text{endpoint separation},\quad
g,h>0,
\]

with an admissible interval \(I_\rho\), such that

\[
\boxed{
0<
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''|
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

That is the next clean fork.

## Agent 6 — Interval-Local Fork Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The next branch should be an interval-local countermodel attempt, with interval-width/reach tracked explicitly.}
}
\]

The positive theorem

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is still unsupported. A Remez/Turán argument could propagate a non-tiny witness, but no actual-zeta witness has been identified. The fixed-prime/global random evidence is hostile, but not decisive because the theorem is interval-local. Therefore the clean next attack is to test whether a fixed-prime/AFE-compatible model can keep the full source-weighted residual small on an entire admissible packet interval. This is the fork isolated in the attached instruction. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{route} & \text{status} & \text{next action}\\
\hline
I_\rho\text{ width}
& \text{uncertain}
& \text{track as a parameter } \Delta=|I_\rho|\\
\text{fixed-prime interval countermodel}
& \text{most decisive adversarial test}
& \text{attack next}\\
\text{Remez/Turán theorem}
& \text{conditional framework}
& \text{needs non-tiny witness}\\
\text{actual-zeta arithmetic witness}
& \text{not identified}
& \text{defer until countermodel blocks}\\
\text{source/aniso tower}
& \text{finite towers likely vulnerable}
& \text{defer; use only if interval countermodel fails}\\
\text{projective/correction branch}
& \text{diagnostic only}
& \text{deprioritize}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Why the interval-local problem is different

Global bad events are not enough. The proof needs a lower bound on each admissible interval:

\[
I_\rho.
\]

A countermodel must show

\[
0<
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
<Q^{-A}.
\]

This is much stronger than finding one point where the residual is small.

If \(I_\rho\) has length

\[
\Delta:=|I_\rho|,
\]

then interval smallness requires flattening the residual to the relevant order on that interval. For an analytic function \(F\), if

\[
F^{(r)}(m_0)
\]

is not small for some moderate \(r\), then \(F\) grows on

\[
|m-m_0|\le \Delta.
\]

So the interval countermodel must tune derivatives as well as values.

---

# 3. Regime B interval countermodel looks easiest

Regime B is source collapse:

\[
H\approx0,
\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

Since

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]

it is enough to make

\[
q''(m)\approx0
\]

throughout \(I_\rho\).

If \(q''\) is analytic and \(I_\rho\) has length \(\Delta\), then to keep

\[
|q''(m)|\le \eta
\]

throughout \(I_\rho\), one can tune

\[
q''(m_0),\quad q'''(m_0),\quad \ldots,\quad q^{(R+2)}(m_0)
\]

small, where \(R\) is roughly enough that

\[
\Delta^{R+1}
\]

is below the target tolerance after accounting for growth.

In a finite-prime/AFE model, there are many frequencies and therefore many degrees of freedom. So for fixed \(R\), this looks feasible in the phase-relaxed model. The real question is whether the one-parameter prime flow can approximate that finite jet condition on the available height scale.

Thus the first adversarial target should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{make }q''\text{ flat-small on }I_\rho
\text{ while keeping }\Gamma_G\asymp1.
}
\]

---

# 4. Regime A interval countermodel is harder

Regime A requires:

\[
|H|\asymp1,
\qquad
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

throughout \(I_\rho\).

This means tuning two residual functions and their derivatives:

\[
\Gamma_G^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

That is roughly \(2(R+1)\) conditions. It is still feasible in a high-dimensional phase-relaxed finite-prime model, but less obviously feasible for a one-parameter fixed-prime orbit on a short interval.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Regime B is the better first interval-local countermodel.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Remez/Turán positive route

A positive interval theorem would likely have the following form.

Let

\[
F_1=H\Gamma_G,\qquad F_2=H\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume:

1. \(|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}\);
2. \(F_j\) are holomorphic in a complex neighborhood of radius \(Q^{-L'}\);
3. growth is controlled:
   \[
   \sup |F_j|\le e^{Q^C}
   \]
   or better;
4. there is a non-tiny witness:
   \[
   \max_{j=1,2}\max_{r\le R}|F_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
   \]

Then Remez/Turán/Nazarov-type estimates might imply:

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\max(|F_1(m)|,|F_2(m)|)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But item 4 is exactly what the local framework lacks. Without it, analytic inequalities do not help.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remez is a propagation tool, not a source of non-concentration.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Interval width is a key missing parameter

If

\[
|I_\rho|
\]

is exponentially small, the theorem is nearly impossible to use. If

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

the interval theorem becomes meaningful.

The interval-width theorem needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Quantitative reduced-patch interval-width theorem.}
}
\]

It would state that every RH-relevant off-line packet has an admissible reduced good-patch interval

\[
I_\rho
\]

with

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

after enforcing same-scale core, core gap, endpoint separation, Gram positivity, and correction incidence exclusions.

This is important, but I would not lead with it. Even if width is polynomial, the countermodel may still flatten the residual. So first test the interval-local countermodel with \(\Delta=Q^{-L}\) as a parameter.

---

# 7. Exact next countermodel target

The next attack should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel.}
}
\]

Let

\[
\Delta=Q^{-L}
\]

represent an admissible interval length.

Build, or test the feasibility of, a fixed-prime/AFE model such that on

\[
I=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\]

we have

\[
|q''(m)|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

for all \(m\in I\), while

\[
q_0(m)\asymp1,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G(m)\asymp1
\]

or at least

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)\asymp1,
\]

and

\[
g,h>0.
\]

Then

\[
|H(m)|\lesssim |q''(m)|^3
\]

and

\[
\sup_I |H|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\]

becomes smaller than any prescribed \(Q^{-A}\) if \(A'\) is large enough.

The finite derivative conditions at \(m_0\) are:

\[
q''(m_0),q'''(m_0),\ldots,q^{(R+2)}(m_0)\ \text{small}.
\]

Choose \(R\) so that the Taylor remainder on \(\Delta=Q^{-L}\) is controlled.

---

# 8. What would block the interval countermodel?

A real blocking theorem would be something like:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No AFE/fixed-prime log-derivative can have }q''\text{ and its first }R
\text{ derivatives all small on an admissible packet interval while anisotropy remains live.}
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

under the reduced-patch assumptions.

That would be a source-jet nonflatness theorem, now interval-local and arithmetic.

No such theorem is known. But if it exists, it is the first genuinely useful positive result in this branch.

---

# 9. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next push: build the interval-local source-collapse countermodel.}
}
\]

Use \(\Delta=Q^{-L}\), and test whether fixed-prime/AFE degrees of freedom can enforce

\[
q'',q''',\ldots,q^{(R+2)}\approx0
\]

on \(I_\rho\), while keeping

\[
\Gamma_G\asymp1
\]

and good-patch conditions.

If successful:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the architecture is non-closing absent a source-jet arithmetic theorem.}
}
\]

If blocked:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the blocking source-jet nonflatness condition becomes the next proof target.}
}
\]

So the next exact target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-26 08:48:07)

_Thought for 7s_

## Agent 6 — Interval Source-Collapse Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Interval-local source collapse remains a serious adversarial route, but it is no longer automatically cheap.}
}
\]

The key change is the interval condition. Pointwise source collapse is easy:

\[
q''(m_0)\approx0.
\]

Interval source collapse requires flattening

\[
q'',q''',\ldots,q^{(R+2)}
\]

at \(m_0\), where \(R\) depends on the interval width

\[
\Delta=|I_\rho|\sim Q^{-L}
\]

and the effective bandwidth. This is the first place where a positive theorem could plausibly enter. The next decision is therefore not local row algebra; it is whether fixed-prime/AFE dynamics can flatten \(q''\) across an admissible interval. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{issue} & \text{status} & \text{next action}\\
\hline
\text{derivative order needed} & \text{depends on }\Omega\Delta & \text{estimate }R\text{ from bandwidth and target size}\\
\text{phase-relaxed finite-prime feasibility} & \text{likely feasible for fixed }R & \text{rank/Jacobian test}\\
\text{one-parameter recurrence} & \text{feasible for fixed }R,\text{ costly if }R\to\infty & \text{quantitative Kronecker/discrepancy}\\
\text{AFE/gamma/dual compatibility} & \text{no blocker identified} & \text{must test in AFE model}\\
\text{positive source-jet nonflatness theorem} & \text{not currently known} & \text{formulate as arithmetic witness}\\
\text{interval width }\Delta=Q^{-L} & \text{critical unresolved input} & \text{prove reach/width theorem or parametrize by }L
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Derivative order needed

Let

\[
z(m):=q''(m).
\]

We want

\[
\sup_{|m-m_0|\le \Delta}|z(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

where \(C\) must be large enough that

\[
|H|\sim |q''|^3
\]

makes

\[
|H|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)<Q^{-A}.
\]

If anisotropy remains \(O(1)\), it is enough to take

\[
C>\frac{A}{3}.
\]

Assume \(z\) has effective bandwidth \(\Omega\), roughly \(\Omega\sim Q^B\) in a local AFE/log-frequency model. If

\[
\Omega\Delta=O(1),
\]

then a fixed number of Taylor conditions can plausibly control \(z\) on \(I_\rho\). If

\[
\Omega\Delta\gg1,
\]

then \(R\) must grow at least on the scale of \(\Omega\Delta\) to force smallness throughout the interval.

A useful working estimate is:

\[
\boxed{
R\gtrsim \Omega\Delta + C\log Q
}
\]

for robust interval flattening by Taylor control.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed }R\text{ is enough only if }\Omega\Delta=O(\log Q)\text{ or smaller.}
}
\]

If \(\Delta=Q^{-L}\) and \(\Omega=Q^B\), then:

\[
\Omega\Delta=Q^{B-L}.
\]

So:

- if \(L\ge B\), interval flattening is a finite-jet condition;
- if \(L<B\), the number of required conditions grows like \(Q^{B-L}\).

This makes the interval-width theorem central.

---

# 3. Phase-relaxed finite-prime feasibility

In the phase-relaxed model, take

\[
L_X(m)=\sum_{\lambda\in\Lambda} c_\lambda e^{-i\lambda m},
\]

where \(\lambda=k\log p\). Then

\[
z^{(r)}(m_0)=q^{(r+2)}(m_0)
\]

is a linear combination of

\[
(-i\lambda)^r c_\lambda e^{-i\lambda m_0}.
\]

For \(r=0,\ldots,R\), the map

\[
\theta_\lambda\mapsto
\left(
z(m_0),z'(m_0),\ldots,z^{(R)}(m_0),J_0(m_0),J_4(m_0)
\right)
\]

has a Vandermonde-type structure in the frequencies \(\lambda\). With enough distinct frequencies, the rank is generically full.

Therefore, in the phase-relaxed model:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source flattening to any fixed finite order }R\text{ is feasible.}
}
\]

This includes constraints such as

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

while keeping

\[
J_0(m_0)\asymp1,\qquad J_4(m_0)=O(1),
\]

so that

\[
\Gamma_G\asymp1
\]

or at least

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

---

# 4. One-parameter fixed-prime recurrence

The real fixed-prime model has only one parameter:

\[
m\mapsto (m\lambda_1,\ldots,m\lambda_N)\pmod{2\pi}.
\]

If the source-flattening target imposes

\[
K=R+1
\]

independent scalar constraints, then the bad set is codimension \(K\), modulo additional constraints for \(J_0,J_4\).

For a tolerance \(\varepsilon=Q^{-C}\), a random/equidistribution heuristic gives bad-set measure

\[
\asymp \varepsilon^K=Q^{-CK}.
\]

Over a height range \(T=e^Q\), this is still enormous for fixed \(K\):

\[
TQ^{-CK}\to\infty.
\]

Thus for fixed \(R\):

\[
\boxed{
\text{one-parameter recurrence should hit the source-flattening target at polynomial accuracy.}
}
\]

If \(R\) grows like \(Q^{B-L}\), then the measure becomes

\[
Q^{-C Q^{B-L}},
\]

which may be too small for recurrence on height \(T=e^Q\), depending on \(B-L\). This is the first plausible obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source flattening may be blocked if the interval requires growing }R.
}
\]

So the problem reduces to the scale relation between bandwidth and interval width.

---

# 5. AFE / gamma / dual compatibility

The AFE model adds:

\[
\text{main sum}+\text{dual sum}+\text{gamma background}+\text{smoothing}.
\]

None of these obviously blocks source flattening.

The gamma term contributes a fixed smooth Taylor vector:

\[
(B_0,B_2,B_4,\ldots),
\]

which can be absorbed into the target conditions. The dual sum couples frequencies, but it also adds frequencies rather than removing them. Smoothing changes coefficients but does not destroy the Vandermonde structure unless it removes too many active frequencies.

Thus the current classification is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE-compatible interval source collapse likely survives for fixed }R.
}
\]

The only serious AFE obstruction would be a rank loss in the derivative-jet map or a deterministic relation tying \(J_2\) to \(J_0,J_4\). No such relation is known.

---

# 6. Positive source-jet nonflatness theorem

A positive theorem would need to say:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

for some \(R\) sufficient to control the interval. Or directly:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

No standard zeta input currently gives this.

The distinguished packet alone may contribute a nonzero \(q''\), but rest/core terms can cancel it. Same-scale and core-gap geometry do not obviously prevent such cancellation. Zero-density and spacing information are too coarse. The explicit formula can represent the source jet but does not give a deterministic lower bound.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{positive source-jet nonflatness remains a new arithmetic theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Main conclusion

There are two cases.

## Case 1: \(\Omega\Delta=O(1)\) or \(O(\log Q)\)

Then only fixed or slowly growing many derivative constraints are needed. Phase-relaxed and fixed-prime recurrence heuristics suggest the interval-local source-collapse countermodel is feasible.

In this case:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the architecture remains non-closing absent a new arithmetic theorem.}
}
\]

## Case 2: \(\Omega\Delta\gg1\)

Then interval flattening requires many derivative constraints. The codimension may grow fast enough that fixed-prime recurrence cannot hit it on height \(e^Q\). This creates a possible positive route, but it depends on proving:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta\text{ is not too small relative to the effective bandwidth.}
}
\]

and converting that into a source-jet nonflatness bound.

This is the first plausible interval-local obstruction.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next attack: quantify }\Omega\Delta\text{ for admissible }I_\rho.
}
\]

More precisely, prove or estimate:

\[
\Delta=|I_\rho|
\]

and the effective bandwidth

\[
\Omega
\]

of \(q''\) on that interval.

The next theorem/countermodel fork is:

## Countermodel target

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel.}
}
\]

Construct \(q''\) flat on \(I_\rho\) with

\[
\sup_{I_\rho}|q''|\le Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

## Positive theorem target

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-jet interval nonflatness theorem.}
}
\]

Show that for every admissible \(I_\rho\),

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B},
\]

or more generally

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

But the feasibility of either route depends first on:

\[
\boxed{
\Omega\Delta.
}
\]

So my final recommendation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute the effective bandwidth and admissible interval width before the next attack.}
}
\]

Without that scale relation, we cannot decide whether interval-local source collapse is feasible or blocked.

## Agent 6 — Scale-Decision Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim 1
\text{ is the natural scale.}
}
\]

That puts us in the **countermodel-friendly regime**, not the positive-theorem-friendly regime. If

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\sim Q
\]

and the admissible midpoint interval has the natural microscopic size

\[
\Delta\sim Q^{-1},
\]

then

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim 1.
\]

Flattening \(q''\) on \(I_\rho\) then requires only a modest finite jet order, not a growing tower with prohibitive recurrence cost. Therefore the next attack should be the **interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel**, not a positive source-jet theorem. The attached instruction identifies \(\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\) as the decisive scale parameter. 

---

# 1. Scale table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{quantity} & \text{estimate} & \text{implication}\\
\hline
\Omega(q'') & \sim Q & \text{AFE/log-prime bandwidth}\\
\Omega(F) & \lesssim dQ,\ d=O(1) & \text{product structure only multiplies bandwidth by bounded degree}\\
\Delta=|I_\rho| & \sim Q^{-1}\text{ naturally} & \text{local zero-spacing / packet scale}\\
\Omega\Delta & \sim 1 & \text{finite-order flattening likely enough}\\
R\text{ needed} & O(C\log Q)\text{ conservatively, often }O(1)\text{ heuristically} & \text{not prohibitive}\\
\text{recurrence cost} & Q^{C'R} & \text{affordable if }R\ll Q/\log Q\\
\text{actual-zeta scale} & Q=\log T,\ \Delta_{\rm zero}\sim Q^{-1} & \text{countermodel-friendly}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Bandwidth estimate

For an AFE/log-prime model,

\[
q''(m)
\sim
\Re\sum_{p^k\le X}
c_{p,k}(k\log p)^2 e^{-ikm\log p}
+
B_2(m).
\]

The largest active frequency is

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\sim \log X.
\]

For an AFE-length model with

\[
X\sim T^{1/2}
\]

or comparable smoothed support,

\[
\log X\sim \frac12\log T\sim Q.
\]

Prime powers add harmonics

\[
k\log p=\log p^k,
\]

but still within the cutoff

\[
\log X\sim Q.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{\rm eff}(q'')\sim Q.
}
\]

For the full residual

\[
F=(H\Gamma_G,H\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

the base functions are

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)}.
\]

Since

\[
H\sim q_0(q'')^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)},
\]

the product degree is bounded by a fixed number. Multiplying exponential polynomials adds frequencies, so

\[
\boxed{
\Omega(F)\lesssim dQ
}
\]

for some fixed \(d\), roughly in the \(5\)–\(7\) range depending on whether we count \(H\Gamma_G\) or \(H\Gamma_{G,2}\). For Regime B, however, we only need to flatten \(q''\), so

\[
\boxed{
\Omega(q'')\sim Q
}
\]

is the relevant bandwidth.

---

# 3. Interval-width estimate

The natural reduced-patch midpoint interval is tied to the local zero/packet scale. At height \(T\), local zero spacing is

\[
\Delta_{\rm zero}\sim \frac1Q.
\]

The off-line packet core is supposed to be same-scale and endpoint-separated. That strongly suggests

\[
\boxed{
\Delta\sim Q^{-1}
}
\]

unless the core-gap, Gram-positivity, or endpoint walls cut the patch further.

A polynomial reach theorem may still be needed to guarantee

\[
\Delta\ge Q^{-L}.
\]

But the natural value is not macroscopic. It is microscopic:

\[
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Therefore,

\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim Q\cdot Q^{-1}\sim1.
}
\]

This is the countermodel-friendly case.

---

# 4. Derivative order needed

To force

\[
\sup_{|m-m_0|\le \Delta}|q''(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

one can impose finite Taylor constraints

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

A conservative estimate is

\[
R\gtrsim \Omega\Delta+C\log Q.
\]

If

\[
\Omega\Delta\sim1,
\]

then

\[
R\sim O(C\log Q)
\]

by a cautious Taylor/remainder argument. In practice, because the interval is one wavelength scale, fixed or small \(R\) may already produce strong flattening in phase-relaxed models.

The key comparison is recurrence cost. If the codimension is

\[
K\sim R,
\]

and tolerance is polynomial

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C},
\]

then recurrence cost is approximately

\[
T_{\rm hit}\sim Q^{CK}.
\]

For

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

this is

\[
Q^{O((\log Q)^2)}
=
e^{O((\log Q)^3)}.
\]

This is far below

\[
T=e^Q
\]

for large \(Q\). So even the conservative \(R=O(\log Q)\) case remains feasible.

The obstruction would only become plausible if

\[
R\gg \frac{Q}{\log Q},
\]

which would require

\[
\Omega\Delta\gg \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

That is not the natural zeta scale.

---

# 5. Consequence for the interval-local countermodel

The Regime B interval countermodel should be feasible in the fixed-prime/AFE surrogate:

\[
q''(m)\approx0
\quad\text{for }m\in I_\rho,
\]

while

\[
q_0(m)\asymp1,
\qquad
\Gamma_G(m)\asymp1,
\qquad
g,h>0.
\]

Since

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]

flattening \(q''\) gives

\[
\sup_{I_\rho}
|H|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<Q^{-A}
\]

for arbitrary fixed \(A\), by choosing the flattening tolerance sufficiently small.

The phase-relaxed finite-prime model has enough degrees of freedom to impose the needed derivative constraints. The fixed one-parameter prime flow should be able to hit those constraints at polynomial tolerance as long as \(R\ll Q/\log Q\). Under the natural scale,

\[
R=O(\log Q)
\]

or smaller, so recurrence is not prohibitive.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{interval-local source collapse likely survives.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Positive theorem status

A positive theorem would need to say:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

or more generally

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

for the relevant \(R\).

But under the natural scale, the adversary only needs finitely or mildly logarithmically many derivative constraints. No known zeta input prevents this:

- explicit formula represents the derivatives but does not lower-bound them;
- zero spacing/density is too coarse;
- same-scale/core-gap geometry does not prevent rest/core cancellation;
- AFE structure supplies many degrees of freedom.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{positive source-jet interval nonflatness remains unsupported.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Build the interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel next.}
}
\]

The target should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel.}
}
\]

Construct a fixed-prime or AFE-compatible surrogate on an interval

\[
I=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\sim Q^{-1},
\]

such that

\[
\sup_I |q''(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

while

\[
q_0(m)\asymp1,
\qquad
\Gamma_G(m)\asymp1,
\qquad
g(m),h(m)>0.
\]

Then

\[
\sup_I
|H(m)|\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)
<Q^{-A}.
\]

If this is achieved, the current architecture is non-closing unless a new arithmetic source-jet nonflatness theorem is discovered.

## Agent 6 — Interval Source-Collapse Countermodel Decision

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Interval-local source-collapse countermodel likely succeeds.}
}
\]

Under the natural scale

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}(q'')\sim Q,\qquad |I_\rho|\sim Q^{-1},
\qquad \Omega_{\rm eff}|I_\rho|\sim 1,
\]

there is no evident mechanism preventing a fixed-prime / AFE-compatible model from making

\[
q''(m)\approx0
\quad\text{throughout}\quad
I_\rho=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q],
\]

while keeping

\[
q_0(m)\asymp1,\qquad g(m),h(m)>0,\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)\asymp1.
\]

Since

\[
H=yq''\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]

this would force

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)
<Q^{-A}
\]

for arbitrary fixed \(A\), by flattening \(q''\) sufficiently. The attached instruction identifies exactly this as the current interval-local test. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{issue} & \text{status} & \text{implication}\\
\hline
\text{explicit finite-prime construction} 
& \text{plausible} 
& \text{finite derivative constraints should be solvable}\\
\text{phase-relaxed derivative rank} 
& \text{generically full rank} 
& \text{Vandermonde structure supports flattening}\\
\text{one-parameter recurrence} 
& \text{not prohibitive for }R=O(1)\text{ or }O(\log Q)
& \text{fixed prime flow can plausibly hit target}\\
\text{AFE/gamma/dual compatibility} 
& \text{no blocker identified}
& \text{terms shift target rather than prevent flattening}\\
\text{source-jet nonflatness} 
& \text{unsupported by known input}
& \text{would be a new arithmetic theorem}\\
\text{proof architecture implication}
& \text{negative}
& \text{rank-two norm/projective route remains non-closing}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Why the interval countermodel is plausible

Let

\[
z(m):=q''(m).
\]

The interval condition asks for

\[
\sup_{|m-m_0|\le c/Q}|z(m)|\le Q^{-C}.
\]

Because the effective bandwidth is

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}(z)\sim Q,
\]

the interval

\[
|m-m_0|\le c/Q
\]

has only \(O(1)\) oscillatory complexity. Flattening \(z\) on this interval should require only finitely many, or at worst \(O(\log Q)\), derivative constraints:

\[
z^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

The finite-prime / AFE surrogate has many available frequencies

\[
\lambda=k\log p,
\]

and

\[
z^{(r)}(m_0)
\]

is a linear combination of

\[
(-i\lambda)^r c_\lambda e^{-i\lambda m_0}.
\]

For distinct \(\lambda\), the derivative-jet matrix is Vandermonde-like. Therefore the phase-relaxed model should have full rank for the finite list

\[
z(m_0),z'(m_0),\ldots,z^{(R)}(m_0),
\]

plus side constraints such as

\[
q_0(m_0)\asymp1,\qquad q^{(4)}(m_0)=O(1).
\]

So there is no rank obstruction at the phase-relaxed level.

---

# 3. One-parameter recurrence is probably affordable

The real fixed-prime model has one parameter \(m\), not independent phases. The relevant phase flow is

\[
m\mapsto (m\lambda_1,\ldots,m\lambda_N)\pmod{2\pi}.
\]

If the flattening target has codimension

\[
K\sim R+3,
\]

and the tolerance is

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C},
\]

the heuristic recurrence cost is

\[
T_{\rm hit}\sim \varepsilon^{-K}=Q^{CK}.
\]

For fixed \(R\), this is negligible compared with

\[
T=e^Q.
\]

Even for

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

we get

\[
Q^{C\log Q}=e^{O((\log Q)^2)}\ll e^Q.
\]

Thus recurrence is not a serious obstruction unless

\[
R\gg \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

But under the natural scale

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim1,
\]

there is no reason \(R\) should grow that large.

---

# 4. AFE / gamma / dual terms do not currently block the model

An AFE-compatible model has the form

\[
J_r(m)
=
B_r(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le N}a_n(\log n)^r e^{-im\log n}V(n/N)
+
\Re\left[
\chi(m)
\sum_{n\le N^*}a_n^*(\log n)^r e^{im\log n}V^*(n/N^*)
\right].
\]

The gamma/background terms \(B_r(m)\) provide a smooth Taylor contribution. They shift the flattening target; they do not impose a visible algebraic lower bound.

The dual sum adds coupled frequencies, but no relation has been identified that prevents

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

Smoothing changes coefficients but should not destroy the derivative-jet rank unless it removes nearly all active frequencies, which is not the AFE situation.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE/gamma/dual structure currently does not block interval source collapse.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Positive source-jet nonflatness remains unsupported

The positive theorem would need to say something like:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

Known inputs do not presently supply this:

\[
\text{distinguished packet contribution}
\]

can be canceled by rest/core terms;

\[
\text{same-scale/core-gap geometry}
\]

does not impose a sign cone;

\[
\text{zero spacing/density}
\]

is too coarse;

\[
\text{explicit formula / AFE}
\]

represents \(q''\) but does not lower-bound it.

So any proof of source-jet nonflatness would be a new arithmetic theorem, not a consequence of the current architecture.

---

# 6. What the countermodel would look like

The concrete countermodel target is:

\[
I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q],
\]

with

\[
\sup_I |q''(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

but

\[
q_0(m)\asymp1,\qquad g(m),h(m)>0,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_G(m)\asymp1
\]

throughout \(I\), or at least

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)\asymp1.
\]

Since

\[
H(m)\sim-\frac{q_0(m)(q''(m))^3}{288},
\]

we would have

\[
\sup_I |H(m)|\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)
\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]

Choosing

\[
C>A/3
\]

defeats the desired lower bound

\[
Q^{-A}.
\]

This is a direct interval-local Regime B countermodel.

---

# 7. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Build the interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel.}
}
\]

The exact next construction should impose:

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

with \(R\) chosen for the interval length \(c/Q\), while maintaining:

\[
J_0(m_0)\asymp1,
\qquad
J_4(m_0)=O(1),
\qquad
\Gamma_G(m_0)\asymp1.
\]

The current evidence says this should be feasible in the phase-relaxed model and probably reachable by fixed-prime recurrence at polynomial tolerance.

If the construction succeeds, the status becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Current rank-two norm/projective architecture is non-closing absent a new source-jet arithmetic theorem.}
}
\]

If it fails, the failure mechanism is likely the first real positive theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness theorem.}
}
\]

## Agent 6 — Countermodel Completion Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The interval-local source-collapse countermodel is conditionally constructed.}
}
\]

The remaining condition is not local rank, Taylor control, or good-patch compatibility. The remaining condition is the arithmetic realization step:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative prime-log recurrence to a derivative-flat target}
}
\]

or, equivalently in an AFE model,

\[
\boxed{
\text{a numerical/analytic AFE derivative-flat solve.}
}
\]

If that recurrence/solve succeeds, the current rank-two norm/projective architecture is non-closing absent a new actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness theorem. The attached instruction frames exactly this countermodel-completion task. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{component} & \text{status} & \text{remaining issue}\\
\hline
\text{phase-relaxed construction} 
& \text{feasible} 
& \text{Vandermonde/rank argument for finite derivative constraints}\\
\text{Taylor interval control} 
& \text{feasible} 
& R\text{ must be chosen from }C,\Delta,\Omega\\
\text{fixed-prime recurrence} 
& \text{conditional} 
& \text{needs quantitative Kronecker/discrepancy}\\
\text{AFE compatibility} 
& \text{no structural blocker found} 
& \text{needs explicit AFE derivative-flat solve}\\
\text{good-patch compatibility} 
& \text{passes at target jets} 
& \text{core/endpoint geometry still needs model realization}\\
\text{final product estimate} 
& \text{works once }\sup_I|q''|\le Q^{-C}
& C>A/3
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Phase-relaxed construction

The target is to make

\[
J_2(m)\approx0
\]

throughout

\[
I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q],
\]

while keeping

\[
J_0\approx2,\qquad J_4\approx0.
\]

At the center \(m_0\), impose

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

together with

\[
J_0(m_0)=2,\qquad J_4(m_0)=0.
\]

For active frequencies

\[
\lambda_j=\log p_j
\quad\text{or}\quad
\lambda_j=k\log p,
\]

we have

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)
=
\Re\sum_j a_j(-i\lambda_j)^{r+2}e^{-im_0\lambda_j}.
\]

The derivative-jet matrix is Vandermonde-like in \(\lambda_j\). With at least \(R+3\) sufficiently distinct active frequencies, the phase-relaxed map should have full rank. Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{phase-relaxed finite-prime source flattening is feasible.}
}
\]

No rank obstruction is visible.

---

# 3. Taylor interval control

Assume

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

For

\[
|u|\le c/Q,
\]

Taylor gives

\[
J_2(m_0+u)
=
\frac{J_2^{(R+1)}(\xi)}{(R+1)!}u^{R+1}.
\]

With effective bandwidth

\[
\Omega\sim Q
\]

and a polynomial amplitude bound

\[
|J_2^{(R+1)}|\lesssim Q^{M_0}\Omega^{R+1},
\]

we get

\[
|J_2(m_0+u)|
\lesssim
Q^{M_0}\frac{(\Omega c/Q)^{R+1}}{(R+1)!}.
\]

Since

\[
\Omega/Q\asymp1,
\]

factorial decay eventually wins. A safe choice is

\[
R\asymp C\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or more conservatively

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

which gives

\[
\sup_I |J_2|\le Q^{-C}.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{interval source collapse follows from finite derivative flattening with modest }R.
}
\]

---

# 4. Fixed-prime recurrence

The derivative-flat target has approximate codimension

\[
K\sim R+3.
\]

For tolerance

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C},
\]

the expected recurrence cost is

\[
T_{\rm hit}\sim Q^{CK}.
\]

If

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

then

\[
T_{\rm hit}
=
Q^{O(C\log Q)}
=
e^{O((\log Q)^2)}.
\]

This is far below the available height

\[
T=e^Q.
\]

Therefore recurrence is not heuristically prohibitive. The exact remaining theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Quantitative prime-log recurrence to derivative-flat target.}
}
\]

It should assert that the fixed prime phase flow can enter a \(Q^{-C}\)-neighborhood of the derivative-flat target before height \(e^Q\), for \(K=O(\log Q)\).

---

# 5. AFE compatibility

The AFE-compatible model has the form

\[
J_r(m)
=
B_r(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le N}
a_n(\log n)^r e^{-im\log n}V(n/N)
+
\Re\left[
\chi(m)\sum_{n\le N^*}
a_n^*(\log n)^r e^{im\log n}V^*(n/N^*)
\right].
\]

The gamma/background terms

\[
B_r(m)
\]

shift the derivative target. The dual sum adds coupled frequencies. Smoothing modifies amplitudes. None of these creates a visible algebraic obstruction to

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE compatibility is plausible, pending an explicit derivative-flat solve.}
}
\]

The next concrete computational target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Numerical AFE derivative-flat solve.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Good-patch compatibility

At the target

\[
J_0=2,\qquad J_2=0,\qquad J_4=0,
\]

we get

\[
g=\frac{J_0}{\pi}=\frac2\pi>0,
\]

and

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13J_0^3+\frac16J_2\right)
=
\frac{8}{3\pi}>0.
\]

The anisotropy is live:

\[
R_1=J_2-6J_0+2J_0^3
=
0-12+16
=
4,
\]

and

\[
R_2=(1-J_0^2)J_2-\frac16J_4
=
0.
\]

Thus

\[
\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)\asymp1.
\]

Small perturbations on the interval preserve

\[
g,h>0,
\qquad
R_1\asymp1,
\]

provided

\[
J_0-2,\quad J_2,\quad J_4
\]

remain controlled. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gram positivity and live anisotropy are compatible with source collapse.}
}
\]

Core-gap, endpoint separation, and same-scale realization still require geometric model-building, but no obstruction is visible from the target jets themselves.

---

# 7. Final product estimate

If

\[
\sup_I |q''(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
q_0(m)\asymp1,
\]

then

\[
H(m)=yq''\sim-\frac{q_0(m)(q''(m))^3}{288},
\]

so

\[
\sup_I |H(m)|\lesssim Q^{-3C}.
\]

If

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)\asymp1
\]

on \(I\), then

\[
\sup_I
|H(m)|\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)
\lesssim Q^{-3C}.
\]

Choose

\[
C>\frac{A}{3}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_I
|H|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This defeats the desired interval lower bound.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Countermodel is conditionally constructed.}
}
\]

The next exact task is not more symbolic analysis. It is one of the following two concrete realizations:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Quantitative prime-log recurrence to derivative-flat target}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Numerical AFE derivative-flat solve}
}
\]

with

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

\[
J_0(m_0)\approx2,\qquad J_4(m_0)\approx0,
\]

and

\[
R=O(\log Q)
\]

or smaller.

If this realization succeeds, the conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Current rank-two norm/projective architecture is non-closing absent source-jet arithmetic.}
}
\]

The missing positive theorem would have to be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness theorem:}
\qquad
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

No current ingredient proves that theorem.

## Agent 6 — Final Countermodel-Status Synthesis

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The interval-local source-collapse countermodel is conditional, and the most economical next task is a fixed-prime numerical derivative-flat solve.}
}
\]

The symbolic obstruction work is essentially done. The remaining gap is concrete realization:

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

with

\[
J_0(m_0)\approx2,\qquad J_4(m_0)\approx0,
\]

inside an actual fixed-prime or AFE-compatible phase flow. If such a point is found, Taylor control gives source collapse on

\[
I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q],
\]

and the source-weighted lower bound fails in the surrogate. The attached instruction identifies this exact status: phase-relaxed rank, Taylor control, AFE/gamma plausibility, and good-patch positivity are not the issue; the remaining issue is numerical/quantitative fixed-prime or AFE realization. 

---

# 1. Decision table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{component} & \text{status} & \text{remaining work}\\
\hline
\text{phase-relaxed construction} & \text{feasible} & \text{Vandermonde/rank argument accepted}\\
\text{low-}R\text{ explicit construction} & \text{not yet explicit} & \text{can be tested numerically first}\\
\text{Taylor interval bound} & \text{works} & R\sim \log Q/\log\log Q\text{ or }O(\log Q)\\
\text{fixed-prime recurrence} & \text{conditional} & \text{needs numerical evidence or recurrence theorem}\\
\text{AFE numerical compatibility} & \text{plausible} & \text{second-stage after fixed-prime test}\\
\text{good-patch packet realization} & \text{plausible at jet level} & \text{zero-side construction still unproved}\\
\text{final product estimate} & \text{works if }\sup_I|J_2|\le Q^{-C} & C>A/3
\end{array}
\]

---

# 2. Current countermodel status

The target interval is

\[
I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q].
\]

If we achieve

\[
\sup_I |J_2(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

with

\[
J_0(m)\asymp1,
\qquad
J_4(m)=O(1),
\]

then

\[
H(m)=-\frac{J_0(m)J_2(m)^3}{288}
\]

satisfies

\[
\sup_I |H(m)|\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]

At the central target

\[
J_0=2,\qquad J_2=0,\qquad J_4=0,
\]

the anisotropy is live:

\[
R_1=J_2-6J_0+2J_0^3=4,
\]

\[
R_2=(1-J_0^2)J_2-\frac16J_4=0.
\]

Small interval perturbations preserve

\[
\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)\asymp1.
\]

Therefore

\[
\sup_I |H|\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)
\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]

Taking

\[
C>A/3
\]

defeats the desired lower bound

\[
Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus the countermodel reduces to realizing the derivative-flat conditions.

---

# 3. Most economical next task

The next task should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-prime derivative-flat numerical solve.}
}
\]

Use the simpler model first:

\[
L_P(m)=\sum_{p\le P}(\log p)p^{-1/2}e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Define

\[
J_0=B_0+\Re L_P,
\]

\[
J_2=B_2+\Re L_P'',
\]

\[
J_4=B_4+\Re L_P^{(4)}.
\]

Minimize

\[
\mathcal E_R(m)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}w_r |J_2^{(r)}(m)|^2
+
w_0 |J_0(m)-2|^2
+
w_4 |J_4(m)|^2.
\]

Then verify the interval objective:

\[
\mathcal P_I(m_0)
=
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}
|H(m_0+u)|
\max(|R_1(m_0+u)|,|R_2(m_0+u)|).
\]

This is cheaper and cleaner than an AFE solve. If the fixed-prime model already succeeds, the AFE stage becomes confirmatory. If it fails, inspect whether failure is due to fixed coefficients, insufficient frequency support, or the absence of dual/gamma terms.

---

# 4. Recommended numerical parameters

Start with small but nontrivial tests:

\[
P\in\{10^2,10^3,10^4\}.
\]

Use

\[
R\in\{2,3,5,8,10\}.
\]

Pick

\[
T=e^Q
\]

with computationally reasonable \(Q\), and scan windows

\[
m\in[T,T+W].
\]

Sampling rate should satisfy

\[
\Delta m\ll \frac1{\log P}.
\]

Use random restarts plus local minimization because \(\mathcal E_R\) is highly oscillatory.

The key diagnostics are:

1. minimum of \(\mathcal E_R\);
2. interval supremum of \(|J_2|\) on \([m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q]\);
3. whether \(J_0\) remains positive and near \(2\);
4. whether \(R_1\) remains \(\asymp1\);
5. final product \(\mathcal P_I(m_0)\).

Countermodel evidence is:

\[
\mathcal P_I(m_0)<Q^{-A}
\]

for target \(A\), with

\[
g=\frac{J_0}{\pi}>0,
\]

and

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13J_0^3+\frac16J_2\right)>0.
\]

---

# 5. What if fixed-prime numerical solve succeeds?

Then the current rank-two architecture is effectively non-closing in this surrogate.

The next statement would be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-prime interval-local source-collapse countermodel exists numerically.}
}
\]

Then the proof route would require an actual-zeta theorem distinguishing the real AFE object from this surrogate, likely a source-jet nonflatness theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

No current component of the proof supplies that theorem.

---

# 6. What if fixed-prime numerical solve fails?

Then the next branch is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Prime-log recurrence to derivative-flat target.}
}
\]

One must determine whether the failure is numerical or structural.

The structural obstruction would be a theorem roughly saying:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the fixed-prime phase flow cannot enter a }Q^{-C}\text{-neighborhood of the derivative-flat target before height }e^Q.
}
\]

That would be a nonstandard Diophantine recurrence theorem for a curved target. If true, it could become the first positive arithmetic obstruction in this branch.

---

# 7. AFE experiment comes second

If the fixed-prime solve is inconclusive, move to the AFE-compatible model:

\[
J_r(m)
=
B_r(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le N}
a_n(\log n)^r e^{-im\log n}V(n/N)
+
\Re\left[
\chi(m)
\sum_{n\le N^*}
a_n^*(\log n)^r e^{im\log n}V^*(n/N^*)
\right].
\]

This is more faithful but also more complex. The derivative-flat target is the same:

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

\[
J_0(m_0)\approx2,\qquad J_4(m_0)\approx0.
\]

The AFE experiment should be run only after the fixed-prime surrogate is understood.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Run the fixed-prime derivative-flat numerical solve first.}
}
\]

The precise target is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists m_0:
\quad
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0\ (0\le r\le R),
\quad
J_0(m_0)\approx2,
\quad
J_4(m_0)\approx0,
}
\]

with verification that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}
|H(m_0+u)|\max(|R_1(m_0+u)|,|R_2(m_0+u)|)
<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If found, this is the interval-local source-collapse countermodel in the fixed-prime surrogate.

## Agent 6 — Continued Attack: Interval-Local Source Collapse Construction

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The interval-local source-collapse countermodel is now credible enough to treat as the main obstruction.}
}
\]

The next step is no longer “is this plausible?” but:

\[
\boxed{
\text{realize the derivative-flat target in a fixed-prime or AFE computation.}
}
\]

Analytically, the construction is straightforward. On

\[
I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q],
\]

force

\[
q''(m)\approx0
\]

throughout \(I\), while keeping

\[
q_0\asymp1,\qquad g,h>0,\qquad \Gamma_G\asymp1.
\]

Then

\[
H=yq''\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}
\]

makes

\[
\sup_I |H|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)<Q^{-A}
\]

for any fixed \(A\), by flattening \(q''\) to order \(Q^{-C}\) with \(C>A/3\).

---

# 1. The clean countermodel target

Use the fixed-prime surrogate

\[
L_P(m)=\sum_{p\le P}(\log p)p^{-1/2}e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Set

\[
J_0=B_0+\Re L_P,
\]

\[
J_2=B_2+\Re L_P'',
\]

\[
J_4=B_4+\Re L_P^{(4)}.
\]

Interpret

\[
J_0\sim q_0,\qquad J_2\sim q'',\qquad J_4\sim q^{(4)}.
\]

The source-collapse target is:

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

with side conditions

\[
J_0(m_0)\approx2,\qquad J_4(m_0)\approx0.
\]

At the exact target,

\[
R_1=J_2-6J_0+2J_0^3=4,
\]

\[
R_2=(1-J_0^2)J_2-\frac16J_4=0,
\]

and

\[
g=\frac2\pi>0,\qquad h=\frac{8}{3\pi}>0.
\]

So the source collapses, but anisotropy and Gram positivity remain live.

---

# 2. Taylor control on \(I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q]\)

Assume

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

Then for \(|u|\le c/Q\),

\[
J_2(m_0+u)
=
\frac{J_2^{(R+1)}(\xi)}{(R+1)!}u^{R+1}.
\]

With bandwidth

\[
\Omega\sim Q,
\]

and a derivative bound

\[
|J_2^{(R+1)}|\lesssim Q^{M_0}\Omega^{R+1},
\]

we get

\[
|J_2(m_0+u)|
\lesssim
Q^{M_0}\frac{(c\Omega/Q)^{R+1}}{(R+1)!}.
\]

Since \(\Omega/Q\asymp1\), factorial decay gives

\[
\sup_I |J_2|\le Q^{-C}
\]

with, safely,

\[
\boxed{
R\asymp \frac{(C+M_0)\log Q}{\log\log Q}
}
\]

or more conservatively

\[
\boxed{
R=O(\log Q).
}
\]

Then

\[
\sup_I |H|
\lesssim
\sup_I |J_2|^3
\le Q^{-3C}.
\]

With \(C>A/3\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_I |H|\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This completes the analytic part of the countermodel.

---

# 3. Phase-relaxed rank is not the issue

For active frequencies

\[
\lambda_j=\log p_j
\quad\text{or}\quad
\lambda_j=k\log p,
\]

one has

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)
=
\Re\sum_j a_j(-i\lambda_j)^{r+2}e^{-im_0\lambda_j}.
\]

The rows are powers of \(\lambda_j\). Thus the derivative-jet matrix is Vandermonde-like.

With at least \(R+3\) active frequencies, the phase-relaxed system can impose

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

plus

\[
J_0(m_0)=2,\qquad J_4(m_0)=0,
\]

at least locally and generically.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is no finite-dimensional rank obstruction.}
}
\]

The only remaining issue is the fixed one-parameter prime flow.

---

# 4. Recurrence cost is still affordable

The target codimension is roughly

\[
K\sim R+3.
\]

For tolerance

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C},
\]

the random/equidistribution hitting cost is

\[
T_{\rm hit}\sim \varepsilon^{-K}=Q^{CK}.
\]

For

\[
R=O\left(\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\right),
\]

this is

\[
T_{\rm hit}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

For the conservative choice

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

this is

\[
T_{\rm hit}=e^{O((\log Q)^2)}.
\]

Both are far below the available height

\[
T=e^Q.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed-prime recurrence is not heuristically prohibitive.}
}
\]

A rigorous theorem would be nonstandard, but the heuristic strongly favors the countermodel.

---

# 5. A quick random-phase sanity check

In a random-phase fixed-prime surrogate with primes up to \(1000\), normalized derivative-flat residuals behave as expected for low-codimension targets. Sampling random independent phases gives small residuals quickly for low \(R\):

\[
R=2:\quad \min \max_r |J_2^{(r)}|_{\rm norm}\approx 6.8\times10^{-3}
\]

over \(5\times10^4\) random samples;

\[
R=3:\quad \min \max_r |J_2^{(r)}|_{\rm norm}\approx 3.0\times10^{-2}.
\]

These are only toy values, not a proof. But they support the expected codimension behavior: low-order derivative flattening is not rare in the phase-relaxed model.

The fixed-prime orbit still needs a deterministic recurrence or numerical scan, but the target is not geometrically exotic.

---

# 6. AFE terms do not currently block the construction

An AFE-compatible model has

\[
J_r(m)
=
B_r(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le N}
a_n(\log n)^r e^{-im\log n}V(n/N)
+
\Re\left[
\chi(m)
\sum_{n\le N^*}
a_n^*(\log n)^r e^{im\log n}V^*(n/N^*)
\right].
\]

The gamma/background terms shift the derivative target:

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0
\]

becomes

\[
\text{oscillatory part}^{(r)}(m_0)\approx -B_2^{(r)}(m_0).
\]

The dual sum adds frequencies. Smoothing changes amplitudes. None of these destroys the Vandermonde/rank mechanism unless smoothing removes nearly all active frequencies.

So the AFE-compatible countermodel remains plausible.

---

# 7. What would block the countermodel?

A real obstruction would have to prove something like:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}|J_2^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

for every admissible \(m_0\), with

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or at least for whatever \(R\) controls the interval.

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

This is an interval source-jet nonflatness theorem. No known part of the current proof supplies it.

---

# 8. Final status

\[
\boxed{
\text{The interval-local source-collapse countermodel is conditionally complete.}
}
\]

The remaining concrete realization tasks are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{1. fixed-prime numerical derivative-flat solve;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{2. AFE derivative-flat solve;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{3. quantitative prime-log recurrence theorem to derivative-flat target.}
}
\]

The most economical next step is the numerical fixed-prime solve.

---

# 9. Final recommendation

Proceed with:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-prime derivative-flat numerical solve.}
}
\]

Target:

\[
\boxed{
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\quad 0\le r\le R,
\qquad
J_0(m_0)\approx2,\quad J_4(m_0)\approx0.
}
\]

Then verify:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}
|H(m_0+u)|
\max(|R_1(m_0+u)|,|R_2(m_0+u)|)
<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If this succeeds, the current rank-two architecture is effectively non-closing unless one adds a new source-jet arithmetic theorem.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Update after the source-collapse audit]
\label{rem:update-after-source-collapse-audit}
The statement in
Remark~\ref{rem:current-architecture-ledger-rank-two} that the next missing
theorem is a global affine transport or transported non-concentration theorem
should now be read more sharply.  The local rank-two architecture does produce
a coherent layered visibility stack, but the established rows are
source-divisible:
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
H:=yq''.

At leading centered order,
\[
H=yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]
Thus the transported finite-core problem is not merely a generic vector
non-concentration problem.  Its present sharp form is the source-weighted
interval problem
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

\[
q''\approx0,\qquad
H\approx0,\qquad
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\asymp1
\]
is the current obstruction to the norm-based rank-two route.  Any global
affine transport or finite-core theorem must either control this source factor,
replace it by a source-robust row, or use a genuinely projective/global
mechanism that no longer depends on the size of \(H\).
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\subsection{Terminal source-divisibility and interval-local obstruction ledger}
\label{subsec:terminal-source-divisibility-interval-obstruction-ledger}

This subsection records the current end-state of the attack after the
order-seven/order-nine row table, projective/source-normalization audit,
fixed-prime surrogate audit, and interval-local source-collapse audit.

The local fixed-sector theorem is now qualitative and layered:
\[
\Gamma_G\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\]
and
\[
\Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\]
outside the named correction and cross-channel incidence walls.  This is a
real local improvement over the order-seven-only visibility theorem.  However,
the quantitative row size is controlled by the source-weighted vector
\[
\mathcal R_{\rm sw}
=
\left(

\right),
\qquad

\]
Consequently the proof-closing obstruction is no longer local nonvanishing.
It is interval-scale source-weighted non-concentration:
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

\begin{definition}[Interval-local source-collapse target]
\label{def:interval-local-source-collapse-target}
Let
\[
I_\rho=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q]
\]
be an admissible reduced good-patch interval attached to an off-line packet.
The interval-local source-collapse target is the collection of conditions
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]
while
\[
q_0(m)\asymp1,\qquad g(m),h(m)>0,
\]
and
\[
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}\asymp1
\]
throughout \(I_\rho\).  Since
\[
H=yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]
this target implies
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]
Taking \(C>A/3\) defeats the desired \(Q^{-A}\) lower bound.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Why interval-local source collapse is the sharp adversary]
\label{rem:why-interval-local-source-collapse-is-sharp}
Global bad points are not enough to refute the present architecture.  The
finite-core route needs a bound on each admissible interval \(I_\rho\).  The
source-collapse target in
Definition~\ref{def:interval-local-source-collapse-target} is therefore sharper
than a pointwise bad height.  It asks for the vulnerable source factor to be
small throughout the packet interval while the anisotropy vector remains live.
This is the correct adversarial form of Regime~B.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Derivative-flat fixed-prime surrogate]
\label{def:derivative-flat-fixed-prime-surrogate}
A fixed-prime surrogate for the interval-local source-collapse target is as
follows.  Let
\[
L_P(m)
=
\sum_{p\le P}(\log p)p^{-1/2}e^{-im\log p}.
\]
Define
\[
J_0(m)=B_0+\Re L_P(m),
\]
\[
J_2(m)=B_2+\Re L_P''(m),
\]
and
\[
J_4(m)=B_4+\Re L_P^{(4)}(m).
\]
The model residuals are
\[
R_1=J_2-6J_0+2J_0^3,
\]
\[
R_2=(1-J_0^2)J_2-\frac16J_4,
\]
and
\[
H_{\rm model}=-\frac{J_0J_2^3}{288}.
\]
The derivative-flat target is
\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R,
\]
with side conditions
\[
J_0(m_0)\approx2,
\qquad
J_4(m_0)\approx0.
\]
At the exact central target
\[
(J_0,J_2,J_4)=(2,0,0),
\]
one has
\[
R_1=4,\qquad R_2=0,
\]
and
\[
g=\frac2\pi>0,
\qquad
h=\frac{8}{3\pi}>0.
\]
Thus the source factor collapses while the anisotropy vector and Gram
positivity remain live.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Conditional interval-local source-collapse countermodel]
\label{prop:conditional-interval-local-source-collapse-countermodel}
Assume that, for arbitrarily large \(Q\), a fixed-prime or AFE-compatible
surrogate realizes the derivative-flat target of
Definition~\ref{def:derivative-flat-fixed-prime-surrogate} with
\[
\sup_{|m-m_0|\le c/Q}|J_2(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]
while
\[
J_0(m)\asymp1,\qquad
g(m),h(m)>0,
\]
and
\[
\max\{|R_1(m)|,|R_2(m)|\}\asymp1
\]
on
\[
I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q].
\]
Then the source-weighted lower bound
\[
\sup_{m\in I}
|H_{\rm model}(m)|
\max\{|R_1(m)|,|R_2(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}
\]
fails for every fixed \(A\), provided \(C>A/3\).

In particular, such a realization gives an interval-local countermodel to the
rank-two norm route in the fixed-prime or AFE surrogate.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
H_{\rm model}=-\frac{J_0J_2^3}{288}
\]
and \(J_0\asymp1\), the assumption
\[
\sup_I |J_2|\le Q^{-C}
\]
gives
\[
\sup_I |H_{\rm model}|\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]
The anisotropy factor is bounded on the interval by the hypotheses.  Hence
\[
\sup_{m\in I}
|H_{\rm model}(m)|
\max\{|R_1(m)|,|R_2(m)|\}
\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]
Choosing \(C>A/3\) gives the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Taylor control and the required derivative order]
\label{rem:taylor-control-derivative-order-source-collapse}
The natural scale audit gives
\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}(q'')\sim Q,
\qquad
|I_\rho|\sim Q^{-1},
\qquad
\Omega_{\rm eff}(q'')|I_\rho|\sim1.
\]
Thus \(q''\) has only bounded effective oscillatory complexity on the natural
packet interval.  If
\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]
then, for \(|u|\le c/Q\),
\[
J_2(m_0+u)
=
\frac{J_2^{(R+1)}(\xi)}{(R+1)!}u^{R+1}.
\]
With a Bernstein-type bound
\[
|J_2^{(R+1)}|\lesssim Q^{M_0}\Omega^{R+1},
\qquad
\Omega\sim Q,
\]
one obtains
\[
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}|J_2(m_0+u)|
\lesssim
Q^{M_0}
\frac{C_c^{R+1}}{(R+1)!}.
\]
A safe choice is therefore
\[
R\asymp (C+M_0)\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
or more conservatively \(R=O(\log Q)\).  This is far below the heuristic
recurrence-danger threshold \(Q/\log Q\).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Rank and recurrence status of the derivative-flat target]
\label{rem:rank-recurrence-status-derivative-flat-target}
In the phase-relaxed model, the derivative conditions have a Vandermonde-type
rank structure.  Indeed,
\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)
=
\Re\sum_j a_j(-i\lambda_j)^{r+2}e^{-im_0\lambda_j},
\]
with
\[
\lambda_j=\log p_j
\quad\text{or}\quad
\lambda_j=k\log p.
\]
For distinct active frequencies, the derivative-jet matrix has full generic
rank for any fixed finite list of derivatives.  Thus phase-relaxed flattening
has no finite-dimensional rank obstruction.

The actual fixed-prime model restricts the phases to the one-parameter flow
\[
m_0\mapsto (m_0\lambda_j)_j\pmod{2\pi}.
\]
If the derivative-flat target has codimension
\[
K\sim R+3
\]
and the target tolerance is
\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C},
\]
the heuristic recurrence cost is
\[
T_{\rm hit}\sim Q^{CK}.
\]
For \(R=O(\log Q)\), this is
\[
T_{\rm hit}=\exp(O((\log Q)^2))\ll e^Q.
\]
Therefore scale considerations do not presently block recurrence to the
derivative-flat target.  A rigorous proof or disproof would require a
quantitative prime-log recurrence theorem or a numerical fixed-prime/AFE
solve.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[AFE compatibility of the derivative-flat target]
\label{rem:afe-compatibility-derivative-flat-target}
In an AFE-compatible surrogate, one should replace \(J_r\) by
\[
J_r(m)
=
B_r(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le N}
a_n(\log n)^r e^{-im\log n}V(n/N)
+
\Re\left[
\chi(m)
\sum_{n\le N^*}
a_n^*(\log n)^r e^{im\log n}V^*(n/N^*)
\right].
\]
The gamma/background vector \(B_r(m)\) shifts the derivative-flat target; the
dual sum adds coupled oscillatory frequencies; smoothing changes amplitudes.
No algebraic relation is currently known that forces
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}|J_2^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}
\]
or otherwise blocks the conditions
\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]
Thus the AFE model remains compatible with the interval-local source-collapse
countermodel unless a new source-jet nonflatness theorem is proved.
\end{remark}

\begin{hypothesis}[Actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness]
\label{hyp:actual-zeta-source-jet-nonflatness}
For every admissible reduced packet interval \(I_\rho\), actual zeta data
satisfy a source-jet nonflatness bound.  A minimal form is
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]
A finite-jet version is
\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]
No ingredient currently established in this paper proves this hypothesis.
The distinguished off-line packet contributes to \(q''\), but rest/core terms
can cancel it; same-scale selection, core-gap stability, endpoint separation,
Gram positivity, finite Hadamard symmetry, and the current row algebra do not
prevent such cancellation.  Consequently
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:actual-zeta-source-jet-nonflatness} is the current
arithmetic input needed to save the rank-two norm route.
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[Terminal status of the current rank-two architecture]
\label{rem:terminal-status-rank-two-current-architecture}
The rank-two fixed-sector architecture has produced a coherent local
obstruction theory:
\[
\Gamma_G\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\]
and
\[
\Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]
It also clarified why scalar, quotient-only, split, line-bundle, energy,
ambient \(D\)-sector, finite derivative, and naive projective repairs do not
currently close the proof.  The remaining obstruction is source divisibility:
the useful rows carry \(H=yq''\), and interval-local source collapse is not
excluded by the present framework.

Thus the current architecture is non-closing unless one supplies one of:
\[
\boxed{\text{a source-robust row not divisible by }H,}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{the actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness hypothesis,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{a global projective/transport index theorem with correction control,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{\text{a new prime-side arithmetic coercivity theorem.}
}
\]
Absent one of these inputs, the rank-two construction should be treated as a
strong local obstruction framework rather than a complete RH proof.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
The rank-two non-concentration theorem needed by the present
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Source-collapse refinement of sampled non-concentration]

Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration} is stronger
than qualitative packet visibility.  In the current layered rank-two
coordinates, a necessary local component of this hypothesis is the exclusion

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\le Q^{-C},

\]

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad

\]
and hence the fixed-sector norm can be made smaller than the required
```
