## Edit 5 — Optional paper-wide audit note near the end of the rank-two section

**Where:** At the end of the rank-two architecture block, immediately before the next major subsection/section after `Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration`, or, if you prefer to keep all of this before the finite-core section, after **Edit 2**.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Attack-status summary]
\label{rem:attack-status-summary-after-rank-two-source-collapse}
The current attack has the following status.

\begin{enumerate}
\item The scalar Bottleneck-C flatness route remains open-negative: no
pointwise identity has been found forcing the rebuilt obstruction coefficient
to vanish.

\item Quotient, split, line-bundle, energy, and simple projective repairs are
diagnostic but not proof-closing.  Quotient loses line anomalies; split
recovers the full obstruction; line-bundle transport lacks global covariance;
energy has no monotonicity or endpoint theorem; and projective data lack a
global index/holonomy contradiction.

\item The rank-two fixed-sector bundle is the best current local language.
It turns the active \(\eta\eta\) row into tensorial affine forcing rather than
a scalar defect.

\item Local packet visibility is now layered:
\[
\Gamma_G\ne0\Rightarrow A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0\Rightarrow A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

\item The useful rows are nevertheless source-divisible:
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
H=yq''.
\]

\item The source factor has cubic leading behavior
\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]
Thus source collapse \(q''\approx0\) kills the norm rows even when layered
anisotropy is live.

\item Fixed finite derivative towers and transported first derivatives do not
currently rescue the norm route.  They require a new source-jet nonflatness
theorem.

\item The clean projective ratio
\[
[A_7:A_9]=[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}]
\]
cancels \(H\) only in the idealized factorized model.  Correction rows and
Regime~A, where
\[
\Gamma_G\approx\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0,
\]
prevent it from being a proof gate at present.

\item The interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel is the
sharp adversarial object.  It asks whether one can make
\[
q''(m)\approx0
\]
throughout \(I_\rho\) while keeping Gram positivity and anisotropy live.

\item The exact positive input now needed is an actual-zeta arithmetic theorem,
such as
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B},
\]
or a source-robust row/global invariant that replaces the source-divisible
rank-two norm vector.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 1 — Replace stale “proof has four pillars” language in the Introduction

**Why:** The introduction now correctly says the proof is not closed, but immediately after that it still says “The proof has four main pillars” and describes the method as arguing that an off-line zero forces a forbidden mode. That is now too strong. The current state is a framework / attack architecture, not a proof.

**Where:** In `\section{Introduction}`, replace this block:

```latex
We introduce a normalized local jet-Gramian associated to the corrected local phase geometry. This object encodes the intrinsic local deformation after removal of the dominant value-channel and background effects, and it is the basic carrier of the odd quotient information used in the argument.

The proof has four main pillars.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\arabic*.,nosep]
    \item \emph{Jet normalization:} replace raw point samples by local value/derivative coordinates.
    \item \emph{Value/curvature splitting:} separate the leading background-subtracted value channel from the curvature and tail corrections.
    \item \emph{Canonical calibration:} extract the correct value scale from the actual leading zeta-side value matrix rather than from an ad hoc scalar functional.
    \item \emph{$N$-point transverse cancellation:} use an odd holomorphic expansion and explicit cancellation coefficients to crush the zeta transverse channel exponentially in the local height parameter.
\end{enumerate}

This approach is not aimed at discovering new direct relations among primes. Rather, it studies a local, normalized geometric object attached to the zeta function and argues that an off-line zero would force a forbidden transverse odd mode in that object. In that sense, the method is primarily a zeta-side rigidity argument, with prime-distribution consequences entering only indirectly through the arithmetic content encoded in the zeta phase and, more broadly, through the classical zero--prime linkage expressed by the explicit formula \cite{Bombieri2000,Conrey2003,Edwards2001,Titchmarsh1986}. This local geometric viewpoint is not standard among the main classical families of approaches to $\RH$ surveyed in the literature \cite{Bombieri2000,Conrey2003}.
```

**Replace with:**

```latex
We introduce a normalized local jet-Gramian associated to the corrected local
phase geometry. This object encodes the intrinsic local deformation after
removal of the dominant value-channel and background effects, and it is the
basic carrier of the odd quotient and rank-two fixed-sector information used
in the attack.

The framework has four main technical layers.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\arabic*.,nosep]
    \item \emph{Jet normalization:} replace raw point samples by local
    value/derivative coordinates.
    \item \emph{Value/curvature splitting:} separate the leading
    background-subtracted value channel from the curvature and tail
    corrections.
    \item \emph{Canonical calibration:} extract the correct value scale from
    the actual leading zeta-side value matrix rather than from an ad hoc
    scalar functional.
    \item \emph{Rank-two fixed-sector visibility:} replace the failed scalar
    Bottleneck-C closure by a layered rank-two obstruction, with order-seven
    and order-nine visibility on the reduced base.
\end{enumerate}

This approach is not aimed at discovering new direct relations among primes.
Rather, it studies a local, normalized geometric object attached to the zeta
function and isolates what an off-line zero would have to force in that object.
The current local analysis does not by itself rule out all off-line
configurations: after the rank-two repair, the proof-closing obstruction has
moved to a source-weighted interval non-concentration problem for actual zeta
data.  Prime-distribution information therefore re-enters through the
arithmetic content encoded in the zeta phase and, more concretely, through the
source-jet nonflatness problem recorded later in the paper.  This local
geometric viewpoint is not standard among the main classical families of
approaches to $\RH$ surveyed in the literature
\cite{Bombieri2000,Conrey2003}.
```

## Edit 2 — Add a “next arithmetic attack” subsection before the terminal architecture ledger

**Why:** The paper now records the no-go, but it does not yet give future agents enough “ammo” for the next attack. The Big Picture explicitly says the next target is source-curvature observability / actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness, not more row algebra. It also says the first step is to make \(q''\) canonical on the zero side and prime/AFE side. turn70file6

**Where:** Immediately before:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Terminal status of the current architecture]
\label{rem:terminal-status-current-architecture}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Arithmetic source-curvature observability: the next attack}
\label{subsec:arithmetic-source-curvature-observability-next-attack}

The preceding source-collapse countermodels show that the current rank-two
norm route cannot close from local row algebra, same-scale packet geometry, or
finite Hadamard/quartet symmetry alone.  The exact missing input is now an
arithmetic source-jet theorem for actual zeta data.  The minimal useful form is
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]
A stronger and more stable form is the interval energy estimate
\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]
This is the positive theorem that would block the interval-local
source-collapse branch.

\begin{definition}[Canonical source-curvature representation problem]
\label{def:canonical-source-curvature-representation-problem}
The first arithmetic task is to put the source curvature \(q''\) into a
canonical actual-zeta form on both sides of the explicit formula.  One needs a
zero-side representation
\[
q''(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_\rho K_2(m;\rho),
\]
with all source/core and background conventions fixed, and an AFE or
prime-side representation of the form
\[
q''(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
\Re\sum_n b_n(\log n)^2 n^{-im}
+
\text{\rm dual/gamma/error terms}.
\]
The coefficients \(b_n\), the smoothing, the dual term, the gamma/background
contribution, and the error terms must be specified in the same normalization
used by the rank-two local rows.  Until this representation is fixed, the
phrase ``actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness'' is not a precise theorem.
\end{definition}

\begin{hypothesis}[Off-line-packet source-curvature observability]
\label{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}
Let \(I_\rho\) be an admissible reduced good-patch interval attached to a
hypothetical off-line packet \(\rho\).  Actual zeta data satisfy
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]
for some fixed \(B\), outside the already named reduced-base and correction
incidence loci.
Equivalently, in a weaker pointwise form,
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[Why this theorem is genuinely arithmetic]
\label{rem:source-curvature-observability-is-arithmetic}
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability} cannot
follow from the local packet geometry developed above.  The same-scale
source-flattening theorem and finite quadrature corollary show that positive
same-distance packet configurations can make
\[
q''(m_0),\ q^{(4)}(m_0),\ldots,q^{(2M)}(m_0)
\]
vanish to arbitrary finite order while keeping
\[
q_0>0,\qquad g>0,\qquad h>0,
\]
and while keeping
\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]
bounded away from zero after normalization, for example near \(q_0=2\).
Thus any proof of
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability} must use
actual-zeta arithmetic beyond finite same-scale positive packet geometry.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Prime-side observability formulation]
\label{rem:prime-side-source-curvature-observability-formulation}
After fixing the representation in
Definition~\ref{def:canonical-source-curvature-representation-problem}, the
source-curvature problem becomes a short-interval non-approximation problem.
Writing
\[
q''(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m),
\]
where \(P_2\) is the oscillatory prime/AFE part, source collapse means
\[
P_2(m)\approx -B_2(m)
\quad\text{throughout }I_\rho.
\]
The desired arithmetic theorem is therefore an observability estimate of the
form
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|B_2(m)+P_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
A proof would likely have to use fixed zeta coefficients, not merely generic
Dirichlet-polynomial flexibility.  Candidate tools include localized large
sieve estimates, Montgomery--Vaughan mean-value estimates, explicit-formula
energy identities, or a zero-side theorem excluding the same-scale quadrature
configuration for actual zeta zeros.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Finite-jet version of the arithmetic problem]
\label{rem:finite-jet-source-nonflatness-problem}
The interval energy estimate may also be attacked through finite jets.  On an
interval
\[
I_\rho=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q],
\]
source collapse requires simultaneous smallness of
\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0),\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]
where the scale audit gives
\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]
or more conservatively \(R=O(\log Q)\).  In an AFE model this becomes a finite
system
\[
\sum_n b_n(-i\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx
-B_2^{(r)}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]
The positive theorem would be a prime-log derivative-jet nonrecurrence
statement:
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]
The recurrence heuristics developed above suggest that this is a difficult
arithmetic theorem and may be false in fixed-prime or AFE surrogates.  This is
therefore the sharp next branch of the attack.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
These fixed-prime and AFE models should be read as adversarial surrogates, not
as statements about actual zeta.  They do not settle the exact AFE
normalization, the exact gamma/background rows, the paper's precise
normalization of \(q_0,q'',q^{(4)}\), the zero-side packet/core realization, or
the deterministic existence theorem for actual zeta.  Their role is narrower:
they show that increasingly arithmetic-looking oscillatory models do not
automatically supply the source-jet nonflatness needed by the rank-two norm
route.  The actual proof-closing question is still
```

# Edits I would not make

1. **Do not add more order-11 tower material.** The current obstruction is source-collapse, and higher anisotropy rows remain source-divisible unless a new source-robust channel is found.

2. **Do not promote projectivization to theorem status.** It is still diagnostic because correction rows are not controlled and no global projective endpoint/index theorem exists.

3. **Do not insert the long numerical tables from the chat.** The current fixed-prime/AFE surrogate text and the zonotope/recurrence remarks are enough. Too much numerical detail will make the paper look empirical rather than structural.

4. **Do not state source-jet nonflatness as proved.** Keep it as a hypothesis / next attack theorem.

## Edit 3 — Add the off-line-packet conditional version of source observability

**Where:** Immediately after:

```latex
\end{hypothesis}
```

closing:

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Off-line-packet source-curvature observability]
\label{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}
```

and before:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Why this theorem is genuinely arithmetic]
\label{rem:source-curvature-observability-is-arithmetic}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Off-line-packet conditional form]
\label{rem:offline-packet-conditional-source-observability}
A more targeted version of
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability} uses the
hypothetical off-line packet itself.  Write
\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R,
\]
where \(q''_P\) is the contribution of the distinguished off-line packet and
\(q''_R\) is the contribution of the remaining core, tail, background, and
error terms in the fixed source/core convention.  The interval observability
claim may be sharpened to
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_P(m)+q''_R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
Equivalently, the rest term cannot satisfy
\[
q''_R(m)=-q''_P(m)+O(Q^{-B})
\]
throughout the packet interval.  This formulation uses the off-line-packet
hypothesis directly and is stronger than a generic short-interval lower bound
for \(q''\).  The same-scale source-flattening construction shows that this
cannot be proved from arbitrary positive same-scale packet geometry alone; it
must use actual-zeta arithmetic or a restriction on how actual zero packets
may be arranged around \(\rho\).
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This gives future work the sharpest theorem to attack. It incorporates the important insight that the theorem only needs to hold on intervals attached to a hypothetical off-line packet, not on arbitrary intervals. This is the best remaining positive route.

---

## Edit 4 — Add a zero-side quadrature obstruction remark

**Where:** Immediately after:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Why this theorem is genuinely arithmetic]
\label{rem:source-curvature-observability-is-arithmetic}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Zero-side quadrature obstruction to local proofs]
\label{rem:zero-side-quadrature-obstruction-to-local-proofs}
The same-scale source-flattening model gives a concrete obstruction to any
purely local zero-side proof of
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}.  The
continuous measure in
Theorem~\ref{thm:continuous-same-scale-source-flattening-model} lives on the
same-distance curve
\[
x^2+c^2=d^2
\]
and has positive density
\[
d\mu(\theta)=\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta.
\]
It makes the averaged packet profile locally constant, and finite quadrature
then matches arbitrary finite even jets while keeping positive weights and
same-distance packet scale.  Therefore actual zeta must exclude, or fail to
approximate, this quadrature pattern if the rank-two norm route is to close.
A plausible arithmetic formulation is:
actual zeta zeros near a hypothetical off-line packet cannot realize the
finite same-scale quadrature needed to make
\[
q''(m_0),q^{(4)}(m_0),\ldots,q^{(2M)}(m_0)
\]
all small while \(q_0>0\) and the Gram block remains positive.  This is the
zero-side form of the source-curvature observability problem.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** The current draft has the theorem and the general arithmetic hypothesis, but this insertion makes explicit what actual zeta must forbid: approximation of the same-scale quadrature distribution. This is important “ammo” for the next attack.

---

## Edit 5 — Add a short “why this is the next attack” ledger

**Where:** Immediately after:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Finite-jet version of the arithmetic problem]
\label{rem:finite-jet-source-nonflatness-problem}
...
\end{remark}
```

and before:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Terminal status of the current architecture]
\label{rem:terminal-status-current-architecture}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Why source-curvature observability is the next attack]
\label{rem:why-source-curvature-observability-next}
The preceding reductions force the next attack to be
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}.
The reason is the following chain.

First, the local row algebra succeeds only qualitatively:
\[
\Gamma_G\ne0\Rightarrow A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0\Rightarrow A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]
Second, the useful rows are source-divisible:
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
H=yq''.
\]
Third,
\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]
so source-flatness of \(q''\) collapses the current norm vector cubically.
Fourth, the same-scale source-flattening theorem shows that positive
same-scale packet geometry does not prevent finite-order source-flatness.
Finally, fixed-prime and AFE-style surrogates do not currently reveal an
automatic source-jet nonflatness mechanism.

Thus the least nonlinear and most targeted positive theorem is not the full
source-weighted residual estimate, but the source-curvature observability
estimate
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
If this theorem fails, the present rank-two norm/projective architecture is
non-closing unless a genuinely source-robust row or global projective/affine
index theorem is found.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This compactly explains the logic of the entire attack phase without changing the abstract, introduction, or conclusion.

